# C9911 ‚Äî C99 + C11 Conformance Source of Truth (mcc vs gcc vs clang)

A clause-by-clause index of ISO/IEC 9899:1999 (**C99**, working draft N1256) and
ISO/IEC 9899:2011 (**C11**, working draft N1570), with **every normative
requirement rewritten as a TODO checkbox** and cross-referenced against three
compilers: the in-tree **`mcc`**, **gcc 15.3**, and **clang 22**.

It is built to be the single source of truth for "what does the standard require,
and where does `mcc` agree with or diverge from gcc/clang?". Requirement text is
**paraphrased** (the ISO text is copyrighted), with a precise `¬ßclause¬∑paragraph`
citation on every item.

**Totals:** 3,837 requirement checkboxes ¬∑ 2,875 confirmed `mcc:‚úì` ¬∑ 111 rows
carry a non-`‚úì` mcc tag (88 `~` / 23 `‚úó`), of which 52 are mcc-specific
divergences from the gcc==clang consensus (45 `~` / 7 `‚úó`) and the rest are
consensus `‚úó`/`~` shared with gcc/clang ¬∑ remainder are non-testable spec/UB
items. The residual mcc-specific `‚úó`/`~` rows are the deliberate / no-consensus /
UB / not-separately-testable items catalogued in [TODO.md](TODO.md).

## Legend

Each requirement is a checkbox of the form:

```
- [ ] ¬ß<clause>p<paragraph> ‚Äî <paraphrased requirement>. ‚Äî mcc:<s> gcc:<s> clang:<s> (note)
```

- `¬ß...p...` ‚Äî the precise N1256/N1570 clause and paragraph. Library function
  rules cite the function's subclause.
- `(C11)` ‚Äî a requirement new in or changed by C11. `(C99-only)` ‚Äî a C99 rule
  that C11 removed or altered. `(C90)` ‚Äî noted where the lineage matters.
- Per-compiler status:
  - `‚úì` ‚Äî conforms / behaves as the standard requires (and matches the
    gcc==clang consensus where one exists).
  - `‚úó` ‚Äî diverges: rejects valid code, miscompiles, or is missing the feature.
  - `~` ‚Äî partial: diagnoses but does not reject, diagnostic-only, or
    standards-optional/implementation-defined latitude.
  - A parenthetical records the nature of any `mcc` divergence from the
    gcc==clang consensus.
- `(spec; not separately testable)` ‚Äî a pure definition, an undefined/unspecified/
  implementation-defined behavior, or an optimization/aliasing rule with no direct
  compile-or-run probe.
- `[ ]` is an open checkbox throughout: this is a *specification map*, not a work
  tracker ‚Äî an unchecked box means "this requirement exists", and the status tag
  records who satisfies it. (Items tagged `mcc:‚úó`/`mcc:~` are the actionable
  conformance gaps; see [TODO.md](TODO.md) for the ones already triaged/fixed.)

## How it is organized

Sections follow the standard's own numbering: ¬ß4‚Äì¬ß5 (conformance & environment),
¬ß6 (language), ¬ß7 (library), and the normative + cataloging annexes. The clause 7
library numbering shifted between C99 and C11 (e.g. C99 ¬ß7.16 `<stdarg.h>` ‚Üí
C11 ¬ß7.16 `<stdint.h>`); part titles note both where relevant.

## ¬ß4 Conformance & ¬ß5 Environment

> mcc status: 250 checkbox requirements tracked in this section; 1 carries a non-`‚úì` mcc tag, and it
> is a single substantive mcc-gap relative to the gcc==clang consensus: mcc advertises
> `__STDC_VERSION__ == 199901L` (C99) while actually shipping the C11 freestanding headers, atomics,
> threads and `_Noreturn` ‚Äî a by-design default, since gcc 15 defaults to C23 and clang 22 to C17.
> ¬ß6.11.6 obsolescent empty-paren declarators now draw mcc's `-Wstrict-prototypes` diagnostic, mcc
> predefines both `__STDC_UTF_16__` and `__STDC_UTF_32__` (value `1`), and the ¬ß5.1.2.3 / ¬ß5.1.2.4
> volatile-and-atomic ordering items are inspectable via `-S` and conform. Everything numeric ‚Äî
> `<limits.h>` and `<float.h>`, including all C11 additions ‚Äî is byte-for-byte identical to gcc/clang,
> and `#error`, trigraphs, UCNs, `main` startup/termination, escape-sequence values and all probed
> translation limits conform.

> C99‚ÜîC11 deltas in this section: C11 adds `#error` as a translation-failure trigger (¬ß4p4), adds `<stdalign.h>`/`<stdnoreturn.h>` to the freestanding header set (¬ß4p6), replaces the C99 "sequence point" wording of ¬ß5.1.2.3 with the *sequenced-before* relation and adds the entire ¬ß5.1.2.4 multi-threaded/data-race model, and adds the `*_HAS_SUBNORM`, `*_DECIMAL_DIG`, and `*_TRUE_MIN` `<float.h>` macros (¬ß5.2.4.2.2). Several ¬ß5.2.4.1 translation limits and ¬ß5.2.4.2.1 magnitudes were already raised from C90 to their current values in C99.

### ¬ß4 Conformance

- ¬ß4p1 ‚Äî "shall" is to be interpreted as a requirement on an implementation or on a program; "shall not" is to be interpreted as a prohibition. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p2 ‚Äî If a "shall"/"shall not" requirement that appears outside of a constraint or runtime-constraint is violated, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p2 ‚Äî Undefined behavior is indicated either by the words "undefined behavior", by the omission of any explicit definition of behavior, or by a "shall"/"shall not" outside a constraint; there is no difference in emphasis among these three forms ‚Äî they all describe behavior that is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p3 ‚Äî A program that is correct in all other aspects, operating on correct data, containing unspecified behavior shall be a correct program and act in accordance with ¬ß5.1.2.3. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß4p4 ‚Äî (C11) The implementation shall not successfully translate a preprocessing translation unit containing a `#error` preprocessing directive unless it is part of a group skipped by conditional inclusion. (Added in C11; absent in C99.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three reject a live `#error`; all three accept `#error` inside a `#if 0` skipped group)
- ¬ß4p5 ‚Äî A *strictly conforming program* shall use only those features of the language and library specified in this International Standard. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p5 ‚Äî A strictly conforming program shall not produce output dependent on any unspecified, undefined, or implementation-defined behavior, and shall not exceed any minimum implementation limit. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî The two forms of conforming implementation are *hosted* and *freestanding*; a conforming hosted implementation shall accept any strictly conforming program. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__STDC_HOSTED__ == 1` by default for all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî A conforming freestanding implementation shall accept any strictly conforming program in which the use of clause-7 library features is confined to the standard headers `<float.h>`, `<iso646.h>`, `<limits.h>`, `<stdalign.h>` (C11), `<stdarg.h>`, `<stdbool.h>`, `<stddef.h>`, `<stdint.h>`, and `<stdnoreturn.h>` (C11). (C99 freestanding set omits `<stdalign.h>` and `<stdnoreturn.h>`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all nine headers `#include` cleanly under `-ffreestanding` in mcc; `__STDC_HOSTED__ == 0` under `-ffreestanding` for all three)
- ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî A conforming implementation may have extensions (including additional library functions), provided they do not alter the behavior of any strictly conforming program. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p7 ‚Äî A *conforming program* is one that is acceptable to a conforming implementation. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p8 ‚Äî An implementation shall be accompanied by a document that defines all implementation-defined and locale-specific characteristics and all extensions. ‚Äî (spec; documentation requirement, not separately testable)
- ¬ß4p8 (footnote) ‚Äî Strictly conforming programs are intended to be maximally portable among conforming implementations, and may use conditional features (e.g. those in annexes) provided their use is guarded by an appropriate conditional-feature macro test. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß5 Environment

- ¬ß5p1 ‚Äî An implementation translates C source files and executes C programs in two data-processing-system environments ‚Äî the *translation environment* and the *execution environment* ‚Äî referred to as such whether or not they share the same physical machine. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß5.1 Conceptual models

#### ¬ß5.1.1 Translation environment

##### ¬ß5.1.1.1 Program structure

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.1p1 ‚Äî A C *program* need not all be translated at the same time. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all support separate `-c` translation + later link)
- ¬ß5.1.1.1p1 ‚Äî The text of the program is kept in units called *source files* (or *preprocessing files*). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.1.1p1 ‚Äî A source file together with all the headers and source files included via `#include` is a *preprocessing translation unit*; after preprocessing it is called a *translation unit*. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.1p1 ‚Äî Previously translated translation units may be preserved individually or in libraries. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc produces ELF `.o` objects linkable into archives)
- ¬ß5.1.1.1p1 ‚Äî The separate translation units of a program communicate by (for example) calls to functions whose identifiers have external linkage, manipulation of objects whose identifiers have external linkage, or manipulation of data files. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.1p1 ‚Äî Translation units may be separately translated and then later linked to produce an executable program. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß5.1.1.2 Translation phases

- ¬ß5.1.1.2p1 ‚Äî The precedence among the syntax rules of translation is specified by the following eight phases. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(1) ‚Äî Phase 1: Physical source file multibyte characters are mapped, in an implementation-defined manner, to the source character set (introducing new-line characters for end-of-line indicators) if necessary; trigraph sequences are replaced by their corresponding single-character internal representations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (trigraph replacement under `-trigraphs`; off by default for all three ‚Äî see ¬ß5.2.1.1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(2) ‚Äî Phase 2: Each instance of a backslash (`\`) immediately followed by a new-line character is deleted, splicing physical source lines into logical source lines; only the last backslash on any physical source line is eligible for such a splice. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a\<NL>b=5;` splices to identifier `ab` in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(2) ‚Äî Phase 2: A source file that is not empty shall end in a new-line character, which shall not be immediately preceded by a backslash character before any such splicing takes place. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (a missing final newline is UB, not a constraint; all three silently accept even under `-std=c11 -pedantic-errors`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(3) ‚Äî Phase 3: The source file is decomposed into preprocessing tokens and sequences of white-space characters (including comments); a source file shall not end in a partial preprocessing token or in a partial comment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three diagnose an unterminated `/*` comment)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(3) ‚Äî Phase 3: Each comment is replaced by one space character; new-line characters are retained; whether each nonempty sequence of white-space characters other than new-line is retained or replaced by one space character is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (comment-to-space tokenization, e.g. `a/**/b` ‚Üí two tokens, behaves identically)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(4) ‚Äî Phase 4: Preprocessing directives are executed, macro invocations are expanded, and `_Pragma` unary operator expressions are executed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Pragma` recognized; see ¬ß6.11.8 probe)
- ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(4) ‚Äî Phase 4: If a character sequence that matches the syntax of a universal character name is produced by `##` token concatenation, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(4) ‚Äî Phase 4: A `#include` directive causes the named header or source file to be processed from phase 1 through phase 4, recursively; all preprocessing directives are then deleted. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(5) ‚Äî Phase 5: Each source character set member and escape sequence in character constants and string literals is converted to the corresponding member of the execution character set; if there is no corresponding member, it is converted to an implementation-defined member other than the null (wide) character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (escape-sequence values identical; see ¬ß5.2.2)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(6) ‚Äî Phase 6: Adjacent string literal tokens are concatenated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`"a" "b"` ‚Üí `"ab"`; verified at runtime)
- ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(7) ‚Äî Phase 7: White-space characters separating tokens are no longer significant; each preprocessing token is converted into a token; the resulting tokens are syntactically and semantically analyzed and translated as a translation unit. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable as a discrete phase)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.2p1(8) ‚Äî Phase 8: All external object and function references are resolved; library components are linked to satisfy external references not defined in the current translation; all such translator output is collected into a program image containing information needed for execution in its execution environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc invokes/embeds a linker to produce a runnable image)
- ¬ß5.1.1.2p2 (footnote) ‚Äî Implementations shall behave as if these separate phases occur, even though in practice many phases might be folded together. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.1.2p2 (footnote) ‚Äî Source files, translation units, and translated translation units need not be stored as files, nor need there be any one-to-one correspondence between these entities and any external representation; the description is conceptual only and does not specify any particular implementation. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß5.1.1.3 Diagnostics

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.3p1 ‚Äî A conforming implementation shall produce at least one diagnostic message (identified in an implementation-defined manner) if a preprocessing translation unit or translation unit contains a violation of any syntax rule or constraint, even if the behavior is also explicitly specified as undefined or implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (syntax error `return }` ‚Üí diagnostic + non-zero exit in all three; constraint violation `int x = "string";` ‚Üí mcc emits a warning by default ‚Äî satisfying "at least one diagnostic" ‚Äî but translates successfully unless `-Werror`, whereas gcc/clang make it an error. The standard's last sentence explicitly permits successfully translating an invalid program, so mcc conforms; it is merely more permissive by default.)
- ¬ß5.1.1.3p1 ‚Äî Diagnostic messages need not be produced in other circumstances. ‚Äî (spec; permission, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.1.3p1 (footnote) ‚Äî The intent is that an implementation identify the nature of, and where possible localize, each violation; an implementation is free to produce any number of diagnostics so long as a valid program is still correctly translated, and may also successfully translate an invalid program. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc localizes diagnostics with `file:line:` prefixes)

#### ¬ß5.1.2 Execution environments

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2p1 ‚Äî Two execution environments are defined: *freestanding* and *hosted*; in both, *program startup* occurs when a designated C function is called by the execution environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-ffreestanding` vs default hosted both supported)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2p1 ‚Äî All objects with static storage duration shall be initialized (set to their initial values) before program startup; the manner and timing of such initialization are otherwise unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (static/global initializers observed before `main`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2p1 ‚Äî *Program termination* returns control to the execution environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß5.1.2.1 Freestanding environment

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.1p1 ‚Äî In a freestanding environment (in which C program execution may take place without any benefit of an operating system), the name and type of the function called at program startup are implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all accept `-ffreestanding -nostdlib` with a custom entry, e.g. `_start`)
- ¬ß5.1.2.1p1 ‚Äî Any library facilities available to a freestanding program, other than the minimal set required by clause 4, are implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.1p2 ‚Äî The effect of program termination in a freestanding environment is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)

##### ¬ß5.1.2.2 Hosted environment

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2p1 ‚Äî A hosted environment need not be provided, but shall conform to the following specifications if present. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (hosted is the default)

###### ¬ß5.1.2.2.1 Program startup

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p1 ‚Äî The function called at program startup is named `main`; the implementation declares no prototype for this function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p1 ‚Äî `main` shall be defined with a return type of `int` and either no parameters (`int main(void)`) or two parameters (`int main(int argc, char *argv[])`) or in some other implementation-defined manner. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both standard forms compile and run)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p1 (footnote) ‚Äî `int` can be replaced by a typedef name defined as `int`, or the type of `argv` can be written as `char **argv`, and so on. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`char **argv` form accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî If defined, the `main` parameters shall obey: the value of `argc` shall be nonnegative, and `argv[argc]` shall be a null pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime check `argv[argc]==NULL` true for all three; supplied by the host C runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî If `argc` is greater than zero, the array members `argv[0]` through `argv[argc-1]` inclusive shall contain pointers to strings, given implementation-defined values by the host environment prior to program startup. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (host-supplied; runtime-verified)
- ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî If the host environment cannot supply strings with letters in both uppercase and lowercase, the implementation shall ensure the strings are received in lowercase. ‚Äî (spec; host-environment property, not separately testable on Linux)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî If `argc` is greater than zero, the string pointed to by `argv[0]` represents the program name; `argv[0][0]` shall be the null character if the program name is not available from the host environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`argv[0]` carries the invocation name; supplied by the runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî If `argc` is greater than one, the strings pointed to by `argv[1]` through `argv[argc-1]` represent the *program parameters*. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî The parameters `argc` and `argv` and the strings pointed to by the `argv` array shall be modifiable by the program, and retain their last-stored values between program startup and program termination. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (writes to `argv[i][j]` persist)

###### ¬ß5.1.2.2.2 Program execution

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.2p1 ‚Äî In a hosted environment, a program may use all the functions, macros, type definitions, and objects described in the library clause (clause 7). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc links against the system libc; clause-7 facilities available)

###### ¬ß5.1.2.2.3 Program termination

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.3p1 ‚Äî If the return type of `main` is compatible with `int`, a return from the initial call to `main` is equivalent to calling `exit` with the value returned by `main` as its argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`return 42` ‚Üí process exit status 42 in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.2.3p1 ‚Äî Reaching the `}` that terminates `main` returns a value of 0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (fall-off `int main(void){}` ‚Üí exit status 0 in all three)
- ¬ß5.1.2.2.3p1 ‚Äî If the return type of `main` is not compatible with `int`, the termination status returned to the host environment is unspecified. ‚Äî (unspecified; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.2.3p1 (footnote) ‚Äî In accordance with ¬ß6.2.4, the lifetimes of objects with automatic storage duration declared in `main` will have ended when returning from `main`, even where they would not have when calling `exit` from within `main`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß5.1.2.3 Program execution

> C99 specifies ordering of evaluations entirely through *sequence points* (¬ß5.1.2.3p2); C11 reframes this as the *sequenced-before* / *sequenced-after* / *unsequenced* / *indeterminately-sequenced* relation (¬ß5.1.2.3p3) and adds lvalue value computation (¬ß5.1.2.3p2).

- ¬ß5.1.2.3p1 ‚Äî The semantic descriptions describe the behavior of an abstract machine in which issues of optimization are irrelevant. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p2 ‚Äî Accessing a volatile object, modifying an object, modifying a file, or calling a function that does any of those operations are all *side effects* ‚Äî changes in the state of the execution environment. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p2 ‚Äî Evaluation of an expression in general includes both value computations and initiation of side effects. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) Value computation for an lvalue expression includes determining the identity of the designated object. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p2 ‚Äî (C99-only) At certain specified points in the execution sequence called *sequence points*, all side effects of previous evaluations shall be complete and no side effects of subsequent evaluations shall have taken place. (Annex C lists the sequence points; replaced by the sequenced-before model in C11.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (sequence-point semantics honored; e.g. full-expression `;` ordering verified, ¬ß5.1.2.3 EXAMPLE)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) *Sequenced before* is an asymmetric, transitive, pair-wise relation between evaluations executed by a single thread, inducing a partial order; if A is sequenced before B then the execution of A shall precede that of B, and B is *sequenced after* A. ‚Äî (spec; abstract-machine relation, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) If A is not sequenced before or after B, then A and B are *unsequenced*; they are *indeterminately sequenced* when A is sequenced either before or after B but it is unspecified which. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) The presence of a *sequence point* between the evaluation of A and B implies that every value computation and side effect associated with A is sequenced before every value computation and side effect associated with B. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p4 ‚Äî In the abstract machine, all expressions are evaluated as specified by the semantics; an actual implementation need not evaluate part of an expression if it can deduce that its value is not used and that no needed side effects are produced. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (dead-code/value elision permitted and performed)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p5 ‚Äî When the abstract machine is interrupted by receipt of a signal, the values of objects that are neither lock-free atomic objects (C11) nor of type `volatile sig_atomic_t` are unspecified, as is the state of the floating-point environment. ‚Äî (unspecified; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p5 ‚Äî The value of any object modified by the signal handler that is neither a lock-free atomic object (C11) nor of type `volatile sig_atomic_t` becomes indeterminate when the handler exits, as does the state of the floating-point environment if modified by the handler and not restored. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p6 ‚Äî The least requirements on a conforming implementation are: accesses to volatile objects are evaluated strictly according to the rules of the abstract machine. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (now verifiable via `mcc -S`: each `volatile` object is accessed with a real load/store emitted in program order, matching gcc -O0 ‚Äî no elision or reordering)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p6 ‚Äî At program termination, all data written into files shall be identical to the result that execution of the program according to the abstract semantics would have produced. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (file output identical across all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p6 ‚Äî The input and output dynamics of interactive devices shall take place as specified in ¬ß7.21.3, with the intent that unbuffered or line-buffered output appear as soon as possible. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (delegated to the shared libc stdio implementation)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p6 ‚Äî Accesses to volatile objects, file-write identity, and interactive-device I/O dynamics are collectively the *observable behavior* of the program. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p7 ‚Äî What constitutes an interactive device is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p8 ‚Äî More stringent correspondences between abstract and actual semantics may be defined by each implementation. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p9 (EXAMPLE 1) ‚Äî An implementation might define a one-to-one correspondence between abstract and actual semantics. ‚Äî (informative example; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.3p10 (EXAMPLE 2) ‚Äî Alternatively, an implementation might optimize within each translation unit so that semantics agree only at cross-translation-unit function calls. ‚Äî (informative example; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p11 (EXAMPLE 3) ‚Äî Floating-point expression rearrangement is constrained by limited precision; `(x*y)*z` need not equal `x*(y*z)`, and rearrangements changing special-value handling or raised exceptions are disallowed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none of the three reassociate FP without `-ffast-math`-style opt-in)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p12 (EXAMPLE 4) ‚Äî Use of a volatile object in `a = b = c;` requires the implementation to read `c`, store into `b`, read `b`, then store into `a`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (now inspectable via `mcc -S`: mcc emits read `c` ‚Üí store `b` ‚Üí store `a`, the identical volatile-access strategy gcc -O0 uses ‚Äî both reuse the assigned value rather than re-reading `b`, which the standard permits)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3p13 (EXAMPLE 5) ‚Äî When a value is dead, the implementation need not perform the access; the abstract semantics permit eliding it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (dead non-volatile computations elided)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.3 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî A `printf` of a function call demonstrates that all side effects associated with the full expression are complete before the next full expression is evaluated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß5.1.2.4 Multi-threaded executions and data races (C11)

> Entire subclause is C11-only; absent from C99. mcc ships `<threads.h>`, `<stdatomic.h>`, `_Atomic`,
> `_Thread_local`, and `_Noreturn`, and defines neither `__STDC_NO_THREADS__` nor `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`
> (matching gcc/clang) ‚Äî so it claims support for the entire memory model, even though
> `__STDC_VERSION__` still reads `199901L`.

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Under a hosted implementation, a program can have more than one *thread of execution* running concurrently; the execution of the entire program consists of an execution of all of its threads. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`<threads.h>` `thrd_create`/`thrd_join` program compiles, links `-lpthread`, and runs in all three)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Under a freestanding implementation, it is implementation-defined whether a program can have more than one thread of execution. ‚Äî (implementation-defined; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) The value of an object visible to a thread T at a particular point is the *initial value*, a value stored by T, or a value stored by another thread, according to the rules below. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p3 ‚Äî (C11) Two expression evaluations *conflict* if one of them modifies a memory location and the other reads or modifies the same memory location. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.4p4 ‚Äî (C11) The library defines synchronization operations (¬ß7.17 atomics, ¬ß7.26.4 mutexes); a synchronization operation is an acquire, a release, both, or a consume operation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_store`/`atomic_load`/`atomic_thread_fence` with `memory_order_*` available via `<stdatomic.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.4p4 ‚Äî (C11) An operation without an associated memory location is a fence ‚Äî acquire, release, or both; additionally there are relaxed atomic operations and atomic read-modify-write operations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_thread_fence`, `atomic_fetch_add`, relaxed RMW provided)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p5 ‚Äî (C11) A *full expression* is one that is not part of another expression, nor part of a (abstract) declarator; there is also an implicit full expression (e.g. a `while` controlling expression). (Definition relocated here in C11; corresponds to ¬ß6.8 in C99.) ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p6 ‚Äî (C11) Certain library calls *synchronize with* others; a release on atomic M synchronizes with an acquire on M that takes its value from the release sequence headed by it. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.4p7 ‚Äî (C11) An evaluation A *carries a dependency* to B if A's value is used as an operand of B, subject to the listed exceptions (`kill_dependency`, left operand of `&&`/`||`/`?:`/`,`, etc.). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`kill_dependency` macro provided by `<stdatomic.h>`)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p8 ‚Äî (C11) A is *dependency-ordered before* B per the consume/release-sequence rules. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p9 ‚Äî (C11) A is *inter-thread happens before* B if A synchronizes with B, A is dependency-ordered before B, or the listed transitive combinations hold. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p10 ‚Äî (C11) A *happens before* B if A is sequenced before B or A inter-thread happens before B. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p11 ‚Äî (C11) A *visible side effect* A on M w.r.t. value computation B satisfies the happens-before/no-intervening-X conditions; the value of a non-atomic scalar M as determined by B is the value stored by the visible side effect A. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p12 ‚Äî (C11) The execution of a program contains a *data race* if it contains two conflicting actions in different threads, at least one not atomic, and neither happens before the other; any such data race results in undefined behavior. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p13 ‚Äî (C11) The visible sequence of side effects on an atomic M w.r.t. value computation B is a maximal contiguous sub-sequence in the modification order of M; the value of M as determined by B shall be the value stored by some operation in that sequence. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p14 ‚Äî (C11) If A modifying atomic M happens before B modifying M, then A is earlier than B in the modification order of M. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p15 ‚Äî (C11) If a value computation A of atomic M happens before B of M, and A takes its value from side effect X, then B's value equals A's or is from a Y following X in the modification order. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.4p16 ‚Äî (C11) The four coherence requirements disallow compiler reordering of atomic operations to a single object even for relaxed loads. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (now inspectable via `mcc -S`: a relaxed store/load/store to one atomic emits three distinct in-order operations with no reordering or CSE across them; mcc performs no optimizing passes that could reorder, so coherence holds)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p17 ‚Äî (C11) The value of an atomic M as determined by B is the value stored by some side effect A modifying M where B does not happen before A. ‚Äî (spec; memory-model, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.1.2.4p18 ‚Äî (C11) Atomic read-modify-write operations shall always read the last value (in modification order) written before the associated write. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_fetch_add` lowers to an atomic RMW instruction)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p19 ‚Äî (C11, recommended practice) An implementation should ensure the last value assigned by an atomic/synchronization operation becomes visible to all threads in finite time. ‚Äî (recommended practice; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.1.2.4p20‚Äìp25 (NOTEs/EXAMPLEs) ‚Äî (C11) Informative notes on `memory_order_seq_cst`, fence pairing, sequential consistency, and example data-race scenarios. ‚Äî (informative; not separately testable)

### ¬ß5.2 Environmental considerations

#### ¬ß5.2.1 Character sets

- ¬ß5.2.1p1 ‚Äî Two sets of characters and their collating sequences shall be defined: the *source character set* and the *execution character set*. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.1p1 ‚Äî Each set is divided into a *basic character set* and a set of locale-specific *extended characters*; the combined set is the *extended character set*. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p1 ‚Äî The values of the members of the execution character set are implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all use ASCII/UTF-8 execution set; basic-character values identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p2 ‚Äî In a character constant or string literal, members of the execution character set shall be represented by corresponding source characters or by escape sequences (`\` followed by one or more characters). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p2 ‚Äî A byte with all bits 0, the *null character*, shall exist in the basic execution character set; it is used to terminate a character string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\0'` == 0; string termination works)
- ¬ß5.2.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî The trigraph sequences allow entry of characters not in the Invariant Code Set of ISO/IEC 646. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî Both basic character sets shall include the 26 uppercase letters `A`‚Äì`Z`, the 26 lowercase letters `a`‚Äì`z`, and the 10 decimal digits `0`‚Äì`9`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî Both basic character sets shall include the 29 graphic characters `! " # % & ' ( ) * + , - . / : ; < = > ? [ \ ] ^ _ { | } ~`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî Both basic character sets shall include the space character and control characters for horizontal tab, vertical tab, and form feed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî In both basic character sets, the value of each character after `0` in the decimal digits shall be one greater than the previous (digits contiguous and increasing). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'9'-'0'==9`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî In source files, there shall be some way of indicating the end of each line; the standard treats an end-of-line indicator as a single new-line character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî In the basic execution character set there shall be control characters representing alert, backspace, carriage return, and new line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`\a \b \r \n` all defined; see ¬ß5.2.2)
- ¬ß5.2.1p3 ‚Äî If any other characters are encountered in a source file (except in an identifier, character constant, string literal, header name, comment, or never-converted preprocessing token), the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.1p4 ‚Äî A *letter* is an uppercase or lowercase Latin letter as defined above; the term excludes letters of other alphabets. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The universal character name construct (`\u`, `\U`) provides a way to name other characters (see ¬ß6.4.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (extended characters usable in identifiers `int √©=5;` and string literals `"caf√©"` compile and run in all three; mcc defines `__STDC_ISO_10646__ == 201706L`)

##### ¬ß5.2.1.1 Trigraph sequences

> Trigraphs are normative in both C99 and C11. All three compilers default trigraphs OFF in their
> modern modes and require `-trigraphs` to enable them ‚Äî a documented, shared deviation.

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.1p1 ‚Äî All occurrences of the nine trigraph sequences are replaced with the corresponding single character: `??=`‚Üí`#`; `??(`‚Üí`[`; `??/`‚Üí`\`; `??)`‚Üí`]`; `??'`‚Üí`^`; `??<`‚Üí`{`; `??!`‚Üí`|`; `??>`‚Üí`}`; `??-`‚Üí`~`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-trigraphs`, mcc replaces `??<`/`??>` to `{`/`}`; without it mcc, gcc, and clang all leave them unreplaced ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.1p2 ‚Äî No other trigraph sequences exist; each `?` that does not begin a listed trigraph is not changed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.1p3 (EXAMPLE 1) ‚Äî `??=define arraycheck(a,b) a??(b??) ??!??! b??(a??)` becomes `#define arraycheck(a,b) a[b] || b[a]`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-trigraphs`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.1p4 (EXAMPLE 2) ‚Äî `printf("Eh???/n");` becomes `printf("Eh?\n");` after replacing `??/` with `\`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-trigraphs`, all three emit bytes `E h ? \n`)

##### ¬ß5.2.1.2 Multibyte characters

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.2p1 ‚Äî The source character set may contain multibyte characters; the execution character set may also, and need not share the source encoding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UTF-8 multibyte in source accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.2p1 ‚Äî For both sets: the basic character set shall be present and each basic character encoded as a single byte; presence/meaning/representation of additional members is locale-specific. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß5.2.1.2p1 ‚Äî A multibyte character set may have a *state-dependent encoding* with an *initial shift state* and other *shift states*. ‚Äî (spec; locale property, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.1.2p1 ‚Äî While in the initial shift state, all single-byte characters retain their usual interpretation and do not alter the shift state; subsequent-byte interpretation depends on the current shift state. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.1.2p2 ‚Äî A byte with all bits zero is a null character independent of shift state, and shall not occur in the second or subsequent bytes of a multibyte character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UTF-8 guarantees this)
- ¬ß5.2.1.2p3 ‚Äî For source files, an identifier, comment, string literal, character constant, or header name shall begin and end in the initial shift state and consist of valid multibyte characters. ‚Äî (spec; locale property, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß5.2.2 Character display semantics

- ¬ß5.2.2p1 ‚Äî The *active position* is the location where the next character output by `fputc` would appear. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.2p1 ‚Äî Writing a printing character (per `isprint`) displays a graphic at the active position then advances the active position; line-writing direction is locale-specific. ‚Äî (spec; display-device behavior, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.2p1 ‚Äî If the active position is at the final position of a line, the behavior of the display device is unspecified. ‚Äî (unspecified; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\a` (alert) produces an audible or visible alert without changing the active position. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\a'` == 7 in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\b` (backspace) moves the active position to the previous position; at the initial position, display behavior is unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\b'` == 8)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\f` (form feed) moves the active position to the initial position at the start of the next logical page. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\f'` == 12)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\n` (new line) moves the active position to the initial position of the next line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\n'` == 10)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\r` (carriage return) moves the active position to the initial position of the current line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\r'` == 13)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\t` (horizontal tab) moves the active position to the next horizontal tab stop; at/past the last, display behavior is unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\t'` == 9)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p2 ‚Äî `\v` (vertical tab) moves the active position to the next vertical tab stop; at/past the last, display behavior is unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'\v'` == 11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.2p3 ‚Äî Each of these escape sequences shall produce a unique implementation-defined value storable in a single `char`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (the seven values `7 8 12 10 13 9 11` are pairwise distinct and identical across all three)
- ¬ß5.2.2p3 ‚Äî The external representations in a text file need not be identical to the internal representations and are outside this Standard's scope. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß5.2.3 Signals and interrupts

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.3p1 ‚Äî Functions shall be implementable such that they may be interrupted at any time by a signal, or called by a signal handler, or both, with no alteration to earlier still-active invocations' control flow, return values, or automatic objects. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc uses a per-invocation stack frame; reentrancy holds, consistent with gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.3p1 ‚Äî All such objects shall be maintained outside the *function image* (the instructions composing the executable representation of a function) on a per-invocation basis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (automatic objects live on the stack, not in the code image)

#### ¬ß5.2.4 Environmental limits

- ¬ß5.2.4p1 ‚Äî Both the translation and execution environments constrain implementations; this subclause summarizes the language-related environmental limits (library limits are in clause 7). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß5.2.4.1 Translation limits

> All values shown are the C99/C11 minimums. mcc, like gcc and clang, imposes no fixed low limits;
> every spot-probe well past the minimum translated successfully.

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî The implementation shall be able to translate and execute at least one program containing at least one instance of every one of the following limits. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (spot-probes below all pass)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 127 nesting levels of blocks. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (130 nested blocks compile in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 63 nesting levels of conditional inclusion. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 12 pointer, array, and function declarators modifying an arithmetic/structure/union/void type in a declaration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 63 nesting levels of parenthesized declarators within a full declarator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 63 nesting levels of parenthesized expressions within a full expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (70 nested parens compile in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 63 significant initial characters in an internal identifier or macro name (each UCN or extended source character counts as one). (C90 value was 31.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three treat the full identifier as significant)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 31 significant initial characters in an external identifier (UCN char-counts per the rule). (C90 value was 6, case-insensitive.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (two externals differing at char 40 stay distinct in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 4095 external identifiers in one translation unit. (C90 value was 511.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 511 identifiers with block scope declared in one block. (C90 value was 127.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 4095 macro identifiers simultaneously defined in one preprocessing translation unit. (C90 value was 1024.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 127 parameters in one function definition. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 127 arguments in one function call. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 127 parameters in one macro definition. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 127 arguments in one macro invocation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 4095 characters in a logical source line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 4095 characters in a character string literal or wide string literal (after concatenation). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (a 4100-byte string literal compiles in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 65535 bytes in an object (hosted only). (C90 value was 32767.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 15 nesting levels for `#include`d files. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 1023 `case` labels for a `switch` (excluding nested switches). (C90 value was 257.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 1023 members in a single structure or union. (C90 value was 127.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 1023 enumeration constants in a single enumeration. (C90 value was 127.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 ‚Äî 63 levels of nested structure/union definitions in a single struct-declaration-list. (C90 value was 15.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1p1 (footnote) ‚Äî Implementations should avoid imposing fixed translation limits whenever possible. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc imposes no fixed low limits in any probe)

##### ¬ß5.2.4.2 Numerical limits

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2p1 ‚Äî A conforming implementation shall document all the limits in this subclause, specified in `<limits.h>` and `<float.h>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc ships both headers; values verified below)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) Additional limits are specified in `<stdint.h>` (see ¬ß7.20.2/¬ß7.20.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc bundles `<stdint.h>`)

###### ¬ß5.2.4.2.1 Sizes of integer types `<limits.h>`

> mcc's `<limits.h>` values are byte-for-byte identical to gcc's and clang's on x86-64 Linux.

- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî The values below shall be replaced by constant expressions suitable for use in `#if` directives. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if INT_MAX < 32767` / `#if ULLONG_MAX < ‚Ä¶ULL` evaluate in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî Except for `CHAR_BIT` and `MB_LEN_MAX`, the macros shall have the same type as the corresponding object after integer promotions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî Their implementation-defined values shall be equal or greater in magnitude than those shown, with the same sign. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `CHAR_BIT` ‚â• `8`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `8`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SCHAR_MIN` ‚â§ `-127`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `-128`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SCHAR_MAX` ‚â• `+127`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `127`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `UCHAR_MAX` ‚â• `255`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `255`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `CHAR_MIN` ‚Äî `SCHAR_MIN` if `char` is signed, else `0`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `-128`, signed `char`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `CHAR_MAX` ‚Äî `SCHAR_MAX` if `char` is signed, else `UCHAR_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `127`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `MB_LEN_MAX` ‚â• `1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `16`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SHRT_MIN` ‚â§ `-32767`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `-32768`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SHRT_MAX` ‚â• `+32767`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `32767`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `USHRT_MAX` ‚â• `65535`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `65535`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `INT_MIN` ‚â§ `-32767`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `-2147483648`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `INT_MAX` ‚â• `+32767`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `2147483647`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `UINT_MAX` ‚â• `65535`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `4294967295`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LONG_MIN` ‚â§ `-2147483647`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `-9223372036854775808`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LONG_MAX` ‚â• `+2147483647`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `9223372036854775807`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `ULONG_MAX` ‚â• `4294967295`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `18446744073709551615`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LLONG_MIN` ‚â§ `-9223372036854775807`. (C99/C11; absent in C90.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `-9223372036854775808`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LLONG_MAX` ‚â• `+9223372036854775807`. (C99/C11; absent in C90.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `9223372036854775807`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `ULLONG_MAX` ‚â• `18446744073709551615`. (C99/C11; absent in C90.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `18446744073709551615`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî If a `char` value is treated as signed, `CHAR_MIN`==`SCHAR_MIN` and `CHAR_MAX`==`SCHAR_MAX`; otherwise `CHAR_MIN`==`0` and `CHAR_MAX`==`UCHAR_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all signed-char: `CHAR_MIN==SCHAR_MIN==-128`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî `UCHAR_MAX` shall equal `2^CHAR_BIT ‚àí 1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`255 == 2^8 ‚àí 1`)
- [ ] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî See ¬ß6.2.5: `char` has the same range/representation/behavior as either `signed char` or `unsigned char`, but is a distinct type. ‚Äî (spec; cross-reference, see ¬ß6.2.5 section)

###### ¬ß5.2.4.2.2 Characteristics of floating types `<float.h>`

> mcc's `<float.h>` (including every C11 addition ‚Äî `*_HAS_SUBNORM`, `*_DECIMAL_DIG`, `*_TRUE_MIN`)
> is byte-for-byte identical to gcc's and clang's output for an x86-64 IEC-60559 `float`/`double`/
> 80-bit `long double` configuration.

- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p1 ‚Äî Floating-type characteristics are defined via a model describing a floating-point representation. ‚Äî (spec; model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p1 ‚Äî A *floating-point number* x is defined by x = s¬∑b^e¬∑Œ£ f_k¬∑b^(‚àík), e_min ‚â§ e ‚â§ e_max, with s the sign, b the radix, e the exponent, p the precision, and f_k the significand digits. ‚Äî (spec; model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) A floating-point number that is zero or whose magnitude is in [b^(e_min‚àí1), b^(e_max)] is *normalized* if f_1 > 0. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p3 ‚Äî (C11) x is *subnormal* if 0 < x < b^(e_min‚àí1) and f_1 = 0; *unnormalized* if f_1 = 0 and not subnormal; b, p, e_min, e_max are fixed per type. ‚Äî (spec; definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p4 ‚Äî The accuracy of `+ - * /` and of `<math.h>`/`<complex.h>` floating-result functions, and of float‚Üîstring conversions in `<stdio.h>`/`<stdlib.h>`/`<wchar.h>`, is implementation-defined; the implementation may state the accuracy is unknown. ‚Äî (implementation-defined; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p5 ‚Äî All integer values in `<float.h>` except `FLT_ROUNDS` shall be `#if`-usable constant expressions; all floating values shall be constant expressions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if DECIMAL_DIG<10` / `#if FLT_EVAL_METHOD<0` evaluate in all three; note `FLT_ROUNDS` is correctly NOT guaranteed `#if`-usable ‚Äî clang errors on it in `#if` since it expands to `__builtin_flt_rounds()`, while mcc and gcc happen to keep it `#if`-usable; this is a documented latitude, not a defect)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p5 ‚Äî All macros except `DECIMAL_DIG`, `FLT_EVAL_METHOD`, `FLT_RADIX`, `FLT_ROUNDS` have separate `FLT_`/`DBL_`/`LDBL_` names. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three families present in mcc's header)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p6 ‚Äî `FLT_ROUNDS` characterizes the addition rounding mode: `-1` indeterminable, `0` toward zero, `1` to nearest, `2` toward +‚àû, `3` toward ‚àí‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p6 ‚Äî Except for assignment and cast, operator/conversion/constant values may be evaluated to a greater range and precision than the type; `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` characterizes this. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` characterizes evaluation formats: `-1` indeterminable; `0` just to the type; `1` float/double‚Üídouble, long double‚Üílong double; `2` all‚Üílong double. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p8 ‚Äî (C11) `FLT_HAS_SUBNORM`/`DBL_HAS_SUBNORM`/`LDBL_HAS_SUBNORM`: `-1` indeterminable, `0` absent, `1` present. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `1 1 1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_RADIX` ‚â• `2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `2`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_MANT_DIG`/`DBL_MANT_DIG`/`LDBL_MANT_DIG` ‚Äî number of base-`FLT_RADIX` significand digits, `p`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `24 / 53 / 64`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `DECIMAL_DIG` ‚â• `10`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `21`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî (C11) `FLT_DECIMAL_DIG` ‚â• 6, `DBL_DECIMAL_DIG` ‚â• 10, `LDBL_DECIMAL_DIG` ‚â• 10. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `9 / 17 / 21`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_DIG` ‚â• 6, `DBL_DIG` ‚â• 10, `LDBL_DIG` ‚â• 10. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `6 / 15 / 18`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_MIN_EXP`/`DBL_MIN_EXP`/`LDBL_MIN_EXP` = `e_min`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_MIN_EXP == -125`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_MIN_10_EXP`/‚Ä¶ ‚â§ `‚àí37`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_MIN_10_EXP == -37`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_MAX_EXP`/`DBL_MAX_EXP`/`LDBL_MAX_EXP` = `e_max`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_MAX_EXP == 128`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_MAX_10_EXP`/‚Ä¶ ‚â• `+37`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_MAX_10_EXP == 38`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p10 ‚Äî `FLT_MAX`/`DBL_MAX`/`LDBL_MAX` ‚â• `1√ó10^+37`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_MAX‚âà3.40282e+38`, `DBL_MAX‚âà1.79769e+308`)
- [ ] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p11 ‚Äî The following shall have values ‚â§ those shown. ‚Äî (spec; header introductory clause)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p11 ‚Äî `FLT_EPSILON` ‚â§ `1√ó10^‚àí5`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `‚âà1.19209e-07`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p11 ‚Äî `DBL_EPSILON` ‚â§ `1√ó10^‚àí9`; `LDBL_EPSILON` ‚â§ `1√ó10^‚àí9`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `DBL_EPSILON‚âà2.22045e-16`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p11 ‚Äî `FLT_MIN`/`DBL_MIN`/`LDBL_MIN` ‚â§ `1√ó10^‚àí37` (minimum normalized positive). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_MIN‚âà1.17549e-38`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p11 ‚Äî (C11) `FLT_TRUE_MIN`/`DBL_TRUE_MIN`/`LDBL_TRUE_MIN` ‚â§ `1√ó10^‚àí37` (minimum positive, subnormal if supported). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `FLT_TRUE_MIN‚âà1.4013e-45`, `DBL_TRUE_MIN‚âà4.94066e-324`, `LDBL_TRUE_MIN‚âà3.6452e-4951`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p12 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî Example IEC 60559 single/double values illustrate the model. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc's actual single/double values match the IEC-60559 example, e.g. `FLT_EPSILON==1.19209290E-07F`)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p13 (Recommended practice) ‚Äî Conversions and arithmetic should correspond to one of the documented `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` modes. ‚Äî (recommended practice; not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2 (footnote) ‚Äî The floating-point model only clarifies the description and does not require identical implementation arithmetic. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

###### ¬ß5.2.4.2.3 Characteristics of decimal floating types

- [ ] ¬ß5.2.4.2.3 ‚Äî (Not part of base C99/C11; decimal floating types live in the optional TS/Annex. Placeholder only ‚Äî out of scope for base C11.) ‚Äî mcc:n/a gcc:n/a clang:n/a (none of the three define `<float.h>` decimal `_Decimal*` limits in base mode)

### ¬ß6.11 Future language directions

#### ¬ß6.11.1 Floating types

- ¬ß6.11.1p1 ‚Äî Future standardization may include additional floating-point types with greater range/precision than `long double`. ‚Äî (spec; future direction, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß6.11.2 Linkages of identifiers

- [ ] ¬ß6.11.2p1 ‚Äî Declaring an identifier with internal linkage at file scope without `static` is an obsolescent feature. ‚Äî (obsolescent note; no diagnostic required ‚Äî none of mcc/gcc/clang warn by default)

#### ¬ß6.11.3 External names

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.11.3p1 ‚Äî Restricting an external name's significance to fewer than 255 characters is an obsolescent concession to existing implementations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three keep external names significant well past 255 chars)

#### ¬ß6.11.4 Character escape sequences

- ¬ß6.11.4p1 ‚Äî Lowercase letters as escape sequences are reserved for future standardization; other characters may be used in extensions. ‚Äî (spec; future direction, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß6.11.5 Storage-class specifiers

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.11.5p1 ‚Äî Placing a storage-class specifier other than at the beginning of the declaration specifiers (e.g. `int static x;`) is an obsolescent feature. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three accept `int static x;`; the obsolescent form draws no diagnostic from any, even under `-pedantic`)

#### ¬ß6.11.6 Function declarators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.11.6p1 ‚Äî Using function declarators with empty parentheses (non-prototype form, `int f();`) is an obsolescent feature. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three accept it; under `-Wstrict-prototypes` mcc emits "function declaration isn't a prototype" for the obsolescent empty-paren declarator, matching gcc and clang, which warn "function declaration isn't a prototype / without a prototype is deprecated")

#### ¬ß6.11.7 Function definitions

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.11.7p1 ‚Äî Using function definitions with separate parameter identifier and declaration lists (K&R form) is an obsolescent feature. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three accept the K&R definition `int f(a) int a; {‚Ä¶}`; clang additionally warns `-Wdeprecated-non-prototype`, mcc and gcc accept silently ‚Äî the obsolescent diagnostic is optional, so all conform)

#### ¬ß6.11.8 Pragma directives

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.11.8p1 ‚Äî Pragmas whose first preprocessing token is `STDC` are reserved for future standardization. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc accepts `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT/FENV_ACCESS/CX_LIMITED_RANGE` silently; gcc emits an `-Wunknown-pragmas` "ignoring" warning for some, clang accepts silently ‚Äî all conform, mcc matches clang)

#### ¬ß6.11.9 Predefined macro names

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.11.9p1 ‚Äî Macro names beginning with `__STDC_` are reserved for future standardization. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc predefines `__STDC__`, `__STDC_VERSION__`, `__STDC_HOSTED__`, `__STDC_IEC_559__`, `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__`, `__STDC_ISO_10646__`)

### Added gaps & cross-checks (not in the consolidated draft)

#### Predefined conformance macros (¬ß6.10.8 / ¬ß6.11.9-adjacent)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC__` shall be defined as the integer constant `1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC_HOSTED__` shall be `1` for a hosted implementation, `0` for freestanding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `1` hosted, `0` under `-ffreestanding`)
- [~] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC_VERSION__` shall reflect the supported standard revision. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `199901L` = C99, while gcc defaults to `202311L` and clang to `201710L`; mcc advertises C99 yet ships the full C11 freestanding header set, `<stdatomic.h>`, `<threads.h>`, `_Atomic`, `_Noreturn`, and `__STDC_ISO_10646__ == 201706L` ‚Äî its advertised version under-states its actual C11 feature coverage)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 ‚Äî `__STDC_ISO_10646__` (C95/C11) indicates `wchar_t` holds ISO/IEC 10646 values of the given yyyymmL edition. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all: `201706L`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_UTF_16__` (C11) shall be defined (value `1`) when `char16_t` values are UTF-16 encoded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc predefines `__STDC_UTF_16__ == 1`, matching gcc and clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_UTF_32__` (C11) shall be defined (value `1`) when `char32_t` values are UTF-32 encoded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc predefines `__STDC_UTF_32__ == 1`, matching gcc and clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_IEC_559__` (C99/C11, conditional feature for IEC 60559 floating point) indicates IEC-60559-conforming `float`/`double`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all define `__STDC_IEC_559__ == 1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__` (C99/C11) indicates IEC-60559-compatible complex arithmetic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all define `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__ == 1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` (C11) shall be defined to `1` if the implementation does NOT support atomic types/`<stdatomic.h>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none of the three define it, consistent with all three supporting atomics ‚Äî verified by a working `<stdatomic.h>` program in mcc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_THREADS__` (C11) shall be defined to `1` if the implementation does NOT provide `<threads.h>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none define it; mcc's `<threads.h>` `thrd_create`/`thrd_join` program runs)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_VLA__` / `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__` (C11) shall be defined to `1` if VLAs / `<complex.h>` are unsupported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none define either; mcc supports both VLAs and `<complex.h>`)

#### Freestanding header content (¬ß4p6 detail)

- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî `<stdbool.h>` shall define `bool`, `true`, `false`, and `__bool_true_false_are_defined`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `bool`‚Üí`_Bool`, `true`‚Üí`1`, `false`‚Üí`0`, `__bool_true_false_are_defined`‚Üí`1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî `<stdnoreturn.h>` (C11) shall define `noreturn` as `_Noreturn`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `#define noreturn _Noreturn`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî `<iso646.h>` shall define the 11 alternative-spelling macros `and`, `and_eq`, `bitand`, `bitor`, `compl`, `not`, `not_eq`, `or`, `or_eq`, `xor`, `xor_eq`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all 11 present in mcc's `<iso646.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 ‚Äî `<stdalign.h>` (C11) shall define `alignas`/`alignof` and `__alignas_is_defined`/`__alignof_is_defined`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc bundles `<stdalign.h>`; `-ffreestanding` include succeeds)

#### ATOMIC initialization macro (¬ß7.17.2)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.2 ‚Äî `<stdatomic.h>` provides `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT` (C11; deprecated in C17, removed in C23) and `ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úó(C23 default) clang:~ (mcc still provides the C11 `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT`; gcc 15 in its default C23 mode has removed it ‚Äî `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT` is undeclared there; clang keeps it but marks it deprecated. mcc's behavior matches C11.)


## ¬ß6.2.1-¬ß6.2.4 Scopes, linkages, name spaces, storage durations

> mcc status: 0 mcc-gaps (no `‚úó`/`~` mcc tags in this section). Core scope/linkage/name-space/storage-duration rules conform and match gcc==clang on point-of-declaration, label/tag/member name spaces, internal-vs-external linkage merges, automatic/static/VLA/compound-literal lifetimes, and VLA placement constraints. mcc diagnoses a typedef name redeclared as an ordinary object in the same scope (ordinary-namespace clash), rejects a non-static file-scope redeclaration following a static one (6.2.2p7), and ships a `<threads.h>` that defines the `thread_local` convenience macro ‚Äî all matching the gcc==clang consensus. mcc still emits no warning for a tag whose only declaration sits in a function-prototype parameter list, but that diagnostic is informative/optional (¬ßI), so it is conforming and not a tagged divergence.

### ¬ß6.2.1 Scopes of identifiers

- ¬ß6.2.1p1 ‚Äî Recognize that one identifier may designate different kinds of entities (object, function, tag/member of a struct/union/enum, typedef name, label, macro, macro parameter); at each occurrence the syntactic context plus the active name space pick which. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß6.2.1p2 ‚Äî Restrict the visibility of each entity an identifier denotes to a contiguous region of program text (its scope), and support exactly the four scope kinds: function, file, block, function-prototype. ‚Äî (spec; structural)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p3 ‚Äî Give label names function scope: a label is visible anywhere in its enclosing function body and a `goto` may target a label declared later or in an enclosing block. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p3 ‚Äî Make a label name local to its function so the same label spelling can be reused independently in different functions without conflict. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p4 ‚Äî Assign file scope to an identifier whose declarator/type-specifier sits outside every block and parameter list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p4 ‚Äî Assign block scope to an identifier declared inside a block or in the parameter list of a function *definition*; its scope ends with the block. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p4 ‚Äî Assign function-prototype scope to a parameter name in a declaration that is not part of a definition, terminating that scope at the end of the function declarator (the name is not visible afterward). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `void f(int xyzzy); int g(void){return xyzzy;}` ‚Üí undeclared on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p4 ‚Äî When two declarations of the same identifier in the same name space have overlapping scopes, hide the outer entity throughout the inner scope; uses inside the inner scope bind to the inner entity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (block-scope object shadowing file-scope object, and inner-block redeclaration both behave correctly)
- ¬ß6.2.1p5 ‚Äî When the standard's prose says "identifier" to mean an entity, resolve it to the entity in the relevant name space whose declaration is visible at that point. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.2.1p6 ‚Äî Treat two identifiers as having the same scope iff their scopes end at the same point. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p7 ‚Äî Begin a struct/union/enum tag's scope immediately after the tag appears in the specifier that declares it (so a tag may refer to itself via a pointer). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p7 ‚Äî Begin an enumeration constant's scope just after its defining enumerator, so a later enumerator may use it (`enum{A=10,B=A+1}`) but an enumerator may not reference itself (`enum{X=X+1}` is an error). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.1p7 ‚Äî Begin any other identifier's scope only after its declarator completes, so an initializer/size that names the same identifier binds to the *new* (block) entity (`int g=g;`) and a file-scope `int foo[sizeof(foo)];` is rejected as use-before-declaration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.2.2 Linkages of identifiers

- ¬ß6.2.2p1 ‚Äî Use linkage so that the same identifier declared in different scopes, or several times in one scope, can be made to denote the same object or function; support the three linkage kinds external, internal, and none. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.2p2 ‚Äî Within one translation unit, make every declaration of an internal-linkage identifier denote the same entity; make an external-linkage identifier denote the same entity across the whole program. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (block-scope `extern int v;` resolves to the file-scope definition of `v`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.2p3 ‚Äî Give a file-scope object or function declared with `static` internal linkage. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.2p4 ‚Äî For an identifier declared `extern`, inherit the linkage of a prior visible file-scope declaration (internal stays internal: `static int x; extern int x;` keeps internal linkage); with no prior visible declaration, or a prior one with no linkage, give it external linkage. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.2p5 ‚Äî Treat a function identifier declared with no storage-class specifier as if `extern` (external linkage), and give a file-scope object with no storage-class specifier external linkage. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (block-scope `int puts(const char*);` links to the external `puts`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.2p6 ‚Äî Give *no linkage* to: identifiers that are not objects/functions (typedef names, enum constants, tags, members, labels), function parameters, and block-scope identifiers declared without `extern`; reject two no-linkage declarations of the same identifier in the same scope (`{int x; int x;}`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.2p7 ‚Äî Treat an identifier that ends up with both internal and external linkage in one translation unit as undefined behavior; gcc and clang reject `static int x; int x;` while mcc accepts it silently. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc diagnoses the internal‚Üíexternal file-scope conflict ‚Äî "non-static declaration of 'x' follows static declaration" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang; the reverse order `int x; static int x;` is likewise rejected by all three)

### ¬ß6.2.3 Name spaces of identifiers

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.3p1 ‚Äî Keep label names in their own name space, disambiguated by the `goto`/label-definition syntax, so a label may share a spelling with an object, tag, or typedef in the same scope (`{int x=0; x: ... goto x;}`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.3p1 ‚Äî Keep struct/union/enum tags in a single tag name space selected by the `struct`/`union`/`enum` keyword, so a tag and an ordinary identifier may share a name (`struct s{...}; int s;`), and a block-scope tag may shadow a file-scope tag of the same name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.3p1 ‚Äî Give each structure or union its own separate member name space reached only via `.`/`->`, so different aggregates may reuse member names and a member name never clashes with an object/tag/typedef of the same spelling. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.3p1 ‚Äî Place all other identifiers (objects, functions, typedef names, and enumeration constants) in one shared "ordinary identifiers" name space, so two of these with the same name in the same scope conflict; gcc/clang reject `typedef int T; int T;` but mcc accepts it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc diagnoses a typedef name redeclared as an object in the same scope ‚Äî "'T' redeclared as different kind of symbol" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang; conflicting object redeclarations like `int x; double x;` are likewise caught)

### ¬ß6.2.4 Storage durations of objects

- [ ] ¬ß6.2.4p1 ‚Äî Associate every object with one of four storage durations ‚Äî static, thread (C11), automatic, allocated ‚Äî that fix its lifetime; (C99: only static, automatic, allocated). ‚Äî (spec; structural) `(C11)` adds thread duration
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p2 ‚Äî Guarantee that during an object's lifetime its storage is reserved, it holds a constant address, and (for declared objects) it retains its last-stored value; treat any access outside the lifetime as undefined and treat a pointer to an object past its lifetime as indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (lifetime/address semantics observable via static-retains-value and compound-literal probes; the UB cases are spec-only)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p3 ‚Äî Give static storage duration (lifetime = whole program run, single zero-or-constant initialization before startup) to any object with external/internal linkage or declared with `static`; a block-scope `static` keeps its value across calls. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî Give thread storage duration to an object declared `_Thread_local` (lifetime = its thread's execution, initialized once before the thread starts, one instance per thread); accept `_Thread_local` at file scope, combined with `static`, and on a block-scope `static`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî Reject `_Thread_local` on a block-scope object that is not also `static`/`extern` (a bare automatic thread-local is a constraint violation). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1 / ¬ß6.2.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî Provide the `thread_local` convenience macro in `<threads.h>` expanding to `_Thread_local`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc's bundled `<threads.h>` defines `thread_local`, so `thread_local int t;` parses and compiles, matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p5 ‚Äî Give automatic storage duration to a block-scope object with no linkage and no `static`; reserve its storage on each entry to the block, release it when the block exits by any path, create a fresh instance on recursive/repeated entry, leave it indeterminate when uninitialized, and re-run any initializer every time the declaration is reached. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p5 ‚Äî Give a compound literal that appears outside any function (file scope) static storage duration (usable as an initializer for a file-scope pointer), and one inside a block automatic storage duration tied to the enclosing block. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p7 ‚Äî Begin a VLA object's lifetime at its declaration and end it when execution leaves the scope of the declaration; re-evaluate its size and allocate a fresh instance on each block entry (looping `int a[n]` yields per-iteration sizes), and leave its initial contents indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p7 / ¬ß6.8.6.1 ‚Äî Forbid jumping (via `goto`) into the scope of a variably modified declaration, since that would bypass establishing the VLA's lifetime. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.4p7 ‚Äî Reject a variable-length array where automatic storage is not available: at file scope and for a `static` block-scope array (no VLA storage duration there). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.2.4p8 ‚Äî Provide allocated storage duration via the `malloc`-family functions, with lifetime from allocation until deallocation as specified in ¬ß7.22.3. ‚Äî (spec; covered under ¬ß7.22.3)


## ¬ß6.2.5-¬ß6.2.8 Types, representations, compatible/composite types, alignment

> mcc status: Core type system, integer/object representation, compatible & composite types, and the full C11 `_Alignof`/`_Alignas`/`_Atomic` surface all conform and match the gcc==clang consensus on every mechanical probe. The only standards-optional gap is extended integer types: mcc rejects `__int128`/`unsigned __int128` (gcc and clang accept them) ‚Äî conforming, since extended integer types are optional, but a capability difference. `_Imaginary` (Annex G, optional) is rejected by all three.

### ¬ß6.2.5 Types

- ¬ß6.2.5p1 ‚Äî Classify every type as either an object type (fully describes objects) or a function type (describes a function), modulo incompleteness. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p1 ‚Äî Treat a type as incomplete when it describes objects but lacks the information to size them; track separately from object/function classification. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (incomplete `int a[];` later completed by `int a[10];` accepted by all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p19 ‚Äî Provide `void`: an incomplete object type that can never be completed; reject declaring an object of type `void`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void v;` rejected by all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p2 ‚Äî Provide `_Bool`, an unsigned integer type large enough to store the two values 0 and 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p2 ‚Äî When any scalar value is converted to `_Bool`, store 1 for every nonzero (including nonzero floating) value and 0 otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Bool b=5`‚Üí1, `_Bool c=0.3`‚Üí1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p3 ‚Äî Provide the three character types `char`, `signed char`, `unsigned char`, each occupying one byte (`sizeof==1`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p3 ‚Äî Make plain `char` a distinct type from both `signed char` and `unsigned char` even though it shares the range/representation of one of them. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Generic` distinguishes all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p15 ‚Äî Make plain `char`'s signedness (signed-like vs unsigned-like behavior) implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: `char` is signed on x86-64 ‚Üí `(char)-1<0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p4 ‚Äî Provide the standard signed integer types `signed char`, `short int`, `int`, `long int`, `long long int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.2.5p4 ‚Äî Permit (optional) implementation-defined extended signed integer types; standard + extended signed types form the signed integer types. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none required; mcc provides no extended signed type, gcc/clang accept `__int128`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p6 ‚Äî For each signed integer type provide a corresponding unsigned integer type using the same amount of storage (and alignment). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(int)==sizeof(unsigned)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p6 ‚Äî Standard unsigned integer types = `_Bool` plus the unsigned counterparts of the standard signed types; standard + extended unsigned form the unsigned integer types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.2.5p7 ‚Äî Treat `_Bool`, plain `char`, the signed integer types, the unsigned integer types, and the enumerated types collectively as the integer types. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p9 ‚Äî Make unsigned arithmetic modular: a result that cannot be represented is reduced modulo 2^N, so unsigned computations never overflow. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`UINT_MAX+1u==0`, `(unsigned char)255+1` wraps)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p9 ‚Äî Give a nonnegative value of a signed type the identical representation in the corresponding unsigned type (subrange representations coincide). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (bit-reinterpret of positive `int` equals `(unsigned)` cast)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p10 ‚Äî Provide the real floating types `float`, `double`, `long double`, with non-decreasing range/precision in that order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(float)<=sizeof(double)<=sizeof(long double)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p11 ‚Äî Provide the complex types `float _Complex`, `double _Complex`, `long double _Complex` (when complex is supported). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.2.5p11 ‚Äî Optionally provide the imaginary types `float/double/long double _Imaginary` (Annex G); support is optional. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (all three reject `_Imaginary` ‚Äî "imaginary types are not supported"; conforming since optional)
- ¬ß6.2.5p11 ‚Äî Group the real floating and complex types together as the floating types. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p13 ‚Äî Lay out each complex type with the same representation and alignment as a two-element array of the corresponding real type, real part first, imaginary part second. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(double _Complex)==sizeof(double[2])`, `_Alignof(_Complex float)==_Alignof(float[2])`)
- ¬ß6.2.5p17 ‚Äî Treat the integer and real floating types collectively as the real types. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.2.5p18 ‚Äî Treat the integer and floating types collectively as the arithmetic types. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p16 ‚Äî Provide enumerated types comprising a set of named integer constant values. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p16 ‚Äî Implementation-defined: choose for each enum a compatible integer type able to represent all its enumerators (and that choice may differ per enum). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all pick a 4-byte type for `enum E{A,B,C}`; `enum` value freely usable as/with `int`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p20 ‚Äî Provide array types: a contiguously-allocated nonempty set of N objects of one element type; an array of unknown size is incomplete. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p20 ‚Äî Provide structure types: a sequentially-allocated nonempty set of named members of (possibly different) types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p20 ‚Äî Provide union types: an overlapping set of named members that occupy the same storage. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
