- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p20 ‚Äî Provide function types: a return type plus the number/types of parameters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p20 ‚Äî Provide pointer types, each derived from a referenced (function/object/incomplete) type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p20 (C11) ‚Äî Provide atomic types `_Atomic(T)` / `_Atomic T` derived from an existing type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Atomic int`/`_Atomic(long)` with `atomic_load`/`atomic_store`)
- ¬ß6.2.5p21 ‚Äî Treat arithmetic types plus pointer types as scalar types; array and structure types as aggregate types. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p22 ‚Äî Treat an array of unknown size and a struct/union of unknown content as incomplete types completable later in the same scope. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (tentative `int a[]` then `int a[10]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p23 ‚Äî Build derived types (array/struct/union/function/pointer/atomic) recursively from other types; there is no limit on derivation depth beyond translation limits. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.5p27 ‚Äî Make the integer conversion rank ordering (prose introduced here, fully defined in ¬ß6.3.1.1) well-defined for usual-arithmetic-conversion purposes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (rank-dependent promotions behave consistently; see ¬ß6.3.1.1 part)

### ¬ß6.2.6 Representations of types

#### ¬ß6.2.6.1 General

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.1p2 ‚Äî Represent every value of type T as `sizeof(T)` bytes (the object representation), interpretable as an array of `unsigned char`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.1p3 ‚Äî Represent values stored in `unsigned char` objects and unsigned bit-fields in pure binary with no padding bits (so `UCHAR_MAX == 2^CHAR_BIT ‚àí 1`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.2.6.1p4 ‚Äî Leave the mapping of values to bytes unspecified for object types other than `unsigned char`, except where the standard fixes it. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.1p4 ‚Äî Allow any object's representation to be inspected/copied byte-by-byte through an `unsigned char` lvalue (no aliasing violation, no trap on read of valid bytes). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (per-byte copy of an `int` reproduces the value)
- ¬ß6.2.6.1p5 ‚Äî Permit certain bit patterns ("trap representations") that do not represent a value of the type; reading such a representation by a non-character lvalue is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî UB)
- ¬ß6.2.6.1p6 ‚Äî Define the value of a structure/union object's representation in terms of its member (and any bit-field) representations, with bytes outside members ("padding") taking unspecified values. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.1p6 ‚Äî Allow structure/union padding bytes (and bytes beyond bit-field storage) to hold unspecified values; do not assume they are zero or stable. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (no implementation guarantees padding contents)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.1p7 ‚Äî Forbid padding at the very beginning of a structure object (first member shares the struct's address). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.2.6.1p8 ‚Äî When a value is stored into a member of a union/structure, leave bytes not corresponding to that member (including padding) with unspecified values. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß6.2.6.2 Integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p1 ‚Äî For unsigned integer types other than `_Bool`, partition the bits into value bits and padding bits, and interpret the value bits as a pure-binary place-value magnitude. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (no padding bits on the targets; `UCHAR_MAX==255`, `CHAR_BIT==8`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p2 ‚Äî For signed integer types, partition the bits into M value bits, padding bits, and exactly one sign bit; the value bits mirror those of the corresponding unsigned type so M ‚â§ N. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p2 ‚Äî Implementation-defined: choose one of the three signed encodings ‚Äî sign-and-magnitude, two's complement, or ones' complement ‚Äî for how the sign bit modifies the value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three are two's complement: `INT_MIN == -INT_MAX-1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p2 ‚Äî With the sign bit 0, give the signed value the same magnitude as the corresponding unsigned interpretation of the value bits. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p2 ‚Äî Define the all-value-bits-zero, sign-bit-one pattern as either a negative zero (sign-and-magnitude / ones'-complement) or, for two's complement, the most negative value ‚àí2^M (or, implementation-defined, a trap representation). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (two's complement: that pattern is `INT_MIN`, not a trap)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p3 ‚Äî (C11) Specify whether a negative zero, if generated, is stored as-is or normalized to a normal zero by `&`, `|`, `^`, `~`, `<<`, `>>` ‚Äî implementation-defined; only relevant on non-two's-complement hardware. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (n/a on two's-complement targets; consistent)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.6.2p4 ‚Äî Keep the value bits of a signed type and its corresponding unsigned type at identical positions so non-negative values share the same representation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (positive `int` bit-pattern equals `(unsigned)` value)
- ¬ß6.2.6.2p5 ‚Äî Treat any other combination of sign/value/padding bits not described above (where it occurs) as either a normal or a trap representation, implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.2.7 Compatible type and composite type

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p1 ‚Äî Treat two types as compatible when they are the same type, subject to the additional structural rules of ¬ß6.7.2 (specifiers), ¬ß6.7.3 (qualifiers), and ¬ß6.7.6 (declarators). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p1 ‚Äî Require identical (matching) qualifiers for two qualified types to be compatible; diagnose discarding qualifiers across pointer assignment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int* = const int*` warns on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p1 ‚Äî Within one translation unit, treat two declarations of the same struct/union/enum tag as referring to the same (compatible) type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (re-declared `struct S;` shares the type)
- ¬ß6.2.7p1 ‚Äî Across separate translation units, make two struct/union/enum types compatible iff tags match and members correspond (same names, same count, compatible member types, same order; same constant values for enums). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable in a single TU)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p1 ‚Äî Make an enumerated type compatible with the implementation-chosen integer type that represents it (so enum/integer mixing needs no diagnostic). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int i = e; e = (enum E)(i+1)` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p3 ‚Äî Build the composite type of two compatible types: for arrays, adopt a known constant bound from either side. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`extern int a[]` + `int a[5]` ‚Üí `sizeof(a)==5*sizeof(int)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p3 ‚Äî Composite type rule: if one of two compatible function types has a parameter-type list (prototype) and the other does not, use the prototyped one; combine recursively for return/parameter/derived types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (prototype vs non-prototype function declarations reconciled; clang warns under newer prototype-deprecation rules but accepts)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p3 ‚Äî Form the composite of two compatible derived types by taking the composite of the corresponding referenced/element types and re-deriving. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.7p2 ‚Äî Permit a later declaration to refer to an entity declared with a compatible (not necessarily identical) type; the effective type is the composite. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.2.8 Alignment of objects (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p1 (C11) ‚Äî Model each complete object type as having an alignment requirement: a power-of-two byte count constraining the addresses at which objects of that type may be placed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignof(char)==1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p4 (C11) ‚Äî Restrict every valid alignment value to a nonnegative integral power of two. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p2 (C11) ‚Äî Define fundamental alignments as those not exceeding `_Alignof(max_align_t)`, and support them for all storage durations and object types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignof(max_align_t) >= _Alignof(double)`; `max_align_t` from `<stddef.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p3 (C11) ‚Äî Define extended (over-)alignments as those greater than `_Alignof(max_align_t)`; whether, and for which storage durations, they are supported is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(16)` over-aligned static accepted and honored)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p4 (C11) ‚Äî Make the alignment of an array type equal to the alignment of its element type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignof(float[2])==_Alignof(float)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p5 (C11) ‚Äî Let `_Alignof` yield, and `_Alignas` request, alignment; honor an `_Alignas` request that is at least the type's natural alignment (including on struct members). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct{char c;_Alignas(8) int x;}` ‚Üí `_Alignof>=8`; over-aligned buffer is 16-byte aligned at runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p5 (C11) ‚Äî Diagnose (constraint violation) an `_Alignas` specifier weaker than the type's required alignment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(1) int` rejected by all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p5 (C11) ‚Äî Treat `_Alignas(0)` (and an `_Alignas` with a zero expression) as having no effect on alignment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(0) int x;` accepted, alignment unchanged)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.2.8p6 (C11) ‚Äî Make alignment requirements equal for compatible/identical types (so `_Alignof` agrees across equivalent spellings, e.g. complex vs array-of-real). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignof(double _Complex)==_Alignof(double)`)
- ¬ß6.2.8p7 (C11) ‚Äî Treat accessing an object through a pointer to a type with a stricter alignment than the object actually has as undefined behavior (no requirement to diagnose). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî UB)


## ¬ß6.3 Conversions

> mcc status: 41 TODOs, 1 mcc-gap (modifiable-lvalue enforcement is warn-only: assignment to a const-qualified lvalue or to a struct/union with a const member ‚Äî incl. nested ‚Äî is accepted with a diagnostic, where gcc/clang reject it as an error).

### ¬ß6.3 (introduction)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3p1 ‚Äî Perform implicit operand conversions where an operator requires it: change an operand's value from its own type to another type as dictated by the operator together with the operand types, and treat this clause as specifying the result of every such required conversion (explicit casts trigger the same conversions). ‚Äî (spec umbrella; exercised by the per-rule probes below) mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3p2 ‚Äî Guarantee that converting a value to a type compatible with its own type leaves both the value and its representation unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (identity conversions preserve value)

### ¬ß6.3.1 Arithmetic operands

### ¬ß6.3.1.1 Boolean, characters, and integers
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.1p1 ‚Äî Assign every integer type an integer conversion rank such that: no two distinct signed integer types share a rank; a signed type of greater precision/width has rank greater than or equal to one of lesser precision; the standard signed types rank long long > long > int > short > signed char; each unsigned integer type has the same rank as its corresponding signed type; _Bool ranks below every other standard integer type; char ranks equal to signed char and unsigned char; and the rank relation is consistent/transitive. ‚Äî (spec; rank is a model, observed via UAC ¬ß6.3.1.8 probes) mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.1p1 ‚Äî Rank extended integer types: an extended signed integer type ranks relative to another signed type by precision (greater precision implies greater-or-equal rank), and its rank relative to same-precision standard types is implementation-defined but still consistent with the other ordering rules; each extended unsigned type shares its signed counterpart's rank. ‚Äî (spec; no extended integer types beyond standard ones exposed) mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.3.1.1p1 ‚Äî Give an enumerated type the same integer conversion rank as the (implementation-chosen) integer type with which it is compatible. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.1p2 ‚Äî Define and apply the integer promotions: an operand of an integer type whose conversion rank is less than or equal to that of int/unsigned int, or a bit-field of type _Bool, int, signed int, or unsigned int, is converted to int if int can represent all of its values and otherwise to unsigned int; operands of all other types are unchanged by the promotion; and the promotion preserves the value including its sign. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (sizeof(+(char/short/unsigned char))==sizeof(int))
- ¬ß6.3.1.1p2 footnote ‚Äî Apply the integer promotions only in the contexts the standard explicitly names; elsewhere the conversion rank is used solely to define behavior (e.g. usual arithmetic conversions) and no promotion is performed. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.3.1.2 Boolean type
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.2p1 ‚Äî When converting any scalar value to _Bool, produce 0 if the value compares equal to 0 and 1 otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((_Bool)2.5==1, (_Bool)0.0==0, (_Bool)&x==1, (_Bool)(void*)0==0)

### ¬ß6.3.1.3 Signed and unsigned integers
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.3p1 ‚Äî When an integer is converted to an integer type other than _Bool that can represent its value, leave the value unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.3p2 ‚Äî When converting a value to an unsigned integer type that cannot represent it, reduce it modulo two-to-the-N (where N is the number of value bits) by repeatedly adding/subtracting one more than the maximum representable value until it lies in range. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((unsigned char)257==1, (unsigned)-1==0xFFFFFFFF)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.3p3 ‚Äî When converting a value to a signed integer type that cannot represent it, either yield an implementation-defined result or raise an implementation-defined signal; document the choice. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (impl-defined; all three take low-order bits / modulo: (signed char)300==44, no trap)

### ¬ß6.3.1.4 Real floating and integer
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.4p1 ‚Äî When converting a finite real floating value to an integer type, discard the fractional part (truncate toward zero), and treat the conversion as undefined behavior when the truncated integral part cannot be represented in the target integer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((int)3.9==3, (int)-3.9==-3)
- [ ] ¬ß6.3.1.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî Note the C11 addition that the FE_INVALID floating-point exception may be raised when the real value is not representable in the integer type. ‚Äî (spec; C11 wording note, optional behavior)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.4p2 ‚Äî When converting an integer to a real floating type: keep the value if it is exactly representable; if it is within range but not exactly representable, round to an adjacent representable value in an implementation-defined direction; and treat as undefined behavior when the value is outside the representable range. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.3.1.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî Note the C11 addition that the inexact (rounded) case may raise FE_INEXACT and is governed by the current rounding mode. ‚Äî (spec; C11 wording note)

### ¬ß6.3.1.5 Real floating types
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.5p1 ‚Äî When converting to a real floating type of greater or equal range and precision (e.g. float‚Üídouble, float/double‚Üílong double), preserve the value exactly. (C11 reframes this in terms of one format's value set including another's.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((double)(float)1.0f==1.0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.5p2 ‚Äî When converting to a real floating type of narrower range/precision (or otherwise representing a value in narrower precision): keep the value if exactly representable; if within range but inexact, round to an adjacent representable value in an implementation-defined manner; and treat as undefined behavior when the value is outside the target's representable range. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((float)0.1 != (double)0.1)
- [ ] ¬ß6.3.1.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî Note the C11 addition that this narrowing conversion may raise FE_INEXACT and follows the current rounding mode. ‚Äî (spec; C11 wording note)

### ¬ß6.3.1.6 Complex types
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.6p1 ‚Äî When converting between complex types, convert the real part and the imaginary part independently, each according to the conversion rules for the corresponding real type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((float complex)(1.5+2.5i) keeps both parts)

### ¬ß6.3.1.7 Real and complex
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.7p1 ‚Äî When converting a real value to a complex type, convert it (per the corresponding real-type rules) to become the result's real part and set the result's imaginary part to a positive zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (imag is +0.0, signbit clear)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.7p2 ‚Äî When converting a complex value to a real type, discard the imaginary part and convert the real part according to the corresponding real-type rules. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((double)(5+9i)==5.0)

### ¬ß6.3.1.8 Usual arithmetic conversions
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî Determine a common real type for two arithmetic operands via the usual arithmetic conversions, then convert each operand to a type whose corresponding real type is that common real type; the result is complex if either operand is complex (otherwise real), and the common real type also determines the expression's result type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî Floating selection: if either operand's corresponding real type is long double, make the common real type long double; otherwise if either is double, make it double; otherwise if either is float, make it float (converting the other operand, integer or floating, accordingly). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî Integer path: if neither operand has a floating type, first apply the integer promotions to both operands, then apply the following same-/mixed-sign rules. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî If after promotion both operands have the same type, perform no further conversion. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî If both operands are signed or both unsigned (and types differ), convert the operand of lesser integer conversion rank to the type of the operand of greater rank. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî If the operands have differing signedness and the unsigned operand has rank greater than or equal to the signed operand's rank, convert the signed operand to the unsigned operand's type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (-1 < 0u evaluates false)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî If the operands have differing signedness and the signed operand's type can represent every value of the unsigned operand's type, convert the unsigned operand to the signed operand's type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((long)-1 < 0u is true on LP64 where long > unsigned int)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p1 ‚Äî In the remaining differing-signedness case, convert both operands to the unsigned integer type corresponding to the signed operand's type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.1.8p2 ‚Äî Allow floating operands and floating-expression results to be evaluated and represented with greater range and precision than the type requires (as reported by FLT_EVAL_METHOD), while leaving the operand types and the expression's declared result type unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all report FLT_EVAL_METHOD==0 on x86-64)

### ¬ß6.3.2 Other operands

### ¬ß6.3.2.1 Lvalues, arrays, and function designators
- [~] ¬ß6.3.2.1p1 ‚Äî Define an lvalue as an expression with object type, or an incomplete type other than void, that potentially designates an object; treat evaluating an lvalue that does not designate an object when evaluated as undefined behavior; and define a modifiable lvalue as an lvalue that is not an array type, not an incomplete type, not const-qualified, and‚Äîif a structure or union‚Äîhas no const-qualified member (recursively, at any nesting depth). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc detects the violations ‚Äî incl. nested const members ‚Äî but only **warns** ("assignment of read-only location") and exits 0; gcc/clang reject as hard errors. Array assignment is correctly an error in all three.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.1p2 ‚Äî Perform lvalue-to-rvalue conversion: except when it is the operand of sizeof, of unary &, of ++ or --, or is the left operand of the . operator or of an assignment operator, convert a non-array lvalue to the value stored in the designated object; the result has the lvalue's type stripped of qualifiers (and of _Atomic in C11) and is not itself an lvalue; and treat the conversion as undefined behavior if the lvalue has an incomplete type. ‚Äî (spec; result-is-not-an-lvalue and qualifier-stripping are observable indirectly) mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.3.2.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Additionally treat as undefined behavior reading, via lvalue-to-rvalue conversion, an object of automatic storage duration that could have been declared with register storage class (its address is never taken) while its stored value is indeterminate/uninitialized. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not reliably diagnosable ‚Äî mcc does track register-eligible params per recent ¬ß6.7.1 diag work but this read case is not diagnosed)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.1p3 ‚Äî Convert an expression of array type to a pointer to its initial element (yielding a non-lvalue of the element-pointer type), except when the array expression is the operand of sizeof, the operand of unary &, or a string literal used to initialize an array; note that no object need exist beyond the array's elements. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (sizeof a / &a keep array type; `int *p=a` decays; `char s[]="abc"` keeps sizeof 4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.1p4 ‚Äî Convert a function designator (an expression of function type) to a pointer to that function, except when it is the operand of sizeof, of _Alignof (C11), or of unary &. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (function name assigned to a function pointer decays)

### ¬ß6.3.2.2 void
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.2p1 ‚Äî Treat the (nonexistent) value of a void expression as unusable: never require or use such a value, allow any expression to be converted to void implicitly or by an explicit cast (its value/designator is then discarded but side effects still occur), and never implicitly convert a void expression to any non-void type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (initializing int from a void call is an error: "cannot convert 'void' to 'int'"; `(void)expr` cast accepted)

### ¬ß6.3.2.3 Pointers
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p1 ‚Äî Allow a pointer to void to be converted to or from a pointer to any object type and back, with the round-tripped pointer comparing equal to the original. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p2 ‚Äî Allow a pointer to a qualified or unqualified type to be converted to a pointer to a more-qualified version of that type (additional qualifiers), preserving the pointer value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int* -> const volatile int*` accepted, value preserved; dropping qualifiers warns in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p3 ‚Äî Recognize a null pointer constant (an integer constant expression with value 0, or such an expression cast to void*); when converted to any pointer type it yields a null pointer that is guaranteed to compare unequal to any pointer to an actual object or function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int *p=0`==NULL, p != &obj)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p4 ‚Äî Guarantee that two null pointers, converted to any (compatible) pointer types, compare equal to each other. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((void*)0 == (char*)0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p5 ‚Äî When converting an integer to a pointer type, produce an implementation-defined result that need not be correctly aligned, need not point at an entity of the referenced type, and may be a trap representation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (impl-defined; intptr_t‚Üípointer round-trips)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p6 ‚Äî When converting a pointer to an integer type, produce an implementation-defined result; if the result cannot be represented in the integer type the behavior is undefined, and the result need not be in the range of any integer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (impl-defined; pointer‚Üíintptr_t‚Üípointer round-trips)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p7 ‚Äî Allow conversion of a pointer to one object type into a pointer to a different object type: if the result is not correctly aligned for the referenced type the behavior is undefined; otherwise converting it back yields a pointer equal to the original; and require that a pointer to an object converted to a pointer to a character type points at the object's lowest-addressed byte, with successive increments of the result pointing at the remaining bytes of the object in order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ((unsigned char*)&obj == (void*)&obj; byte walk valid)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.3.2.3p8 ‚Äî Allow conversion of a pointer to a function of one type into a pointer to a function of another type and back to recover a pointer equal to the original; but treat a call through a function pointer whose type is incompatible with the called function's type as undefined behavior. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (round-trip through `void(*)(int)` recovers original; the incompatible-call clause is UB, not diagnosed)


## ¬ß6.4 Lexical elements

> mcc status: 152 TODO items below; mcc passes the mechanically-testable lexical core (all keywords, UCNs, hex floats, `long long`, C11 char/string prefixes, digraphs, `//` comments, maximal munch). 0 mcc-gaps: mcc flags `0b` binary integer constants and the `\e` non-standard escape under `-pedantic`/`-pedantic-errors`, matching gcc/clang. The `__func__` array `&` mismatch and the `'$'`/octal-range/large-int diagnostics are warnings vs errors, but those are diagnostic-strength only and match gcc, not conformance gaps.

### ¬ß6.4 General
- ¬ß6.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *token* is one of: *keyword*, *identifier*, *constant*, *string-literal*, or *punctuator*. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *preprocessing-token* is one of: *header-name*, *identifier*, *pp-number*, *character-constant*, *string-literal*, *punctuator*, or each non-white-space character that cannot be one of the preceding. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4p1 (Constraints) ‚Äî Each preprocessing token that is converted to a token shall have the lexical form of a keyword, an identifier, a constant, a string literal, or a punctuator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4p2 ‚Äî A token is the minimal lexical element of the language in translation phases 7 and 8 (categories: keywords, identifiers, constants, string literals, punctuators). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4p2 ‚Äî A preprocessing token is the minimal lexical element in translation phases 3 through 6 (categories: header names, identifiers, preprocessing numbers, character constants, string literals, punctuators, and single non-white-space characters that do not lexically match the other categories). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4p2 ‚Äî If a `'` or a `"` character matches the last (single-non-white-space-character) category, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4p2 ‚Äî Preprocessing tokens can be separated by white space, consisting of comments, or white-space characters (space, horizontal tab, new-line, vertical tab, and form-feed), or both. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (vertical-tab/form-feed between tokens accepted by all three)
- ¬ß6.4p2 ‚Äî As described in ¬ß6.10, in certain circumstances during translation phase 4, white space (or its absence) serves as more than preprocessing-token separation. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4p2 ‚Äî White space may appear within a preprocessing token only as part of a header name or between the quotation characters in a character constant or string literal. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4p3 ‚Äî Where the input stream has been parsed into preprocessing tokens up to a given character, the next preprocessing token is the longest sequence of characters that could constitute a preprocessing token (maximal munch). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`x+++++y` ‚Üí `x ++ ++ + y`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4p4 (EXAMPLE 1) ‚Äî `x+++++y` is parsed as `x ++ ++ + y`, which violates a constraint on increment operators even though `x ++ + ++ y` might yield a correct expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all reject: lvalue required as increment operand)

### ¬ß6.4.1 Keywords
> C99 added `inline`, `restrict`, `_Bool`, `_Complex`, `_Imaginary`; C11 added `_Alignas`, `_Alignof`, `_Atomic`, `_Generic`, `_Noreturn`, `_Static_assert`, `_Thread_local`.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî The following are keywords: `auto break case char const continue default do double else enum extern float for goto if inline int long register restrict return short signed sizeof static struct switch typedef union unsigned void volatile while _Bool _Complex _Imaginary`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.1p1 ‚Äî `inline`, `restrict`, `_Bool`, `_Complex`, and `_Imaginary` are keywords added in C99 relative to C90. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.1p1 ‚Äî `_Alignas`, `_Alignof`, `_Atomic`, `_Generic`, `_Noreturn`, `_Static_assert`, and `_Thread_local` are also keywords. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all seven accepted under `-std=c11`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.1p2 (Semantics) ‚Äî The above tokens (case sensitive) are reserved for use as keywords, and shall not be used otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.1p2 ‚Äî `_Imaginary` is reserved for specifying imaginary types even though imaginary-type support is an optional feature (Annex G). (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc & clang treat `_Imaginary` as a reserved keyword ‚Üí "imaginary types are not supported"; gcc does **not** reserve it and treats it as an ordinary identifier)

### ¬ß6.4.2 Identifiers

#### ¬ß6.4.2.1 General
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *identifier* is `identifier-nondigit`, or `identifier identifier-nondigit`, or `identifier digit`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *identifier-nondigit* is a `nondigit`, a `universal-character-name`, or other implementation-defined characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *nondigit* is `_` or one of `a`‚Äì`z`, `A`‚Äì`Z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *digit* is one of `0`‚Äì`9`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî An identifier is a sequence of nondigit characters (including underscore `_`, lowercase and uppercase Latin letters, and other characters) and digits, which designates one or more entities as described in ¬ß6.2.1. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî Lowercase and uppercase letters are distinct. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî There is no specific limit on the maximum length of an identifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (70+ char identifiers distinct, no truncation)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p3 (Constraints) ‚Äî Each universal character name in an identifier shall designate a character whose encoding in ISO/IEC 10646 falls into one of the ranges specified in Annex D. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`A` rejected: "not valid in an identifier")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p3 (Constraints) ‚Äî The initial character of an identifier shall not be a universal character name designating a digit. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p3 ‚Äî An implementation may allow multibyte characters that are not part of the basic source character set to appear in identifiers; which characters and their correspondence to universal character names is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UTF-8 `√Ä` and explicit `√Ä` both accepted in identifiers)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p4 ‚Äî When preprocessing tokens are converted to tokens during translation phase 7, if a preprocessing token could be converted to either a keyword or an identifier, it is converted to a keyword. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p5 (Semantics) ‚Äî As discussed in ¬ß5.2.4.1, an implementation may limit the number of significant initial characters in an identifier; the limit for an external name may be more restrictive than that for an internal name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.4.2.1p5 ‚Äî The number of significant characters in an identifier is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (impl-defined; mcc/gcc/clang all treat full length as significant)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1p5 ‚Äî Any identifiers that differ in a significant character are different identifiers. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.2.1p5 ‚Äî If two identifiers differ only in nonsignificant characters, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable ‚Äî no truncation observed)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1 (related limit) ‚Äî The implementation shall support at least 63 significant initial characters in an internal identifier or a macro name. (C99; C90 required 31) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (70-char internal names distinct)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.1 (related limit) ‚Äî The implementation shall support at least 31 significant initial characters in an external identifier (with each universal character name or extended source character counting as a number of characters). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß6.4.2.2 Predefined identifiers (`__func__`)
> `__func__` is C99 (not present in C90).
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.2p1 (Semantics) ‚Äî The identifier `__func__` shall be implicitly declared by the translator as if, immediately following the opening brace of each function definition, the declaration `static const char __func__[] = "function-name";` appeared, where *function-name* is the name of the lexically-enclosing function. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(__func__)` in `main` == 5; array type `const char[5]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.2p2 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî Within a function `myfunc`, `__func__` provides the string `"myfunc"` (e.g. `printf("%s\n", __func__);` prints the function name). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all print `main`)

### ¬ß6.4.3 Universal character names
> Universal character names are a C99 addition (not present in C90).
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.3p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *universal-character-name* is `\u hex-quad` or `\U hex-quad hex-quad`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.3p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *hex-quad* is four `hexadecimal-digit`s. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.3p2 (Constraints) ‚Äî A universal character name shall not specify a character whose short identifier is less than `00A0` other than `0024` (`$`), `0040` (`@`), or `0060` (`` ` ``), nor one in the range `D800` through `DFFF` inclusive. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:~ (mcc & gcc accept the `$` exception per the standard; clang **rejects** `$` "character '$' cannot be specified by a universal character name", diverging from the spec exception)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.3p3 (Semantics) ‚Äî A universal character name designates a character in ISO/IEC 10646. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.3p3 ‚Äî `\Unnnnnnnn` designates the character whose eight-digit short identifier is `nnnnnnnn`; `\unnnn` designates the character whose four-digit short identifier is `nnnn` (i.e. eight-digit short identifier `0000nnnn`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.4.4 Constants
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *constant* is an `integer-constant`, a `floating-constant`, an `enumeration-constant`, or a `character-constant`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4p2 (Constraints) ‚Äî Each constant shall have a type and the value of a constant shall be in the range of representable values for its type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4p3 (Semantics) ‚Äî Each constant has a type, determined by its form and value, as detailed later. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß6.4.4.1 Integer constants
> `long long`/`unsigned long long` types and the `ll`/`LL` suffix are C99; the extended-integer-type fallback (p6) is C99.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *integer-constant* is a `decimal-constant`, `octal-constant`, or `hexadecimal-constant`, each optionally followed by an `integer-suffix`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *decimal-constant* is a `nonzero-digit`, or `decimal-constant digit`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *octal-constant* is `0`, or `octal-constant octal-digit`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0777` == 511)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *hexadecimal-constant* is a `hexadecimal-prefix` followed by one or more `hexadecimal-digit`s; the *hexadecimal-prefix* is `0x` or `0X`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *nonzero-digit* is `1`‚Äì`9`; an *octal-digit* is `0`‚Äì`7`; a *hexadecimal-digit* is `0`‚Äì`9`, `a`‚Äì`f`, or `A`‚Äì`F`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *integer-suffix* is: `unsigned-suffix long-suffix?`, `unsigned-suffix long-long-suffix`, `long-suffix unsigned-suffix?`, or `long-long-suffix unsigned-suffix?`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî *unsigned-suffix* is `u` or `U`; *long-suffix* is `l` or `L`; *long-long-suffix* is `ll` or `LL`. (`ll`/`LL` are C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4.1p2 (Description) ‚Äî An integer constant begins with a digit, but has no period or exponent part; it may have a prefix that specifies its base and a suffix that specifies its type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p3 (Semantics) ‚Äî The value of a decimal constant is computed base 10; that of an octal constant, base 8; that of a hexadecimal constant, base 16; the lexically first digit is the most significant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 ‚Äî The type of an integer constant is the first of the corresponding list (per its form/suffix) in which its value can be represented. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(0x7FFFFFFFFFFFFFFF)`==8, `sizeof(0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF)`==8, `sizeof(1U)`==4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Unsuffixed *decimal* constant: `int`, `long int`, `long long int`. (`long long int` is C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Unsuffixed *octal/hexadecimal* constant: `int`, `unsigned int`, `long int`, `unsigned long int`, `long long int`, `unsigned long long int`. (`(unsigned) long long int` are C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Constant with `u`/`U` suffix (any base): `unsigned int`, `unsigned long int`, `unsigned long long int`. (`unsigned long long int` is C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Decimal constant with `l`/`L` suffix: `long int`, `long long int`. (`long long int` is C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Octal/hexadecimal constant with `l`/`L` suffix: `long int`, `unsigned long int`, `long long int`, `unsigned long long int`. (`(unsigned) long long int` are C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Constant with both `u`/`U` and `l`/`L` suffix (any base): `unsigned long int`, `unsigned long long int`. (`unsigned long long int` is C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Decimal constant with `ll`/`LL` suffix: `long long int`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`9223372036854775807LL` works)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Octal/hexadecimal constant with `ll`/`LL` suffix: `long long int`, `unsigned long long int`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p5 (type list) ‚Äî Constant with both `u`/`U` and `ll`/`LL` suffix (any base): `unsigned long long int`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`18446744073709551615ULL` works)
- [ ] ¬ß6.4.4.1p6 ‚Äî If an integer constant cannot be represented by any type in its list, it may have an extended integer type, if the extended integer type can represent its value. (C99) ‚Äî (impl-defined; no extended integer types in mcc/gcc/clang on x86-64)
- ¬ß6.4.4.1p6 ‚Äî If all of the types in the list for the constant are signed, the extended integer type shall be signed. (C99) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî no extended types)
- ¬ß6.4.4.1p6 ‚Äî If all of the types in the list for the constant are unsigned, the extended integer type shall be unsigned. (C99) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.4.1p6 ‚Äî If the list contains both signed and unsigned types, the extended integer type may be signed or unsigned. (C99) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1p6 ‚Äî If an integer constant cannot be represented by any type in its list and has no extended integer type, then the integer constant has no type (and the program is ill-formed; a diagnostic is required). (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc warns "integer constant overflow", gcc warns "too large", clang errors "too large to be represented in any integer type" ‚Äî all diagnose)

#### ¬ß6.4.4.2 Floating constants
> Hexadecimal floating constants (the `0x‚Ä¶p¬±‚Ä¶` form, binary-exponent-part, and the p3/p7 hex-rounding rules) are C99.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *floating-constant* is a `decimal-floating-constant` or a `hexadecimal-floating-constant`. (hexadecimal form is C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *decimal-floating-constant* is `fractional-constant exponent-part? floating-suffix?`, or `digit-sequence exponent-part floating-suffix?`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *hexadecimal-floating-constant* is `hexadecimal-prefix hexadecimal-fractional-constant binary-exponent-part floating-suffix?`, or `hexadecimal-prefix hexadecimal-digit-sequence binary-exponent-part floating-suffix?`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0x1.8p1`==3.0, `0x1p-1f`==0.5, `0x1.0p4L`==16)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *fractional-constant* is `digit-sequence? . digit-sequence` or `digit-sequence .`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *exponent-part* is `e sign? digit-sequence` or `E sign? digit-sequence`; *sign* is `+` or `-`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *hexadecimal-fractional-constant* is `hexadecimal-digit-sequence? . hexadecimal-digit-sequence` or `hexadecimal-digit-sequence .`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *binary-exponent-part* is `p sign? digit-sequence` or `P sign? digit-sequence`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *floating-suffix* is one of `f`, `l`, `F`, `L`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4.2p2 (Description) ‚Äî A floating constant has a significand part that may be followed by an exponent part and a suffix that specifies its type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.4.2p2 ‚Äî The significand part's components may include a digit sequence (whole-number part), a period, and a digit sequence (fraction part). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p2 ‚Äî The exponent part's components are an `e`, `E`, `p`, or `P` followed by an optionally signed digit sequence. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p2 ‚Äî Either the whole-number part or the fraction part has to be present; for decimal floating constants, either the period or the exponent part has to be present; for hexadecimal floating constants the binary-exponent-part is required. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0x1.8` with no `p` rejected: "exponent expected"/"requires an exponent")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p3 (Semantics) ‚Äî The significand part is interpreted as a (decimal or hexadecimal) rational number; the digit sequence in the exponent part is interpreted as a decimal integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p3 ‚Äî For decimal floating constants, the exponent indicates the power of 10 by which the significand part is to be scaled. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p3 ‚Äî For hexadecimal floating constants, the exponent indicates the power of 2 by which the significand part is to be scaled. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4.2p3 ‚Äî For decimal floating constants, and for hex floating constants when `FLT_RADIX` is not a power of 2, the result is the nearest representable value, or an adjacent representable value, chosen in an implementation-defined manner. ‚Äî (impl-defined; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p3 ‚Äî For hexadecimal floating constants when `FLT_RADIX` is a power of 2, the result is correctly rounded. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (exact-power-of-two hex floats reproduce exactly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p4 ‚Äî An unsuffixed floating constant has type `double`; if suffixed by `f`/`F`, `float`; if suffixed by `l`/`L`, `long double`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof` 8/4/16)
- ¬ß6.4.4.2p5 ‚Äî Floating constants are converted to internal format as if at translation time. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.4.2p5 ‚Äî The conversion of a floating constant shall not raise an exceptional condition or a floating-point exception at execution time. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.2p6 ‚Äî All floating constants of the same source form shall convert to the same internal format with the same value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úó] ¬ß6.4.4.2p7 (Recommended practice) ‚Äî The implementation should produce a diagnostic if a hexadecimal constant cannot be represented exactly in its evaluation format, and should then proceed with translation. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (recommended practice only; none of the three diagnose inexact hex float constants ‚Äî not a conformance failure)
- ¬ß6.4.4.2p7 (Recommended practice) ‚Äî Translation-time conversion of floating constants should match execution-time `strtod`-style conversion for matching inputs/format/rounding. ‚Äî (recommended practice; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß6.4.4.3 Enumeration constants
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.3p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *enumeration-constant* is an `identifier`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.3p2 (Semantics) ‚Äî An identifier declared as an enumeration constant has type `int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(A)`==4 for an enumerator)
- ¬ß6.4.4.3 (forward ref) ‚Äî The semantics of declaring enumeration constants are described in ¬ß6.7.2.2. ‚Äî (cross-ref; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß6.4.4.4 Character constants
> The `u'‚Ä¶'` and `U'‚Ä¶'` prefixes (and the `char16_t`/`char32_t` constraint/type wording) are C11; `L'‚Ä¶'` and universal character names are C99/earlier.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *character-constant* is `' c-char-sequence '`, `L' c-char-sequence '`, `u' c-char-sequence '`, or `U' c-char-sequence '`. (`u'‚Ä¶'` and `U'‚Ä¶'` are C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`u'A'`==65, `U'B'`==66 via `<uchar.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *c-char-sequence* is one or more `c-char`; a *c-char* is any member of the source character set except `'`, `\`, or new-line, or an `escape-sequence`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *escape-sequence* is a `simple-escape-sequence`, `octal-escape-sequence`, `hexadecimal-escape-sequence`, or `universal-character-name`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *simple-escape-sequence* is one of `\'  \"  \?  \\  \a  \b  \f  \n  \r  \t  \v`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *octal-escape-sequence* is `\` followed by one, two, or three octal digits. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *hexadecimal-escape-sequence* is `\x` followed by one or more hexadecimal digits. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p2 (Description) ‚Äî An integer character constant is a sequence of one or more multibyte characters enclosed in single-quotes; a wide character constant is the same, except prefixed by `L`, `u`, or `U`. (`u`/`U` prefixes are C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4.4p2 ‚Äî With a few exceptions, the elements of the sequence are any members of the source character set; they are mapped in an implementation-defined manner to members of the execution character set. ‚Äî (impl-defined; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p3 ‚Äî The escape sequences map: `\'`‚Üí`'`, `\"`‚Üí`"`, `\?`‚Üí`?`, `\\`‚Üí`\`, `\a`‚Üíalert, `\b`‚Üíbackspace, `\f`‚Üíform feed, `\n`‚Üínew line, `\r`‚Üícarriage return, `\t`‚Üíhorizontal tab, `\v`‚Üívertical tab. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p4 ‚Äî `"` and `?` are representable by themselves or by `\"`/`\?`; the single-quote `'` and the backslash `\` shall be `\'` and `\\` respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p5 ‚Äî The octal digits following the backslash form a single character; the numerical value of the octal integer specifies the desired value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p6 ‚Äî The hexadecimal digits following `\x` form a single character; the numerical value of the hexadecimal integer specifies the desired value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p7 ‚Äî A universal character name is constituted in the same way as for identifiers and string literals; the construction is described in ¬ß6.4.3. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.4.4.4p9 (Constraints) ‚Äî The value of an octal or hexadecimal escape sequence shall be in the range of representable values for `unsigned char` (integer char constant), or the unsigned type corresponding to `wchar_t`/`char16_t`/`char32_t` (wide). (C11 extends to `u`/`U`) ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (`'\477'`: mcc & gcc emit a **warning** "octal escape sequence out of range"; clang **errors**. All diagnose the constraint violation; mcc matches gcc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p10 (Semantics) ‚Äî An integer character constant has type `int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof('A')`==4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p10 ‚Äî The value of an integer character constant containing a single character mapping to a single-byte execution character is the numerical value of that character interpreted as an integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'A'`==65)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p10 ‚Äî The value of an integer character constant with more than one character (e.g. `'ab'`) or a non-single-byte mapping is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all give `'ab'`==24930 with a multichar warning; impl-defined value matches)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p10 ‚Äî If an integer character constant contains a single character/escape, its value is that of a `char` object holding it, converted to `int` (so sign matters). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p11 ‚Äî A wide character constant prefixed by `L` has type `wchar_t`; by `u` has type `char16_t`; by `U` has type `char32_t`. (`u`/`U` are C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4.4p11 ‚Äî The value of a single-multibyte-character wide constant is the `mbtowc` wide value under an implementation-defined current locale. ‚Äî (impl-defined; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.4.4p11 ‚Äî The value of a multi-character / multi-mapping / unrepresented wide character constant is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (impl-defined; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p12 (EXAMPLE 1) ‚Äî `'\0'` is commonly used to represent the null character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.4.4p13 (EXAMPLE 2) ‚Äî Distinct interpretations exist for `'\1234'`, `'\x1234'`, etc. ‚Äî (example/impl-defined; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p14 (EXAMPLE 3) ‚Äî Even where `char` is signed, the value of `'\xFF'` is determined by conversion of the escape value to `char` then to `int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.4.5 String literals
> The `u8`, `u`, and `U` encoding prefixes (and the p2 constraint, p5 mixed-prefix rule, and `char16_t`/`char32_t`/UTF-8 array-element rules) are C11; only `L` existed in C99.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *string-literal* is `encoding-prefix? " s-char-sequence? "`. (encoding-prefix is C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *encoding-prefix* is one of `u8`, `u`, `U`, `L`. (`u8`, `u`, `U` are C11; only `L` existed in C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`u8"‚Ä¶"`, `u"‚Ä¶"`, `U"‚Ä¶"`, `L"‚Ä¶"` all compile)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *s-char-sequence* is one or more `s-char`; an *s-char* is any member of the source character set except `"`, `\`, or new-line, or an `escape-sequence`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p2 (Constraints) ‚Äî A sequence of adjacent string literal tokens shall not include both a wide string literal and a UTF-8 string literal. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`L"a" u8"b"` rejected by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p3 (Description) ‚Äî A character string literal is a sequence of zero or more multibyte characters enclosed in double-quotes (e.g. `"xyz"`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p3 ‚Äî A UTF-8 string literal is the same, except prefixed by `u8`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`char a[]=u8"h√©llo"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p3 ‚Äî A wide string literal is the same, except prefixed by `L`, `u`, or `U`. (`u`/`U` are C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p4 ‚Äî The same considerations apply per element as for integer/wide character constants, except `'` is representable by itself or `\'`, but `"` shall be `\"`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p5 (Semantics) ‚Äî In translation phase 6, adjacent character and identically-prefixed string literal tokens are concatenated into a single multibyte character sequence. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`"ab" "cd"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p5 ‚Äî If any token has an encoding prefix the result has that prefix; this shall be the only prefix, except an unprefixed literal may be concatenated with a prefixed one, giving that prefix. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`"ab" L"cd"` ‚Üí `wchar_t[]`, runs; `"no" u8"prefix-ok"` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p5 ‚Äî Whether differently-prefixed wide string literals can be concatenated, and the treatment, is implementation-defined. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc/gcc/clang all **reject** `u"a" U"b"` as unsupported ‚Äî a permitted implementation-defined choice; consistent)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî In translation phase 7, a byte or code of value zero is appended to each multibyte character sequence resulting from a string literal. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî The sequence initializes an array of static storage duration and length just sufficient to contain it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî For character string literals, array elements have type `char`, initialized with the individual bytes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî For UTF-8 string literals, array elements have type `char`, initialized with the UTF-8 encoding. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`u8"h√©llo"` fits in `char[]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî For `L` wide string literals, array elements have type `wchar_t`, initialized via `mbstowcs` under an implementation-defined locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî For `u` wide string literals, array elements have type `char16_t`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`char16_t b[]=u"hi"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p6 ‚Äî For `U` wide string literals, array elements have type `char32_t`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`char32_t c[]=U"hi"`)
- ¬ß6.4.5p7 ‚Äî It is unspecified whether these arrays are distinct provided their elements have the appropriate values. ‚Äî (unspecified; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.5p7 ‚Äî If the program attempts to modify such an array, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5p8 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî `"\x12" "3"` is two characters (`'\x12'`, `'3'`), not a single hex escape, because concatenation occurs after each token is scanned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.4.6 Punctuators
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.6p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *punctuator* is one of: `[ ] ( ) { } . ->`, `++ -- & * + - ~ !`, `/ % << >> < > <= >= == != ^ | && ||`, `? : ; ...`, `= *= /= %= += -= <<= >>= &= ^= |=`, `, # ##`, and the digraphs `<: :> <% %> %: %:%:`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.6p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî The digraph punctuators `<:`, `:>`, `<%`, `%>`, `%:`, and `%:%:` are provided. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.6p2 (Semantics) ‚Äî A punctuator has independent syntactic and semantic significance; depending on context it may be an operator (yielding a value/function designator, side effect, or both). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.6p2 ‚Äî An operand is an entity on which an operator acts. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.6p3 ‚Äî The six tokens `<: :> <% %> %: %:%:` behave the same as `[ ] { } # ##` respectively, except for spelling. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (program written entirely with digraphs compiles & runs; `a %:%: b` pastes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.6p4 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî Constructs using digraphs, e.g. `%:define`, behave identically to `#`-spelled equivalents. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%:include <stdio.h>` works)

### ¬ß6.4.7 Header names
> The `__has_include` and `#pragma`-location recognition contexts in p3 are C11; the `< >` / `" "` header-name forms are C90/C99.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.7p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *header-name* is `< h-char-sequence >` or `" q-char-sequence "`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.7p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî An *h-char-sequence* is one or more `h-char`; an *h-char* is any member of the source character set except new-line and `>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.7p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *q-char-sequence* is one or more `q-char`; a *q-char* is any member of the source character set except new-line and `"`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.7p2 (Semantics) ‚Äî The sequences in both forms of header names are mapped in an implementation-defined manner to headers or external source file names as specified in ¬ß6.10.2. ‚Äî (impl-defined; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.7p3 ‚Äî If the characters `'`, `\`, `"`, `//`, or `/*` occur between the `<` and `>` delimiters, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.4.7p3 ‚Äî If the characters `'`, `\`, `//`, or `/*` occur between the `"` delimiters, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.7p3 ‚Äî A header name preprocessing token is recognized only within a `#include` directive, in a `__has_include` expression, or in an implementation-defined location within a `#pragma`. (the `__has_include` and `#pragma` allowances are C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__has_include(<stdio.h>)` supported and `defined(__has_include)` is true)
- ¬ß6.4.7p4 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî `0x3<1/a.h>1e2` is a sequence of preprocessing tokens whose header-name interpretation depends on context (recognized only in the p3 contexts). ‚Äî (example; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.4.8 Preprocessing numbers
> The `p`/`P` sign productions (hexadecimal-float exponents) are C99.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.8p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî A *pp-number* is: `digit`; `. digit`; `pp-number digit`; `pp-number identifier-nondigit`; `pp-number e sign`; `pp-number E sign`; `pp-number p sign` (C99); `pp-number P sign` (C99); or `pp-number .`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0x1.2p3.4e+5` survives stringization as one token)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.8p2 (Description) ‚Äî A pp-number begins with a digit optionally preceded by `.` and may be followed by valid identifier characters and `e¬±`, `E¬±`, `p¬±`, `P¬±`. (`p¬±`/`P¬±` are C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.4.8p3 (Semantics) ‚Äî A pp-number has no type or value until a successful phase-7 conversion to a floating or integer constant token. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.4.9 Comments
> `//` line comments are a C99 addition (not present in C90).
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.9p1 ‚Äî Except within a character constant, a string literal, or a comment, the characters `/*` introduce a comment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.9p1 ‚Äî The contents of a `/* ... */` comment are examined only to identify multibyte characters and to find the terminating `*/`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (unterminated `/*` rejected: "unexpected end of file in comment")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.9p2 ‚Äî Except within a character constant, a string literal, or a comment, `//` introduces a comment including all multibyte characters up to but not including the next new-line. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.9p2 ‚Äî The contents of a `//` comment are examined only to identify multibyte characters and to find the terminating new-line. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.9p2 ‚Äî A `//` comment continues through a line-splice (a `\` immediately before the new-line is removed in phase 2), so it extends to the next non-spliced physical new-line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (spliced `//` swallows the following `return 1;` line in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.9p3 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî `"a//b"` is a single string literal (not a comment); `f(a//\\b c)` shows `//` comment with line splicing; `/\\/ k();` is a `//` comment because of the line splice in phase 2. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.4 mcc-specific lexical gaps (added in gap analysis)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.1 (extension) ‚Äî Binary integer constants `0b‚Ä¶`/`0B‚Ä¶` are a GNU/C23 extension, **not** in C99/C11; a conforming-mode compiler should diagnose them under `-pedantic`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-pedantic-errors` mcc rejects `0b1010` ‚Äî "binary integer constants are a C23/GNU extension" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, which reject it as "binary constants are a C23 feature/extension")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4 (extension) ‚Äî `\e` (ESC) is a non-ISO escape sequence, **not** in C99/C11; should be diagnosed under `-pedantic`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-pedantic-errors` mcc rejects `'\e'` ‚Äî "\e is a non-ISO escape sequence" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, which flag "non-ISO-standard escape sequence `\e`")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p1 (edge) ‚Äî An empty character constant `''` has no `c-char` and is a constraint violation requiring a diagnostic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:~ (mcc & gcc **error** "empty character constant"; clang only **warns** under `-Winvalid-pp-token`. mcc matches gcc and is the stricter/correct behavior)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4p6 (edge) ‚Äî A `\x` hexadecimal escape with no following hex digit is ill-formed (a diagnostic is required). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (covered by escape-sequence syntax; all reject)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.2.1 (extension) ‚Äî `$` as an ordinary (non-UCN) identifier character is an implementation-defined extension; mcc, gcc and clang all accept `a$b`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (consistent extension)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.3p2 (edge) ‚Äî The `$` (`$`) UCN exception: mcc & gcc honor the standard exception and accept it in identifiers; clang rejects it ‚Äî a clang-side divergence, mcc conforms. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úó
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.5 (multibyte) ‚Äî A universal character name / UTF-8 multibyte character inside a narrow string literal is encoded as its UTF-8 bytes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`"√©"` ‚Üí first byte 0xC3 == 195 at runtime on all three)


## ¬ß6.5.1-¬ß6.5.4 Primary/postfix/unary expressions

> mcc status: 96 TODOs in this section; mcc-gaps = 2 (const-qualified operand of `++`/`--` is only a *warning*, not an error; cast of a non-scalar to its own type is not diagnosed even under `-pedantic-errors`). Everything else (generic selection, compound literals, `_Alignof`, anonymous members, atomic RMW `++`, VLA-`sizeof` evaluation, K&R default-argument promotions, all the operand/operator constraints) conforms and matches the gcc==clang consensus.

### ¬ß6.5 Expressions (general)

> C11 reframes evaluation order in terms of *sequenced/unsequenced/indeterminately-sequenced* (footnote-defined in ¬ß5.1.2.3); C99 used "sequence points" plus an explicitly *unspecified* order of subexpression evaluation. The ¬ß6.5p2 data-race/multiple-modification rule is therefore worded differently in the two standards but covers the same UB.

- ¬ß6.5p1 ‚Äî An expression is a sequence of operators and operands that specifies a computation of a value, designates an object or a function, generates side effects, or performs a combination thereof. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî The value computations of the operands of an operator are sequenced before the value computation of the result of the operator. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5p2 (C99-only) ‚Äî Between the previous and next sequence point an object shall have its stored value modified at most once by the evaluation of an expression; furthermore, the prior value shall be read only to determine the value to be stored (otherwise undefined behavior). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; all three warn: mcc "operation on 'i' may be undefined", gcc `-Wsequence-point`, clang `-Wunsequenced`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî If a side effect on a scalar object is unsequenced relative to either a different side effect on the same scalar object or a value computation using the value of the same scalar object, the behavior is undefined; and if multiple orderings of the subexpressions exist, the behavior is undefined if such an unsequenced side effect occurs in any of them. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (diagnosed for `i = i++ + 1`)
- ¬ß6.5p3 ‚Äî The grouping of operators and operands is indicated by the syntax (except as specified later for `()`/`&&`/`||`/`?:`/`,`). (C11: "Except as specified later, side effects and value computations of subexpressions are unsequenced." C99: the order of evaluation of subexpressions and the order in which side effects take place are both unspecified.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5p4 (footnote/normative note) ‚Äî The bitwise operators ‚Äî the unary `~` and the binary `<<`, `>>`, `&`, `^`, `|` ‚Äî require operands of integer type, yield values that depend on the internal representation of integers, and have implementation-defined and undefined aspects for signed types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`~d` on a `double` rejected by all three)
- ¬ß6.5p5 ‚Äî If an exceptional condition occurs during the evaluation of an expression (the result is not mathematically defined or not in the range of representable values for its type), the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5p6 ‚Äî The effective type of an object for an access to its stored value is the declared type of the object, if any. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5p6 ‚Äî If a value is stored into an object having no declared type through an lvalue whose type is not a character type, the lvalue's type becomes the effective type of the object for that access and for subsequent non-modifying accesses. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5p6 ‚Äî If a value is copied into an object having no declared type using `memcpy` or `memmove`, or is copied as an array of character type, the effective type of the modified object for that access and subsequent non-modifying accesses is the effective type of the source object, if it has one. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5p6 ‚Äî For all other accesses to an object having no declared type, the effective type is simply the type of the lvalue used for the access. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5p7 ‚Äî An object shall have its stored value accessed only by an lvalue expression of one of the following types (strict aliasing rule): a type compatible with the effective type; a qualified version of a compatible type; the signed or unsigned type corresponding to the effective type; the signed or unsigned type corresponding to a qualified version of the effective type; an aggregate or union type that includes one of the foregoing among its members (including, recursively, a member of a subaggregate or contained union); or a character type. ‚Äî (UB/optimization; not separately testable here)
- ¬ß6.5p8 ‚Äî A floating expression may be *contracted* ‚Äî evaluated as though a single operation, omitting source-implied rounding errors; the `FP_CONTRACT` pragma in `<math.h>` can disallow contraction, otherwise whether and how expressions are contracted is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (impl-defined; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.5.1 Primary expressions

> C11 adds *generic-selection* to the primary-expression grammar (new ¬ß6.5.1p6 and ¬ß6.5.1.1).

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a primary expression is an *identifier*, a *constant*, a *string-literal*, `( expression )`, or (C11) a *generic-selection*. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p2 ‚Äî An identifier is a primary expression provided it has been declared as designating an object (then it is an lvalue) or a function (then it is a function designator). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p2 ‚Äî An identifier that has not been declared is a constraint violation (C99/C11 removed implicit function declaration; an undeclared identifier used as a primary expression is ill-formed). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`error: 'undeclared_xyz' undeclared`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p3 ‚Äî A constant is a primary expression whose type depends on its form and value (per ¬ß6.4.4). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p4 ‚Äî A string literal is a primary expression; it is an lvalue with type as detailed in ¬ß6.4.5. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&"abc"` yields `char(*)[4]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p5 ‚Äî A parenthesized expression is a primary expression whose type and value are identical to those of the unparenthesized expression; it is an lvalue, a function designator, or a void expression iff the unparenthesized expression is, respectively, an lvalue, a function designator, or a void expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(x)=5` assigns)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1p6 (C11) ‚Äî A generic selection is a primary expression; its type and value are those described in ¬ß6.5.1.1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.1.1 Generic selection (C11)

> Entire subsection is C11-only.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Syntax: `_Generic ( assignment-expression , generic-assoc-list )`, where *generic-assoc-list* is a comma-separated list of *generic-associations*, each `type-name : assignment-expression` or `default : assignment-expression`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: a generic selection shall have no more than one `default` generic association. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (two `default` rejected)
- [~] ¬ß6.5.1.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: the type name in a generic association shall specify a complete object type other than a variably modified type. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (VLA assoc `int[n]:` rejected by all three; **none** of the three diagnose an *incomplete* assoc type `struct X:` when it does not match the controller ‚Äî all silently accept)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: no two generic associations in the same generic selection shall specify compatible types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int:‚Ä¶, int:‚Ä¶` ‚Üí mcc "specifies two compatible types")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: the controlling expression's type (after lvalue, array-to-pointer, and function-to-pointer conversion) shall be compatible with at most one of the listed type names. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`const int` controller matches `int` assoc, not `const int`; `a[5]` controller matches `int*`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: if there is no `default` association, the controlling expression's type shall be compatible with exactly one listed type name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`long` with only `int`/`double` assocs and no default ‚Üí `error: type 'long' does not match any association`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî Semantics: the controlling expression of a generic selection is not evaluated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Generic(side(),‚Ä¶)` does not run `side()`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî The result expression is the expression of the generic association whose type name is compatible with the controlling expression's type, or otherwise the expression of the `default` association. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`default` selected regardless of its list position)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî None of the expressions from any non-selected generic association is evaluated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1p4 (C11) ‚Äî The type and value of the generic selection are identical to those of its result expression; it is an lvalue, a function designator, or a void expression iff its result expression is, respectively, one of those. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Generic(x,int:x,‚Ä¶) = 99` assigns through the selected lvalue)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.1.1 (added; constraint corner) ‚Äî A *function-type* generic association (`void(void):`) is a non-object type: mcc and gcc accept it, **clang rejects** it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úó (clang stricter; mcc matches gcc)

### ¬ß6.5.2 Postfix operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *postfix-expression* is a primary-expression, or a postfix-expression followed by one of: `[ expression ]` (array subscript), `( argument-expression-list_opt )` (function call), `. identifier` or `-> identifier` (member access), `++` or `--` (postfix increment/decrement), or `( type-name ) { initializer-list }` / `( type-name ) { initializer-list , }` (compound literal). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2p1 ‚Äî The *argument-expression-list* is a comma-separated list of *assignment-expression*s. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.2.1 Array subscripting

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.1p1 ‚Äî Constraint: in `E1[E2]`, one expression shall have type "pointer to complete object type", the other shall have integer type, and the result has type "type". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.1p2 ‚Äî Semantics: `E1[E2]` is by definition identical to `(*((E1)+(E2)))`; because of the conversion rules for binary `+`, if `E1` is (a pointer to the initial element of) an array object and `E2` is an integer, `E1[E2]` designates the `E2`-th element (counting from zero). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1[a]` == `a[1]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.1p3 ‚Äî Successive subscripts designate elements of a multidimensional array: for an n-dimensional array (n ‚â• 2) with dimensions `i √ó j √ó ‚Ä¶ √ó k`, `E` used as other than an lvalue is converted to a pointer to an (n‚àí1)-dimensional array `j √ó ‚Ä¶ √ó k`; applying `*` (explicitly or implicitly via `[]`) yields the referenced (n‚àí1)-dimensional array, itself converted to a pointer if used as other than an lvalue ‚Äî so arrays are stored in row-major order (last subscript varies fastest). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`a[1][2]==(&a[0][0])[5]`; `sizeof(a[0])==12`)

### ¬ß6.5.2.2 Function calls

> C99 says an argument may be "any object type"; C11 tightens this to "any *complete* object type". C99 ¬ß6.5.2.2p9 states the order of evaluation of designator/arguments/subexpressions is unspecified with a sequence point before the call; C11 ¬ß6.5.2.2p9 instead specifies a sequence point after the evaluations but before the call and makes other evaluations *indeterminately sequenced* with respect to the called function's body.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the expression denoting the called function shall have type pointer to function returning `void` or returning a complete object type other than an array type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (calling a non-function ‚Üí mcc "function pointer expected"; a function returning an array type is rejected at declaration)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p2 ‚Äî Constraint: if the function's type includes a prototype, the number of arguments shall agree with the number of parameters, and each argument shall have a type assignable to an object with the unqualified version of its corresponding parameter's type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (too-few ‚Üí "too few arguments to function"; too-many ‚Üí "too many arguments to function")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p3 ‚Äî Semantics: a postfix expression followed by parentheses containing a possibly-empty comma-separated list of expressions is a function call; the postfix expression denotes the called function and the list specifies the arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p4 ‚Äî An argument may be an expression of any complete object type (C99: any object type); in preparing for the call, the arguments are evaluated and each parameter is assigned the value of its corresponding argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p5 ‚Äî If the called function's type does not include a prototype, the *default argument promotions* are performed on each argument: the integer promotions, and arguments of type `float` are promoted to `double`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (K&R `f(char, float)` against `f(int a; double b;)` returns 7 on all three)
- ¬ß6.5.2.2p5 ‚Äî If the number of arguments does not equal the number of parameters, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5.2.2p5 ‚Äî If a no-prototype call reaches a function *defined* with a prototype, the behavior is undefined if that prototype ends with an ellipsis or the promoted argument types are incompatible with the parameter types. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5.2.2p5 ‚Äî If a no-prototype call reaches a function defined *without* a prototype, the behavior is undefined if the promoted argument types are incompatible with the promoted parameter types, except: (a) one promoted type is a signed integer type and the other is the corresponding unsigned integer type and the value is representable in both; or (b) both types are pointers to qualified or unqualified versions of a character type or of `void`. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p6 ‚Äî If the called function's type includes a prototype, the arguments are implicitly converted, as if by assignment, to the unqualified versions of the corresponding parameters' declared types; the ellipsis notation stops argument-type conversion after the last declared parameter, and the default argument promotions are performed on trailing (variadic) arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`printf("%g", floatval)` promotes `float`‚Üí`double`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p7 ‚Äî No other conversions are performed implicitly; in particular, the number and types of arguments are not compared with those of the parameters in a function definition that does not include a prototype declarator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.5.2.2p8 ‚Äî If the function is *defined* with a type incompatible with the type pointed to by the expression that denotes the called function, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5.2.2p9 ‚Äî There is a sequence point after the evaluations of the function designator and the actual arguments but before the actual call. (C11: every evaluation in the caller not otherwise sequenced is indeterminately sequenced with respect to the called function's body. C99: the order of evaluation of the function designator, arguments, and their subexpressions is unspecified.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.2p10 ‚Äî Recursive function calls shall be permitted, both directly and indirectly through any chain of other functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fib(10)==55`)

### ¬ß6.5.2.3 Structure and union members

> C11 adds *atomic* qualified types to the operand constraints (p1/p2), the rule that accessing a member of an *atomic* struct/union is UB (p3), and anonymous structures/unions (p6 in N1570).

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the first operand of `.` shall have atomic (C11), qualified, or unqualified structure or union type, and the second operand shall name a member of that type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p2 ‚Äî Constraint: the first operand of `->` shall have type "pointer to atomic (C11), qualified, or unqualified structure" or "pointer to atomic, qualified, or unqualified union", and the second operand shall name a member of the pointed-to type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
