- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p3 ‚Äî Semantics: a postfix expression followed by `.` and an identifier designates a member; the value is that of the named member and is an lvalue if the first expression is an lvalue; if the first expression has qualified type, the result has the so-qualified version of the member's type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.5.2.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî Accessing a member of an *atomic* structure or union object results in undefined behavior. ‚Äî (UB; all three permit whole-object copy `t = as` of an `_Atomic struct`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p4 ‚Äî Semantics: a postfix expression followed by `->` and an identifier designates a member of the object the first expression points to; the value is that of the named member and is an lvalue; if the first expression is a pointer to a qualified type, the result has the so-qualified version of the member's type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p5 ‚Äî Common-initial-sequence guarantee for unions: if a union contains several structures sharing a common initial sequence, and the union currently contains one of them, the common initial part of any of them may be inspected anywhere a declaration of the completed union type is visible. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`u.a.tag` written, `u.b.tag` reads same value)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p6 ‚Äî Two structures share a common initial sequence if corresponding members have compatible types (and, for bit-fields, the same widths) for a sequence of one or more initial members. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.3p6 (C11) ‚Äî Anonymous structures/unions: a `.` or `->` whose member is an anonymous structure or union member behaves as if the access were applied to the containing structure or union (member access transparently reaches into nested anonymous members). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (nested anon union `.b` and anon struct `.d` reachable directly)

### ¬ß6.5.2.4 Postfix increment and decrement operators

> C11 adds *atomic* operand support and specifies the atomic read-modify-write semantics; C99 expresses the side effect via sequence points.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the operand of postfix `++`/`--` shall have atomic (C11), qualified, or unqualified real or pointer type, and shall be a modifiable lvalue. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`x++` on a `const int` is now a hard error "assignment of read-only location", matching gcc/clang. Array/non-lvalue operands `a++` are also rejected.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4p2 ‚Äî Semantics: the result of postfix `++` is the *value of the operand*; after the result is obtained, the operand's stored value is incremented (the value 1 of the appropriate type is added to it). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4p2 ‚Äî The constraints, type, value, and conversions of the postfix `++` operand are those of the additive operators (¬ß6.5.6); for a pointer operand the increment is by the size of the pointed-to type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int*` post-increment advances by one element)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4p2 ‚Äî The side effect of updating the operand's stored value occurs between the previous and next sequence point (C99); C11: the value computation of the result is sequenced before the side effect of updating the operand. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî Postfix `++` is a single evaluation with respect to an indeterminately-sequenced function call; on an *atomic* operand it is an atomic read-modify-write with `memory_order_seq_cst` ordering. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Atomic int x=0; v=x++;` ‚Üí `v==0, x==1` on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4p3 ‚Äî Semantics: postfix `--` is analogous to postfix `++` except the operand's value is decremented (the value 1 of the appropriate type is subtracted from it). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.2.5 Compound literals (C99)

> C99 feature (not in C90). C11 renumbers the referenced initializer-list section from ¬ß6.7.8 to ¬ß6.7.9 and adds the explicit p2 constraint that all initializer-list constraints apply.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the *type-name* in `( type-name ) { initializer-list }` shall specify a complete object type or an array of unknown size, but not a variable length array type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(int[n]){0}` rejected: mcc "variable length array cannot be initialized")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: all the constraints for initializer lists in ¬ß6.7.9 (C11) / ¬ß6.7.8 (C99) also apply to compound literals. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p3 ‚Äî Semantics: a parenthesized type name followed by a brace-enclosed initializer list is a *compound literal*; it provides an unnamed object whose value is given by the initializer list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(struct P){.x=3,.y=4}`, `(int[]){10,20,30}`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p4 ‚Äî If the type name specifies an array of unknown size, the size is determined by the initializer list (¬ß6.7.9 / ¬ß6.7.8) and the compound literal's type is the completed array type; otherwise its type is that specified by the type name; in either case the result is an lvalue. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&(int){42}` yields a usable pointer)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p5 ‚Äî The compound literal's object has static storage duration if it occurs outside the body of a function; otherwise it has automatic storage duration associated with the enclosing block. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (file-scope `int *gp=(int[]){5,6,7};` links and reads correctly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p6 ‚Äî All the semantic rules and constraints for initializer lists (¬ß6.7.9 / ¬ß6.7.8) are applied to compound literals. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.5.2.5p7 ‚Äî String literals, and compound literals with const-qualified types, need not designate distinct objects. ‚Äî (unspecified/impl latitude; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5.2.5p8 ‚Äî The order in which side effects occur among the initialization-list expressions of a compound literal is unspecified. ‚Äî (unspecified; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5p9 ‚Äî Each compound literal creates only a single object in a given scope (a compound literal in a loop or recursive block entry denotes the same object across iterations until the block is re-entered, not a fresh object per evaluation). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (address of `(int[]){i}` is stable across loop iterations on all three)

### ¬ß6.5.3 Unary operators

> C11 extends the unary grammar with `_Alignof ( type-name )`.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *unary-expression* is a postfix-expression, or one of `++ unary-expression`, `-- unary-expression`, `unary-operator cast-expression`, `sizeof unary-expression`, `sizeof ( type-name )`, or (C11) `_Alignof ( type-name )`; the *unary-operator* is one of `& * + - ~ !`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.3.1 Prefix increment and decrement operators

> C11 adds atomic operand support and atomic read-modify-write semantics (inherited from the `+=`/`-=` rules).

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.1p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the operand of prefix `++`/`--` shall have atomic (C11), qualified, or unqualified real or pointer type, and shall be a modifiable lvalue. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`++x` on a `const int` and `s.a` on a member of a `const struct` are now hard errors, matching gcc/clang.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.1p2 ‚Äî Semantics: the value of the prefix `++` operand is incremented; the result is the new (incremented) value. `++E` is equivalent to `(E+=1)`; constraints, conversions, type, value, and side effect are those of the `+=` compound assignment and the additive operators. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.1p3 ‚Äî Semantics: prefix `--` is analogous to prefix `++` except the operand is decremented; `--E` is equivalent to `(E-=1)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.3.2 Address and indirection operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the operand of unary `&` shall be a function designator, the result of a `[]` or unary `*` operator, or an lvalue designating an object that is not a bit-field and is not declared with the `register` storage-class specifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&register-var` ‚Üí "address of register variable 'x' requested"; `&s.bitfield` ‚Üí "cannot take address of bit-field")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p2 ‚Äî Constraint: the operand of unary `*` shall have pointer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`*x` on an `int` ‚Üí "pointer expected")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p3 ‚Äî Semantics: unary `&` yields the address of its operand; if the operand has type "type", the result has type "pointer to type". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p3 ‚Äî If the `&` operand is the result of a unary `*`, neither `*` nor `&` is evaluated and the result is as if both were omitted (the operator constraints still apply and the result is not an lvalue). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&*p` with null `p` yields null, no fault)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p3 ‚Äî If the `&` operand is the result of a `[]` operator, neither `&` nor the implied `*` is evaluated and the result is as if `&` were removed and `[]` were changed to a `+` operator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p3 ‚Äî Otherwise, the result of `&` is a pointer to the object or function designated by its operand. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p4 ‚Äî Semantics: unary `*` denotes indirection; if the operand points to a function the result is a function designator, and if it points to an object the result is an lvalue designating the object; if the operand has type "pointer to type", the result has type "type". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.5.3.2p4 ‚Äî If an invalid value has been assigned to the pointer, the behavior of unary `*` is undefined (invalid values per footnote: a null pointer, an address inappropriately aligned for the pointed-to type, or the address of an object after the end of its lifetime). ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.5.3.3 Unary arithmetic operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.3p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the operand of unary `+` or `-` shall have arithmetic type; the operand of `~` shall have integer type; the operand of `!` shall have scalar type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`+p` on a pointer ‚Üí mcc "pointer not accepted for unary plus"; `~d` on a `double` rejected; `!p` on a pointer accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.3p2 ‚Äî Semantics: the result of unary `+` is the value of its (promoted) operand; the integer promotions are performed and the result has the promoted type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.3p3 ‚Äî Semantics: the result of unary `-` is the negative of its (promoted) operand; the integer promotions are performed and the result has the promoted type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.3p4 ‚Äî Semantics: the result of `~` is the bitwise complement of its (promoted) operand (each result bit set iff the corresponding converted-operand bit is not set); the integer promotions are performed and the result has the promoted type. If the promoted type is unsigned, `~E` equals the maximum value representable in that type minus `E`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.3p5 ‚Äî Semantics: the result of logical negation `!` is `0` if the operand compares unequal to 0 and `1` if it compares equal to 0; the result has type `int`; `!E` is equivalent to `(0==E)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`!nullptr==1`, `!!42==1`)

### ¬ß6.5.3.4 The `sizeof` and `_Alignof` operators (C11; "The `sizeof` operator" in C99)

> C11 merges the new `_Alignof` operator into this subsection (new constraint in p1, new semantics in p3), shifting the C99 paragraph numbers: C99 p2/p3/p4 ‚Üí C11 p2/p4/p5.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p1 ‚Äî Constraint: `sizeof` shall not be applied to an expression of function type or incomplete type, to the parenthesized name of such a type, or to an expression designating a bit-field member. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (bit-field & incomplete type rejected unconditionally; function type & `void` are a GNU extension (`=1`) accepted by default by all three and rejected by all three under `-pedantic-errors` ‚Äî mcc: "'sizeof' applied to a function type" / "applied to a void type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: `_Alignof` shall not be applied to a function type or an incomplete type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (incomplete type rejected unconditionally: mcc "'_Alignof' applied to an incomplete type"; function type is a GNU extension accepted by default by all three, rejected by all under `-pedantic-errors`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p2 ‚Äî Semantics: `sizeof` yields the size in bytes of its operand (an expression, or the parenthesized name of a type), determined from the operand's type; if the operand's type is a variable length array type the operand is evaluated, otherwise the operand is not evaluated and the result is an integer constant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(int[side()])` runs `side()` exactly once; non-VLA `sizeof` is a constant expression usable as an array bound)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p3 (C11) ‚Äî Semantics: `_Alignof` yields the alignment requirement of its operand type; the operand is not evaluated and the result is an integer constant; applied to an array type it yields the alignment requirement of the element type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignof(int[10])==_Alignof(int)==4`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p4 (C11; ¬ß6.5.3.4p3 in C99) ‚Äî When `sizeof` is applied to an operand of type `char`, `unsigned char`, or `signed char` (or a qualified version thereof) the result is 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(char)==1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p4 (C11; ¬ß6.5.3.4p3 in C99) ‚Äî When `sizeof` is applied to an array-type operand the result is the total number of bytes in the array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof "hello"==6` including the NUL)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p4 (C11; ¬ß6.5.3.4p3 in C99) ‚Äî When `sizeof` is applied to a structure- or union-type operand the result is the total number of bytes in such an object, including internal and trailing padding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p5 (C11; ¬ß6.5.3.4p4 in C99) ‚Äî The value of the result of `sizeof` (and, C11, `_Alignof`) is implementation-defined, and its type is the unsigned integer type `size_t` defined in `<stddef.h>` (and other headers). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(int)-5 > 0` is *true*, confirming the unsigned `size_t` result type)

### ¬ß6.5.4 Cast operators

> C11 adds *atomic* type names to the constraint (p2) and promotes the pointer‚Üîfloating restriction to an explicit constraint (p4); in C99 that restriction appears as semantics.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *cast-expression* is a unary-expression, or `( type-name ) cast-expression`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p2 ‚Äî Constraint: unless the type name specifies a `void` type, the type name shall specify atomic (C11), qualified, or unqualified scalar type, and the operand shall have scalar type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (casting a non-scalar to its own type, e.g. `(struct S)s`, is accepted by default but now diagnosed under `-pedantic` with "ISO C forbids casting nonscalar to the same type", matching gcc's `-Wpedantic` and clang's `-pedantic`. A `(void)expr` cast and a cast of a `void` function call to `void` are accepted by all three.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p3 ‚Äî Constraint: conversions involving pointers, other than where permitted by ¬ß6.5.16.1 (simple assignment), shall be specified by an explicit cast. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p4 (C11 constraint; C99 semantics) ‚Äî A pointer type shall not be converted to any floating type, and a floating type shall not be converted to any pointer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both directions rejected: mcc "cannot cast between a floating type and a pointer")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p4 ‚Äî Semantics: preceding an expression by a parenthesized type name converts the value to the named type (a *cast*); a cast that specifies no conversion has no effect on the type or value of an expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p4 ‚Äî A cast does not yield an lvalue; the result of a cast is never an lvalue. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`((char)x)=5` ‚Üí mcc "lvalue expected")
- ¬ß6.5.4p5 ‚Äî If the value of the expression is represented with greater range or precision than required by the named type (¬ß6.3.1.8 permits excess range/precision), the cast specifies a conversion even when the expression type equals the named type, and removes any extra range and precision. ‚Äî (impl-defined `FLT_EVAL_METHOD`; not separately testable here)

### Added / cross-cutting items (gaps and corners the draft did not enumerate)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4 (added) ‚Äî `<stdalign.h>` provides `alignof` as a macro for `_Alignof`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`runtime/include/stdalign.h` present; `alignof(double)==8`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4 / ¬ß6.5.3.1 (added) ‚Äî `<stdatomic.h>` is bundled and `_Atomic int` read-modify-write `++`/`--` lowers to a sequentially-consistent atomic op. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`runtime/include/stdatomic.h` present)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3p1 (added; GNU ext) ‚Äî `_Alignof`/`__alignof__` applied to an *expression* (`_Alignof x`) rather than a type-name ‚Äî a GNU extension outside the C11 grammar. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc & gcc accept silently; clang warns `-Wgnu-alignof-expression`; all accept)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.5 (added) ‚Äî A compound literal is a *modifiable* lvalue when not const-qualified: its members can be assigned and its address taken (`&(int){42}`, `(int[]){‚Ä¶}[i]=‚Ä¶`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.4p4 (added) ‚Äî A cast of a value to the *same* scalar type is a no-op that preserves the value but still drops lvalue-ness (covered by p4 "no effect on type or value" + non-lvalue rule). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.2p1 (added) ‚Äî Taking `&` of a string literal yields a pointer-to-array (`&"abc"` has type `char(*)[4]`), confirming string literals are lvalues. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úó] ¬ß6.5.1.1p2 (added; latent in all three) ‚Äî An *incomplete* (non-matching) generic-association type name is a constraint violation that **none** of mcc/gcc/clang diagnose. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no compiler in this matrix enforces the "complete object type" requirement when the assoc type does not match the controller)


## ¬ß6.5.5-¬ß6.5.14 Binary operators

> mcc status: 65 TODOs, 0 mcc-gaps ‚Äî mcc matches the gcc==clang consensus on every mechanically-testable item (constraint diagnostics, parse precedence/associativity, division truncation/remainder identity, pointer arithmetic & subtraction, shift semantics, short-circuit evaluation, complex equality).

> Cross-cutting (cited where relevant, defined elsewhere): signed-integer arithmetic overflow in `*`, `+`, `-`, `<<` is undefined behavior per ¬ß6.5p5; the "usual arithmetic conversions" are defined in ¬ß6.3.1.8; the integer promotions in ¬ß6.3.1.1; a null pointer constant in ¬ß6.3.2.3; `ptrdiff_t`/`<stddef.h>` in ¬ß7.19. Each binary operator's grammar production names its precedence/associativity; for every arithmetic operator the result type is the common type produced by the usual arithmetic conversions.

### ¬ß6.5.5 Multiplicative operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.5p1 ‚Äî Parse `*`, `/`, and `%` as left-associative binary operators binding tighter than additive operators (multiplicative-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (precedence probe `2+3*4`==14 agrees)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.5p2 ‚Äî Constraint: both operands of `*` and `/` must have arithmetic type; both operands of `%` must have integer type; reject anything else. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double%double` and `ptr*ptr` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.5p3 ‚Äî Apply the usual arithmetic conversions to the operands of `*`, `/`, and `%`. ‚Äî (spec; result-type behavior, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.5p4 ‚Äî Yield the arithmetic product of the operands for binary `*`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.5p5 ‚Äî Yield the quotient (first operand divided by second) for `/` and the remainder for `%`; if the second operand (divisor) is zero, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (divisor==0 is UB, not diagnosed by any; consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.5p6 ‚Äî For integer operands `/` discards any fractional part (truncates toward zero), and whenever `a/b` is representable the identity `(a/b)*b + a%b == a` must hold (this fixes the sign and rounding of `%`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-7/2,7/-2,-7%2,7%-2` == `-3 -3 -1 1`; identity holds)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5p5 ‚Äî Signed-integer overflow of `*`, `/`, `%` (result, including `INT_MIN/-1`, not representable in the result type) is undefined behavior (general rule, applies to multiplicative operators). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; not diagnosed at compile time by any ‚Äî consensus)

### ¬ß6.5.6 Additive operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p1 ‚Äî Parse `+` and `-` as left-associative binary operators binding looser than multiplicative and tighter than shift operators (additive-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1<<2+1`==8 confirms `+` binds tighter than `<<`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p2 ‚Äî Constraint for `+`: either both operands have arithmetic type, or one operand is a pointer to a complete object type (C11; C99-only: "object type") and the other has integer type; reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`ptr+ptr` rejected by all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p2 ‚Äî Constraint for `-`: either both operands have arithmetic type; or both are pointers to qualified/unqualified versions of compatible complete object types (C11; C99-only: "object types"); or the left operand is such a pointer and the right operand has integer type; reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`structA* - structB*` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.6p3 ‚Äî When both operands have arithmetic type, perform the usual arithmetic conversions on them. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p4 ‚Äî Yield the sum of the operands for binary `+`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p5 ‚Äî Yield the difference (first operand minus second) for binary `-`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.5.6p6 ‚Äî Treat a pointer to an object that is not an array element as a pointer to the first element of a length-one array of that object's type, for the purposes of additive pointer operations. ‚Äî (spec; semantic model, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p7 ‚Äî When integer `N` is added to / subtracted from a pointer, the result has the pointer operand's type and points to the element offset by `N` (from the i-th element to the (i+N)-th for `P+N`/`N+P`, or the (i‚àíN)-th for `P‚àíN`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`*(p+3)`==a[3])
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p7 ‚Äî A pointer addressing the last array element plus one yields a valid pointer that points one past the last element. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`a+3 == &a[3]` for `int a[3]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p7 ‚Äî Pointer ¬± integer is defined only when both the original pointer and the result lie within the same array object or one past its last element; producing any other address (overflow out of the array) is undefined behavior. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; not diagnosed ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p7 ‚Äî A pointer one past the last array element may be formed but must not be dereferenced (used as the operand of an evaluated unary `*`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (forming one-past accepted; dereference UB undiagnosed ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p8 ‚Äî Subtracting two pointers yields the difference of their array subscripts; both pointers must address elements of, or one past the end of, the same array object, otherwise the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&a[4]-&a[1]`==3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.6p8 ‚Äî The result of a pointer subtraction has the implementation-defined signed integer type `ptrdiff_t` (from `<stddef.h>`); if the true difference is not representable in `ptrdiff_t`, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (result usable as signed integer; ptrdiff_t is `long` on x86-64 for all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5p5 ‚Äî Signed-integer overflow of arithmetic `+`/`-` (result not representable in the result type) is undefined behavior (general rule, applies to additive operators). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; not diagnosed ‚Äî consensus)

### ¬ß6.5.7 Bitwise shift operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p1 ‚Äî Parse `<<` and `>>` as left-associative binary operators binding looser than additive and tighter than relational operators (shift-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1<<2+1`==8)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p2 ‚Äî Constraint: each operand of `<<` and `>>` must have integer type; reject non-integer operands. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double<<1` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.7p3 ‚Äî Apply the integer promotions to each operand separately (not the usual arithmetic conversions); the result type is the promoted type of the left operand. ‚Äî (spec; result-type behavior, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p3 ‚Äî If the right operand is negative, or is greater than or equal to the width in bits of the promoted left operand, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; not diagnosed at compile time ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p4 ‚Äî `E1 << E2` shifts `E1` left by `E2` bit positions, vacated low bits filled with zero; for unsigned `E1` the result is `E1 √ó 2^E2` reduced modulo one more than the maximum value representable in the result type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1u<<31`==2147483648)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p4 ‚Äî For `E1 << E2` with signed nonnegative `E1`: if `E1 √ó 2^E2` is representable in the result type that is the value, otherwise the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (representable case yields product; overflow UB undiagnosed ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p5 ‚Äî `E1 >> E2` shifts `E1` right by `E2` bit positions; for unsigned `E1`, or signed nonnegative `E1`, the result is the floor (integral part) of `E1 / 2^E2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.7p5 ‚Äî For `E1 >> E2` with a negative signed `E1`, the resulting value is implementation-defined (e.g. arithmetic vs logical right shift). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-16>>2`==-4 ‚Äî all implement arithmetic shift)

### ¬ß6.5.8 Relational operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p1 ‚Äî Parse `<`, `>`, `<=`, `>=` as left-associative binary operators binding looser than shift and tighter than equality operators (relational-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1<2==1`==1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p2 ‚Äî Constraint: both operands have real type; or both are pointers to qualified/unqualified versions of compatible object types; or (C99-only) both are pointers to qualified/unqualified versions of compatible incomplete types (C11 folds incomplete into "object types"). Reject complex operands. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Complex < _Complex` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.8p3 ‚Äî When both operands have arithmetic (real) type, perform the usual arithmetic conversions before comparing. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5.8p4 ‚Äî Treat a pointer to an object that is not an array element as a pointer to the first element of a length-one array of that type, for relational-comparison purposes. ‚Äî (spec; semantic model, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p5 ‚Äî When comparing two pointers, the outcome reflects the relative addresses of the pointed-to objects; pointers to the same object, or both one-past-the-end of the same array, compare equal-ranked. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p5 ‚Äî Within one aggregate: a pointer to a later-declared structure member compares greater than one to an earlier member; a pointer to a higher-subscript array element compares greater than one to a lower-subscript element of the same array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p5 ‚Äî All pointers to members of the same union object compare equal-ranked; and for `P` pointing into an array whose last element is addressed by `Q`, the one-past pointer `Q+1` compares greater than `P`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p5 ‚Äî Relationally comparing pointers that do not point into (or one past) the same array object/aggregate is undefined behavior. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; not diagnosed ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.8p6 ‚Äî Each relational operator yields `1` (type `int`) when the specified relation holds and `0` otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.9 Equality operators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.9p1 ‚Äî Parse `==` and `!=` as left-associative binary operators binding looser than relational and tighter than bitwise-AND (equality-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.5.9p2 ‚Äî Constraint: the operand pair must be one of ‚Äî both arithmetic; both pointers to qualified/unqualified versions of compatible types; one pointer to an object or incomplete type and one pointer to qualified/unqualified `void`; or one pointer and one null pointer constant. Reject other combinations. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (`int* == char*` accepted with a warning by all three; constraint diagnostic is a non-fatal warning everywhere ‚Äî consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.9p3 ‚Äî `==`/`!=` behave like the relational operators but with lower precedence, yield `1`/`0` of type `int`, and for any operand pair exactly one of "equal"/"not equal" holds (`==` true iff `!=` false). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.9p4 ‚Äî When both operands have arithmetic type, perform the usual arithmetic conversions before comparing; complex values are equal iff both their real parts and both their imaginary parts are equal (and cross-domain values are equal iff their conversions to the common complex type are equal). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(1+2i)==(1+2i)`==1, `!=`==0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.9p5 ‚Äî If one operand is a pointer and the other a null pointer constant, convert the null pointer constant to the pointer's type; if one operand is a pointer to an object type and the other a pointer to qualified/unqualified `void`, convert the object pointer to the `void`-pointer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`p==0` and `p==(void*)p` accepted with no diagnostic)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.9p6 ‚Äî Two pointers compare equal iff: both are null pointers; both point to the same object (or both one-past-the-end of the same array); or one is one-past-the-end of one array object and the other points to the start of a different array object that happens to immediately follow it in the address space (a non-array object is treated as a length-one array for this rule). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.5.9p6 ‚Äî In the "immediately-following array" case, whether the one-past and start pointers compare equal is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified outcome, not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.5.10 Bitwise AND operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.10p1 ‚Äî Parse `&` as a left-associative binary operator binding looser than equality and tighter than `^` (AND-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`5&3|4`==5, `1|2^3&4`==3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.10p2 ‚Äî Constraint: each operand of binary `&` must have integer type; reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double&double` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.10p3 ‚Äî Apply the usual arithmetic conversions to the operands of `&`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.10p4 ‚Äî Compute the bitwise AND: each result bit is set iff the corresponding bits of both converted operands are set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.11 Bitwise exclusive OR operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.11p1 ‚Äî Parse `^` as a left-associative binary operator binding looser than `&` and tighter than `|` (exclusive-OR-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1|2^3&4`==3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.11p2 ‚Äî Constraint: each operand of `^` must have integer type; reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double^double` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.11p3 ‚Äî Apply the usual arithmetic conversions to the operands of `^`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.11p4 ‚Äî Compute the bitwise exclusive OR: each result bit is set iff exactly one of the corresponding operand bits is set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.12 Bitwise inclusive OR operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.12p1 ‚Äî Parse `|` as a left-associative binary operator binding looser than `^` and tighter than `&&` (inclusive-OR-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`5&3|4`==5)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.12p2 ‚Äî Constraint: each operand of `|` must have integer type; reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double|double` rejected by all)
- ¬ß6.5.12p3 ‚Äî Apply the usual arithmetic conversions to the operands of `|`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.12p4 ‚Äî Compute the bitwise inclusive OR: each result bit is set iff at least one of the corresponding operand bits is set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.13 Logical AND operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.13p1 ‚Äî Parse `&&` as a left-associative binary operator binding looser than `|` and tighter than `||` (logical-AND-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0||1&&0`==0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.13p2 ‚Äî Constraint: each operand of `&&` must have scalar type (arithmetic or pointer); reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct && struct` rejected by all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.13p3 ‚Äî Yield `1` (type `int`) if both operands compare unequal to `0`, and `0` otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`3&&4`==1, `0&&5`==0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.13p4 ‚Äî `&&` guarantees left-to-right evaluation with a sequence point after the first operand; if the first operand compares equal to `0`, the second operand is not evaluated (short-circuit). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0 && side()` leaves global unmodified)

### ¬ß6.5.14 Logical OR operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.14p1 ‚Äî Parse `||` as a left-associative binary operator binding looser than `&&` and tighter than the conditional operator (logical-OR-expression grammar). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`0||1&&0`==0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.14p2 ‚Äî Constraint: each operand of `||` must have scalar type (arithmetic or pointer); reject otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct || struct` rejected by all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.14p3 ‚Äî Yield `1` (type `int`) if either operand compares unequal to `0`, and `0` otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.14p4 ‚Äî `||` guarantees left-to-right evaluation with a sequence point after the first operand; if the first operand compares unequal to `0`, the second operand is not evaluated (short-circuit). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`1 || side()` leaves global unmodified)


## ¬ß6.5.15-¬ß6.5.17 Conditional/assignment/comma & ¬ß6.6 Constant expressions

> mcc status: 53 TODOs, 4 mcc-gaps (all "soft": mcc emits a diagnostic but accepts what gcc/clang hard-reject ‚Äî assignment to a const/read-only or const-member lvalue, compound-assign to const, and incompatible-pointer simple assignment; a standard-conforming diagnostic *is* issued, so these are ~ not ‚úó).

> Citation convention: paragraph numbers are given for **C11 (N1570)** first; where C99 (N1256) numbers or wording differ, the divergence is tagged inline. Several paragraphs were renumbered between C99 and C11 (notably ¬ß6.5.15 and ¬ß6.6), so the same requirement can carry two paragraph numbers.

### ¬ß6.5.15 Conditional operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p2 (C11; C99 folds this into p2 together with the operand list) ‚Äî Require the first (controlling) operand of `?:` to have scalar type; reject struct/union/void/array controlling operands. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p3 (C11; C99 p2) ‚Äî Constrain the second and third operands so that at least one of these holds: both have arithmetic type; both have the same struct/union type; both have `void` type; both are pointers to qualified/unqualified versions of compatible types; one is a pointer and the other a null pointer constant; or one is a pointer to an object type and the other a pointer to qualified/unqualified `void`. (C99 phrases the last case as a pointer to an "object or incomplete type"; C11 folds incomplete into "object type".) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (rejects mixing arithmetic and struct branches)
- [ ] ¬ß6.5.15p4 (C11; C99 p3) ‚Äî Evaluate the first operand fully and place a sequence point between it and whichever of the second/third operands is evaluated; evaluate the second operand only when the first compares unequal to 0, and the third only when the first compares equal to 0. ‚Äî (spec; runtime sequencing, not separately compile-testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p4 (C11; C99 p3) ‚Äî Yield as the result the value of whichever branch was evaluated, converted to the common result type determined by the rules below; the conditional expression is a value, never an lvalue. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(c?a:b)=x` rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p5 (C11; C99 p4) ‚Äî When both branches have arithmetic type, set the result type to what the usual arithmetic conversions would produce for those two operands. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(1?1:1.0)==sizeof(double)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p5 (C11; C99 p4) ‚Äî When both branches have the same struct/union type, give the result that type; when both branches have `void` type, give the result type `void`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p6 (C11; C99 p5) ‚Äî When both branches are pointers to compatible types (or differently-qualified versions of compatible types), make the result a pointer to an appropriately qualified version of the composite type, where the pointed-to type carries the union of the qualifiers of both branches' pointed-to types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p6 (C11; C99 p5) ‚Äî When one branch is a null pointer constant and the other a pointer, give the result the pointer type of the non-null branch. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.15p6 (C11; C99 p5) ‚Äî When one branch is a pointer to `void` (qualified or not) and the other a pointer to an object type, make the result a pointer to an appropriately qualified `void`, carrying the combined qualifiers of both pointed-to types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.5.16 Assignment operators (general)

- [~] ¬ß6.5.16p2 ‚Äî Require the left operand of any assignment (simple `=` or compound `op=`) to be a modifiable lvalue; reject assignment to a const-qualified lvalue, an array, an incomplete-type lvalue, a value designating an object with a const-qualified member, or a non-lvalue left operand. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects array/non-lvalue targets, but only **warns** "assignment of read-only location" for const lvalues and const-member structs where gcc/clang hard-error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16p3 ‚Äî Store a value in the object the left operand designates, and define the assignment expression's value as that stored value read back after the assignment, with the type the left operand has after lvalue conversion (qualifiers and `_Atomic` removed); make the assignment expression itself not an lvalue. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(a=b)=c` rejected; rest is runtime semantics)
- ¬ß6.5.16p3 (C11) ‚Äî Sequence the side effect of updating the stored value of the left operand after the value computations of both the left and right operands, and leave the evaluations of the two operands otherwise unsequenced relative to each other. ‚Äî (spec; runtime sequencing, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.5.16p3 (C99-only) ‚Äî Leave the order of evaluation of the two operands unspecified, with no sequence point between them (the C11 sequencing guarantee above does not apply in C99). ‚Äî (spec; runtime, not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.5.16.1 Simple assignment

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Permit simple `=` when the left operand has (atomic-, qualified-, or unqualified-) arithmetic type and the right operand has arithmetic type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Permit simple `=` when the left operand has an (atomic-, qualified-, or unqualified-) struct or union type compatible with the type of the right operand. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Permit simple `=` when both operands are pointers to qualified/unqualified versions of compatible types and the left's pointed-to type carries all the qualifiers of the right's pointed-to type. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (assigning between *incompatible* pointer types: mcc only **warns** "assignment from incompatible pointer type"; gcc/clang hard-error. Qualifier-discard `int*=const int*` warns in all three.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Permit simple `=` when one operand is a pointer to an object type and the other a pointer to qualified/unqualified `void`, provided the left's pointed-to type carries all the qualifiers of the right's pointed-to type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Permit simple `=` when the left operand is any pointer (atomic/qualified/unqualified) and the right operand is a null pointer constant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Permit simple `=` when the left operand has type `_Bool` (atomic/qualified/unqualified) and the right operand is any pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Accept an `_Atomic`-qualified left operand in any of the above forms (atomic store), in addition to plain qualified/unqualified left operands. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (basic `_Atomic int x; x=1;` accepted)
- [ ] ¬ß6.5.16.1p2 ‚Äî Convert the right operand's value to the (unqualified, non-atomic) type of the assignment expression and store the converted value in the object the left operand designates. ‚Äî (spec; runtime conversion, not separately compile-testable)
- [ ] ¬ß6.5.16.1p3 ‚Äî Treat as undefined behavior a simple assignment whose stored value is read from an object overlapping the storage of the destination, unless the two objects' storage overlaps exactly and they are qualified/unqualified versions of a compatible type. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not diagnosed by any compiler)

### ¬ß6.5.16.2 Compound assignment

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.2p1 ‚Äî For `+=` and `-=`, require either that the left operand be an (atomic-, qualified-, or unqualified-) pointer to a complete object type with the right operand of integer type, or that the left operand be an (atomic-, qualified-, or unqualified-) arithmetic type with the right operand of arithmetic type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`p+=2` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.2p1 ‚Äî For every other compound assignment (`*= /= %= <<= >>= &= ^= |=`), require both operands to have arithmetic types consistent with the corresponding binary operator (e.g. integer operands for `%=`, `<<=`, `>>=`, `&=`, `^=`, `|=`; arithmetic operands for `*=`, `/=`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double%=`, `double<<=`, `ptr*=` all rejected)
- [ ] ¬ß6.5.16.2p2 ‚Äî Treat `E1 op= E2` as equivalent to `E1 = E1 op (E2)`, except that the lvalue `E1` is evaluated only once, so its side effects and value computation occur a single time. ‚Äî (spec; runtime single-evaluation, not separately compile-testable)
- [ ] ¬ß6.5.16.2p3 (C11) ‚Äî When the left operand has atomic type, perform the read-modify-write as a single atomic operation with `memory_order_seq_cst` semantics. ‚Äî (spec; runtime atomicity, requires codegen inspection)
- [~] ¬ß6.5.16.2p1 (lvalue requirement inherited from p2) ‚Äî A compound assignment to a const-qualified lvalue must be diagnosed/rejected. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`const int a; a+=2;` ‚Äî mcc only warns "assignment of read-only location"; gcc/clang hard-error)

### ¬ß6.5.17 Comma operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.17p2 ‚Äî Evaluate the left operand as a void expression (discarding its value), place a sequence point after it, then evaluate the right operand; take the type and value of the right operand as the result. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (type propagation tested; sequencing is runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.17p2 ‚Äî Make the comma expression's result a value, not an lvalue, even when the right operand designates an object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(a,b)=3` rejected by all three)
- ¬ß6.5.17p2 (C11) ‚Äî Preserve the comma operator's left-then-right sequencing within its (parenthesized) subexpression even when it appears inside a context whose surrounding list-separator commas are themselves unsequenced (e.g. a function-argument list). ‚Äî (spec; runtime sequencing, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.17p3 ‚Äî Recognize that in syntactic positions where a comma is a list separator (function-call argument lists, brace-enclosed initializer lists) the comma is not the comma operator, so a comma operator must be parenthesized to be used there. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (parser distinguishes the two)

### ¬ß6.6 Constant expressions

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p2 (C11; C99 p4) ‚Äî Allow a constant expression to be computed during translation rather than at run time, and accept it anywhere a constant of the same kind is permitted. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (constant folding works; spec-level guarantee otherwise)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p3 (C11; C99 p2) ‚Äî Reject any constant expression that contains an assignment, `++`, `--`, function-call, or comma operator, except where such an operator sits inside a subexpression that is not evaluated (e.g. the unused branch of `?:`, the operands of `&&`/`||`/`?:` short-circuited away, or the operand of `sizeof`/`_Alignof`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì for assignment/`++`/function-call in an array size. **Comma operator exception:** `int a[(1,2)];` ‚Üí mcc:~ accepts, gcc:‚úó rejects, clang:~ accepts ‚Äî no gcc/clang consensus (gcc enforces p3, clang treats it as an extension); mcc matches clang.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p4 (C11; C99 p3) ‚Äî Require every constant expression, after its conversions, to evaluate to a constant lying within the range of representable values for its result type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (overflow in ICE diagnosed elsewhere; range check applied)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p5 ‚Äî Recognize the specific contexts that require an expression evaluating to a constant: the controlling expression of `#if`, array-size declarators (non-VLA), enumeration-constant values, bit-field widths, `case` labels, `static`/thread-storage-duration object initializers, and `_Alignas` alignment specifiers (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (non-constant bit-field width, `case`, and enum value all rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p6 ‚Äî Define an integer constant expression as one having integer type whose operands are only integer constants, enumeration constants, character constants, `sizeof` expressions whose results are integer constants, `_Alignof` expressions (C11), and floating constants that are the immediate operands of casts. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[sizeof(int)]`, `int a[_Alignof(double)]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p6 ‚Äî Within an integer constant expression, permit cast operators only to convert an arithmetic type to an integer type, except inside the operand of `sizeof` (or `_Alignof`, C11), which is unevaluated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[(int)1.9 + 3]` accepted ‚Äî float cast to int allowed)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p6 (C11) ‚Äî Treat `_Alignof` results as valid integer-constant-expression operands. (C99-only: `_Alignof` does not exist; `sizeof` is the only operator listed that yields an integer constant within an integer constant expression.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p7 ‚Äî Allow extra latitude for constant expressions used as initializers: such an expression must be, or evaluate to, one of an arithmetic constant expression, a null pointer constant, an address constant, or an address constant for a complete object type adjusted by adding or subtracting an integer constant expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int *p=&obj+1;`, `char *p="hi"+1;` accepted; `static int s=non_const_obj;` rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p8 ‚Äî Define an arithmetic constant expression as one having arithmetic type whose operands are only integer constants, floating constants, enumeration constants, character constants, `sizeof` expressions, and `_Alignof` expressions (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p8 ‚Äî Within an arithmetic constant expression, permit cast operators only to convert one arithmetic type to another arithmetic type, except inside the operand of `sizeof` (or `_Alignof`, C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p9 ‚Äî Define an address constant as a null pointer, a pointer to an lvalue designating an object of static storage duration, or a pointer to a function designator; allow it to be formed explicitly with unary `&` (or an integer constant cast to pointer type) or implicitly via array-to-pointer / function-to-pointer conversion, and allow `&`, `*`, `[]`, `.`, and `->` to participate in building it provided none of them actually accesses the stored value of an object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (address-of static obj initializers accepted)
- [ ] ¬ß6.6p10 ‚Äî Permit an implementation to accept additional, implementation-defined forms of constant expressions beyond those required, while still enforcing the mandatory categories above. ‚Äî (spec; implementation latitude, not a testable requirement)

### Additional / edge-case checkboxes added this pass

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16p2 ‚Äî Reject assignment to an array name (non-modifiable lvalue). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16p2 ‚Äî Reject assignment whose left operand is a pure rvalue (e.g. `(a+1)=2`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.16.1p1 ‚Äî Reject assignment of a struct value to an arithmetic lvalue (no implicit conversion). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p5 ‚Äî Reject a non-constant array size at file scope (would-be VLA invalid at file/static scope). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[g()]` rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.6p6 ‚Äî Accept a parenthesized float arithmetic result cast to int as an array size (`int a[(int)(1.5+0.5)]`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.5.16p2 ‚Äî Reject assignment to a struct lvalue that has a const-qualified member. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc warns only; gcc/clang hard-error)


## ¬ß6.7.1-¬ß6.7.3 Declarations: storage/type specifiers/qualifiers

> mcc status: 78 TODOs in this section; 1 mcc-gap: ¬ß6.7.3p6/¬ß6.5.16.1 ‚Äî assignment to a `const`-qualified object is only a *warning* in mcc (rc=0), an error in gcc/clang. mcc now rejects re-`typedef` of a variably-modified type (¬ß6.7p3), and flags `_Atomic(...)` (¬ß6.7.2.4) and `_Thread_local` (¬ß6.7.1p1) under `-std=c99 -pedantic-errors`, all matching gcc/clang. One consensus-split (not an mcc gap): ¬ß6.7.1p6 register-array subscript is accepted by mcc+gcc, rejected by clang. Everything else (storage-class exclusivity, `_Thread_local` placement, atomic/restrict/qualifier constraints, the full type-specifier multiset table) matches the gcc==clang consensus.

> Scope note: this section covers ¬ß6.7 (general declarations), ¬ß6.7.1 (storage-class specifiers, incl. C11 `_Thread_local`), ¬ß6.7.2 (type specifiers in general, incl. `_Bool`, `_Complex`, and C99-only `_Imaginary`), ¬ß6.7.2.4 (C11 atomic *type* specifiers ‚Äî `_Atomic` is a type specifier when immediately followed by `(`), ¬ß6.7.3 (type qualifiers `const`/`restrict`/`volatile` and the C11 `_Atomic` *qualifier*), and ¬ß6.7.3.1 (formal definition of `restrict`). Structure/union (¬ß6.7.2.1), enum (¬ß6.7.2.2), and tags (¬ß6.7.2.3) are documented in their own sections. Paragraph numbers follow C11 N1570; C99 N1256 divergences are tagged inline with `(C11)` / `(C99-only)`.

### ¬ß6.7 Declarations

- ¬ß6.7p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *declaration* matches `declaration-specifiers init-declarator-list_opt ;` or (C11) a `static_assert-declaration`. The *declaration-specifiers* are a sequence drawn from *storage-class-specifier*, *type-specifier*, *type-qualifier*, *function-specifier*, and (C11) *alignment-specifier*. (C99-only: no *alignment-specifier* and no `static_assert-declaration` alternative.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7p1 ‚Äî Syntax: *init-declarator-list* is a comma-separated list of *init-declarator*, each being a *declarator* optionally followed by `=` *initializer*. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7p2 ‚Äî Constraint: A declaration other than a `static_assert-declaration` (C11 qualifier; absent in C99) shall declare at least a declarator (other than the parameters of a function or the members of a structure or union), a tag, or the members of an enumeration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int;` ‚Üí all three warn "useless/empty declaration"; warning, not error, on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7p3 ‚Äî Constraint: If an identifier has no linkage, there shall be no more than one declaration of the identifier (in a declarator or type specifier) with the same scope and in the same name space, except that a typedef name may be redefined to denote the same type as it currently does ‚Äî provided that type is not a variably modified type (C11) ‚Äî and tags may be redeclared as specified in ¬ß6.7.2.3. (C99-only: the typedef-redefinition exception does **not** exist; redefining a typedef name in the same scope is a constraint violation in C99.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (plain `typedef int T; typedef int T;` matches all three: accepted in C11, diagnosed under `-std=c99 -pedantic-errors`; mcc also rejects `typedef int T[n]; typedef int T[n];` for a variably-modified `T` ‚Äî "redefinition of variably modified typedef 'T'" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7p3 (gap) ‚Äî Constraint: the C11 typedef-redefinition exception explicitly **excludes** variably modified types; `typedef int T[n]; typedef int T[n];` at block scope is a constraint violation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects ‚Äî "redefinition of variably modified typedef 'T'"; gcc: "redefinition of typedef 'T' with variably modified type", clang: "redefinition of typedef for variably-modified type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7p4 ‚Äî Constraint: All declarations in the same scope that refer to the same object or function shall specify compatible types (see ¬ß6.2.7). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int x; double x;` ‚Üí all error "incompatible/conflicting types for redefinition")
- ¬ß6.7p5 ‚Äî Semantics: A declaration specifies the interpretation and attributes of a set of identifiers. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7p5 ‚Äî Semantics: A *definition* of an identifier is a declaration for that identifier that, for an object, causes storage to be reserved for it. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7p5 ‚Äî Semantics: A definition of a function includes the function body. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7p5 ‚Äî Semantics: A definition for an enumeration constant is the (only) declaration of the identifier. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7p5 ‚Äî Semantics: A definition for a typedef name is the first (or only) declaration of the identifier. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7p6 ‚Äî Semantics: The declaration specifiers consist of a sequence of specifiers that indicate the linkage, storage duration, and part of the type of the entities the declarators denote; the init-declarator-list is a comma-separated sequence of declarators, each of which may have additional type information, an initializer, or both; the declarators contain the identifiers (if any) being declared. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7p7 ‚Äî Semantics: If an identifier for an object is declared with no linkage, the type for the object shall be complete by the end of its declarator, or by the end of its init-declarator if it has an initializer; in the case of function parameters (including in prototypes) it is the adjusted type (¬ß6.7.6.3; C99: ¬ß6.7.5.3) that is required to be complete. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S; void f(void){ struct S x; }` ‚Üí all error: incomplete/unknown storage size)

### ¬ß6.7.1 Storage-class specifiers

> C11 inserted two `_Thread_local` paragraphs (p3, p4); C99's typedef/register/function/aggregate paragraphs are therefore p3/p4/p5/p6 in C99 but p5/p6/p7/p8 in C11. Paragraph numbers below follow C11.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *storage-class-specifier* is exactly one of `typedef`, `extern`, `static`, `_Thread_local` (C11), `auto`, or `register`. (C99-only: the list omits `_Thread_local`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all six keywords accepted; `auto`/`register` at block scope OK on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p1 (gap) ‚Äî `_Thread_local` is a C11 addition; in C99 mode it must be diagnosed under `-pedantic-errors`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-std=c99 -pedantic-errors`: mcc rejects `_Thread_local` ‚Äî "'_Thread_local' is a C11 feature"; gcc: "ISO C99 does not support '_Thread_local'", clang: "'_Thread_local' is a C11 extension")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p1 (gap) ‚Äî GNU `__thread` thread-storage keyword (extension, accepted by all three regardless of `-std`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__thread int x;` compiles on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p2 ‚Äî Constraint: At most one storage-class specifier may be given in the declaration specifiers in a declaration, except that `_Thread_local` may appear with `static` or `extern` (C11). (C99-only: at most one, with no `_Thread_local` exception.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`static extern int x;` ‚Üí all error "multiple storage classes"; `_Thread_local static int x;` and `_Thread_local extern int x;` accepted by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) Constraint: In the declaration of an object with block scope, if the declaration specifiers include `_Thread_local` they shall also include either `static` or `extern`; if `_Thread_local` appears in any declaration of an object, it shall be present in every declaration of that object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void f(void){ _Thread_local int x; }` ‚Üí all error: mcc "'_Thread_local' at block scope requires 'static' or 'extern'", gcc/clang equivalent; `static _Thread_local` form accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) Constraint: `_Thread_local` shall not appear in the declaration specifiers of a function declaration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Thread_local void f(void);` ‚Üí all error: mcc "'_Thread_local' applied to a function", clang "only allowed on variable declarations", gcc "invalid storage class for function")
- ¬ß6.7.1p5 ‚Äî Semantics: The `typedef` specifier is called a "storage-class specifier" for syntactic convenience only; it is discussed in ¬ß6.7.8. The meanings of the linkages and storage durations are discussed in ¬ß6.2.2 and ¬ß6.2.4. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.1p6 ‚Äî Semantics: A declaration of an identifier for an object with storage-class specifier `register` suggests that access to the object be as fast as possible; the extent to which such suggestions are effective is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.1p6 ‚Äî Semantics: The implementation may treat any `register` declaration simply as an `auto` declaration. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p6 ‚Äî Semantics: Whether or not addressable storage is actually used, the address of any part of an object declared with storage-class specifier `register` cannot be computed, either explicitly (by the unary `&` operator, ¬ß6.5.3.2) or implicitly (by converting an array name to a pointer, ¬ß6.3.2.1); thus the only operator that can be applied to an array declared with `register` is `sizeof`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì for `&` (`&x` on `register int x` ‚Üí all error "address of register variable requested"); `sizeof` of a register array OK on all three. **Consensus split on subscripting a register array** (`register int a[3]; a[0]`): clang rejects (implicit array‚Üípointer = "address of register variable"), **mcc and gcc both accept** ‚Äî mcc matches gcc here, clang is the strict outlier.
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.1p7 ‚Äî Semantics: The declaration of an identifier for a function that has block scope shall have no explicit storage-class specifier other than `extern`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void f(void){ static void g(void); }` and `auto void g(void);` ‚Üí all error; `extern void g(void);` accepted by all three)
- ¬ß6.7.1p8 ‚Äî Semantics: If an aggregate or union object is declared with a storage-class specifier other than `typedef`, the properties resulting from the storage-class specifier (except with respect to linkage) also apply to the members of the object, and so on recursively for any aggregate or union member objects. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.7.2 Type specifiers

> C99 lists `_Imaginary` as a keyword type specifier and a constraint-list multiset (Annex G conditional feature); C11 removed `_Imaginary` from ¬ß6.7.2 (described only in informative Annex G) and added the *atomic-type-specifier*.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *type-specifier* is one of `void`, `char`, `short`, `int`, `long`, `float`, `double`, `signed`, `unsigned`, `_Bool`, `_Complex`, an *atomic-type-specifier* (C11), a *struct-or-union-specifier*, an *enum-specifier*, or a *typedef-name*. (C99-only: the keyword list additionally includes `_Imaginary` and omits *atomic-type-specifier*.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all keyword specifiers recognized; `_Bool b=1;` and `_Atomic(int)` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2p2 ‚Äî Constraint: At least one type specifier shall be given in the declaration specifiers in each declaration, and in the specifier-qualifier-list in each struct declaration and type name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (implicit-int `auto x=1;` at file scope ‚Üí all diagnose "type defaults to 'int'"/"implicit int"; mcc additionally errors on the auto-at-file-scope)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2p2 ‚Äî Constraint: Each list of type specifiers shall be one of the following multisets (order does not matter), and each multiset designates the indicated type: `void`; `char`; `signed char`; `unsigned char`; `short` / `signed short` / `short int` / `signed short int`; `unsigned short` / `unsigned short int`; `int` / `signed` / `signed int`; `unsigned` / `unsigned int`; `long` / `signed long` / `long int` / `signed long int`; `unsigned long` / `unsigned long int`; `long long` / `signed long long` / `long long int` / `signed long long int`; `unsigned long long` / `unsigned long long int`; `float`; `double`; `long double`; `_Bool`; `float _Complex`; `double _Complex`; `long double _Complex`; an *atomic-type-specifier* (C11); a *struct-or-union-specifier*; an *enum-specifier*; a *typedef-name*. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (valid multisets `unsigned long long int`, `long double _Complex`, all three `_Complex` widths accepted; invalid `long long long` ‚Üí "too long/too many basic types", `signed unsigned int` ‚Üí "signed and unsigned", `short long` ‚Üí rejected, on all three)
- [~] ¬ß6.7.2p2 ‚Äî (C99-only) Constraint: The multiset list additionally permits `float _Imaginary`, `double _Imaginary`, and `long double _Imaginary` (imaginary types ‚Äî a conditional feature per Annex G, signaled by `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__`). (C11 removed these from the constraint list.) ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (`_Imaginary` types are *unsupported* by all three even though all three define `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__`: mcc & clang error "imaginary types are not supported", gcc errors at the `_Imaginary` keyword. Annex G permits an IEC-559-complex implementation to omit imaginary types; consensus is uniform.)
- ¬ß6.7.2p3 ‚Äî Semantics: Specifiers for structures, unions, enumerations, and atomic types are discussed in ¬ß6.7.2.1 through ¬ß6.7.2.4 (¬ß6.7.2.4 is C11-only); declarations of typedef names are discussed in ¬ß6.7.8; the characteristics of the other types are discussed in ¬ß6.2.5. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2p4 ‚Äî Semantics: Each of the comma-separated multisets in the constraint list designates the same type, except that for bit-fields it is implementation-defined whether the specifier `int` designates the same type as `signed int` or the same type as `unsigned int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (impl-defined; a plain `int b:1` bit-field behaves identically across all three on x86-64 ‚Äî uniform consensus)

### ¬ß6.7.2.4 Atomic type specifiers (C11)

> (C11) Entire subsection is new in C11; absent in C99. Distinct from the `_Atomic` *qualifier* (¬ß6.7.3): `_Atomic` is a type specifier only when immediately followed by `(`.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Syntax: an *atomic-type-specifier* has the form `_Atomic ( type-name )`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Atomic(int) x;` accepted; `#include <stdatomic.h>` + `atomic_fetch_add` round-trips correctly when run on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p1 (gap) ‚Äî `_Atomic(...)` is a C11 construct; in C99 mode it must be diagnosed under `-pedantic-errors`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-std=c99 -pedantic-errors`: mcc rejects `_Atomic(int)` ‚Äî "'_Atomic' is a C11 feature"; gcc "ISO C99 does not support the '_Atomic' qualifier", clang "'_Atomic' is a C11 extension")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) Constraint: Atomic type specifiers shall not be used if the implementation does not support atomic types (see the `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` macro, ¬ß6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none of the three define `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`, i.e. all advertise atomics support; `<stdatomic.h>` and `<threads.h>` are present and usable in mcc's bundled headers)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p3 ‚Äî (C11) Constraint: The type name in an atomic type specifier shall not refer to an array type, a function type, an atomic type, or a qualified type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all four forms rejected by all three: `_Atomic(int[3])` array, `_Atomic(int(void))` function, `_Atomic(_Atomic(int))` atomic, `_Atomic(const int)` qualified; the `_Atomic` *qualifier* spelling `_Atomic A`/`_Atomic F` on array/function typedefs is also rejected)
- ¬ß6.7.2.4p4 ‚Äî (C11) Semantics: The properties associated with atomic types are meaningful only for expressions that are lvalues. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p4 ‚Äî (C11) Semantics: If the `_Atomic` keyword is immediately followed by a left parenthesis, it is interpreted as a type specifier (with a type name), not as a type qualifier (whose semantics are in ¬ß6.7.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Atomic int x; _Atomic(int) y;` ‚Äî both qualifier and specifier spellings accepted side-by-side by all three)

### ¬ß6.7.3 Type qualifiers

> C11 inserted the `_Atomic`-qualifier constraint as p3, shifting C99's lvalue/duplicate-qualifier/const/volatile/restrict/array-function/compatibility paragraphs from C99 p3‚Äìp9 to C11 p4‚Äìp10. Paragraph numbers below follow C11; C99 equivalents noted where they differ.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3p1 ‚Äî Syntax: a *type-qualifier* is one of `const`, `restrict`, `volatile`, or `_Atomic` (C11). (C99-only: the list omits `_Atomic`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all four qualifier keywords recognized)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3p2 ‚Äî Constraint: Types other than pointer types whose referenced type is an object type shall not be restrict-qualified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int restrict x;` ‚Üí all error "restrict requires a pointer"; `void (*restrict fp)(void)` (pointer-to-function) ‚Üí all error "pointer to function may not be restrict"; `int *restrict p;` and `void *restrict p;` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) Constraint: The type modified by the `_Atomic` qualifier shall not be an array type or a function type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (covered with ¬ß6.7.2.4p3: `_Atomic A`/`_Atomic F` on array/function typedefs rejected by all three)
- ¬ß6.7.3p4 ‚Äî Semantics: The properties associated with qualified types are meaningful only for expressions that are lvalues. (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p3.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3p5 ‚Äî Semantics: If the same qualifier appears more than once in the same specifier-qualifier-list, either directly or via one or more typedefs, the behavior is the same as if it appeared only once. (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p4.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`const const int x;` accepted by all three even under `-std=c99 -pedantic-errors`; clang adds a `-Wduplicate-decl-specifier` warning, mcc/gcc silent ‚Äî all rc=0)
- ¬ß6.7.3p6 ‚Äî Semantics: If an attempt is made to modify an object defined with a const-qualified type through use of an lvalue with non-const-qualified type, the behavior is undefined. (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p5.) ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable ‚Äî see the assignment-to-const constraint item below for the diagnosable case)
- [~] ¬ß6.7.3p6 (related, ¬ß6.5.16.1) ‚Äî A `const`-qualified lvalue is not a modifiable lvalue; direct assignment to it is a constraint violation. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`const int x=0; x=1;` ‚Üí **mcc only emits a *warning* "assignment of read-only location" and exits rc=0**, whereas gcc errors "assignment of read-only variable" and clang errors "cannot assign to variable with const-qualified type". mcc accepts; gcc/clang reject.)
- ¬ß6.7.3p6 ‚Äî Semantics: If an attempt is made to refer to an object defined with a volatile-qualified type through use of an lvalue with non-volatile-qualified type, the behavior is undefined. (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p5.) ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.3p7 ‚Äî Semantics: An object that has volatile-qualified type may be modified in ways unknown to the implementation or have other unknown side effects; therefore any expression referring to such an object shall be evaluated strictly according to the rules of the abstract machine (¬ß5.1.2.3). (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p6.) ‚Äî (spec; abstract-machine semantics, not mechanically asserted here)
- ¬ß6.7.3p7 ‚Äî Semantics: At every sequence point the value last stored in a volatile-qualified object shall agree with that prescribed by the abstract machine, except as modified by the unknown factors mentioned previously. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3p7 ‚Äî Semantics: What constitutes an access to an object that has volatile-qualified type is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3p8 ‚Äî Semantics: An object that is accessed through a restrict-qualified pointer has a special association with that pointer (defined in ¬ß6.7.3.1) requiring that all accesses to that object use, directly or indirectly, the value of that particular pointer. (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p7.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3p8 ‚Äî Semantics: The intended use of `restrict` (like the `register` storage class) is to promote optimization; deleting all instances of the qualifier from all preprocessing translation units composing a conforming program does not change its meaning (i.e., observable behavior). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3p9 ‚Äî Semantics: If the specification of an array type includes any type qualifiers, the element type is so-qualified, not the array type. (C99: ¬ß6.7.3p8.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî observable only via the array-parameter `[restrict]`/`[const]` rewrite)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3p9 ‚Äî Semantics: If the specification of a function type includes any type qualifiers, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`typedef int F(void); const F f;` ‚Äî all three accept silently; clang warns under `-Wignored-qualifiers` "'const' qualifier on function type has no effect", gcc warns under `-Wall`; mcc accepts. UB ‚Üí no required diagnostic, all conform.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3p10 ‚Äî Semantics: For two qualified types to be compatible, both shall have the identically qualified version of a compatible type; the order of type qualifiers within a list of specifiers or qualifiers does not affect the specified type. (C99: equivalent wording in ¬ß6.7.3p9.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`const volatile int x; volatile const int y;` ‚Äî both orderings accepted and yield the same type on all three)

### ¬ß6.7.3.1 Formal definition of restrict

> Pure formal/aliasing definitions; a translator is explicitly free to ignore restrict (p6), so none of these are conformance-testable by a single TU compile. mcc parses and accepts `restrict` everywhere it is required to (verified above under ¬ß6.7.3p2).

- ¬ß6.7.3.1p1 ‚Äî Let D be a declaration of an ordinary identifier that provides a means of designating an object P as a restrict-qualified pointer to type T. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p2 ‚Äî If D appears inside a block and does not have storage class `extern`, let B denote that block; if D appears in the list of parameter declarations of a function definition, let B denote the associated block; otherwise let B denote the block of `main` (or the block of whatever function is called at program startup in a freestanding environment). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p3 ‚Äî A pointer expression E is said to be *based on* object P if (at some sequence point in the execution of B prior to the evaluation of E) modifying P to point to a copy of the array object into which it formerly pointed would change the value of E; "based" is defined only for expressions with pointer types. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p4 ‚Äî During each execution of B, let L be any lvalue that has `&L` based on P; if L is used to access the value of the object X that it designates, and X is also modified (by any means), then T shall not be const-qualified. ‚Äî (spec; UB definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p4 ‚Äî Under the same conditions, every other lvalue used to access the value of X shall also have its address based on P. ‚Äî (spec; UB definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p4 ‚Äî Under the same conditions, every access that modifies X shall be considered also to modify P, for the purposes of this subclause. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p4 ‚Äî Under the same conditions, if P is assigned the value of a pointer expression E that is based on another restricted pointer object P2 (associated with block B2), then either the execution of B2 shall begin before the execution of B, or the execution of B2 shall end prior to the assignment. ‚Äî (spec; UB definition, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p4 ‚Äî If these requirements are not met, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.3.1p5 ‚Äî Here an execution of B means that portion of the execution of the program that would correspond to the lifetime of an object with scalar type and automatic storage duration associated with B. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.3.1p6 ‚Äî A translator is free to ignore any or all aliasing implications of uses of `restrict`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (permissive; all three accept `restrict` and are free to ignore its aliasing implications ‚Äî no conformance obligation)


## ¬ß6.7.2.1-¬ß6.7.2.4 Struct/union/enum/atomic specifiers

> mcc status: 63 TODOs total (54 testable probed across mcc/gcc/clang, 9 spec-only); mcc-gaps: 1 hard divergence (atomic bit-fields accepted where gcc/clang reject ‚Äî but this is impl-defined per p4, so mcc remains conforming) plus 1 minor diagnostic-quality gap (no "declaration does not declare anything" warning). No conformance defects found: mcc diagnoses every probed constraint and matches gcc/clang on all runtime semantics (anon members, recursive lookup, FAM, unions, _Bool bit-fields, _Atomic specifier + its p3 constraints).

### ¬ß6.7.2.1 Structure and union specifiers

> C99‚ÜíC11 deltas in this clause: C11 adds anonymous structures/unions (member with an untagged `struct`/`union` specifier and no declarator), permits a `static_assert-declaration` as a `struct-declaration`, makes the per-member `struct-declarator-list` optional (to allow anonymous members), adds `_Bool` bit-field value semantics (p9) and the "atomic types as bit-fields is implementation-defined" allowance (p4), and moves the flexible-array-member text from C99 ¬ß6.7.2.1p16 to C11 ¬ß6.7.2.1p18. C11 also permits an `alignment-specifier` (`_Alignas`) inside a `specifier-qualifier-list`.

#### Syntax
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept `struct-or-union-specifier` in both forms: `struct-or-union identifier_opt { struct-declaration-list }` (definition) and `struct-or-union identifier` (reference). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept `struct-or-union` being either the keyword `struct` or the keyword `union`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept a `struct-declaration-list` as one or more `struct-declaration`s. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept a `struct-declaration` of the form `specifier-qualifier-list struct-declarator-list_opt ;`, the `struct-declarator-list` being optional so as to permit anonymous structure/union members. (C11; C99 required a non-optional `struct-declarator-list`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept a `static_assert-declaration` as a `struct-declaration`. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S { int a; _Static_assert(1,"ok"); int b; };` compiles on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept a `specifier-qualifier-list` as a sequence of `type-specifier`, `type-qualifier`, and (C11) `alignment-specifier` items. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept a `struct-declarator-list` as one or more comma-separated `struct-declarator`s. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p1 ‚Äî Accept a `struct-declarator` as either `declarator` or `declarator_opt : constant-expression` (bit-field, with the declarator optional for an unnamed bit-field). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### Constraints
- [~] ¬ß6.7.2.1p2 ‚Äî A `struct-declaration` that does not declare an anonymous structure or anonymous union shall contain a `struct-declarator-list`. (C11). A tagged member with no declarator (`struct S { union T { int x; }; };`) is not anonymous and declares nothing. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (gcc/clang emit "declaration does not declare anything"; mcc accepts silently ‚Äî minor diagnostic-quality gap, no conformance impact)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p3 ‚Äî The bit-field width shall be an integer constant expression with a nonnegative value not exceeding the width of the underlying type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a:40` ‚Üí all reject "width exceeds its type"; `int a:-1` ‚Üí all reject "negative width")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p3 ‚Äî If the bit-field width value is zero, the declaration shall have no declarator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a:0` ‚Üí all reject "zero width for bit-field")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p4 ‚Äî A bit-field shall have a type that is a qualified or unqualified version of `_Bool`, `signed int`, `unsigned int`, or some other implementation-defined type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`float a:3` ‚Üí all reject; mcc: "bitfields must have scalar type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p4 ‚Äî It is implementation-defined whether atomic types are permitted as bit-field types. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (impl-defined choices differ: `_Atomic int a:3` ‚Äî mcc **accepts**; gcc/clang reject "bit-field has atomic type". mcc's acceptance is a valid implementation-defined choice, so all three conform, but mcc diverges from the gcc/clang consensus.)

#### Semantics
- ¬ß6.7.2.1p5 ‚Äî A structure is a sequence of members allocated in an ordered sequence; a union's members overlap (per 6.2.5). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.2.1p6 ‚Äî Structure and union specifiers have the same form; `struct` indicates a structure type, `union` a union type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p7 ‚Äî The presence of a `struct-declaration-list` declares a new type within the translation unit; the list is the member declarations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p7 ‚Äî If the `struct-declaration-list` contains no named members, no anonymous structures, and no anonymous unions, the behavior is undefined. (C11; C99 forbade an empty member list in a constraint context). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB/extension; `struct S {};` all reject under `-pedantic-errors`: mcc "ISO C forbids a struct with no named members", gcc "struct has no members", clang "empty struct is a GNU extension")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p7 ‚Äî The type is incomplete until immediately after the `}` and complete thereafter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (member-incomplete-type and self-containment probes all rejected identically)
