- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p8 ‚Äî A member may have any complete object type other than a variably modified type; not incomplete (except FAM p18) and not function type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (function member ‚Üí all reject "declared as a function"; incomplete member ‚Üí all reject "incomplete type"; variably-modified member `int a[n]` ‚Üí all reject under `-pedantic-errors`: mcc "ISO C forbids a member with a variably modified type", clang rejects unconditionally)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p8 ‚Äî A member may be declared as a specified number of bits (a bit-field) whose width follows a colon. ‚Äî (spec; covered by p3 probes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p9 ‚Äî A bit-field is interpreted as a signed or unsigned integer type of the specified number of bits. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p9 ‚Äî Storing 0 or 1 into a nonzero-width `_Bool` bit-field compares equal to the stored value; a `_Bool` bit-field has `_Bool` semantics. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime: `s.b=1; s.b==1` ‚Üí 1 on all three; `s.b=2` ‚Üí reads back 1 on all three)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p10 ‚Äî An implementation may allocate any addressable storage unit large enough to hold a bit-field. ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined, not a conformance check)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p10 ‚Äî If enough space remains, a bit-field immediately following another is packed into adjacent bits of the same unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct{unsigned a:5;unsigned b:5;}` packs; sizeof matches gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p10 ‚Äî Whether a bit-field that does not fit is put into the next unit or overlaps adjacent units is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p10 ‚Äî The order of allocation of bit-fields within a unit is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined, ABI-determined)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p10 ‚Äî The alignment of the addressable storage unit is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p11 ‚Äî A bit-field with no declarator (colon + width only) is an unnamed bit-field. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p11 ‚Äî A width-0 unnamed bit-field forces no further bit-field into the current unit (alignment break). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`unsigned a:5; unsigned :0; unsigned b:5;` ‚Üí sizeof 8 on all three)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p12 ‚Äî Each non-bit-field member is aligned in an implementation-defined manner appropriate to its type. ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined/ABI)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p13 ‚Äî An unnamed member whose type specifier is a tagless `struct`/`union` specifier is an anonymous structure/union. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p13 ‚Äî Members of an anonymous structure/union are members of the containing structure/union (for lookup and `.`/`->`), applied recursively. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime: `s.deep+s.mid+s.top` through two nested anonymous levels ‚Üí 6 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p14 ‚Äî Within a structure object, non-bit-field members and bit-field units have addresses increasing in declaration order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p14 ‚Äî A pointer to a structure, suitably converted, points to its initial member (or its bit-field unit), and vice versa. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(void*)&s==(void*)&s.a` ‚Üí 1 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p14 ‚Äî There may be unnamed padding within a structure, but not at its beginning. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p15 ‚Äî The size of a union is sufficient to contain the largest member. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`union{char;double;int;}` ‚Üí sizeof 8 on all three)
- ¬ß6.7.2.1p15 ‚Äî The value of at most one member can be stored in a union at any time. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p15 ‚Äî A pointer to a union, suitably converted, points to each member (or its bit-field unit), and vice versa. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&u==&u.d && &u==&u.c` ‚Üí 1 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p16 ‚Äî There may be unnamed padding at the end of a structure or union. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p18 ‚Äî The last element of a structure with >1 named member may have an incomplete array type ‚Äî a flexible array member. (C11 ¬ß6.7.2.1p18; C99 ¬ß6.7.2.1p16). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S{int n;int a[];}` accepted; sizeof excludes FAM)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p18 ‚Äî A structure with a FAM (and unions recursively containing such) shall not be a member of a structure or an array element. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (constraint violation; under `-pedantic-errors` all reject: mcc "ISO C forbids a member that is a structure with a flexible array member", gcc/clang likewise. Accepted as extension by default.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p18 ‚Äî The FAM is ignored for sizeof; size equals the offset of the FAM in an otherwise identical struct with the FAM replaced by a zero-length array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1p18 ‚Äî `.`/`->` naming the FAM behaves as if replaced by the longest array fitting the accessed object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime: malloc'd 3-elem FAM read/write ‚Üí `0 10 20` on all three)
- ¬ß6.7.2.1p18 ‚Äî The offset of the FAM shall remain that of the FAM even if it differs from the replacement array's offset. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.1p18 ‚Äî If the replacement array would have no elements, it behaves as if it had one, but accessing it or forming a one-past pointer is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB)

### ¬ß6.7.2.2 Enumeration specifiers

> C99‚ÜíC11: substantively unchanged. C11 ¬ß6.7.2.2p4 adds the explicit sentence that the enumerated type is incomplete until the closing `}` and complete thereafter.

#### Syntax
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p1 ‚Äî Accept `enum identifier_opt { enumerator-list }`, `enum identifier_opt { enumerator-list , }` (trailing comma), and `enum identifier`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (trailing comma `enum E{A,B,}` accepted on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p1 ‚Äî Accept an `enumerator-list` as one or more comma-separated `enumerator`s. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p1 ‚Äî Accept an `enumerator` as `enumeration-constant` or `enumeration-constant = constant-expression`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### Constraints
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p2 ‚Äî The enumeration-constant value shall be an integer constant expression representable as `int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`A=0x100000000LL` ‚Üí constraint violation; under `-pedantic-errors` all reject: mcc "ISO C restricts enumerator values to the range of 'int'". Accepted as C23 extension by default.)

#### Semantics
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p3 ‚Äî Enumerator identifiers are declared as constants of type `int` and may appear wherever such are permitted. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(A)==4` and `_Generic(A,int:1,...)==1` on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p3 ‚Äî An enumerator with `=` defines its constant as the constant-expression's value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p3 ‚Äî If the first enumerator has no `=`, its value is 0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p3 ‚Äî Each subsequent enumerator with no `=` is the previous value plus 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p3 ‚Äî Enumerators with `=` may produce values duplicating other values in the same enumeration (permitted). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.2.2p3 ‚Äî The enumerators of an enumeration are also known as its members. ‚Äî (spec; terminology)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p4 ‚Äî Each enumerated type shall be compatible with `char`, a signed integer type, or an unsigned integer type capable of representing all members; the choice is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`enum{A,B=4294967295U}` ‚Üí sizeof 4 (unsigned int) on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.2p4 ‚Äî The enumerated type is incomplete until immediately after the `}` and complete thereafter. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (using `enum E e;` before the enum is completed ‚Üí all reject "ISO C forbids forward references to 'enum' types")

### ¬ß6.7.2.3 Tags

> C99‚ÜíC11: C11 adds ¬ß6.7.2.3p7, the standalone forward-declaration form `struct-or-union identifier ;`, which introduces a new (hiding) tag in the current scope; there is no analogous `enum identifier ;` form.

#### Constraints
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p1 ‚Äî A specific type shall have its content defined at most once. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (double `struct S{...}` ‚Üí all reject: mcc "struct/union/enum already defined", gcc/clang "redefinition")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p2 ‚Äî Two declarations using the same tag for the same type shall use the same `struct`/`union`/`enum` keyword. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S` then `union S` ‚Üí all reject; mcc "redeclaration of 'S'", gcc "wrong kind of tag", clang "tag type that does not match")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p3 ‚Äî `enum identifier` without an enumerator list shall only appear after the type is complete. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (forward `enum E;`/`enum E e;` ‚Üí all reject "ISO C forbids forward references to 'enum' types")

#### Semantics
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p4 ‚Äî All declarations of struct/union/enum types in the same scope using the same tag declare the same type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p4 ‚Äî Regardless of tag or other declarations, the type is incomplete until just after the closing brace of its content list, and complete thereafter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p5 ‚Äî Declarations in different scopes or with different tags declare distinct types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p5 ‚Äî Each tagless declaration of such a type declares a distinct type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.7.2.3p6 ‚Äî A defining-form type specifier declares a struct/union/enum type with the list defining its content. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p6 ‚Äî If an identifier is given in a defining form, the specifier also declares that identifier as the tag. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p7 ‚Äî `struct-or-union identifier ;` declares the identifier as a tag introducing a new tag in the current scope, hiding any same-named tag in an enclosing scope (forward declaration). (C11; no `enum` form). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (inner `struct S;` then redefined locally and used ‚Üí accepted on all three; the outer `struct S` is correctly hidden)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p8 ‚Äî A non-defining `struct-or-union identifier` / `enum identifier` form with a visible tag declaration refers to that same type and does not redeclare the tag. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.3p8 ‚Äî Such a form with no visible tag declaration declares an incomplete struct/union type and declares the identifier as its tag. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.7.2.4 Atomic type specifiers (C11)

> Entire clause is C11-only; absent in C99.

#### Syntax
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p1 ‚Äî Accept an `atomic-type-specifier` of the form `_Atomic ( type-name )`. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Atomic(int) g;` + `atomic_store/load` runs identically; `sizeof(_Atomic(int))==sizeof(int)` holds)

#### Constraints
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p2 ‚Äî Atomic type specifiers shall not be used if the implementation does not support atomic types (signaled by `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`, see 6.10.8.3). (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none of the three define `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`, consistent with all three accepting `_Atomic(int)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p3 ‚Äî The type name shall not refer to an array type, a function type, an atomic type, or a qualified type. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (array ‚Üí mcc "_Atomic cannot be applied to an array type"; function ‚Üí "...function type"; atomic ‚Üí "...an atomic type"; qualified `const int` ‚Üí "...a qualified type"; all four rejected by all three)

#### Semantics
- ¬ß6.7.2.4p4 ‚Äî The properties associated with atomic types are meaningful only for expressions with lvalue type. (C11). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4p4 ‚Äî If `_Atomic` is immediately followed by `(`, it is interpreted as a type specifier (`_Atomic ( type-name )`), not the `_Atomic` qualifier of ¬ß6.7.3. (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (using `_Atomic(int)` in an expression position ‚Üí all reject "expression expected"/"expected expression", confirming it is parsed as a type specifier)


## ¬ß6.7.4-¬ß6.7.5 Function specifiers & alignment specifier

> mcc status: `_Noreturn` and every `_Alignas` constraint (typedef/bitfield/param/register/function/weaker/zero/non-pow2/non-ICE) match the gcc==clang consensus. The remaining gaps are all in inline-definition handling (3 `‚úó` rows): mcc emits an external definition for a *plain* `inline` definition (so an `-O0` call links instead of failing, ¬ß6.7.4p6), and silently accepts the constraint-violating `inline` internal-linkage-reference (¬ß6.7.4p2) and `inline main` (¬ß6.7.4p3) cases that gcc/clang diagnose. mcc now warns on the `inline` modifiable-static case (¬ß6.7.4p2), matching gcc/clang.

### ¬ß6.7.4 Function specifiers

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p1 ‚Äî Restrict the `inline` / `_Noreturn` (C11) function specifiers to declarations of a function identifier; reject them on objects/typedefs. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc & clang error on `inline int x;`; gcc only warns ‚Äî mcc matches clang's reject)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p2 ‚Äî Forbid an inline definition of an external-linkage function from defining a modifiable object with static (C11: or thread) storage duration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (constraint requires a diagnostic; mcc warns "'s' is static but declared in inline function 'f' which is not static", as do gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p2 ‚Äî Forbid an inline definition of an external-linkage function from referencing an internal-linkage identifier. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (constraint requires a diagnostic; mcc emits a `-pedantic` warning "'s' has internal linkage but is referenced in an inline function with external linkage" for a static function referenced from an external-linkage inline, matching clang's `-Wstatic-in-inline`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p3 ‚Äî In a hosted environment, forbid a function specifier on the declaration of `main` (C99: just `inline`; C11: any function specifier). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc warns "'main' is not allowed to be declared inline" for hosted `inline int main`; suppressed under `-ffreestanding`; gcc warns, clang errors)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p4 ‚Äî Permit a function specifier to appear more than once in a declaration, treating repeats as a single occurrence. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`inline inline int f(){}` accepted; clang adds a pedantic duplicate-specifier warning only)
- ¬ß6.7.4p5 ‚Äî Treat a function declared `inline` as an inline function: a hint that calls be made fast, with the actual effectiveness implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p6 ‚Äî Allow any internal-linkage function to be inline (`static inline`) with no external-definition obligation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`static inline` compiles and links)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p6 ‚Äî Require that an external-linkage function declared `inline` also be defined in the same translation unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc errors `unresolved reference to 'f'`; gcc/clang warn at compile then fail to link)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.4p6 ‚Äî Form an *inline definition* when every file-scope declaration of the function in the TU has `inline` and none has `extern`. ‚Äî (spec; behavior observed via the linkage tests below)
- [‚úó] ¬ß6.7.4p6 ‚Äî Ensure an inline definition provides NO external definition for the function (and does not forbid one in another TU); it is only an alternative the translator may use for same-TU calls. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (at `-O0` a call to a plain-`inline`-only function must fail to link; gcc/clang give `undefined reference`, mcc wrongly emits a global definition and links cleanly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p6 ‚Äî When a file-scope declaration of the same function uses `extern` (or a non-`inline` declaration is present), emit the external definition for the inline function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (adding `extern int add(...);` makes the `-O0` call link on all three)
- ¬ß6.7.4p6 ‚Äî Leave it unspecified whether a given same-TU call uses the inline definition or the external definition. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p7 ‚Äî (C11) Treat a function declared `_Noreturn` as never returning to its caller; a return at runtime is undefined behavior. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; `<stdnoreturn.h>`'s `noreturn` macro also works on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.4p8 ‚Äî (C11) Recommended practice: diagnose a `_Noreturn` function that appears able to return to its caller. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three warn on a `_Noreturn` function containing a reachable `return`)

### ¬ß6.7.5 Alignment specifier (`_Alignas`) ‚Äî C11

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 ‚Äî (C11) Accept both alignment-specifier forms: `_Alignas(type-name)` and `_Alignas(constant-expression)` (plus the `<stdalign.h>` `alignas` spelling). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both forms and the macro accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) Reject `_Alignas` in a declaration of a typedef. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) Reject `_Alignas` on a bit-field. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) Reject `_Alignas` on a function declaration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) Reject `_Alignas` on a function parameter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) Reject `_Alignas` on an object declared with the `register` storage-class specifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p3 ‚Äî (C11) Require the `_Alignas` constant-expression to be an integer constant expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(n)` with a runtime `n` errors on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p3 ‚Äî (C11) Require the value to be a valid fundamental or implementation-supported extended alignment, or zero (reject non-power-of-two values). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(3)` rejected as not a positive power of two on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p4 ‚Äî (C11) Treat an alignment specification of zero (`_Alignas(0)`) as having no effect. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all accept with no alignment change)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p5 ‚Äî (C11) When multiple alignment specifiers appear, apply the strictest (largest) specified alignment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(8) _Alignas(16)` yields alignment 16)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p6 ‚Äî (C11) Make `_Alignas(type-name)` equivalent to `_Alignas(_Alignof(type-name))`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(double)` gives `_Alignof(double)`; the type-name vs constant forms agree)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p7 ‚Äî (C11) Reject a combined alignment weaker (less strict) than the type's natural required alignment, whether expressed via a constant (`_Alignas(1) int`) or a smaller type (`_Alignas(char) int`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all error: "less than minimum alignment of the type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5 ‚Äî (C11) Honor the requested alignment in generated code/storage (object actually placed at the specified boundary). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(64)` object verified 64-byte aligned at runtime under mcc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5 ‚Äî (C11) Apply `_Alignas` on a struct member so it raises the alignment of the containing aggregate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Alignas(16) int` member makes `_Alignof(struct S)==16`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5 ‚Äî (C11) Interoperate with `_Alignof`: `_Alignof` reports the specified/required alignment used as `_Alignas` input (note: `_Alignof` on an *expression* is a non-ISO GNU extension all three warn about). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì


## ¬ß6.7.6 Declarators

> mcc status: solid on the common cases (pointer/array/function derivation, [static]/[*]/qualifier placement, void/ellipsis/register constraints, VLA placement+no-linkage+goto+single-evaluation). mcc now rejects a zero-size constant array under `-pedantic-errors` and rejects a non-empty identifier list in a non-defining declaration (`int f(a,b);`), matching gcc/clang. The remaining gaps vs the gcc==clang consensus (`~` rows) are in qualifier handling on derived pointer types: (1) a type-qualifier written inside an array parameter's brackets (`int a[const 3]`) is parsed but not applied, so the adjusted pointer is not actually `const` (¬ß6.7.6.2p3/¬ß6.7.6.3p4); (2) reassigning a `const` pointer (`int *const p`) is only a warning in mcc, an error in clang (¬ß6.7.6.1p2).

### ¬ß6.7.6 Declarators (general)

- ¬ß6.7.6p1 ‚Äî Grammar: a declarator is an optional pointer part followed by a direct-declarator; direct-declarators build array `[...]` and function `(...)` derivations around an identifier or a parenthesized declarator. ‚Äî (spec; grammar, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6p2 ‚Äî Each declarator introduces exactly one identifier, derived from the type given by the declaration specifiers via the declarator's pointer/array/function operators. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.7.6p3 ‚Äî A declarator is processed by treating "T D1" (with D1 a derived declarator) as recursively assigning the inner declarator the derived type; the base case gives the identifier the specifier type. ‚Äî (spec; constructive definition, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6p4 ‚Äî A full declarator is one not nested inside another declarator; for a variably modified type the size expressions are evaluated when the full declarator's declaration is reached in execution (in order, once each). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (VLA size expr evaluated exactly once when the declaration is reached)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6p5 ‚Äî Examples of combining specifiers and declarators (informative). ‚Äî (spec; examples, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6 (multi-declarator) ‚Äî A single declaration may carry several declarators that derive different types from the same specifiers (`int *p, a[3], f(void);`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.7.6.1 Pointer declarators

- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.1p1 ‚Äî Grammar: a pointer is one or more `*`, each optionally followed by a type-qualifier-list. ‚Äî (spec; grammar)
- [~] ¬ß6.7.6.1p2 ‚Äî `* type-qualifier-list D` derives a "qualified pointer to T" type ‚Äî the qualifiers attach to the pointer object itself, not to the pointed-to type. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc honors qualifiers written between `*` and the name e.g. `int *const p`, but ignores qualifiers written inside array-parameter brackets ‚Äî see ¬ß6.7.6.3)
- [~] ¬ß6.7.6.1p2 ‚Äî `int *const p` makes the pointer const: reassigning `p` is a constraint violation. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc emits only a warning "assignment of read-only location"; gcc warns, clang errors ‚Äî none is non-conforming, but mcc/gcc are diagnostic-only)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.1p2 ‚Äî `const int *p` qualifies the pointee, not the pointer: writing `*p` is the violation, reassigning `p` is fine. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`*p=...` diagnosed; pointer itself remains modifiable)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.1p3 ‚Äî Two pointer types are compatible iff identically qualified and pointing to compatible types. ‚Äî (spec; folded into type-compatibility, tested under ¬ß6.7.3/¬ß6.2.7)

### ¬ß6.7.6.2 Array declarators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: the element type of an array shall be a complete, non-function object type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S a[3]` with incomplete S, and array-of-function, both rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî Array of function type is forbidden. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî The optional `[` type-qualifier-list / `static` `]` content is permitted only on the outermost array derivation of a function parameter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[static 3]`/`int a[const 3]` accepted as a parameter; the same qualifiers/`static` on a non-parameter array declarator are rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî `static` and/or type qualifiers in an array declarator that is not a function parameter is a constraint violation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: if the size is a (non-`*`) expression it shall have integer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[3.0]` rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: if the size is an integer constant expression it shall have a value greater than zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects a negative size and, under `-pedantic-errors`, rejects a zero-size array ‚Äî "ISO C forbids zero-size array" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, which treat zero size as a GNU extension and reject it with `-pedantic-errors`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî Negative constant array size is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî `static` in an array parameter requires an explicit size expression (cannot be `[static]` alone). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p1 ‚Äî The `[*]` form (unspecified-size VLA) is allowed only where a declaration is a function prototype that is not part of a definition. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void f(int n,int a[*]);` accepted; `[*]` in a definition rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p2 ‚Äî Constraint: a size expression that is not an integer constant expression (a VLA) may appear only in a declarator with block scope or function-prototype scope; the declared object/typedef must have automatic storage (or be a prototype parameter). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p2 ‚Äî VLA forbidden at file scope. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p2 ‚Äî VLA forbidden with static storage duration (`static int a[n]`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p2 ‚Äî An identifier of variably modified type must have no linkage (`extern int a[n]` in a block is forbidden). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.7.6.2p2 ‚Äî A struct/union member shall not have a variably modified (VLA) type. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (clang hard-errors; mcc and gcc accept a VLA struct member as an extension by default and only reject it with -pedantic-errors ‚Äî note the gcc/clang consensus splits here)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p3 ‚Äî `[*]` denotes a VLA of unspecified size; usable only in prototype-scope declarators. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.7.6.2p3 ‚Äî A type-qualifier list and/or `static` between the brackets of the outermost array parameter qualifies/annotates the pointer the parameter is adjusted to. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc parses `int a[const 3]` but does NOT apply `const` to the adjusted `int *const a`; assigning to `a` is silently accepted, whereas gcc/clang reject it)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p3 ‚Äî `static` in `[static n]` is a guarantee that the argument provides access to at least n elements (an optimization hint; affects nullability/aliasing assumptions). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; semantic guarantee is informative, hint honored or ignored conformingly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p4 ‚Äî If the size is an expression that is not a constant expression: when evaluated at declaration time it must be > 0 (undefined behavior otherwise) and a new VLA type is built each time the declaration is reached. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB on non-positive run-time size, not a translation-time diagnostic)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2p5 ‚Äî The size expression of a VLA is evaluated exactly once, when control reaches the declaration; the resulting size is fixed for that array's lifetime even if `sizeof` is later applied. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe: side-effecting size function called once even with a later `sizeof`)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.2p6 ‚Äî For two array types to be compatible the element types must be compatible; if both have constant size the sizes must be equal (mismatch is undefined if one is in a separate translation unit). ‚Äî (spec; folds into ¬ß6.2.7 compatibility)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2 (jump constraint, ref ¬ß6.8.6.1) ‚Äî A `goto`/jump into the scope of an identifier with variably modified type is forbidden. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.2p7 ‚Äî Examples of array declarators (informative). ‚Äî (spec; examples)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.2 ‚Äî A pointer-to-VLA parameter such as `int (*a)[n]` (a variably modified, non-VLA type) is accepted in prototype scope. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.7.6.3 Function declarators (including prototypes)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p1 ‚Äî Constraint: a function's return (element) type shall not be an array type or a function type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both forms rejected via typedef)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p1 ‚Äî Function returning a function type is forbidden. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p2 ‚Äî Constraint: the only storage-class specifier allowed in a parameter declaration is `register`; any other (static/extern/auto/typedef) is a violation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`register int a` accepted; `static int a` rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p3 ‚Äî Constraint: an identifier list (old-style names without types) in a function declarator that is not part of that function's definition shall be empty. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects `int f(a,b);` ‚Äî "parameter names (without types) in function declaration" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, which reject a non-empty identifier list outside a definition)
- [~] ¬ß6.7.6.3p4 ‚Äî A parameter declared with array type is adjusted to "(qualified) pointer to element type", taking any qualifiers/`static` from the outermost `[...]`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (adjustment to pointer works ‚Äî `sizeof` of an `int a[10]` parameter yields pointer size ‚Äî but mcc drops the bracket qualifiers, see p3 of ¬ß6.7.6.2)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p4 ‚Äî `sizeof` an array parameter gives the size of the adjusted pointer, not the original array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (clang additionally warns -Wsizeof-array-argument)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p5 ‚Äî A parameter declared with function type is adjusted to "pointer to function". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void f(int g(void))` ‚Äî `g()` callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p6 ‚Äî If the declarator has a parameter type list, the function has a prototype and the listed types specify the parameter types; the list also fixes whether the function is variadic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p7 ‚Äî A parameter list consisting of the single keyword `void` (unnamed, unqualified) means the function takes no parameters; calling it with arguments is an error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p7 ‚Äî The special `void` parameter must be unnamed: `f(void x)` is invalid. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p7 ‚Äî The special `void` parameter may not be qualified: `f(const void)` is invalid. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p7 ‚Äî `void` may not be combined with any other parameter: `f(void,int)` is invalid. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p8 ‚Äî `,` `...` (ellipsis) declares a variadic function; the ellipsis must follow at least one named/typed parameter (no parameter may follow it). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc rejects a bare `int f(...)`; clang rejects too; gcc accepts it by default as a C23-style extension and only diagnoses with -pedantic; `int f(int,...)` accepted by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p9 ‚Äî Each parameter's declared type is adjusted as in p4/p5; after adjustment the parameter type list gives the function's parameter types, used to check call arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p10 ‚Äî The (obsolescent) identifier-list form names parameters whose types come from the following declaration list in the definition; absent declarations the type defaults (no prototype). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int f(a,b) int a; int b; {...}` accepted; clang warns it is deprecated)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p11 ‚Äî An empty parameter list `()` in a declaration that is not part of a definition specifies no information about the number/types of parameters (no prototype). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p12 ‚Äî In an identifier-list definition, each declared parameter's type after default-argument-promotion considerations forms the type used; the function has no prototype. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p13 ‚Äî For a prototype, declarations of the same function (including any later identifier-list definition) must have compatible/agreeing adjusted parameter types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void f(int a[3]); void f(int *a){...}` ‚Äî array param agrees with pointer param)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.3p14 ‚Äî The identifier-list (old-style) function declarator form is an obsolescent feature. ‚Äî (spec; obsolescence note, not a diagnosable rule ‚Äî clang chooses to warn -Wdeprecated-non-prototype)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.3p15 ‚Äî Two function types are compatible only if return types are compatible and (when both have prototypes) the parameter counts and corresponding adjusted parameter types agree, with default-promotion compatibility rules for prototype-vs-non-prototype. ‚Äî (spec; folds into ¬ß6.2.7/¬ß6.7.3 compatibility, exercised under those clauses)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.6.3p16 ‚Äî `restrict` may qualify only a pointer-to-object parameter (or the pointer an array parameter is adjusted to); on a non-pointer it is invalid. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int *restrict p` accepted; `restrict int x` rejected)
- [ ] ¬ß6.7.6.3p17+ ‚Äî Examples of function declarators (informative). ‚Äî (spec; examples)


## ¬ß6.7.7-¬ß6.7.9 Type names/typedef/initialization

> mcc status: 78 TODOs covering ¬ß6.7.7 (type names), ¬ß6.7.8 (typedef), ¬ß6.7.9 (initialization); 1 mcc-gap ‚Äî a single-expression init of incompatible struct/union type at block scope is rejected with a misleading parse-level message (diagnostic-quality only, ¬ß6.7.9p13). mcc now diagnoses a typedef-name/ordinary-identifier same-scope collision (`typedef int T; int T;`), redundant braces around a scalar initializer (`int y = {{5}};`), and C99 designated initializers used under `-std=c89 -pedantic-errors`, all matching gcc/clang. Everything else (the full type-name grammar including `[*]` and `static`-array forms, the typedef EXAMPLEs, and every Initialization EXAMPLE 1‚Äì13 including brace elision, designators, both-ends overlap-override, UTF-8/char16/char32 string init, and C11 padding-zero) matches the gcc==clang consensus.

> **Numbering note.** These are the **C11 (N1570)** section numbers. In **C99 (N1256)** the same three sections are numbered **¬ß6.7.6 (Type names)**, **¬ß6.7.7 (Type definitions)**, **¬ß6.7.8 (Initialization)**. The *paragraph* numbers within each section are identical between C99 and C11, so citations below give the C11 section number plus the shared paragraph number; the C99 section number is noted in each heading. Content divergences are tagged inline `(C11)` for C11-only text and `(C99-only)` for wording C11 changed/removed.

### ¬ß6.7.7 Type names (C99 ¬ß6.7.6)

> No material C99‚ÜîC11 divergence in this subsection; the grammar and the EXAMPLE are identical (both already include the `[ * ]` unspecified-VLA form and the `static`/qualifier array forms introduced in C99).

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse a *type-name* as `specifier-qualifier-list abstract-declarator_opt` (a declaration specifier list with no storage-class/`inline`, optionally followed by an abstract declarator). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse an *abstract-declarator* as either `pointer` alone, or `pointer_opt direct-abstract-declarator`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse a parenthesized *direct-abstract-declarator*: `( abstract-declarator )`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse the array *direct-abstract-declarator* `direct-abstract-declarator_opt [ type-qualifier-list_opt assignment-expression_opt ]` (abstract array of unknown or sized extent). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse the `static` array forms in a type name: `[ static type-qualifier-list_opt assignment-expression ]` and `[ type-qualifier-list static assignment-expression ]`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[static 3]`, `int a[const static 3]`, `int a[static const 3]` all accepted in prototype scope)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse the unspecified-size VLA array form `direct-abstract-declarator_opt [ * ]` in a type name (e.g. `int (*)[*]`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three accept in function-prototype scope and all three correctly reject `[*]` in block scope per ¬ß6.7.6.2p4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p1 ‚Äî Parse the function *direct-abstract-declarator* `direct-abstract-declarator_opt ( parameter-type-list_opt )`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.7.7p2 ‚Äî Treat a type name (used in any context that requires naming a type) as syntactically a declaration of a function or object of that type with the identifier omitted. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p2 (fn 147) ‚Äî Interpret empty parentheses in a type name as "function with no parameter specification", not as redundant parentheses around the omitted identifier (so `int *()` is "function returning `int *`", not `int *`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(int *(*)())` parses `int *()` as a function type)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.7p3 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî Derive the canonical example types exactly: `int` ‚Üí `int`; `int *` ‚Üí pointer to int; `int *[3]` ‚Üí array of 3 pointers to int; `int (*)[3]` ‚Üí pointer to array of 3 ints; `int (*)[*]` ‚Üí pointer to VLA-of-unspecified-size of int; `int *()` ‚Üí function (unspecified params) returning pointer to int; `int (*)(void)` ‚Üí pointer to function (no params) returning int; `int (*const [])(unsigned int, ...)` ‚Üí array of unknown size of `const` pointers to functions returning int that take one `unsigned int` and a variable number of further arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (every canonical spelling, incl. `int (*const [])(unsigned int, ...)`, accepted)

### ¬ß6.7.8 Type definitions / typedef (C99 ¬ß6.7.7)

> No material C99‚ÜîC11 divergence in this subsection (paragraph layout: p1 Syntax, p2 Constraint, p3 Semantics, p4‚Äìp8 EXAMPLEs 1‚Äì5).

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p1 (Syntax) ‚Äî Recognize a *typedef-name* as an `identifier` that was previously declared with the `typedef` storage-class specifier and is in scope. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p2 (Constraint) ‚Äî Require that a typedef name specifying a variably modified type has block scope (reject file-scope variably-modified typedefs). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects `int n=5; typedef int VLA[n];` at file scope; accepts the same typedef at block scope)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p3 ‚Äî In a declaration whose storage-class specifier is `typedef`, define each declarator's identifier as a typedef name denoting the type specified for that identifier per the declarator rules of ¬ß6.7.6 (C99: ¬ß6.7.5). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p3 ‚Äî Treat a `typedef` declaration as introducing only a synonym for the specified type, **not** a new (distinct) type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`typedef int MILES; int *p; MILES *q; p = q;` accepted ‚Äî type-identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p3 ‚Äî Given `typedef T type_ident; type_ident D;`, give the identifier in `D` the type "derived-declarator-type-list `T`", where the derived-declarator-type-list comes from the declarators of `D` and `T` is the type from the declaration specifiers. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p3 ‚Äî Place a typedef name in the **same name space** as other identifiers declared in ordinary declarators (so a typedef name and an ordinary identifier of the same name in the same scope collide, and an inner ordinary declaration shadows an outer typedef name). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects `typedef int T; int T;` at the same scope ‚Äî "'T' redeclared as different kind of symbol" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, which error "redeclared/redefinition as different kind of symbol". The shadowing half works too ‚Äî inner `int T;` correctly shadows an outer typedef `T` on all three.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p3 ‚Äî Re-evaluate any VLA size expressions in a typedef declarator **each time** the typedef declaration is reached in order of execution (and re-fix the array length each such time). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (size captured at each execution of the typedef; see p8 below)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p4 (EXAMPLE 1) ‚Äî Accept multiple declarators per `typedef` and typedef'd function/struct types, e.g. `typedef int MILES, KLICKSP();` (KLICKSP = "function with no parameter specification returning int") and `typedef struct { double hi, lo; } range;`; and treat objects of a typedef'd arithmetic type as compatible with any other object of the underlying type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`KLICKSP f; int f(){...}` definable through the typedef)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p5 (EXAMPLE 2) ‚Äî Permit a typedef name for an as-yet-incomplete tagged type (`typedef struct tnode TNODE;` before `struct tnode` is completed), allow it inside the struct's own member declarations (`TNODE *left, *right;`), and treat objects declared via the typedef as compatible with / synonymous for the underlying tagged type (`TNODE s, *sp;` ‚â° `struct tnode`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p6 (EXAMPLE 3) ‚Äî Keep a typedef name visible as a type where it interacts with specifiers/qualifiers: in a struct, `unsigned t:4;` makes a type *specifier* shadow typedef `t` so `t` is a member name, whereas `const t:5;` is a *qualifier* applied to the still-visible typedef `t` (an unnamed bit-field), and `plain r:5;` uses typedef `plain`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (the full EXAMPLE 3 struct compiles and `.t` is addressable as a member)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p7 (EXAMPLE 4) ‚Äî Make typedef'd function-type spellings denote exactly the same type as the fully written-out declaration, so the three `signal` declarations (`void (*signal(int, void (*)(int)))(int);`, `fv *signal(int, fv *);`, `pfv signal(int, pfv);`, with `typedef void fv(int), (*pfv)(int);`) are type-identical. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three spellings of `signal` coexist without "conflicting types")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.8p8 (EXAMPLE 5) ‚Äî Fix the length of a variable length array **typedef** at the time the typedef name is *defined*, not each time it is used (the value of `n` captured when `typedef int B[n];` executes governs all later uses of `B`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`typedef int B[n]; n+=1; B a;` ‚Üí `sizeof a` uses the original `n`; all three print 3)

### ¬ß6.7.9 Initialization (C99 ¬ß6.7.8)

> **C99‚ÜîC11 differences in this subsection:** C11 broadened "static storage duration" to "**static or thread** storage duration" throughout p4/p10; changed p3's "an object type" to "a **complete** object type"; in p14 allows a **UTF-8 string literal** (`u8"..."`) and says "successive **bytes**" (C99: "characters"); in p15 allows arrays compatible with **`char16_t`/`char32_t`** (initialized by `u"..."`/`U"..."`) in addition to `wchar_t`/`L"..."`; and in p10 added the requirement that **padding bits/bytes be initialized to zero** for default-initialized static/thread aggregates and unions.

#### Syntax

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p1 ‚Äî Accept an *initializer* that is an `assignment-expression`, `{ initializer-list }`, or `{ initializer-list , }` (trailing comma permitted). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[]={1,2,3,};` and `struct{int x,y;}s={1,2,};` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p1 ‚Äî Accept an *initializer-list* of `designation_opt initializer` items separated by commas. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p1 ‚Äî Accept a *designation* as a *designator-list* followed by `=`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p1 ‚Äî Accept a *designator-list* as one or more *designator*s in sequence (no separators). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`[1].a[0] = 2`, `.d.c = 3` chains accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p1 ‚Äî Accept a *designator* of the form `[ constant-expression ]` (array element) or `. identifier` (member). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p1 (C99 feature gate) ‚Äî Treat designated initializers as a C99-and-later feature, diagnosing them under a strict C90 mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-std=c89 -pedantic-errors` mcc rejects `int a[3]={[1]=2};` ‚Äî "designated initializers are a C99 feature"; gcc errors "ISO C90 forbids specifying subobject to initialize" and clang errors "designated initializers are a C99 feature")

#### Constraints

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p2 ‚Äî Reject any initializer that attempts to provide a value for an object **not contained within** the entity being initialized (e.g. more initializers than an aggregate has subobjects, or a string literal longer than a sized array ‚Äî diagnose; cf. p29 EXAMPLE 6's "a diagnostic message would have been issued"). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all diagnose; **note divergence in severity:** mcc treats excess array/aggregate initializers as a hard **error** and rejects, whereas gcc/clang emit a *warning* and accept ‚Äî both satisfy the "issue a diagnostic" requirement. Over-long string-into-sized-array warns on all three.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p3 ‚Äî Require the type of the initialized entity to be an array of unknown size or a complete object type `(C11; C99-only: "an object type")` that is **not** a variable length array type (reject initializing a VLA, and `(C11)` reject initializing an incomplete non-array object type). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc errors "variable length array cannot be initialized" and "initialization of incomplete type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p4 ‚Äî Require every expression in an initializer for an object of **static or thread** `(C11; C99-only: "static")` storage duration to be a constant expression or a string literal. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc errors "initializer element is not constant" for `static int s = g();`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p5 ‚Äî Reject any initializer on a block-scope declaration of an identifier that has external or internal linkage (e.g. a local `extern int x = 1;`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects with a parse-level "';' expected"; gcc/clang give the semantic "block scope identifier with linkage cannot have an initializer" ‚Äî a diagnostic is issued on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p6 ‚Äî For a `[ constant-expression ]` designator, require the current object to have array type and the constant expression to be an integer constant expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc errors "array type expected" for `.`-on-array and "integer constant expression must have integer type" for `[1.0]`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p6 ‚Äî Permit any nonnegative index value in a `[ constant-expression ]` designator when the array is of unknown size. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[]={[100]=1};` accepted; negative `[-1]` rejected on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p7 ‚Äî For a `. identifier` designator, require the current object to have structure or union type and the identifier to name a member of that type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc errors "field not found: nope" and rejects `.`-designator on a scalar)

#### Semantics ‚Äî model

- ¬ß6.7.9p8 ‚Äî Treat an initializer as specifying the initial value stored in the object. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p9 ‚Äî Except where explicitly stated otherwise, do **not** let unnamed members of structure/union objects participate in initialization, and leave them with indeterminate value even after the object is initialized. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (unnamed `int :0;` bit-field padding skipped; `{1,2}` lands in the two named members on all three)
- ¬ß6.7.9p10 ‚Äî Leave an object of automatic storage duration that is not explicitly initialized with an indeterminate value. ‚Äî (spec; UB on read, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p10 ‚Äî Default-initialize an unspecified-init static/thread `(C11; C99-only: "static")` object of **pointer** type to a null pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (static `int *sp;` reads as `(nil)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p10 ‚Äî Default-initialize an unspecified-init static/thread object of **arithmetic** type to (positive or unsigned) zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p10 ‚Äî Default-initialize an unspecified-init static/thread **aggregate** by initializing every member (recursively per these rules); `(C11)` and set every padding bit/byte to zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (static `struct{char c;int i;}` with internal padding compares byte-equal to an all-zero buffer via `memcmp`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p10 ‚Äî Default-initialize an unspecified-init static/thread **union** by initializing its first named member (recursively per these rules); `(C11)` and set every padding bit/byte to zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### Semantics ‚Äî scalars, strings, single-expression aggregates

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p11 ‚Äî Require a scalar's initializer to be a single expression, optionally enclosed in braces. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int x={5};` accepted everywhere; on the "optionally" boundary, `int y={{5}};` ‚Äî redundant extra braces around a scalar ‚Äî draws a warning from mcc at `-Wall` ("too many braces around scalar initializer"), as it does from gcc ("braces around scalar initializer") and clang ("too many braces around scalar initializer"). mcc produces the correct value.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p11 ‚Äî Set a scalar's initial value to the converted value of its initializer, applying the constraints and conversions of simple assignment, with the scalar's type taken as the *unqualified* version of its declared type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (covered by p24 EXAMPLE 1)
- ¬ß6.7.9p12 ‚Äî Apply the remaining rules (p13‚Äìp23) to objects of aggregate or union type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p13 ‚Äî Permit a structure/union object of automatic storage duration to be initialized either by a brace-enclosed initializer list, or by a single expression of compatible structure/union type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S b = a;` copy-init works; an *incompatible*-type single expression is rejected by all three ‚Äî mcc's block-scope diagnostic is a misleading parse-level "'{' expected", but it does reject)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p13 ‚Äî When a struct/union is initialized from a single compatible-type expression, set its initial value (including unnamed members) to that of the expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p14 ‚Äî Permit an array of character type (`char`, `signed char`, `unsigned char`) to be initialized by a character string literal `(C11: or a UTF-8 string literal u8"...")`, optionally enclosed in braces. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`char a[] = u8"abc";` and `char s[] = { "abc" };` both accepted, size 4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p14 ‚Äî Initialize that array's elements with successive bytes `(C11; C99-only: "characters")` of the string literal, including the terminating null character if there is room or if the array is of unknown size. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`char s[]="abc"` ‚Üí 4 bytes; `char t[3]="abc"` ‚Üí 3 bytes, null dropped, no diagnostic; a `char c[]=L"abc";` cross-type init is rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p15 ‚Äî Permit an array whose element type is compatible with a qualified/unqualified `wchar_t` `(C11: or char16_t or char32_t)` to be initialized by a wide string literal `(C11: with the matching prefix ‚Äî L for wchar_t, u for char16_t, U for char32_t)`, optionally enclosed in braces. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wchar_t w[]=L"abc"`, `char16_t a[]=u"abc"`, `char32_t b[]=U"abc"` all accepted; a *mismatched* prefix like `wchar_t w[]=u"abc";` is rejected on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p15 ‚Äî Initialize that array's elements with successive wide characters of the wide string literal, including the terminating null wide character if there is room or if the array is of unknown size. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### Semantics ‚Äî brace-enclosed lists, current object, designators

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p16 ‚Äî Otherwise (aggregate/union not initialized by string or single expression as above), require the initializer to be a brace-enclosed list of initializers for the elements or named members. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p17 ‚Äî Associate each brace-enclosed initializer list with a "current object". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (model verified through EXAMPLEs 5/6/11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p17 ‚Äî With no current designation, initialize subobjects of the current object in order according to its type: array elements in increasing subscript order, structure members in declaration order, and the first named member of a union. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p17 ‚Äî Make a designation start initialization at the subobject it describes, then continue forward in order beginning with the next subobject after the designated one. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[5]={[1]=10,20,30};` ‚Üí indices 1,2,3 get 10,20,30, rest zero)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p17 (fn 148) ‚Äî When a subaggregate's/contained-union's initializer does not begin with a left brace, initialize its subobjects as usual but do **not** make that subaggregate/union a current object (current objects associate only with brace-enclosed lists). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct{int a[2];int b;}s={1,2,3};` ‚Üí a={1,2}, b=3 ‚Äî flat list flows into and out of the sub-array)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p17 (fn 149) ‚Äî After a union member is initialized, treat the next object as the next subobject of the object *containing* the union, not the next member of the union. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct{union{int a;char b;}u;int c;}s={{5},7};` ‚Üí u.a=5, c=7)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p18 ‚Äî Begin each designator list at the current object associated with the closest surrounding brace pair. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p18 ‚Äî For each designator in the list (in order), select the named/indexed member of the current object and make it the current object for the next designator; the object at the end of the list is the subobject initialized by the following initializer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`.d.c = 3` selects nested member)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p18 (fn 150) ‚Äî Permit a designator to specify a strict subobject of the aggregate/union associated with the surrounding brace pair, and treat each separate designator list as independent. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`{1, .d.c=3, .d.b=2}` initializes independent nested members)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p19 ‚Äî Perform initialization in initializer-list order, each initializer for a given subobject overriding any previously listed initializer for the same subobject. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[3]={[0]=1,[1]=2,[0]=9};` ‚Üí a[0]=9)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p19 ‚Äî Implicitly initialize every subobject not explicitly initialized the same as objects of static storage duration (zero/null fill of un-designated/missing subobjects). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p19 (fn 151) ‚Äî Permit not evaluating at all an initializer for a subobject that is subsequently overridden (and thus never used to initialize that subobject). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (this is a *permission*: mcc conformingly chooses to **still evaluate** the overridden side effect ‚Äî `{[0]=f(),[0]=2}` calls `f` once on mcc, zero times on gcc/clang ‚Äî all three are conforming since the footnote only permits, never requires, skipping)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p20 ‚Äî Apply the brace/elision rules recursively when an aggregate/union contains aggregate or union elements/members. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p20 ‚Äî When a subaggregate's/contained-union's initializer begins with a left brace, initialize that subaggregate/union from the initializers enclosed by that brace and its matching right brace. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (EXAMPLE 4 `{ {1},{2},{3},{4} }`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p20 ‚Äî When a subaggregate's/contained-union's initializer does **not** begin with a left brace (brace elision), take only enough initializers from the list to account for the subaggregate's elements / the union's first member, leaving the rest to initialize the next element or member of the enclosing aggregate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (EXAMPLE 6 `short q[4][3][2]={{1},{2,3},{4,5,6}}` brace-elides correctly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p21 ‚Äî When a brace-enclosed list has fewer initializers than the aggregate has elements/members (or a string literal has fewer characters than a known-size array has elements), initialize the remainder implicitly the same as static-storage objects (partial-init zero fill). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[5]={1,2}` and `struct{int x,y,z;}s={1}` zero-fill the tail)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p22 ‚Äî Determine the size of an array of unknown size from the largest indexed element that has an explicit initializer, and complete the array type at the end of its initializer list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int a[]={[10]=1,[3]=2};` ‚Üí `sizeof` is 11 ints)
- ¬ß6.7.9p23 ‚Äî Treat the evaluations of the initializer-list expressions as indeterminately sequenced with respect to one another, so the order in which their side effects occur is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified behavior, not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.7.9p23 (fn 152) ‚Äî Do not require the evaluation order of initializer expressions to match the order of subobject initialization. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified behavior, not separately testable)

#### Semantics ‚Äî examples (normative behavior illustrated)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p24 (EXAMPLE 1) ‚Äî Apply scalar-assignment conversion in initializers: `int i = 3.5;` yields 3; `double complex c = 5 + 3 * I;` yields 5.0 + i3.0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (prints `3 5.0 3.0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p25 (EXAMPLE 2) ‚Äî Size `int x[] = { 1, 3, 5 };` as a 3-element array from its three initializers. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p26 (EXAMPLE 3) ‚Äî Handle fully bracketed multidimensional init for `int y[4][3]` with trailing rows zero-filled, and treat the equivalent minimally bracketed flat list as identical. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`y` and the flat-list `z` compare element-equal; `y[3][0]==0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p27 (EXAMPLE 4) ‚Äî Initialize only the first column from `int z[4][3] = { {1},{2},{3},{4} };` and zero-fill the rest. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p28 (EXAMPLE 5) ‚Äî Handle inconsistently bracketed init `struct { int a[3], b; } w[] = { {1}, 2 };` ‚Üí `w[0].a[0]==1`, `w[1].a[0]==2`, all other members zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (prints `2 1 0 2 0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p29 (EXAMPLE 6) ‚Äî Handle incompletely-but-consistently bracketed nested init for `short q[4][3][2]` (brace elision consuming up to six items per `[3][2]` subaggregate), and issue a diagnostic if any subaggregate's brace-enclosed list supplies more initializers than that subaggregate has subobjects. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (correct elision; mcc *errors* on the over-full sub-brace `{1,2,3,4,5,6,7}` while gcc/clang *warn* ‚Äî all issue the required diagnostic)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p31 (EXAMPLE 7) ‚Äî Complete an array type given via a block-scope incomplete-array typedef `typedef int A[];` used as `A a = {1,2}, b = {3,4,5};`, identical to `int a[] = {1,2}, b[] = {3,4,5};` (independent sizes 2 and 3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (prints `2 3`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p32 (EXAMPLE 8) ‚Äî Make `char s[] = "abc";` a 4-element modifiable array (incl. `'\0'`); make `char t[3] = "abc";` a 3-element array (null dropped, no diagnostic); make `char *p = "abc";` point to a string-literal array whose modification is undefined behavior. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof s==4`, `sizeof t==3`, no diagnostic on `t`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p33 (EXAMPLE 9) ‚Äî Support array designators whose index is an enumeration constant (`[member_two] = ...`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p34 (EXAMPLE 10) ‚Äî Support member designators in any order (`div_t answer = { .quot = 2, .rem = -1 };`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p35 (EXAMPLE 11) ‚Äî Support mixed/compound designators such as `struct { int a[3], b; } w[] = { [0].a = {1}, [1].a[0] = 2 };`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (prints `2 1 2`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p36 (EXAMPLE 12) ‚Äî Support "allocate from both ends" via a single trailing designator, `int a[MAX] = { 1,3,5,7,9, [MAX-5] = 8,6,4,2,0 };`, with later overlapping initializers overriding earlier ones (so the result depends on `MAX`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`MAX=10` ‚Üí `1 3 5 7 9 8 6 4 2 0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p38 (EXAMPLE 13) ‚Äî Support initializing any named member of a union via a designator (`union { ... } u = { .any_member = 42 };`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`{.l=42}` ‚Üí `u.l==42`)

#### Added gaps / edge cases not in the consolidated draft

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p11 (redundant-brace diagnostic) ‚Äî Diagnose redundant braces surrounding a scalar initializer (`int y = {{5}};`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc warns at `-Wall` ‚Äî "too many braces around scalar initializer" ‚Äî as do gcc/clang. Value is still correct.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p2 (excess-initializer severity) ‚Äî Diagnose an aggregate/string initializer that supplies more elements than the object has subobjects. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì **(divergence: mcc makes this a hard error and rejects; gcc/clang downgrade it to a warning and accept. The standard only requires "a diagnostic", which all three satisfy, but mcc is the strictest ‚Äî code that gcc/clang compile-with-warning will fail to compile on mcc.)**
- [~] ¬ß6.7.9p13 (incompatible single-expression diagnostic quality) ‚Äî Report a clear type error when a struct/union is initialized from a single expression of incompatible struct/union type. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì **(GAP-ish: mcc rejects but with a misleading parse-level message ("'{' expected (got ';')") instead of an "incompatible type" diagnostic; gcc/clang give the precise semantic error. It does reject, so it is conforming, but the diagnostic is low quality.)**
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9 (empty-brace initializer `{}`) ‚Äî Accept/handle the empty brace-enclosed initializer list `int a[3] = {};` (C23 ¬ß6.7.10 / pre-C23 GNU extension; **not** valid ISO C99/C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì **(All three accept it as an extension and zero-fill; note it is a constraint violation under strict C99/C11 and none of the three reject it even with `-std=c11`.)**
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.9p10 / ¬ß6.7.9p21 (static-storage zero/null fill is the partial-init rule) ‚Äî Confirm that a partially-initialized aggregate's missing subobjects (including nested pointers) get the *same* default as fully-default static objects (zero for arithmetic, null for pointers, recursively). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`static struct{int a;int *b;char c[4];}sa;` ‚Üí all members zero/null)


## ¬ß6.8 Statements and blocks

> mcc status: 81 TODO checkboxes below; 2 are mcc-gaps (mcc:‚úó/~ where it diverges from the gcc==clang consensus). Both ¬ß6.8.6.4p1 return-mismatch constraints ‚Äî a `void` function returning a value, or a non-`void` function returning nothing ‚Äî are hard errors by default in mcc (the `return-type`/`return-mismatch` warning is on+error by default), matching gcc 15 and clang 22. The mcc gaps are pedantic-only: mcc accepts the GNU `case 1 ... 5:` range and computed `goto *ptr` even under `-pedantic-errors`, where gcc/clang reject them. All structural syntax, all VLA-scope jump constraints, switch/loop/goto semantics, integer-promotion of `case` values, for-decl scoping, and aggregate-return aliasing match the consensus exactly.

> C99 vs C11: ¬ß6.8p3 lists the runtime semantics of declarations reached in execution order. ¬ß6.8p4 was rewritten between C99 and C11: C99 enumerates the kinds of full expression and ends each with a sequence point; C11 instead defines a full expression structurally, adds the variably-modified-type implicit full expression, and states the inter-full-expression sequence point (the latter migrated from Annex C / ¬ß5.1.2.3). The `for ( declaration ; ... )` form, VLAs, and intermixed declarations/statements in a block are all C99 additions absent from C90.

### ¬ß6.8 Statements and blocks (general)

- ¬ß6.8p1 ‚Äî A `statement` shall be one of: labeled-statement, compound-statement, expression-statement, selection-statement, iteration-statement, or jump-statement (syntax of the `statement` nonterminal). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.8p2 ‚Äî A statement specifies an action to be performed; except as indicated, statements are executed in sequence. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.8p3 ‚Äî A block allows a set of declarations and statements to be grouped into one syntactic unit. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8p3 ‚Äî The initializers of objects that have automatic storage duration, and the variable length array declarators of ordinary identifiers with block scope, are evaluated and the values stored in the objects (including storing an indeterminate value in objects without an initializer) each time the declaration is reached in the order of execution, as if it were a statement (the VLA-declarator evaluation is C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (backward `goto` over a block-scope VLA re-creates it each time the declaration is re-reached; runtime probe `vla=3` matches)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8p3 ‚Äî Within each declaration, the automatic initializers / VLA declarators are evaluated in the order in which the declarators appear. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`for(int i=0,j=10;...)` multi-declarator left-to-right matches)
- ¬ß6.8p4 ‚Äî A full expression is an expression that is not part of another expression, nor part of a declarator or abstract declarator (C11 structural definition; C99 worded it as "not part of another expression or of a declarator"). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.8p4 ‚Äî (C99-only enumeration) Each of the following is a full expression: an initializer; the expression in an expression statement; the controlling expression of a selection statement (`if` or `switch`); the controlling expression of a `while` or `do` statement; each of the optional expressions of a `for` statement; the optional expression in a `return` statement. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.8p4 ‚Äî (C11) There is also an implicit full expression in which the non-constant size expressions for a variably modified type are evaluated; within that full expression, the evaluation of different size expressions is unsequenced with respect to one another. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.8p4 ‚Äî The end of a full expression is a sequence point / there is a sequence point between the evaluation of a full expression and the evaluation of the next full expression to be evaluated (C99 phrases it as "the end of a full expression is a sequence point"; C11 phrases the inter-full-expression sequence point). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.8p5 ‚Äî (Forward references only, no normative requirement: expression and null statements ¬ß6.8.3, selection statements ¬ß6.8.4, iteration statements ¬ß6.8.5, the `return` statement ¬ß6.8.6.4.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.8.1 Labeled statements

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.1p1 ‚Äî A `labeled-statement` shall be one of: `identifier : statement`, `case constant-expression : statement`, or `default : statement` (syntax). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.1p2 ‚Äî Constraint: A `case` or `default` label shall appear only in a `switch` statement (further `case`/`default` constraints are in ¬ß6.8.4.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`case 3:` outside switch ‚áí mcc "switch expected")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.1p3 ‚Äî Constraint: Label names shall be unique within a function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`a: ; a: ;` ‚áí mcc "duplicate label 'a'")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.1p4 ‚Äî Any statement may be preceded by a prefix that declares an identifier as a label name; labels in themselves do not alter the flow of control, which continues unimpeded across them. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.1 (extension) ‚Äî GNU local labels `__label__ name;` declared at the head of a block. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (default); under `-pedantic-errors` mcc:‚úì clang:‚úì but gcc:‚úó rejects (no gcc==clang consensus, so not counted as an mcc gap)
- [~] ¬ß6.8.1 (constraint) ‚Äî A label may prefix a `statement` but a `declaration` is not a statement, so `lbl: int x;` is ill-formed in C99/C11. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (all three accept by default; all three reject under `-pedantic-errors`; mcc matches consensus)

### ¬ß6.8.2 Compound statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.2p1 ‚Äî A `compound-statement` is `{ block-item-list_opt }`, where a `block-item-list` is one or more `block-item`s and a `block-item` is a `declaration` or a `statement` (syntax; C99 permits declarations and statements to be intermixed within a block, whereas C90 required all declarations to precede statements). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (intermixed `int p; p+=3; int q=p*2;` ‚áí `mix=10`)
- ¬ß6.8.2p2 ‚Äî A compound statement is a block. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.8.3 Expression and null statements

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.3p1 ‚Äî An `expression-statement` is `expression_opt ;` (syntax). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.3p2 ‚Äî The expression in an expression statement is evaluated as a void expression for its side effects. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.8.3p2 (footnote) ‚Äî Such side-effect expressions are, e.g., assignments and function calls that have side effects (informative). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.3p3 ‚Äî A null statement (consisting of just a semicolon) performs no operations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.3p4 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE 1, informative) A null statement may be used as the loop body of an iteration statement whose work is done entirely in the controlling/`for` expressions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.3p5 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE 2, informative) A null statement may be used to carry a label immediately before the closing `}` of a compound statement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (a label with NO statement before `}` is accepted by default by all three but rejected by all three under `-pedantic-errors`; mcc matches consensus, rejecting it as "label at end of compound statement is a C23 feature")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.3p6 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE 3, informative) A null statement may be used as the body of a `while` whose controlling expression performs all the work (e.g. `while (*q++ = *p++) ;`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`while(s[len]) len++;` style ‚áí `len=3`)

### ¬ß6.8.4 Selection statements

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4p1 ‚Äî A `selection-statement` shall be one of: `if ( expression ) statement`, `if ( expression ) statement else statement`, or `switch ( expression ) statement` (syntax). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.8.4p2 ‚Äî A selection statement selects among a set of statements depending on the value of a controlling expression. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4p3 ‚Äî A selection statement is a block whose scope is a strict subset of the scope of its enclosing block, and each associated substatement is also a block whose scope is a strict subset of the scope of the selection statement (C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (each substatement is its own block scope)

### ¬ß6.8.4.1 The if statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.1p1 ‚Äî Constraint: The controlling expression of an `if` statement shall have scalar type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`if(struct)` ‚áí mcc rejects)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.1p2 ‚Äî In both forms, the first substatement is executed if the expression compares unequal to 0; in the `else` form, the second substatement is executed if the expression compares equal to 0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.1p2 ‚Äî If the first substatement is reached via a label, the second substatement is not executed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.1p3 ‚Äî An `else` is associated with the lexically nearest preceding `if` that is allowed by the syntax (dangling-else resolution). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`if(a) if(b) r=1; else r=2;` with a=1,b=0 ‚áí `dang=2`, else binds to inner)

### ¬ß6.8.4.2 The switch statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: The controlling expression of a `switch` statement shall have integer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`switch(double)` and `switch(float)` ‚áí mcc "switch value not an integer")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p2 ‚Äî Constraint: If a `switch` statement has an associated `case` or `default` label within the scope of an identifier with a variably modified type, the entire `switch` statement shall be within the scope of that identifier (C99 ‚Äî VLA interaction). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`case` inside a `{int a[n];}` block of the switch body ‚áí mcc "switch jumps into the scope of a variably modified declaration")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p3 ‚Äî Constraint: The expression of each `case` label shall be an integer constant expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`case y:` non-const ‚áí mcc "constant expression expected")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p3 ‚Äî Constraint: No two of the `case` constant expressions in the same `switch` statement shall have the same value after conversion. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both `case 1:` and `case (char)257:` (=1) ‚áí mcc "duplicate case value")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p3 ‚Äî Constraint: There shall be at most one `default` label in a `switch` statement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (two `default:` ‚áí mcc "too many 'default'")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p3 ‚Äî Constraint clarification: Any enclosed `switch` statement may have its own `default` label or `case` constant expressions that duplicate those of the enclosing `switch`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (nested switches with overlapping case/default accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p4 ‚Äî A `switch` statement causes control to jump to, into, or past the statement that is the switch body, depending on the value of the controlling expression and on the presence of a `default` label and the values of any `case` labels on or in the switch body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (fallthrough+default probe ‚áí `sw=221`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p4 ‚Äî A `case` or `default` label is accessible only within the closest enclosing `switch` statement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p5 ‚Äî The integer promotions are performed on the controlling expression, and the constant expression in each `case` label is converted to the promoted type of the controlling expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(char)257`‚Üí1 dup detection demonstrates conversion to promoted type)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p5 ‚Äî If a converted `case` value matches that of the promoted controlling expression, control jumps to the statement following the matched `case` label; otherwise, if there is a `default` label, control jumps to the labeled statement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p5 ‚Äî If no converted `case` constant expression matches and there is no `default` label, no part of the switch body is executed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.8.4.2p6 ‚Äî Implementation limits: As discussed in ¬ß5.2.4.1, the implementation may limit the number of `case` values in a `switch` statement. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2p7 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE, informative) Object declarations within a switch body are reachable but their initializers are not executed if jumped over (e.g. a VLA inside the switch body and a fall-through example). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (non-VLA decl jumped over is uninitialized but reachable; VLA decl in switch body is a ¬ß6.8.4.2p2 constraint error)
- [~] ¬ß6.8.4.2 (extension) ‚Äî GNU `case lo ... hi:` range labels. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all accept by default; **under `-pedantic-errors` mcc accepts but gcc/clang reject** ‚Äî mcc fails to diagnose the extension)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.4.2 (semantics) ‚Äî A `switch` may control an `enum`-typed expression (integer type). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.8.5 Iteration statements

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5p1 ‚Äî An `iteration-statement` shall be one of: `while ( expression ) statement`; `do statement while ( expression ) ;`; `for ( expression_opt ; expression_opt ; expression_opt ) statement`; or `for ( declaration expression_opt ; expression_opt ) statement` (syntax; the `for ( declaration ... )` form is C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5p2 ‚Äî Constraint: The controlling expression of an iteration statement shall have scalar type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`while(struct)` ‚áí mcc rejects)
- [~] ¬ß6.8.5p3 ‚Äî Constraint: The declaration part of a `for` statement shall only declare identifiers for objects having storage class `auto` or `register` (C99). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (all three accept `for(static int..)`, `for(extern int..)`, `for(typedef..)` by default; all three reject under `-pedantic-errors`; mcc matches consensus)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5p4 ‚Äî An iteration statement causes a statement called the loop body to be executed repeatedly until the controlling expression compares equal to 0; the repetition occurs regardless of whether the loop body is entered from the iteration statement or by a jump. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.8.5p4 (footnote) ‚Äî Code jumped over is not executed; in particular, the controlling expression of a `for` or `while` statement is not evaluated before entering the loop body via a jump, nor is clause-1 of a `for` statement (informative). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5p5 ‚Äî An iteration statement is a block whose scope is a strict subset of the scope of its enclosing block, and the loop body is also a block whose scope is a strict subset of the scope of the iteration statement (C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.8.5.1 The while statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5.1p1 ‚Äî The evaluation of the controlling expression takes place before each execution of the loop body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`while(w<3) w++` ‚áí `wh=3`)

### ¬ß6.8.5.2 The do statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5.2p1 ‚Äî The evaluation of the controlling expression takes place after each execution of the loop body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`do{c++;}while(0)` runs body once ‚áí `do=1`)

### ¬ß6.8.5.3 The for statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5.3p1 ‚Äî The statement `for ( clause-1 ; expression-2 ; expression-3 ) statement` behaves as specified in this subclause; `expression-2` is the controlling expression that is evaluated before each execution of the loop body, and `expression-3` is evaluated as a void expression after each execution of the loop body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`for(int i=0;i<5;i++) sum+=i` ‚áí `for=10`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5.3p1 ‚Äî If `clause-1` is a declaration, the scope of any identifiers it declares is the remainder of the declaration and the entire loop, including the other two expressions (C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (loop variable not visible after loop; multi-declarator `for(int i=0,j=10; i<j; i++,j--)` accepted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5.3p1 ‚Äî If `clause-1` is a declaration it is reached in the order of execution before the first evaluation of the controlling expression; if `clause-1` is an expression it is evaluated as a void expression before the first evaluation of the controlling expression (the declaration form is C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.8.5.3p1 (footnote) ‚Äî `clause-1` specifies loop initialization; `expression-2` specifies an evaluation made before each iteration such that execution continues until it compares equal to 0; `expression-3` specifies a per-iteration operation such as incrementing (informative). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.5.3p2 ‚Äî Both `clause-1` and `expression-3` can be omitted; an omitted `expression-2` is replaced by a nonzero constant (i.e. the loop does not terminate on the controlling expression). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`for(;;){...break;}` ‚áí `inf=7`)

### ¬ß6.8.6 Jump statements

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6p1 ‚Äî A `jump-statement` shall be one of: `goto identifier ;`, `continue ;`, `break ;`, or `return expression_opt ;` (syntax). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.8.6p2 ‚Äî A jump statement causes an unconditional jump to another place. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.8.6.1 The goto statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.1p1 ‚Äî Constraint: The identifier in a `goto` statement shall name a label located somewhere in the enclosing function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`goto nope;` undefined ‚áí mcc "label 'nope' used but not defined")
