- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.1p1 ‚Äî Constraint: A `goto` statement shall not jump from outside the scope of an identifier having a variably modified type to inside the scope of that identifier (C99 ‚Äî VLA jump restriction). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`goto` into a `{int a[n]; lbl:}` block ‚áí mcc "goto jumps into the scope of a variably modified declaration")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.1p2 ‚Äî A `goto` statement causes an unconditional jump to the statement prefixed by the named label in the enclosing function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.1p3 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE 1, informative) It is sometimes convenient to jump into the middle of a complicated set of statements; an array declared with a non-VLA bound may be jumped over while a VLA declarator may not, illustrating the ¬ß6.8.6.1p1 VLA constraint. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (jumping over a non-VLA array is allowed; jumping into a VLA's scope is rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.1p4 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE 2, informative) A `goto` may be used to jump back to before a block-scope VLA declaration, in which case the VLA's lifetime ends on the backward jump and the VLA is created anew when its declaration is re-reached. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (backward-`goto` VLA recreation runtime probe ‚áí `vla=3`)
- [~] ¬ß6.8.6.1 (extension) ‚Äî GNU computed goto `goto *expr;` with `&&label` address-of-label. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all accept by default; **under `-pedantic-errors` mcc accepts but gcc/clang reject** ‚Äî mcc fails to diagnose the extension)

### ¬ß6.8.6.2 The continue statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: A `continue` statement shall appear only in or as a loop body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`continue;` outside a loop ‚áí mcc "cannot continue")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.2p2 ‚Äî A `continue` statement causes a jump to the loop-continuation portion (the end) of the smallest enclosing iteration statement; unless the `continue` is in an enclosed iteration statement (in which case it is interpreted within that statement), it is equivalent to `goto contin;` placed just before the closing brace / `while` of the smallest enclosing `while`, `do`, or `for` loop body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (nested-loop `continue` affects only the inner loop ‚áí `cont=6`)
- ¬ß6.8.6.2p2 (footnote) ‚Äî Following the `contin:` label is a null statement (informative). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.8.6.3 The break statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.3p1 ‚Äî Constraint: A `break` statement shall appear only in or as a switch body or loop body. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`break;` outside ‚áí mcc "cannot break")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.3p2 ‚Äî A `break` statement terminates execution of the smallest enclosing `switch` or iteration statement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (nested-loop `break` terminates only the inner loop ‚áí `brk=303`)

### ¬ß6.8.6.4 The return statement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p1 ‚Äî Constraint: A `return` statement with an expression shall not appear in a function whose return type is `void`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void f(void){return 3;}` is a hard error by default in all three; mcc's `warn_return_type` is on+error by default, downgradable via `-Wno-error=return-type`/`-Wno-return-type`.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p1 ‚Äî Constraint: A `return` statement without an expression shall only appear in a function whose return type is `void`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int f(void){return;}` is a hard error by default in all three; see `-Wreturn-type`/`-Wreturn-mismatch`.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p1 (clarification) ‚Äî A `return` with a *void-typed* expression is permitted in a `void` function (e.g. `return g();` where `g` returns `void`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p2 ‚Äî A `return` statement terminates execution of the current function and returns control to its caller; a function may have any number of `return` statements. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p3 ‚Äî If a `return` statement with an expression is executed, the value of the expression is returned to the caller as the value of the function call expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p3 ‚Äî If the expression has a type different from the return type of the function in which it appears, the value is converted as if by assignment to an object having the return type of the function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double retd(){return 3;}`‚áí3.0; `unsigned char retc(){return 300;}`‚áí44)
- ¬ß6.8.6.4p3 (footnote) ‚Äî The `return` statement is not an assignment; the overlap restriction of simple assignment (¬ß6.5.16.1) does not apply to the case of function return (informative). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.8.6.4p4 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE, informative) The `return` expression's value behaves as if assigned to an unnamed object of the return type, so a returned value may alias an object passed by the caller without the simple-assignment overlap constraint applying. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`x = id(x)` with a struct argument ‚áí `1234`, no overlap diagnostic)


## ¬ß6.9 External definitions

> mcc status: 44 TODO checkboxes in this section; 4 are mcc-gaps (mcc diverges from the gcc==clang consensus). Gaps: a declaration-list entry with no declarator is accepted with only a warning (¬ß6.9.1p6); an undeclared/implicit-`int` old-style identifier-list parameter is accepted with only a warning (¬ß6.9.1p6 / C99 no-implicit-int, two rows); a file-scope declaration relying on implicit `int` is accepted with only a warning (¬ß6.9p1). mcc now rejects a function defined through a typedef'd function type (¬ß6.9.1p2), an incomplete return type in a definition (¬ß6.9.1p3), and an incomplete parameter type in a definition (¬ß6.9.1p7), and warns on a never-completed internal-linkage incomplete-array tentative definition (¬ß6.9.2p3), all matching the gcc==clang consensus. Constraints that mcc enforces correctly include file-scope `auto`/`register`, double definition, omitted prototype-parameter names (mcc rejects per C99/C11 where gcc/clang accept the C23 extension), and the multiple-/missing-external-definition link checks.

> Material C99‚ÜíC11 difference in this section: the "used in an expression" exclusions of ¬ß6.9p3 and ¬ß6.9p5 list only `sizeof` in C99, whereas C11 reads "`sizeof` or `_Alignof`". The parameter-adjustment cross-reference is ¬ß6.7.5.3 in C99 (N1256) and ¬ß6.7.6.3 in C11 (N1570).

### ¬ß6.9 External definitions (general)

Syntax:
- ¬ß6.9p1 ‚Äî A *translation-unit* is a sequence of *external-declaration*s: either a single *external-declaration*, or a *translation-unit* followed by an *external-declaration*. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p1 ‚Äî An *external-declaration* is either a *function-definition* or a *declaration*; no other forms are permitted to appear at file scope (outside any function). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (stray file-scope expression `3+4;` rejected by all three)

Constraints:
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p2 ‚Äî The storage-class specifiers `auto` and `register` shall not appear in the declaration specifiers in an external declaration. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects both `auto int x;` and `register int x;` at file scope)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p3 ‚Äî There shall be no more than one external definition for each identifier declared with internal linkage in a translation unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (two `static int x = ‚Ä¶;` defs rejected as "defined twice")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p3 ‚Äî If an identifier declared with internal linkage is used in an expression (other than as part of the operand of a `sizeof` operator, or in C11 a `sizeof` or `_Alignof` operator, whose result is an integer constant), there shall be exactly one external definition for the identifier in the translation unit. *(C11 adds `_Alignof` to the exclusion; C99 lists only `sizeof`.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (a `static` function used but never defined draws a "used but never defined"-class warning from mcc ("'f' used but never defined"), as it does from gcc/clang)

Semantics:
- ¬ß6.9p4 ‚Äî As discussed in 5.1.1.1, the unit of program text after preprocessing is a translation unit, which consists of a sequence of external declarations; these are described as "external" because they appear outside any function (and hence have file scope). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.9p4 ‚Äî As discussed in 6.7, a declaration that also causes storage to be reserved for an object or a function named by the identifier is a *definition*. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.9p5 ‚Äî An *external definition* is an external declaration that is also a definition of a function (other than an inline definition) or an object. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p5 ‚Äî If an identifier declared with external linkage is used in an expression (other than as part of the operand of a `sizeof` operator, or in C11 a `sizeof` or `_Alignof` operator, whose result is an integer constant), somewhere in the entire program there shall be exactly one external definition for the identifier; otherwise, there shall be no more than one. *(C11 adds `_Alignof` to the exclusion; C99 lists only `sizeof`.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (missing external def ‚Üí "unresolved reference" link error; two external defs of `int shared` ‚Üí "defined twice"; one def across two TUs links and runs rc=0)

### ¬ß6.9.1 Function definitions

Syntax:
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p1 ‚Äî A *function-definition* consists of *declaration-specifiers*, a *declarator*, an optional *declaration-list*, and a *compound-statement*, in that order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (well-formed definitions accepted; misordered forms rejected)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p1 ‚Äî A *declaration-list* is one *declaration*, or a *declaration-list* followed by a *declaration* (this is the K&R/old-style parameter declaration list; identifier-list function definitions are an obsolescent feature, ¬ß6.11.7). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int f(x) int x; { ‚Ä¶ }` accepted; gcc/clang warn old-style)

Constraints:
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p2 ‚Äî The identifier declared in a function definition (the name of the function) shall have a function type, as specified by the declarator portion of the function definition. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`typedef int FT(void); FT g { return 1; }` ‚Äî mcc rejects a definition whose function type comes from a typedef rather than the declarator ("function definition declared with a typedef'd function type"), as do gcc/clang, because the declarator portion does not specify a function type)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p3 ‚Äî The return type of a function shall be `void` or a complete object type other than array type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (array return `int f()[3]` and typedef'd-array return rejected by all three; `struct S; struct S f(void){ }` ‚Äî mcc rejects a definition returning an incomplete struct ("return type is an incomplete type"), as do gcc/clang ("incomplete result type"))
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p4 ‚Äî The storage-class specifier, if any, in the declaration specifiers shall be either `extern` or `static`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc rejects `auto`/`register`/`typedef` function definitions; clang rejects too; gcc accepts `auto int f(){‚Ä¶}` with only a warning)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p5 ‚Äî If the declarator includes a parameter type list, the declaration of each parameter shall include an identifier, except for the special case of a parameter list consisting of a single parameter of type `void`, in which case there shall not be an identifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects the unnamed parameter `int f(int, int y){‚Ä¶}` per the C99/C11 constraint ‚Äî gcc/clang now *accept* it as a C23 extension with a `-Wc23-extensions` note; mcc also rejects the named `void` parameter `int f(void v)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p5 ‚Äî If the declarator includes a parameter type list, no declaration list shall follow (the parameter-type-list and identifier-list forms are mutually exclusive). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int f(int x) int x; {‚Ä¶}` rejected by all three)
- [‚úó] ¬ß6.9.1p6 ‚Äî If the declarator includes an identifier list, each declaration in the declaration list shall have at least one declarator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (**gap**: `int f(x) int; { return x; }` ‚Äî mcc accepts with only a "useless type defines no instances" warning; gcc/clang reject "declaration does not declare a parameter")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p6 ‚Äî If the declarator includes an identifier list, those declarators shall declare only identifiers from the identifier list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int f(x) int x; int z; {‚Ä¶}` rejected ‚Äî "declaration for parameter 'z' but no such parameter")
- [‚úó] ¬ß6.9.1p6 ‚Äî If the declarator includes an identifier list, every identifier in the identifier list shall be declared. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (**gap, see added item below**: `int f(x){ return x; }` ‚Äî mcc accepts with "type of 'x' defaults to 'int'" warning; gcc/clang reject the implicit `int` per C99)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p6 ‚Äî An identifier declared as a typedef name shall not be redeclared as a parameter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`typedef int T; int f(T) int T; {‚Ä¶}` rejected by all three ‚Äî the identifier-list slot `T` is a type name, parse error)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p6 ‚Äî The declarations in the declaration list shall contain no storage-class specifier other than `register`, and no initializers. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`static int x` in decl-list rejected; initializer `int x = 5;` in decl-list rejected; `register int x;` accepted)

Semantics:
- ¬ß6.9.1p7 ‚Äî The declarator in a function definition specifies the name of the function being defined and the identifiers of its parameters. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p7 ‚Äî If the declarator includes a parameter type list, the list also specifies the types of all the parameters; such a declarator also serves as a function prototype for later calls to the same function in the same translation unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (after `int f(int a,int b){‚Ä¶}`, the call `f(1)` is rejected "too few arguments" by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p7 ‚Äî If the declarator includes an identifier list, the types of the parameters shall be declared in a following declaration list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (covered by the identifier-list/decl-list probes above)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p7 ‚Äî In either case, the type of each parameter is adjusted as described in 6.7.6.3 (C99: 6.7.5.3) for a parameter type list, and the resulting type shall be a complete object type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct S; int f(struct S s){‚Ä¶}` ‚Äî mcc rejects an incomplete parameter type in a definition ("parameter 's' has incomplete type"), as do gcc/clang ("parameter has incomplete type"))
- ¬ß6.9.1p8 ‚Äî If a function that accepts a variable number of arguments is defined without a parameter type list that ends with the ellipsis notation, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p9 ‚Äî Each parameter has automatic storage duration; its identifier is an lvalue. *(Footnote: a parameter is in effect declared at the head of the compound statement that constitutes the function body.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (parameter is a modifiable lvalue: `int f(int x){ x = 5; return x; }` accepted; redeclaring the parameter at the top block level `int f(int x){ int x; ‚Ä¶ }` rejected "redeclaration of 'x'" by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p10 ‚Äî On entry to the function, the size expressions of each variably modified parameter are evaluated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (VLA parameter `int f(int n, int a[n]){‚Ä¶}` accepted by all three)
- [ ] ¬ß6.9.1p10 ‚Äî On entry to the function, the value of each argument expression is converted to the type of the corresponding parameter as if by assignment. ‚Äî (spec; runtime semantics ‚Äî exercised indirectly by call/return tests, not separately diagnosed)
- ¬ß6.9.1p10 ‚Äî A function may change the values of its parameters, but these changes cannot affect the values of the arguments (parameters are passed by value). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p10 ‚Äî A parameter declared to have array or function type is adjusted to have, respectively, a pointer-to-element or pointer-to-function type as described in 6.7.6.3 (C99: 6.7.5.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (array/function parameters compile and behave as the adjusted pointer types)
- ¬ß6.9.1p11 ‚Äî After all parameters have been assigned, the compound statement that constitutes the body of the function definition is executed. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ß6.9.1p12 ‚Äî If the `}` that terminates a function is reached, and the value of the function call is used by the caller, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (UB, not a constraint; `int f(void){ } ‚Ä¶ return f();` compiles on all three ‚Äî mcc warns "might return no value", clang warns "non-void function does not return a value", gcc is silent at default warning level)

### ¬ß6.9.2 External object definitions

Semantics:
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.2p1 ‚Äî If the declaration of an identifier for an object has file scope and an initializer, the declaration is an external definition for the identifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (an initialized file-scope object plus tentative defs of the same name link to one definition; two *initialized* file-scope defs of the same name are rejected "redefinition")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.2p2 ‚Äî A declaration of an identifier for an object that has file scope without an initializer, and without a storage-class specifier or with the storage-class specifier `static`, constitutes a *tentative definition*. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int x; int x; int x = 5;` ‚Äî repeated tentative defs plus one real def accepted by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.2p2 ‚Äî If a translation unit contains one or more tentative definitions for an identifier, and the translation unit contains no external definition for that identifier, then the behavior is exactly as if the translation unit contains a file scope declaration of that identifier, with the composite type as of the end of the translation unit, with an initializer equal to `0`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (tentative-only objects are emitted as zero-initialized definitions and link/run correctly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.2p3 ‚Äî If the declaration of an identifier for an object is a tentative definition and has internal linkage, the declared type shall not be an incomplete type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (incomplete *struct* `static struct S s;` rejected by all three; for an incomplete *array* `static int arr[];` that is never completed, mcc emits an "array 'arr' assumed to have one element" warning, as do gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.2p2 (EXAMPLE 2, illustrative) ‚Äî A tentatively-defined object whose declared type is an incomplete array (e.g. `int i[];` with external linkage) that is still incomplete at end of translation unit is completed by the implicit `= 0` initializer to a one-element array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int i[];` accepted by all three; gcc/clang add a "assumed to have one element" warning, mcc accepts silently ‚Äî both are conforming, the warning is optional)

### Added gaps and edge cases (not in the consolidated draft)

- [‚úó] ¬ß6.9.1p6 / ¬ß6.7.2p2 (C99 removed implicit `int`) ‚Äî An undeclared old-style identifier-list parameter (`int f(x){ return x; }`) must be diagnosed: C99/C11 removed implicit `int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (**gap**: mcc accepts with a "type of 'x' defaults to 'int'" warning; gcc and clang reject ‚Äî clang: "ISO C99 and later do not support implicit int")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.2p3 (incomplete-array internal-linkage tentative def, never completed) ‚Äî `static int arr[];` with no later completion is a constraint violation (internal linkage + incomplete type). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (mcc warns "array 'arr' assumed to have one element" before completing it to a one-element array, as do gcc/clang ("array assumed to have one element"))
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p2 ‚Äî A function defined with no storage class, `extern`, or `static` keyword but with the function type supplied entirely by a typedef in the declaration-specifiers is ill-formed (the declarator must specify the function type). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (same root cause as the p2 item above; mcc rejects `FT g { ‚Ä¶ }`, matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p3 ‚Äî A definition returning a function type (e.g. via typedef) must be rejected (return type must be a complete *object* type or `void`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (the typedef-function-type construct that would express this is itself rejected at the syntax level by all three)
- [~] ¬ß6.9p1 / ¬ß6.7 (implicit-`int` external declaration) ‚Äî A file-scope declaration with no type specifier (e.g. `x;` or `f(){‚Ä¶}` with no return type) relies on implicit `int`, removed in C99. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `int f(){return 0;}` with empty K&R parens compiles everywhere; bare implicit-`int` object declarations are accepted by mcc with a warning where C99 requires a diagnostic ‚Äî borderline, mcc's default leans permissive)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9.1p5 ‚Äî Omitting a parameter name in a prototype-form definition (`int f(int){‚Ä¶}`) is a C99/C11 constraint violation but a C23 feature; a strictly-C11 compiler should diagnose it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (mcc correctly rejects under C99/C11 semantics; gcc/clang accept it as a forward-looking C23 extension, only noting `-Wc23-extensions`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p5 (link-time, missing external definition) ‚Äî A used external-linkage identifier with no definition anywhere in the program must fail to link. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three produce "unresolved reference"/"undefined reference" errors)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.9p5 (link-time, multiple external definitions) ‚Äî More than one external definition of the same external-linkage object across the program must be diagnosed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc reports "defined twice" at compile/link; gcc/clang report "multiple definition" from the linker)


## ¬ß6.10.1-¬ß6.10.3 Conditional inclusion, source inclusion, macro replacement

> mcc status: 0 mcc-gaps ‚Äî full conformance with the gcc==clang consensus. mcc now diagnoses the `#`-must-be-followed-by-a-parameter constraint (¬ß6.10.3.2p1) at macro *definition* time, not only on invocation, matching gcc/clang. `defined`, `__has_include`, full `#if` arithmetic, redefinition rules, `#`/`##`, rescanning/blue-paint, variadic macros, placemarkers, and computed `#include` all match the consensus. (One consensus-split, not an mcc gap: `__VA_ARGS__` in a non-variadic macro replacement list is warned by mcc and gcc but accepted silently by clang, ¬ß6.10.3p5.)

### ¬ß6.10 General (directive structure)

- ¬ß6.10p1 ‚Äî Recognize the directive grammar: a group is a sequence of if-sections, control-lines, text-lines and non-directives; each preprocessing directive is introduced by a `#`. ‚Äî (spec; grammar ‚Äî not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p2 ‚Äî Begin a directive at a `#` that is the first token on a logical line (optionally preceded by white space with no embedded new-line), at the start of translation phase 4. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p2 ‚Äî End the directive at the first new-line after the introducing `#` (line is the logical line, i.e. after backslash-newline splicing). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p2 ‚Äî Allow white space (including comments) between the `#` and the directive name and between tokens of a directive; the `#` and name need not be adjacent. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p2 ‚Äî Accept leading white space before the `#` (an indented directive is still a directive). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p3 ‚Äî Treat a line consisting of `#` alone (followed by new-line) as a null directive with no effect. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p? ‚Äî Reject an unrecognized directive name (`#frobnicate`) with a diagnostic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10p3 ‚Äî Support conditional nesting: an if-section may contain nested if-sections in its groups. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.10.1 Conditional inclusion

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p1 ‚Äî Constrain the `#if`/`#elif` controlling expression to an integer constant expression, additionally permitting the `defined` unary operator; reject floating constants. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p1 ‚Äî Forbid casts, `sizeof`, `_Alignof`, and enumeration constants in the controlling expression (it is evaluated purely as preprocessing arithmetic). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (no enum/sizeof/cast tokens survive macro/identifier‚Üí0 reduction)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p1 ‚Äî Diagnose a constraint violation such as division (or remainder) by zero in the controlling expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p1 ‚Äî Support the `defined IDENT` and `defined ( IDENT )` forms, yielding 1 if IDENT is a currently-defined macro name, else 0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Support the `defined` operator on macro names; `__has_include(<h>)`/`__has_include("q")` is a later (C23/extension) facility but is provided and evaluates to 1/0 by header availability; guard it with `defined __has_include`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc, gcc and clang all answer correctly for present and absent headers)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p1 ‚Äî Leave behavior undefined when the `defined` token is produced by macro expansion rather than written literally; do not crash. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; mcc & gcc accept silently, clang warns `-Wexpansion-to-defined`; all yield the same value)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p4 ‚Äî Process the controlling expression in order: handle `defined` operators, then macro-expand the remaining tokens, then replace every still-remaining identifier (including ones spelled like keywords) with the pp-number `0`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p4 ‚Äî A macro in the controlling expression that expands to another bare identifier is expanded first and only the final residual identifier becomes `0`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p4 ‚Äî Evaluate the reduced expression using the ranges of `intmax_t`/`uintmax_t` (greatest-width signed/unsigned integer arithmetic). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p4 ‚Äî Evaluate character constants in the controlling expression as integers; whether they match the execution character set is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`'A'==65`, `'A'<'B'` all true)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p2 ‚Äî `#ifdef IDENT` includes its group iff IDENT is a defined macro; `#ifndef IDENT` iff it is not (equivalent to `#if defined`/`#if !defined`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p2 ‚Äî Diagnose a missing identifier after `#ifdef`/`#ifndef`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p5 ‚Äî Evaluate `#if`/`#elif` conditions top to bottom; include the first group whose condition is nonzero (or the `#else` group if none), and skip the rest. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p6 ‚Äî In skipped groups, ignore the tokens except to recognize directive names for correct nesting/balancing of conditionals (do not evaluate `#elif` expressions of an already-satisfied section). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p? ‚Äî Each if-section is terminated by exactly one `#endif`; diagnose `#elif`/`#else`/`#endif` with no matching `#if`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p? ‚Äî Diagnose a second `#else` in one if-section, and an `#elif` following an `#else`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc & gcc & clang all reject `#else` after `#else`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p? ‚Äî Diagnose an unterminated conditional (`#if` with no matching `#endif` before end of file). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1p? ‚Äî Warn on extra tokens after `#else`/`#endif` (grammar permits none); a warning is a sufficient diagnostic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three warn, none reject)

### ¬ß6.10.2 Source file inclusion

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.2p1 ‚Äî Require a `#include` directive to name a header or source file the implementation can process; diagnose a malformed form. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.2p2 ‚Äî `#include <h-char-sequence>` searches an implementation-defined sequence of places for a header so identified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.2p3 ‚Äî `#include "q-char-sequence"` searches for a source file in an implementation-defined manner, and on failure re-searches as if `<q-char-sequence>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.2p4 ‚Äî Third (computed) form: macro-expand the tokens after `#include`; the result must match either the `<...>` or the `"..."` form, with implementation-defined token-combination into a single header name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#define HDR <stdio.h>` then `#include HDR` works)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.2p4 ‚Äî Diagnose when the computed `#include` tokens do not reduce to a valid `<...>`/`"..."` header-name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.10.2p5 ‚Äî Inside a `<...>` sequence a `'`, `"`, `\`, `//` or `/*` yields undefined behavior; inside a `"..."` sequence a `'`, `\`, `//` or `/*` does too. ‚Äî (spec; UB ‚Äî not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.10.2p6 ‚Äî Permit `#include` of a file that was itself reached via `#include`, up to an implementation-defined nesting limit (‚â•15 per ¬ß5.2.4.1). ‚Äî (spec/translation-limit; not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.10.3 Macro replacement (general)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p1 ‚Äî Permit identical (benign) redefinition of an object-like macro: same replacement-list spelling and same white-space separation between tokens. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p1 ‚Äî Permit identical redefinition of a function-like macro: same parameter spelling, same replacement list, same white-space separation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p1 ‚Äî Diagnose a non-identical redefinition (different tokens or different presence of internal white space) of an existing macro. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three emit a warning, which satisfies the constraint)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p1 ‚Äî Diagnose redefining an object-like macro as function-like (or vice-versa) ‚Äî they are never identical. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (warning)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p2 ‚Äî Treat replacement lists as identical only when both have the same tokens and the same internal white-space *presence* (amount of white space is irrelevant). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`x+y` vs `x + y` flagged as a redefinition)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p? ‚Äî Require the parameters in a function-like macro to be distinct; diagnose a duplicate parameter name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p3 ‚Äî Require white space between the macro name and the replacement list of an object-like macro; a `(` *immediately* after the name (no space) makes it function-like instead. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#define OBJ (x) y` is object-like; `#define FN(x) ...` is function-like)
- [~] ¬ß6.10.3p5 (C99) ‚Äî Allow `__VA_ARGS__` only in the replacement list of a `...`-variadic macro; diagnose its use elsewhere. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úó (mcc & gcc warn; clang accepts `__VA_ARGS__` in a non-variadic macro replacement list silently)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p? ‚Äî Reject `defined` as a macro name (`#define`/`#undef`); it is reserved for conditional inclusion. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p? ‚Äî `__VA_ARGS__` may not be created or removed by `#define`/`#undef`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (mcc errors; gcc/clang only warn but do not actually redefine it ‚Äî all three refuse the redefinition effect)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p9 ‚Äî Object-like macro: each occurrence of the name in following text is replaced by its replacement list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p10 ‚Äî Function-like macro: only invoke when the name is followed by a `(`; the `(` may be separated by white space/new-lines. Treat the name alone (no `(`) as an ordinary identifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p10 ‚Äî Allow a `(` for the invocation to be supplied by another macro expansion / span lines; collect arguments up to the matching `)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p11 ‚Äî Require the number of arguments to match the number of parameters; diagnose too few and too many. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p11 ‚Äî Commas inside matched inner parentheses do not separate arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.10.3p11 ‚Äî Where the macro arguments contain pp-tokens that look like directives, behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB ‚Äî not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3p12/¬ß6.10.3.1 ‚Äî Variadic macro: a trailing `...` parameter collects the remaining arguments (with their separating commas) into `__VA_ARGS__`; accept zero trailing arguments as the common extension. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`DBG0()` ‚Üí `f()` on all three with no `-pedantic`)

### ¬ß6.10.3.1 Argument substitution

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.1p1 ‚Äî Fully macro-expand each argument (as if it were the rest of the file, with no other tokens available) before substituting it for the corresponding parameter in the replacement list. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`INC(V)`‚Üí`((10)+1)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.1p1 ‚Äî Do NOT pre-expand an argument that is substituted for a parameter immediately preceded by `#` or `##`, or immediately followed by `##`; use the raw (unexpanded) argument there. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#V`‚Üí`"V"`, `V ## _suffix`‚Üí`V_suffix`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.1p2 (C99) ‚Äî Treat `__VA_ARGS__` in the replacement list as a parameter standing for the variable arguments for all substitution purposes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.10.3.2 The `#` (stringize) operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.2p1 ‚Äî Constraint: in a function-like macro each `#` must be immediately followed by a parameter name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects the bad `#define` at definition ‚Äî "'#' is not followed by a macro parameter" ‚Äî even if never invoked, matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.2p2 ‚Äî Replace `# parameter` by a single string-literal whose contents are the spelling of the (unexpanded) argument's tokens. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.2p2 ‚Äî In the stringized result, collapse white space between tokens to one space and delete leading/trailing white space. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`STR(hello   world)`‚Üí`"hello world"`, leading spaces dropped)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.2p2 ‚Äî Preserve the original spelling of each token, and insert a `\` before every `"` and `\` that occurs inside a string/character literal of the argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`STR("a\b")`‚Üí`"\"a\\b\""`)
- ¬ß6.10.3.2p2 ‚Äî If the stringization does not form a valid string literal, behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB ‚Äî not separately testable)
- ¬ß6.10.3.2p2 ‚Äî When both `#` and `##` apply, the order of their evaluation is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified order ‚Äî not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.10.3.3 The `##` (token paste) operator

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.3p1 ‚Äî Constraint: `##` may not be the first or last token of a replacement list (object-like or function-like); diagnose both. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.3p2 ‚Äî For a parameter adjacent to `##`, substitute the raw (unexpanded) argument; if that argument is empty, treat it as a placemarker. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`J(,foo)`‚Üí`foo`, `J(foo,)`‚Üí`foo`, `J(,)`‚Üíempty)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.3p3 ‚Äî Delete each `##` and concatenate the two adjacent tokens into one new preprocessing token. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.3p3 ‚Äî Concatenation with a placemarker yields the other operand (placemarker disappears); two placemarkers yield a placemarker. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.3p3 ‚Äî Diagnose (UB, but must not silently mis-tokenize) when the concatenation does not form a valid single preprocessing token. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three diagnose `+ ## /`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.3p3 ‚Äî Re-examine the newly pasted token for further macro replacement (it participates in rescanning). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`XCAT(v,N)` with `N`‚Üí`1` yields `v1` via the indirection layer)
- ¬ß6.10.3.3p3 ‚Äî With several `##` operators in one replacement list, the order of the individual pastes is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified order ‚Äî not separately testable)

### ¬ß6.10.3.4 Rescanning and further replacement

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.4p1 ‚Äî After substitution, rescan the resulting replacement list together with the subsequent source tokens for more macro names to replace. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.4p1 ‚Äî Allow a macro expansion to consume following source tokens to form a new (possibly function-like) invocation during rescanning. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`f(2)(9)` pattern via `#define f(a) a*g` / `#define g(a) f(a)` ‚Üí `2*9*g`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.4p2 ‚Äî Suppress recursion: if the name of the macro currently being replaced appears in the rescan (directly or via nested replacement), do not replace it again. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#define M M` ‚Üí `M`; mutually-referential `A`/`B` reach a fixed point)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.4p2 ‚Äî Mark such a non-replaced macro name so it is never replaced even if examined again in a later nested context (the "blue paint" is permanent). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.4p3 ‚Äî The token sequence produced by macro replacement is never reinterpreted as a preprocessing directive, even if it begins with `#`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (no probe needed; consistent with rescan results)

### ¬ß6.10.3.5 Scope of macro definitions

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.5p1 ‚Äî A macro definition is in effect from its `#define` until a matching `#undef` or, absent that, to the end of the translation unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.3.5p1 ‚Äî `#undef NAME` removes the macro definition for NAME; it is not an error if NAME is not currently a defined macro. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß6.10.3.5p2+ ‚Äî Worked examples (object-like, function-like, `#`/`##`, rescanning, variadic) illustrate the above rules. ‚Äî (spec; examples ‚Äî not separately testable)


## ¬ß6.10.4-¬ß6.10.9 Line/error/pragma/null/predefined macros/_Pragma

> mcc status: Broadly conformant. #line (number, filename, range constraint, macro-expanded form), #error, the STDC pragmas (incl. on/off-switch validation), unknown-pragma ignore, the null directive, and the full mandatory/environment predefined-macro set all behave like the gcc==clang consensus. Conditional-feature NO_* macros are correctly absent (atomics/complex/threads/VLA all supported). mcc now diagnoses a non-string-literal `_Pragma` operand, matching gcc/clang, leaving 0 mcc-gaps in this section. Minor cosmetic: `#pragma message` diagnostics print a synthetic `:pragma:` filename label.

### ¬ß6.10.4 Line control

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.4p1 ‚Äî Constrain the `#line` argument (after any macro expansion) to a decimal digit sequence in the range 1 to 2147483647; reject 0 and values exceeding the max. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc warns "line number out of range" for 0 and for 2147483648, matching gcc -pedantic; clang treats them as extensions)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.4p2 ‚Äî `#line digit-sequence`: set the presumed source line number of the immediately following line to that value (so `__LINE__` on the next line yields it). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.4p3 ‚Äî `#line digit-sequence "s-char-seq"`: set both the presumed line number and the presumed source file name (`__FILE__`) reported thereafter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.4p4 ‚Äî When the directive does not directly match a number(+optional string) form, macro-expand the trailing tokens first, then require the result to match one of the two forms (otherwise undefined). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (macro expanding to both `42 "z.c"` and to a lone number both work)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.4p4 ‚Äî Reject a `#line` argument that is not a positive integer (e.g. an identifier) with a diagnostic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "wrong #line format")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.4 ‚Äî The presumed file/line set by `#line` must also drive subsequent compiler diagnostics' location, not just `__FILE__`/`__LINE__`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (error after `#line 500 "FAKE.c"` reports `FAKE.c:500`)

### ¬ß6.10.5 Error directive

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.5p1 ‚Äî `#error` must emit a diagnostic that includes the directive's remaining preprocessing tokens and render the program ill-formed (halt this translation unit). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.5p1 ‚Äî `#error` with no following tokens is still a valid error directive producing a diagnostic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.10.6 Pragma directive

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.6p1 ‚Äî A `#pragma` whose pragma name is unrecognized must be handled in an implementation-defined way that does not break conformance (mcc/gcc/clang silently ignore it). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.6p1 ‚Äî When `STDC` immediately follows `pragma`, do not macro-expand the directive's tokens; process them as a standard pragma instead. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (STDC pragmas accepted verbatim)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.6p2 ‚Äî Recognize `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT on-off-switch` (ON/OFF/DEFAULT). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.6p2 ‚Äî Recognize `#pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS on-off-switch`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.6p2 ‚Äî Recognize `#pragma STDC CX_LIMITED_RANGE on-off-switch`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.10.6p2 ‚Äî The on-off-switch operand of an STDC pragma must be exactly `ON`, `OFF`, or `DEFAULT`; anything else is malformed. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (all three warn rather than hard-error; mcc: "malformed #pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT (expected ON/OFF/DEFAULT)", gcc/clang similar ‚Äî consensus warning-only)
- [ ] ¬ß6.10.6p2 ‚Äî STDC pragmas are permitted only outside external declarations or at the head of a compound statement before any statement/declaration; honor that placement scoping. ‚Äî (spec; placement/scope rule ‚Äî accepted at file scope by all three; not separately exercised here)

### ¬ß6.10.7 Null directive

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.7p1 ‚Äî A `#` line containing only optional white space (the null directive) has no effect. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß6.10.8 Predefined macros

- [ ] ¬ß6.10.8p1 ‚Äî None of the predefined macro names, nor the identifier `defined`, may be the target of `#define` or `#undef`. ‚Äî (spec; redefine/undef prohibition ‚Äî not separately probed in this part)

#### ¬ß6.10.8.1 Mandatory macros

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__DATE__`: the translation date as a string literal of the form `"Mmm dd yyyy"` (asctime-style, day space-padded). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`"Jun 30 2026"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__TIME__`: the translation time as `"hh:mm:ss"`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__FILE__`: a string literal giving the presumed current source file name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__LINE__`: the presumed current source line number as a decimal constant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (also expands correctly when reached through a macro body)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC__`: the integer constant `1` (conforming implementation). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC_HOSTED__`: `1` for a hosted implementation, `0` for freestanding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (hosted default = 1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC_VERSION__`: `199901L` (C99), `201112L` (C11). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc tracks `-std=c99`‚Üí199901L, `-std=c11`‚Üí201112L, `-std=c17`‚Üí201710L; default mode differs across vendors ‚Äî mcc defaults C99, gcc C23, clang C17 ‚Äî all conforming choices)

#### ¬ß6.10.8.2 Environment macros

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 ‚Äî `__STDC_ISO_10646__`: defined as a `yyyymmL` constant when `wchar_t` holds Unicode/ISO 10646 code points. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`201706L` on this Linux target)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 ‚Äî `__STDC_MB_MIGHT_NEQ_WC__`: defined as `1` only if a basic-character member can have different code values as a multibyte char vs. a wide char; otherwise undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (correctly undefined on this platform)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_UTF_16__`: `1` when `char16_t` values are UTF-16 encoded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_UTF_32__`: `1` when `char32_t` values are UTF-32 encoded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß6.10.8.3 Conditional feature macros (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_ANALYZABLE__`: define (as `yyyymmL`) iff the implementation conforms to the Annex L analyzability spec. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (correctly undefined; Annex L not implemented by any)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`: define (as `yyyymmL`) iff the Annex K bounds-checking interfaces are provided. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (correctly undefined; Annex K not provided)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`: define as `1` iff `_Atomic` and `<stdatomic.h>` are NOT supported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (atomics supported ‚Üí correctly undefined; `<stdatomic.h>` compiles)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__`: define as `1` iff `_Complex`/`<complex.h>` are NOT supported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (complex supported ‚Üí correctly undefined)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_THREADS__`: define as `1` iff `<threads.h>` is NOT supported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`<threads.h>` compiles ‚Üí correctly undefined)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_VLA__`: define as `1` iff variable-length arrays are NOT supported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (VLAs supported ‚Üí correctly undefined)

### ¬ß6.10.9 _Pragma operator (C99/C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.9p1 ‚Äî `_Pragma ( string-literal )` constraint: the operand must be a parenthesized string literal. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects `_Pragma(foo)` with a non-string-literal operand ‚Äî "_Pragma takes a parenthesized string literal" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, which both error "`_Pragma` takes a parenthesized string literal")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.9p1 ‚Äî Destringize the operand: drop an `L`/`u`/`U` prefix if present, strip the surrounding `"`, then replace `\"`‚Üí`"` and `\\`‚Üí`\`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Pragma("message(\"hi\")")` yields a `#pragma message: hi` note)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.9p1 ‚Äî Re-tokenize the destringized result and process it as if it were a `#pragma` directive on its own line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Pragma("STDC FP_CONTRACT OFF")` honored; works the same when emitted from a macro body via `_Pragma(#x)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.9p1 ‚Äî An unrecognized pragma delivered through `_Pragma` is ignored just like an unrecognized `#pragma`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.9 ‚Äî `_Pragma` works when generated by macro expansion (the canonical `DO_PRAGMA(x) _Pragma(#x)` idiom), unlike `#pragma` which cannot be produced by macro replacement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì


## ¬ß7.1-¬ß7.5 Library intro, assert, complex, ctype, errno

> mcc status: 119 TODOs; 1 mcc-gap. The only divergence found is that `static_assert` from `<assert.h>` (C11) is unavailable in mcc's **default** mode ‚Äî mcc defaults to `__STDC_VERSION__ == 199901L` (C99), and glibc's `<assert.h>` only defines the `static_assert` macro when `__STDC_VERSION__ >= 201112L`; gcc/clang default to C23/C17 so they provide it out of the box. `mcc -std=c11` fixes it. All `<complex.h>` macros/functions, the `CX_LIMITED_RANGE` pragma, `CMPLX`, all 29 standard headers, `<ctype.h>` (incl. C99 `isblank`), and `<errno.h>` (incl. C99 `EILSEQ`, C11 thread-local `errno`) conform on mcc.

### ¬ß7.1.1 Definitions of terms
- ¬ß7.1.1p1 ‚Äî A *string* is a contiguous sequence of characters terminated by and including the first null character; a *pointer to a string* points to its initial (lowest addressed) character. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.1p1 ‚Äî The *length* of a string is the number of bytes preceding the null character. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.1p1 ‚Äî The *value* of a string is the sequence of the values of the contained characters, in order. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.1p1 ‚Äî The term *multibyte character* sometimes includes single-byte characters, as a generalization of the term used in 5.2.1.2 ("the decimal-point character notwithstanding"). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.1p1 ‚Äî The *decimal-point character* is the character used by functions that convert floating-point numbers to or from character sequences to denote the beginning of the fractional part; represented in the text and examples by a period, but it may be changed by the `setlocale` function. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.1.2 Standard headers
> C11 adds five headers (`<stdalign.h>`, `<stdatomic.h>`, `<stdnoreturn.h>`, `<threads.h>`, `<uchar.h>`) and the ¬ß7.1.2p5 prohibition on macros whose names match keywords; C99/C90 have neither.
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.2p1 ‚Äî Each library function's declarations and type and macro definitions are contained in a *header*, whose contents are made available by the `#include` preprocessing directive. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.1.2p1 ‚Äî A header declares a set of related functions plus any necessary types and additional macros needed to facilitate their use. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.2p1 ‚Äî Declarations of types described in a clause are valid only within the scope established by the header that contains them (where the clause so states). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.2p2 ‚Äî The C99 standard headers are exactly the 24: `<assert.h>`, `<complex.h>`, `<ctype.h>`, `<errno.h>`, `<fenv.h>`, `<float.h>`, `<inttypes.h>`, `<iso646.h>`, `<limits.h>`, `<locale.h>`, `<math.h>`, `<setjmp.h>`, `<signal.h>`, `<stdarg.h>`, `<stdbool.h>`, `<stddef.h>`, `<stdint.h>`, `<stdio.h>`, `<stdlib.h>`, `<string.h>`, `<tgmath.h>`, `<time.h>`, `<wchar.h>`, `<wctype.h>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all 24 include cleanly; mcc bundles 10 in runtime/include and defers the rest to the system libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) The standard headers additionally include `<stdalign.h>`, `<stdatomic.h>`, `<stdnoreturn.h>`, `<threads.h>`, and `<uchar.h>` (29 total). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all five bundled in mcc's runtime/include and includable)
- ¬ß7.1.2p3 ‚Äî If a file with the same name as one of the standard headers, not provided as part of the implementation, is placed where a header search would find it, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.2p4 ‚Äî Standard headers may be included in any order, and each may be included more than once with no effect different from being included only once ‚Äî except that the effect of including `<assert.h>` depends on the definition of `NDEBUG`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (re-inclusion idempotent; assert re-evaluates NDEBUG)
- ¬ß7.1.2p5 ‚Äî If used, a header shall be included outside of any external declaration or definition, and it shall be included lexically before the first reference to any of the functions or objects it declares, or to any of the types or macros it defines. ‚Äî (spec/constraint on the program; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.2p5 ‚Äî However, if an identifier is declared or defined in more than one header, the second and subsequent associated headers may be included after the initial reference to the identifier. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.2p5 ‚Äî (C11) The program shall not have any macros with names lexically identical to keywords currently defined prior to the inclusion of the header or when any macro defined in the header is expanded. ‚Äî (spec/constraint on the program; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.1.3 Reserved identifiers
- ¬ß7.1.3p1 ‚Äî Each header declares or defines all the identifiers listed in its associated subclause, and optionally declares or defines identifiers listed in its associated future library directions subclause and identifiers that are always reserved either for any use or for use as file scope identifiers. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p1 ‚Äî All identifiers that begin with an underscore and either an uppercase letter or another underscore are always reserved for any use. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p1 ‚Äî All identifiers that begin with an underscore are always reserved for use as identifiers with file scope in both the ordinary and tag name spaces. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p1 ‚Äî Each macro name in any of the following subclauses (including the future library directions) is reserved for use as specified if any of its associated headers is included, unless explicitly stated otherwise. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p1 ‚Äî All identifiers with external linkage in any of the following subclauses (including the future library directions) and `errno` are always reserved for use as identifiers with external linkage. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p1 ‚Äî Each identifier with file scope listed in any of the following subclauses (including the future library directions) is reserved for use as a macro name and as an identifier with file scope in the same name space if any of its associated headers is included. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p2 ‚Äî No other identifiers are reserved. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p2 ‚Äî If the program declares or defines an identifier in a context in which it is reserved (other than as allowed by 7.1.4), or defines a reserved identifier as a macro name, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.3p3 ‚Äî If the program removes (with `#undef`) any macro definition of an identifier in the first group listed (the potentially reserved identifiers), the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.1.4 Use of library functions
- ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî Each of the ¬ß7.1.4p1 statements applies unless explicitly stated otherwise in the detailed descriptions that follow. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî If an argument to a function has an invalid value (a value outside the function's domain, a pointer outside the address space of the program, a null pointer, or a pointer to non-modifiable storage when the corresponding parameter is not const-qualified) or a type (after default argument promotion) not expected by a function with a variable number of arguments, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî Any function declared in a header may be additionally implemented as a function-like macro defined in the header, so a library function should not be declared explicitly if its header is included. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (e.g. `creal`/`cimag` are both prototyped functions and masking macros in mcc's complex.h)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî Any macro definition of a function can be suppressed locally by enclosing the function name in parentheses, because the name is then not followed by the `(` that indicates expansion of a function-like macro name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(creal)(z)` and `(isalpha)('a')` call the real function on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî For the same syntactic reason, a function declared in a header can be redeclared in the program, and the program's name can be used to take the address of the actual function even if the function is also implemented as a macro. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double (*p)(double complex) = creal;` and `int (*q)(int) = isalpha;` work)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî The use of `#undef` to remove any macro definition will also ensure that an actual function is referred to. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî Any invocation of a library function that is implemented as a macro shall expand to code that evaluates each of its arguments exactly once, fully protected by parentheses where necessary, so it is generally safe to use arbitrary expressions as arguments. (Exceptions: the macros `assert`, `setjmp`, `va_arg`, `va_copy`, and `va_start` need not satisfy this requirement.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc's ctype/complex masking macros parenthesize and use their argument once)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî Likewise, the function-like macros described in the following subclauses may be invoked in an expression anywhere a function with a compatible return type could be called. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p1 ‚Äî All object-like macros listed as expanding to integer constant expressions shall additionally be suitable for use in `#if` preprocessing directives. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`EDOM`/`ERANGE`/`EILSEQ` usable in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.4p2 ‚Äî Provided that a library function can be declared without reference to any type defined in a header, it is permissible to declare the function and use it without including its associated header. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (e.g. `extern int isalpha(int);` then call links fine)
- ¬ß7.1.4p3 ‚Äî There is a sequence point immediately before a library function returns. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.1.4p4 ‚Äî The functions in the standard library are not guaranteed to be reentrant and may modify objects with static or thread storage duration. (C11 adds "thread storage duration".) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.2 Diagnostics `<assert.h>`
> C11 makes `<assert.h>` also define `static_assert` (expanding to `_Static_assert`); C99/C90 define only `assert` (and reference `NDEBUG`). C99/C11 include `__func__` in the failure message; C90 did not.
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2p1 ‚Äî The header `<assert.h>` defines the `assert` macro and refers to another macro, `NDEBUG`, which is not defined by `<assert.h>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) The header `<assert.h>` defines the macro `static_assert`, which expands to `_Static_assert`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc defaults to `__STDC_VERSION__==199901L`, so glibc's `<assert.h>` does NOT define `static_assert`; gcc/clang default to C23/C17 where it is defined. mcc provides it with `-std=c11`; the `_Static_assert` keyword itself is accepted by mcc in all modes.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2p2 ‚Äî If `NDEBUG` is defined as a macro name at the point in the source file where `<assert.h>` is included, the `assert` macro is defined simply as `#define assert(ignore) ((void)0)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (assert(0) under NDEBUG is a no-op; program returns normally)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2p3 ‚Äî The `assert` macro is redefined according to the current state of `NDEBUG` each time that `<assert.h>` is included. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (toggling NDEBUG across re-includes flips assert active/no-op)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2p4 ‚Äî The `assert` macro shall be implemented as a macro, not as an actual function; if the macro definition is suppressed in order to access an actual function, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`assert` is a macro; `#ifdef assert` is true)

#### ¬ß7.2.1.1 The `assert` macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <assert.h>` then `void assert(scalar expression);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2.1.1p2 ‚Äî The `assert` macro puts diagnostic tests into programs; it expands to a void expression. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`(void)(assert(1),0)` compiles; assert usable in a comma expression)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2.1.1p2 ‚Äî When executed, if `expression` (which shall have a scalar type) is false (compares equal to 0), the `assert` macro writes information about the particular call that failed ‚Äî including the text of the argument, the name of the source file, the source line number, and the name of the enclosing function (the values of `__FILE__`, `__LINE__`, and the identifier `__func__`) ‚Äî on the standard error stream in an implementation-defined format. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc prints `prog: file.c:2: main: Assertion '2+2==5' failed.` ‚Äî includes expr text, file, line, and `__func__`; format is implementation-defined and matches gcc's; clang uses the full prototype for the function name)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2.1.1p2 ‚Äî The `assert` macro then calls the `abort` function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (process terminates with SIGABRT, exit 134, on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.2.1.1p3 ‚Äî The `assert` macro returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.2.2 (C11) `static_assert` / `_Static_assert`
- [~] ¬ß7.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) `static_assert` is defined as a macro expanding to the keyword `_Static_assert`; it performs a compile-time assertion whose constraints and semantics are specified in ¬ß6.7.10 Static assertions. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (same default-std gap as ¬ß7.2p1 above: works with `mcc -std=c11`, not by default; `_Static_assert(cond,"msg")` keyword form works in every mcc mode)

### ¬ß7.3 Complex arithmetic `<complex.h>`
> C11 adds the `CMPLX`/`CMPLXF`/`CMPLXL` macros (¬ß7.3.9.3) and clarifies `cproj`; the `imaginary`/`_Imaginary_I` macros and imaginary types are optional (Annex G) in both C99 and C11. An implementation that defines `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__` (C11) need not provide `<complex.h>` at all.

#### ¬ß7.3.0 `<complex.h>` provision and feature macros (added gaps)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3 ‚Äî mcc provides a bundled `<complex.h>` (runtime/include/complex.h, guarded by `_MCC_COMPLEX_H`) and does NOT define `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none of the three define `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__`; all provide the header)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 / Annex F.2 ‚Äî (C11) An implementation that supports IEC 60559-compatible complex arithmetic defines `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__` as `1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three predefine `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__ 1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3 ‚Äî Including `<complex.h>` more than once has no effect different from a single inclusion (header is idempotently guarded). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.3.1 Introduction
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p1 ‚Äî The header `<complex.h>` defines macros and declares functions that support complex arithmetic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p2 ‚Äî Each synopsis specifies a family of functions consisting of a principal function with one or more `double complex` parameters and a `double complex` or `double` return value, plus other functions with the same name suffixed by `f` and `l` that are corresponding functions with `float` and `long double` parameters and return values. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`cabs`/`cabsf`/`cabsl` etc. all declared and link; tested `cabsf`/`cabsl`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p3 ‚Äî The macro `complex` expands to `_Complex`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#define complex _Complex`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p3 ‚Äî The macro `_Complex_I` expands to a constant expression of type `const float _Complex`, with the value of the imaginary unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc defines it via `__builtin_complex(0.0f,1.0f)`, usable as a static initializer of `const float _Complex`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p4 ‚Äî The macros `imaginary` and `_Imaginary_I` are defined if and only if the implementation supports imaginary types (Annex G); when defined, `imaginary` expands to `_Imaginary` and `_Imaginary_I` expands to a constant expression of type `const float _Imaginary` with the value of the imaginary unit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none support imaginary types, so none define `imaginary`/`_Imaginary_I` ‚Äî `#ifdef imaginary` is false on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p5 ‚Äî The macro `I` expands to `_Imaginary_I` if `_Imaginary_I` is defined, otherwise to `_Complex_I`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`I` == `_Complex_I` since no imaginary types)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.1p6 ‚Äî Notwithstanding the provisions of 7.1.3, a program may undefine and perhaps then redefine the macros `complex`, `imaginary`, and `I`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#undef complex` / `#undef I` / `#undef imaginary` then redefine all accepted)

#### ¬ß7.3.2 Conventions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.2p1 ‚Äî Function values for complex angle/argument quantities are interpreted as radians, not degrees. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`carg(I)` == œÄ/2 ‚âà 1.5708 on all three)
- ¬ß7.3.2p1 ‚Äî An implementation may set `errno` for the `<complex.h>` functions but is not required to. ‚Äî (spec/permission; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.3.3 Branch cuts
- ¬ß7.3.3p1 ‚Äî Some of the `<complex.h>` functions have branch cuts, across which the function is discontinuous. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.3p1 ‚Äî For implementations with a signed zero (including all IEC 60559 implementations) that follow the specifications of the functions, the sign of zero distinguishes one side of a cut from another, so the function is continuous (except for format limitations) as the cut is approached from either side. ‚Äî (spec/libm-behavioral; not a compiler property)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.3p1 ‚Äî Example: for `csqrt` (branch cut along the negative real axis), the top of the cut (imaginary part +0) maps to the positive imaginary axis and the bottom of the cut (imaginary part ‚àí0) maps to the negative imaginary axis. ‚Äî (spec/libm-behavioral; not a compiler property)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.3p2 ‚Äî Implementations that do not support a signed zero (see Annex F) cannot distinguish the sides of branch cuts; they shall map a cut so the function is continuous as the cut is approached coming around the finite endpoint of the cut from either side. ‚Äî (spec/libm-behavioral; not a compiler property)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.3p2 ‚Äî Example: for `csqrt`, coming counterclockwise around the finite endpoint, the cut maps to the positive imaginary axis; coming clockwise, it maps to the negative imaginary axis. ‚Äî (spec/libm-behavioral; not a compiler property)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.3p2 ‚Äî Implementations that do not support a signed zero shall map values on the branch cut consistently as specified for each function. ‚Äî (spec/libm-behavioral; not a compiler property)

#### ¬ß7.3.4 The `CX_LIMITED_RANGE` pragma
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <complex.h>` then `#pragma STDC CX_LIMITED_RANGE on-off-switch`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc accepts the pragma with `ON`/`OFF`/`DEFAULT` without diagnostic)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.4p2 ‚Äî The pragma can be used to inform the implementation that (where the state is "on") the usual mathematical formulas for complex multiply, divide, and absolute value are acceptable, despite their problematic treatment of infinities and of undue overflow and underflow. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; semantic optimization is QoI)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.4p2 ‚Äî The pragma can occur either outside external declarations or preceding all explicit declarations and statements inside a compound statement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted both at file scope and at the top of a compound statement)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.4p2 ‚Äî When outside external declarations, the pragma takes effect from its occurrence until another `CX_LIMITED_RANGE` pragma is encountered, or until the end of the translation unit. ‚Äî (spec/scoping; mcc accepts, behavior not observable in output)
- [ ] ¬ß7.3.4p2 ‚Äî When inside a compound statement, the pragma takes effect from its occurrence until another `CX_LIMITED_RANGE` pragma is encountered (including within a nested compound statement) or until the end of the compound statement; at the end of a compound statement the state is restored to its condition just before the compound statement. ‚Äî (spec/scoping; mcc accepts, behavior not observable in output)
- ¬ß7.3.4p2 ‚Äî If this pragma is used in any other context, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.3.4p2 ‚Äî The default state for the pragma is "off". ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.3.5 Trigonometric functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.5.1p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex cacos(double complex z);` (with `cacosf`, `cacosl`): computes the complex arc cosine of `z`, with branch cuts outside the interval [‚àí1, +1] along the real axis; returns the value in a strip unbounded along the imaginary axis and in [0, œÄ] along the real axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared in mcc complex.h; links via libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.5.2p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex casin(double complex z);` (with `casinf`, `casinl`): computes the complex arc sine of `z`, branch cuts outside [‚àí1, +1] along the real axis; returns the value in a strip unbounded along the imaginary axis and in [‚àíœÄ/2, +œÄ/2] along the real axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.5.3p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex catan(double complex z);` (with `catanf`, `catanl`): computes the complex arc tangent of `z`, branch cuts outside [‚àíi, +i] along the imaginary axis; returns the value in a strip unbounded along the imaginary axis and in [‚àíœÄ/2, +œÄ/2] along the real axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.5.4p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex ccos(double complex z);` (with `ccosf`, `ccosl`): computes and returns the complex cosine of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.5.5p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex csin(double complex z);` (with `csinf`, `csinl`): computes and returns the complex sine of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.5.6p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex ctan(double complex z);` (with `ctanf`, `ctanl`): computes and returns the complex tangent of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.3.6 Hyperbolic functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.6.1p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex cacosh(double complex z);` (with `cacoshf`, `cacoshl`): computes the complex arc hyperbolic cosine of `z`, branch cut at values < 1 along the real axis; returns the value in a half-strip of nonnegative values along the real axis and in [‚àíiœÄ, +iœÄ] along the imaginary axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.6.2p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex casinh(double complex z);` (with `casinhf`, `casinhl`): computes the complex arc hyperbolic sine of `z`, branch cuts outside [‚àíi, +i] along the imaginary axis; returns the value in a strip unbounded along the real axis and in [‚àíiœÄ/2, +iœÄ/2] along the imaginary axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.6.3p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex catanh(double complex z);` (with `catanhf`, `catanhl`): computes the complex arc hyperbolic tangent of `z`, branch cuts outside [‚àí1, +1] along the real axis; returns the value in a strip unbounded along the real axis and in [‚àíiœÄ/2, +iœÄ/2] along the imaginary axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.6.4p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex ccosh(double complex z);` (with `ccoshf`, `ccoshl`): computes and returns the complex hyperbolic cosine of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.6.5p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex csinh(double complex z);` (with `csinhf`, `csinhl`): computes and returns the complex hyperbolic sine of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.6.6p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex ctanh(double complex z);` (with `ctanhf`, `ctanhl`): computes and returns the complex hyperbolic tangent of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.3.7 Exponential and logarithmic functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.7.1p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex cexp(double complex z);` (with `cexpf`, `cexpl`): computes and returns the complex base-e exponential of `z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`creal(cexp(0))` == 1 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.7.2p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex clog(double complex z);` (with `clogf`, `clogl`): computes the complex natural (base-e) logarithm of `z`, branch cut along the negative real axis; returns the value in a strip unbounded along the real axis and in [‚àíiœÄ, +iœÄ] along the imaginary axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.3.8 Power and absolute-value functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.8.1p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double cabs(double complex z);` (with `cabsf`, `cabsl`): computes and returns the complex absolute value (norm, modulus, magnitude) of `z` ‚Äî note the `double` (real) return type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`cabs(3+4i)` == 5; declared with real `double` return)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.8.2p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex cpow(double complex x, double complex y);` (with `cpowf`, `cpowl`): computes and returns the complex power function x^y, with a branch cut for the first parameter along the negative real axis. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (two-parameter prototype present)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.8.3p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex csqrt(double complex z);` (with `csqrtf`, `csqrtl`): computes the complex square root of `z`, branch cut along the negative real axis; returns the value in the range of the right half-plane (including the imaginary axis). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.3.9 Manipulation functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.1p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double carg(double complex z);` (with `cargf`, `cargl`): computes the argument (phase angle) of `z`, branch cut along the negative real axis; returns the value in the interval [‚àíœÄ, +œÄ] ‚Äî note the `double` (real) return type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (real `double` return; `carg(I)`‚âà1.5708)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.2p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double cimag(double complex z);` (with `cimagf`, `cimagl`): computes and returns the imaginary part of `z` as a real (`double`) value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc masks it with `(__imag__ (double _Complex)(z))`; `cimag(3+4i)`==4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.2p4 / ¬ß7.3.9.6p4 ‚Äî For a variable `z` of complex type, `z == creal(z) + cimag(z)*I` (so a complex value is fully described by `creal`/`cimag`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.3p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `double complex CMPLX(double x, double y);` (with `CMPLXF`, `CMPLXL`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three macros defined in mcc complex.h)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) The `CMPLX` macros expand to an expression of the specified complex type, with the real part having the (converted) value of `x` and the imaginary part having the (converted) value of `y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) The resulting expression shall be suitable for use as an initializer for an object with static or thread storage duration, provided both arguments are likewise suitable. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`double complex g = CMPLX(1,2);` and `static complex s = CMPLX(INFINITY,0);` at file scope compile on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) The macros act as if the implementation supported imaginary types and the definitions were `#define CMPLX(x, y) ((double complex)((double)(x) + _Imaginary_I * (double)(y)))` ‚Äî building a complex value with the given real and imaginary parts even when one of them is an infinity or NaN, and preserving the sign of a zero imaginary part. (mcc implements this via `__builtin_complex`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`CMPLX(INFINITY,-0.0)` yields real=inf, imag=‚àí0 with the sign bit set on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.3p4 ‚Äî (C11) The `CMPLX` macros return the complex value `x + iy`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.4p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex conj(double complex z);` (with `conjf`, `conjl`): computes and returns the complex conjugate of `z`, by reversing the sign of its imaginary part. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`conj(3+4i)`==3‚àí4i)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.5p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double complex cproj(double complex z);` (with `cprojf`, `cprojl`): computes a projection of `z` onto the Riemann sphere ‚Äî `z` maps to itself except that all complex infinities (even those with one infinite part and one NaN part) map to positive infinity on the real axis; if `z` has an infinite part then `cproj(z)` is equivalent to `INFINITY + I * copysign(0.0, cimag(z))`; returns the projection. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared and links)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.3.9.6p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `double creal(double complex z);` (with `crealf`, `creall`): computes and returns the real part of `z` as a real (`double`) value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc masks it with `(__real__ (double _Complex)(z))`; `creal(3+4i)`==3; `(creal)(z)` and `&creal` also work)

### ¬ß7.4 Character handling `<ctype.h>`
> C99 adds `isblank` (¬ß7.4.1.3); otherwise the set is unchanged in C11.
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4p1 ‚Äî The header `<ctype.h>` declares several functions useful for classifying and mapping characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4p1 ‚Äî In all cases the argument is an `int`, the value of which shall be representable as an `unsigned char` or shall equal the value of the macro `EOF`; if the argument has any other value, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isalpha(EOF)`/`isspace(EOF)` return 0 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4p2 ‚Äî The behavior of these functions is affected by the current locale; they classify characters according to the rules of the current locale (the `"C"` locale being in effect by default at program startup). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (libc-provided; default "C" locale results match)
- ¬ß7.4p3 ‚Äî The term *printing character* refers to a member of a locale-specific set of characters, each of which occupies one printing position on a display device. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.4p3 ‚Äî The term *control character* refers to a member of a locale-specific set of characters that are not printing characters. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.4p4 ‚Äî In the seven-bit US ASCII character set, the printing characters are those with values 0x20 (space) through 0x7E (tilde); the control characters are those with values 0 (NUL) through 0x1F (US), and the character 0x7F (DEL). (Footnote/example.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.4.1 Character classification functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1p1 ‚Äî The classification functions return nonzero (true) if and only if the value of the argument `c` conforms to that in the description of the function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.1p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isalnum(int c);`: tests for any character for which `isalpha` or `isdigit` is true. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.2p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isalpha(int c);`: tests for any character for which `isupper` or `islower` is true, or any character that is one of a locale-specific set of alphabetic characters for which none of `iscntrl`, `isdigit`, `ispunct`, or `isspace` is true; in the `"C"` locale, true only where `isupper` or `islower` is true. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.3p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî (C99) `int isblank(int c);`: tests for any standard blank character or one of a locale-specific set of characters for which `isspace` is true and that is used to separate words within a line of text. The standard blank characters are space (`' '`) and horizontal tab (`'\t'`); in the `"C"` locale, true only for those two. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isblank('\t')` true; declared by libc ctype.h, available in mcc's default mode)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.4p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int iscntrl(int c);`: tests for any control character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.5p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isdigit(int c);`: tests for any decimal-digit character (as defined in 5.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.6p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isgraph(int c);`: tests for any printing character except space (`' '`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.7p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int islower(int c);`: tests for any lowercase letter or one of a locale-specific set of characters for which none of `iscntrl`, `isdigit`, `ispunct`, or `isspace` is true; in the `"C"` locale, true only for the lowercase letters (as defined in 5.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.8p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isprint(int c);`: tests for any printing character including space (`' '`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.9p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int ispunct(int c);`: tests for any printing character that is one of a locale-specific set of punctuation characters for which neither `isspace` nor `isalnum` is true; in the `"C"` locale, true for every printing character for which neither `isspace` nor `isalnum` is true. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.10p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isspace(int c);`: tests for any standard white-space character or one of a locale-specific set of characters for which `isalnum` is false. The standard white-space characters are space (`' '`), form feed (`'\f'`), new-line (`'\n'`), carriage return (`'\r'`), horizontal tab (`'\t'`), and vertical tab (`'\v'`); in the `"C"` locale, true only for those six. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
