- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.11p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isupper(int c);`: tests for any uppercase letter or one of a locale-specific set of characters for which none of `iscntrl`, `isdigit`, `ispunct`, or `isspace` is true; in the `"C"` locale, true only for the uppercase letters (as defined in 5.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.1.12p1‚Äìp2 ‚Äî `int isxdigit(int c);`: tests for any hexadecimal-digit character (as defined in 6.4.4.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isxdigit('f')` true)

#### ¬ß7.4.2 Character case mapping functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.2.1p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `int tolower(int c);`: converts an uppercase letter to a corresponding lowercase letter ‚Äî if the argument is a character for which `isupper` is true and there are one or more corresponding characters (as specified by the current locale) for which `islower` is true, returns one of the corresponding characters (always the same one for any given locale); otherwise returns the argument unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`tolower('A')`=='a')
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.4.2.2p1‚Äìp3 ‚Äî `int toupper(int c);`: converts a lowercase letter to a corresponding uppercase letter ‚Äî if the argument is a character for which `islower` is true and there are one or more corresponding characters (as specified by the current locale) for which `isupper` is true, returns one of the corresponding characters (always the same one for any given locale); otherwise returns the argument unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`toupper('a')`=='A')

### ¬ß7.5 Errors `<errno.h>`
> C99 adds `EILSEQ` (C90 defined only `EDOM` and `ERANGE`). C11 specifies that `errno` has thread-local storage duration and that its value is zero in the initial thread at startup; C99/C90 give a single per-program `errno` that is zero at program startup.
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.5p1 ‚Äî The header `<errno.h>` defines several macros, all relating to the reporting of error conditions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.5p2 ‚Äî The macros `EDOM`, `EILSEQ`, and `ERANGE` expand to integer constant expressions with type `int`, distinct positive values, and which are suitable for use in `#if` preprocessing directives. (`EILSEQ` is C99; C90 had only `EDOM` and `ERANGE`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three defined, distinct, positive, and usable in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.5p2 ‚Äî Additional macro definitions, beginning with `E` and a digit or `E` and an uppercase letter, may also be specified by the implementation (these names are reserved for future error macros ‚Äî see future library directions ¬ß7.31). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc supplies the full `E*` set on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.5p3 ‚Äî The macro `errno` expands to a modifiable lvalue that has type `int` and (C11) thread-local storage duration, the value of which is set to a positive error number by several library functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`&errno` is an `int*`; assigning `errno=ERANGE` then reading it works; thread test below confirms thread-local)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.5p3 ‚Äî `errno` need not be the identifier of an object; it might expand to a modifiable lvalue resulting from a function call (e.g., `*errno()`). It is unspecified whether `errno` is a macro or an identifier declared with external linkage. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc's `errno` expands to `(*__errno_location())` on all three)
- ¬ß7.5p3 ‚Äî If a macro definition is suppressed in order to access an actual object, or a program defines an identifier with the name `errno`, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.5p3 ‚Äî The value of `errno` in the initial thread (C11; "at program startup" in C99) is zero, but is never set to zero by any library function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (libc guarantee; thread-locality verified: a child thread setting `errno=42` leaves the main thread's `errno` unchanged on all three)
- ¬ß7.5p3 ‚Äî The value of `errno` may be set to nonzero by a library function call whether or not there is an error, provided the use of `errno` is not documented in the description of the function in the Standard. ‚Äî (spec/permission; not separately testable)


## ¬ß7.6-¬ß7.8 fenv, float, inttypes

> mcc status: 96 TODOs in this section; 3 are mcc soft-gaps (all tagged `~`): the `FENV_ACCESS` pragma is *recognized and validated* but its placement constraint is not diagnosed and its optimization-inhibition cannot be verified, and bundled `FLT_ROUNDS` is a static `1` rather than dynamic. None of the three is a clean gcc==clang-consensus divergence (gcc and clang themselves disagree on both `FENV_ACCESS` placement diagnosis and `FLT_ROUNDS` dynamism). Everything else conforms: `<fenv.h>` and `<inttypes.h>` resolve to the system glibc headers and glibc runtime (full conformance), and mcc's *bundled* `<float.h>` (`runtime/include/float.h`) is complete including all C11 additions (`*_HAS_SUBNORM`, `*_DECIMAL_DIG`, `*_TRUE_MIN`). mcc's preprocessor genuinely tracks `#pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS` (`src/mccpp.c:1921`, `TOK_STDC`) ‚Äî it validates the `ON`/`OFF`/`DEFAULT` switch and scopes it to the enclosing compound statement, which is *more* than gcc (which warns "ignoring #pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS").

### ¬ß7.6 `<fenv.h>`

> C99‚ÜíC11: C11 adds that the floating-point environment has **thread storage duration** (¬ß7.6p2) and adds the constant-vs-dynamic control-mode model (¬ß7.6p3); the F-annex cross-reference in ¬ß7.6.2.3p2 is **F.8.6** in C11 but **F.7.6** in C99. On this platform `<fenv.h>` resolves to `/usr/include/fenv.h` (glibc) for all three compilers ‚Äî mcc bundles no `fenv.h`.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p1 ‚Äî The header `<fenv.h>` shall declare two types (`fenv_t`, `fexcept_t`) and several macros and functions to provide access to the floating-point environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc header; both types + all funcs compile/link/run)
- ¬ß7.6p1 ‚Äî The floating-point environment refers collectively to any floating-point status flags and control modes supported by the implementation. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.6p1 ‚Äî A floating-point status flag is a system variable whose value is set (but never cleared) when a floating-point exception is raised, which occurs as a side effect of arithmetic operations to inform of exceptional conditions. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.6p1 ‚Äî A floating-point control mode is a system variable whose value may be set by the user to affect the subsequent behavior of floating-point arithmetic. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p2 ‚Äî The floating-point environment has thread storage duration; the initial state for a thread's floating-point environment is the current state of the floating-point environment of the thread that creates it at the time of creation. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc runtime property; not a compiler property)
- ¬ß7.6p2 ‚Äî A function call does not alter its caller's floating-point control modes, clear its caller's floating-point status flags, nor depend on the state of its caller's floating-point status flags unless so documented; a function call is assumed to require default floating-point control modes unless its documentation promises otherwise. ‚Äî (spec; programming-convention, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.6p3 ‚Äî A floating-point control mode may be constant (e.g., the rounding direction set by the rounding-direction macros at compile time) or dynamic; the dynamic floating-point environment includes the dynamic control modes and the status flags. (C11) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p4 ‚Äî The type `fenv_t` represents the entire floating-point environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fenv_t env; fegetenv(&env)` round-trips)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p5 ‚Äî The type `fexcept_t` represents the floating-point status flags collectively (not necessarily a set of bits corresponding to the exceptions). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fexcept_t fl; fegetexceptflag/fesetexceptflag` round-trips)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p6 ‚Äî Each floating-point exception macro `FE_DIVBYZERO`, `FE_INEXACT`, `FE_INVALID`, `FE_OVERFLOW`, `FE_UNDERFLOW` is defined iff the implementation supports the corresponding exception via the 7.6.2 functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all five defined; x86-64 SSE supports all)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p6 ‚Äî Each defined exception macro expands to an integer constant expression such that bitwise ORs of all combinations are distinct. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified in `#if`: all five OR-distinct)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p6 ‚Äî Additional implementation-defined floating-point exceptions may be specified, with names beginning `FE_` + uppercase letter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc adds `FE_DENORMAL` `__FE_DENORM` on x86; permitted)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p7 ‚Äî The macro `FE_ALL_EXCEPT` is the bitwise OR of all exception macros defined by the implementation (expands to `0` if none defined). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified `(FE_DIVBYZERO|FE_INEXACT|FE_INVALID|FE_OVERFLOW|FE_UNDERFLOW)==FE_ALL_EXCEPT` in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p8 ‚Äî Each rounding direction macro `FE_DOWNWARD`, `FE_TONEAREST`, `FE_TOWARDZERO`, `FE_UPWARD` is defined iff that direction can be both got and set via `fegetround`/`fesetround`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all four defined; round-trip through `fesetround`/`fegetround` works)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p8 ‚Äî Each defined rounding direction macro expands to a nonnegative integer constant expression distinct from the others. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified distinct in `#if`)
- ¬ß7.6p8 ‚Äî Additional implementation-defined rounding directions may be specified (`FE_` + uppercase letter). ‚Äî (spec; permission, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6p9 ‚Äî The macro `FE_DFL_ENV` represents the default environment installed at program startup and expands to an expression of type "pointer to const-qualified `fenv_t`". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`const fenv_t *p = FE_DFL_ENV;` compiles; `fesetenv(FE_DFL_ENV)` runs)
- ¬ß7.6p9 ‚Äî Additional environment macros may be specified, each beginning `FE_` + uppercase letter and each of type "pointer to const-qualified `fenv_t`". ‚Äî (spec; permission, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.6.1 The `FENV_ACCESS` pragma

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <fenv.h>` then `#pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS on-off-switch` where `on-off-switch` ‚àà {`ON`, `OFF`, `DEFAULT`}. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc parses + validates the switch ‚Äî warns on malformed e.g. `BOGUSVAL`; gcc warns "ignoring #pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS" i.e. unimplemented; clang accepts)
- ¬ß7.6.1p2 ‚Äî The pragma informs the implementation when a program might access the floating-point environment (test status flags or run under non-default control modes). ‚Äî (spec; intent, not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ß7.6.1p2 ‚Äî The pragma shall occur either outside external declarations or preceding all explicit declarations and statements inside a compound statement; in any other context its behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (clang *errors* on misplacement; mcc accepts misplaced pragma silently (no diagnostic); gcc ignores the pragma entirely ‚Äî no gcc==clang consensus)
- [~] ¬ß7.6.1p2 ‚Äî Outside external declarations the pragma takes effect from its occurrence until another `FENV_ACCESS` pragma or the end of the translation unit. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc tracks state in `MCCState.stdc_*` per `src/mccpp.c:1921`; effect on codegen not separately verifiable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.1p2 ‚Äî Inside a compound statement the pragma takes effect until another `FENV_ACCESS` pragma or the end of the compound statement; at the end of the block the pragma state is restored to its condition just before the block. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc explicitly does not leak the STDC pragma past the closing brace ‚Äî `src/mccgen.c:8393` restores it block-scoped)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.1p2 ‚Äî The default state (`ON` or `OFF`) for the pragma is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all default to OFF; permitted)
- ¬ß7.6.1p3 ‚Äî If part of a program tests status flags / sets control modes / runs under non-default modes but was translated with `FENV_ACCESS` "off", the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ß7.6.1p3 ‚Äî With state "on" the implementation shall not perform optimizations (CSE, code motion, constant folding) that could defeat access to the FP environment; with state "off" it may. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (not separately verifiable at -O0; mcc is a tcc-lineage compiler doing minimal FP optimization, so flag/mode access is preserved in practice; full optimization-barrier semantics unverified for all three)

#### ¬ß7.6.2 Floating-point exceptions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2p1 ‚Äî The functions in 7.6.2 provide access to the floating-point status flags. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2p1 ‚Äî The `int` argument represents a subset of exceptions: zero or the bitwise OR of one or more exception macros (e.g., `FE_OVERFLOW | FE_INEXACT`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (OR'd masks accepted and acted upon)
- ¬ß7.6.2p1 ‚Äî For other argument values the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.6.2.1 The `feclearexcept` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int feclearexcept(int excepts);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.1p2 ‚Äî Attempts to clear the supported exceptions represented by its argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`feclearexcept(FE_ALL_EXCEPT)` then `fetestexcept` reads 0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if `excepts` is zero or all specified exceptions were successfully cleared; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (returns 0)

##### ¬ß7.6.2.2 The `fegetexceptflag` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fegetexceptflag(fexcept_t *flagp, int excepts);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.2p2 ‚Äî Attempts to store an implementation-defined representation of the indicated status flags in `*flagp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.2p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if the representation was successfully stored; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.2.3 The `feraiseexcept` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int feraiseexcept(int excepts);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.3p2 ‚Äî Attempts to raise the supported exceptions represented by its argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`feraiseexcept(FE_INEXACT)` then `fetestexcept(FE_INEXACT)` nonzero)
- ¬ß7.6.2.3p2 ‚Äî The order in which exceptions are raised is unspecified, except as stated in F.8.6 (C11; F.7.6 in C99). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-order, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.6.2.3p2 ‚Äî Whether `feraiseexcept` additionally raises "inexact" when it raises "overflow"/"underflow" is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.3p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if `excepts` is zero or all specified exceptions were successfully raised; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.2.4 The `fesetexceptflag` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fesetexceptflag(const fexcept_t *flagp, int excepts);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.4p2 ‚Äî Attempts to set the indicated status flags to the states stored in `*flagp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.6.2.4p2 ‚Äî `*flagp` shall have been set by a previous `fegetexceptflag` whose second argument covered at least those exceptions. ‚Äî (spec; precondition/UB, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.6.2.4p2 ‚Äî This function does not raise exceptions, only sets the flag state. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.4p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if `excepts` is zero or all specified flags were successfully set; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.2.5 The `fetestexcept` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fetestexcept(int excepts);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.5p2 ‚Äî Determines which of the specified subset of status flags are currently set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (after `1.0/0.0`, `fetestexcept(FE_DIVBYZERO)` is nonzero on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.2.5p3 ‚Äî Returns the bitwise OR of the exception macros corresponding to the currently-set exceptions included in `excepts`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.6.3 Rounding

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3p1 ‚Äî `fegetround`/`fesetround` provide control of rounding direction modes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.3.1 The `fegetround` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fegetround(void);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3.1p2 ‚Äî Gets the current rounding direction. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (returns `FE_TONEAREST`==0 by default)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3.1p3 ‚Äî Returns the rounding-direction macro for the current direction, or a negative value if none / not determinable. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.3.2 The `fesetround` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fesetround(int round);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3.2p2 ‚Äî Establishes the rounding direction represented by `round`; if `round` is not a rounding-direction macro value, the direction is not changed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fesetround(FE_TOWARDZERO)` then `fegetround()` == `FE_TOWARDZERO`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.3.2p3 ‚Äî Returns zero iff the requested direction was established. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.6.4 Environment

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4p1 ‚Äî These functions manage the floating-point environment (status flags and control modes) as one entity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.4.1 The `fegetenv` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fegetenv(fenv_t *envp);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.1p2 ‚Äî Attempts to store the current floating-point environment in `*envp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.1p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if successfully stored; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.4.2 The `feholdexcept` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int feholdexcept(fenv_t *envp);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.2p2 ‚Äî Saves the current environment in `*envp`, clears the status flags, and installs non-stop (continue-on-exception) mode for all exceptions if available. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.2p3 ‚Äî Returns zero iff non-stop exception handling was successfully installed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (returns 0 on x86-64)

##### ¬ß7.6.4.3 The `fesetenv` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fesetenv(const fenv_t *envp);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.3p2 ‚Äî Attempts to establish the environment represented by `*envp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.3p2 ‚Äî `envp` shall point to an object set by `fegetenv`/`feholdexcept`, or equal an environment macro (e.g., `FE_DFL_ENV`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fesetenv(FE_DFL_ENV)` runs)
- ¬ß7.6.4.3p2 ‚Äî `fesetenv` merely installs the flag state represented by its argument and does not raise those exceptions. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.3p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if the environment was successfully established; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.6.4.4 The `feupdateenv` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int feupdateenv(const fenv_t *envp);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.4p2 ‚Äî Saves currently raised exceptions in automatic storage, installs the environment from `*envp`, then re-raises the saved exceptions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.6.4.4p2 ‚Äî `envp` shall point to an object set by `feholdexcept`/`fegetenv`, or equal an environment macro (e.g., `FE_DFL_ENV`). ‚Äî (spec; precondition, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.6.4.4p3 ‚Äî Returns zero if all actions were successfully carried out; otherwise nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.7 `<float.h>`

> mcc serves its **own bundled** `runtime/include/float.h` (109 lines), not the system header ‚Äî confirmed via `-E` (`# 1 "/home/llg/Projects/moderncc/runtime/include/float.h"`). It is complete and includes all C11 additions, with per-`LDBL`-format branches (53/64/113-bit). gcc/clang use their own `float.h`. All values agree at runtime.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.7p1 ‚Äî The header `<float.h>` defines several macros that expand to various limits and parameters of the standard floating types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.7p2 ‚Äî The macros, meanings, and value constraints are listed in 5.2.4.2.2. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.7 (gap) ‚Äî `<float.h>` shall be usable in a freestanding implementation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (header has no includes/decls; compiles under `-ffreestanding`)

#### ¬ß5.2.4.2.2 Characteristics of floating types `<float.h>`

> C99‚ÜíC11: C11 adds `*_HAS_SUBNORM` (p6), `*_DECIMAL_DIG` macros, `*_TRUE_MIN` (p11), and explicit normalized/subnormal/unnormalized terminology (p2); in C11 `DECIMAL_DIG` equals the widest type's `*_DECIMAL_DIG`. mcc's bundled `float.h` provides all of these.

- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p1 ‚Äî Floating types are defined via the model `x = s ¬∑ b^e ¬∑ Œ£(f_k ¬∑ b^(‚àík))`, k=1..p, with parameters s (sign ¬±1), b (radix >1), e (exponent in [e_min,e_max]), p (precision = base-b significand digits), f_k (significand digits, 0 ‚â§ f_k < b). ‚Äî (spec; definitional, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p2 ‚Äî A number is normalized if f_1>0; a subnormal is a nonzero number not normalized with exponent e_min; an unnormalized number is nonzero, not normalized, with exponent > e_min. (C11) ‚Äî (spec; definitional, not separately testable)
- ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p3 ‚Äî The accuracy of `+ - * /` and of the floating-result `<math.h>`/`<complex.h>` library functions is implementation-defined, as is the accuracy of FP‚Üîstring conversions in `<stdio.h>`/`<stdlib.h>`/`<wchar.h>`; the implementation may state the accuracy is unknown. ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p4 ‚Äî `FLT_ROUNDS` characterizes the rounding mode for FP addition: ‚àí1 indeterminable, 0 toward zero, 1 to nearest, 2 toward +‚àû, 3 toward ‚àí‚àû; any other value impl-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (default 1; all three print 1)
- [~] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p4 ‚Äî `FLT_ROUNDS` may change with a call to `fesetround`; it is therefore not necessarily constant and need not be usable in `#if`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (clang's `FLT_ROUNDS` is *dynamic* ‚Äî returns 0 after `fesetround(FE_TOWARDZERO)`; mcc's bundled value is hardcoded `#define FLT_ROUNDS 1` so it stays 1; gcc *also* stays 1 here ‚Äî no gcc==clang consensus, but mcc/gcc both fail to reflect dynamic rounding)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p5 ‚Äî `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` (C99) characterizes evaluation formats: ‚àí1 indeterminable, 0 evaluate to each type's own range/precision, 1 evaluate float/double ops to double, 2 evaluate all ops to long double; other negative values impl-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: 0 on x86-64 SSE; mcc bundles 0/2 branches on `__SSE2_MATH__`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p6 ‚Äî `FLT_HAS_SUBNORM`/`DBL_HAS_SUBNORM`/`LDBL_HAS_SUBNORM` (C11): ‚àí1 indeterminable, 0 absent, 1 present. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc bundled = 1; `#if FLT_HAS_SUBNORM!=1 #error` passes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî The integer-valued macros shall be replaced by constant expressions suitable for `#if`: `FLT_RADIX`, `*_MANT_DIG`, `*_DECIMAL_DIG` (C11), `DECIMAL_DIG`, `*_DIG`, `*_MIN_EXP`, `*_MIN_10_EXP`, `*_MAX_EXP`, `*_MAX_10_EXP`, `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` (and `*_HAS_SUBNORM` in C11) ‚Äî but **not** `FLT_ROUNDS`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (large `#if` chain over all of these compiles on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_RADIX` ‚Äî radix b of the exponent representation; value shall be ‚â• 2. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (=2; `#if FLT_RADIX<2 #error` passes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_MANT_DIG`/`DBL_MANT_DIG`/`LDBL_MANT_DIG` ‚Äî number of base-`FLT_RADIX` significand digits p. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (24/53/64; verified in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_DECIMAL_DIG`/`DBL_DECIMAL_DIG`/`LDBL_DECIMAL_DIG` (C11) ‚Äî round-trip decimal digits n; values ‚â• 6, ‚â• 10, ‚â• 10. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc bundled 9/17/21; verified ‚â• bounds in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `DECIMAL_DIG` (C99) ‚Äî round-trip decimal digits for the widest supported floating type; value ‚â• 10 (in C11 equals widest `*_DECIMAL_DIG`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc bundled 21 on 80-bit long double, == `LDBL_DECIMAL_DIG`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_DIG`/`DBL_DIG`/`LDBL_DIG` ‚Äî decimal digits q surviving decimal‚Üífloat‚Üídecimal round-trip; values ‚â• 6, ‚â• 10, ‚â• 10. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (6/15/18; verified in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_MIN_EXP`/`DBL_MIN_EXP`/`LDBL_MIN_EXP` ‚Äî minimum negative e such that b^(e‚àí1) is normalized (e_min). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (‚àí125/‚àí1021/‚àí16381)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_MIN_10_EXP`/`DBL_MIN_10_EXP`/`LDBL_MIN_10_EXP` ‚Äî min negative integer with 10^x in the normalized range; values ‚â§ ‚àí37. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if FLT_MIN_10_EXP > -37 #error` passes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_MAX_EXP`/`DBL_MAX_EXP`/`LDBL_MAX_EXP` ‚Äî max integer such that b^(e‚àí1) is a representable finite value (e_max). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (128/1024/16384)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p7 ‚Äî `FLT_MAX_10_EXP`/`DBL_MAX_10_EXP`/`LDBL_MAX_10_EXP` ‚Äî max integer with 10^x in the representable finite range; values ‚â• +37. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if FLT_MAX_10_EXP < 37 #error` passes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p8 ‚Äî `FLT_MAX`/`DBL_MAX`/`LDBL_MAX` (max finite value, `(1‚àíb^‚àíp)¬∑b^e_max`) shall be constant expressions ‚â• `1√ó10^37`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (3.40282e+38 / 1.79769e+308 print identically across all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p9 ‚Äî `FLT_EPSILON`/`DBL_EPSILON`/`LDBL_EPSILON` (`b^(1‚àíp)`) shall be constant expressions ‚â§ `1E‚àí5`, `1E‚àí9`, `1E‚àí9` respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (1.19209e-07 etc.; identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p10 ‚Äî `FLT_MIN`/`DBL_MIN`/`LDBL_MIN` (min normalized positive, `b^(e_min‚àí1)`) shall be constant expressions ‚â§ `1E‚àí37` each. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (1.17549e-38 etc.; identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p11 ‚Äî `FLT_TRUE_MIN`/`DBL_TRUE_MIN`/`LDBL_TRUE_MIN` (C11) (min positive value `b^(e_min‚àíp)`, the smallest positive subnormal) shall be constant expressions ‚â§ `1E‚àí37` each. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc bundled 1.4013e-45 etc.; prints identically)
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.2p8‚Äìp11 ‚Äî The floating-valued macros `*_MAX`, `*_MIN`, `*_EPSILON`, and C11 `*_TRUE_MIN` are floating-constant expressions not required to be usable in `#if`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (used as runtime constants; not exercised in `#if`)

### ¬ß7.8 `<inttypes.h>`

> C99‚ÜíC11: `<inttypes.h>` is essentially unchanged (the wide-char forward reference is 7.29.2 in C11 vs 7.24.2 in C99). On this platform it resolves to `/usr/include/inttypes.h` (glibc) for all three compilers; mcc bundles `stdint.h` (which inttypes includes) but not inttypes itself. Full PRI*/SCN* macro families and all four functions verified.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8p1 ‚Äî `<inttypes.h>` includes `<stdint.h>` and extends it with additional facilities for hosted implementations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`INT32_MAX` usable after including only `<inttypes.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8p1 ‚Äî Declares functions for manipulating greatest-width integers and converting numeric strings to greatest-width integers. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`imaxabs`/`imaxdiv`/`strtoimax`/`strtoumax`/`wcstoimax`/`wcstoumax` link and run)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8p1 ‚Äî Declares the type `imaxdiv_t`, a structure that is the type returned by `imaxdiv`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`imaxdiv_t d = imaxdiv(17,5); d.quot d.rem` work)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8p1 ‚Äî For each `<stdint.h>` type, defines corresponding format-specifier macros for the formatted I/O functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.8p2 ‚Äî A program may use the macros to define its own macros for the formatted I/O functions (forward refs: 7.20, 7.21.6, 7.29.2/7.24.2). ‚Äî (spec; permission, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.8.1 Macros for format specifiers

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p1 ‚Äî Each listed object-like macro expands to a character string literal containing a conversion specifier (possibly with a length modifier) suitable for the format argument of a formatted I/O function for the corresponding integer type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p1 ‚Äî Macro names have the form `PRI` (printf/wprintf family) or `SCN` (scanf/wscanf family) + conversion specifier + a name corresponding to a 7.20.1 type name; `N` represents the type width (e.g. 8, 16, 32, 64). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p2 ‚Äî The `fprintf` signed-integer macros shall be defined: `PRIdN`/`PRIdLEASTN`/`PRIdFASTN`/`PRIdMAX`/`PRIdPTR` and `PRIiN`/`PRIiLEASTN`/`PRIiFASTN`/`PRIiMAX`/`PRIiPTR`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`PRIdMAX`, `PRId32`, `PRIiMAX` produce correct output)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p3 ‚Äî The `fprintf` unsigned-integer macros shall be defined: `PRIo*`, `PRIu*`, `PRIx*`, `PRIX*` over `N`/`LEASTN`/`FASTN`/`MAX`/`PTR`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`PRIu64`, `PRIxLEAST16`, `PRIoFAST8`, `PRIuPTR`, `PRIXMAX` all correct)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p4 ‚Äî The `fscanf` signed-integer macros shall be defined: `SCNdN`/`SCNdLEASTN`/`SCNdFASTN`/`SCNdMAX`/`SCNdPTR` and `SCNi*`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`SCNd64` round-trips through `sscanf`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p5 ‚Äî The `fscanf` unsigned-integer macros shall be defined: `SCNo*`, `SCNu*`, `SCNx*` over `N`/`LEASTN`/`FASTN`/`MAX`/`PTR`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`SCNx16`, `SCNu32` round-trip through `sscanf`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p6 ‚Äî For each type the implementation provides in `<stdint.h>`, the corresponding `fprintf` macros shall be defined and the `fscanf` macros shall be defined unless there is no suitable `fscanf` length modifier for the type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.1p7 ‚Äî (EXAMPLE) `printf("%020" PRIdMAX "\n", i)` and `scanf("%10" SCNd64 "\n", &i)` work as shown. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`printf("%020" PRIdMAX, ...)` ‚Üí `-0000001234567890123` on all three)

#### ¬ß7.8.2 Functions for greatest-width integer types

##### ¬ß7.8.2.1 The `imaxabs` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `intmax_t imaxabs(intmax_t j);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.1p2 ‚Äî Computes the absolute value of `j`; if the result cannot be represented, behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`imaxabs(-42)==42`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns the absolute value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.8.2.2 The `imaxdiv` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `imaxdiv_t imaxdiv(intmax_t numer, intmax_t denom);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.2p2 ‚Äî Computes `numer / denom` and `numer % denom` in a single operation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`imaxdiv(17,5)` ‚Üí quot 3, rem 2)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.2p3 ‚Äî Returns an `imaxdiv_t` with both quotient and remainder; the struct contains (in either order) members `quot` and `rem`, each of type `intmax_t`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.8.2.2p3 ‚Äî If either part of the result cannot be represented, behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.8.2.3 The `strtoimax` and `strtoumax` functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `intmax_t strtoimax(const char *restrict nptr, char **restrict endptr, int base);` and `uintmax_t strtoumax(...)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.3p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `strtol`/`strtoll`/`strtoul`/`strtoull` except converting to `intmax_t`/`uintmax_t`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strtoimax("  -ff",&e,16)==-255`; `strtoumax("100",0,10)==100`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.3p3 ‚Äî Returns the converted value (zero if no conversion); on overflow returns `INTMAX_MAX`/`INTMAX_MIN`/`UINTMAX_MAX` per return type/sign and stores `ERANGE` in `errno`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc runtime)

##### ¬ß7.8.2.4 The `wcstoimax` and `wcstoumax` functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis (with `<stddef.h>` for `wchar_t` and `<inttypes.h>`): `intmax_t wcstoimax(const wchar_t *restrict nptr, wchar_t **restrict endptr, int base);` and `uintmax_t wcstoumax(...)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.4p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `wcstol`/`wcstoll`/`wcstoul`/`wcstoull` except converting to `intmax_t`/`uintmax_t`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcstoimax(L"123",0,10)==123`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.8.2.4p3 ‚Äî Returns the converted value (zero if none); on overflow returns `INTMAX_MAX`/`INTMAX_MIN`/`UINTMAX_MAX` per return type/sign and stores `ERANGE` in `errno`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc runtime)


## ¬ß7.9-¬ß7.11 iso646, limits, locale

> mcc status: 92 TODO checkboxes below; 0 mcc-gaps. `<iso646.h>` and `<limits.h>` are mcc-bundled (`runtime/include/`) and conform byte-for-byte to gcc/clang; mcc bundles **no** `<locale.h>` and forwards to the host C library, so all `<locale.h>` behavior is identical to gcc/clang on the same system. Probed: all 11 iso646 macros (value + token identity + `#if` expansion), every `<limits.h>` macro value, `#if`-preprocessor usability, the C11 "same type after promotion" rule via `_Generic`, the freestanding fallback path, and the full "C"-locale `struct lconv` contents.

### ¬ß7.9 Alternative spellings `<iso646.h>`

> mcc ships a complete `runtime/include/iso646.h` defining all eleven macros exactly as required. C99 and C11 are identical here; in C++ these eleven names are keywords rather than macros. Probe: `a and b`, `a or b`, `not b`, `a not_eq b`, `a and_eq ‚Ä¶`, `or_eq`, `xor_eq`, `a bitand b`==2, `a bitor b`==7, `a xor b`==5, `compl a`==‚àí7 all produced identical results on all three compilers.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî The header `<iso646.h>` shall define eleven object-like macros that expand to the corresponding operator tokens. *(mcc: provided in `runtime/include/iso646.h`.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `and` shall expand to `&&`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `and_eq` shall expand to `&=`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `bitand` shall expand to `&`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `bitor` shall expand to `|`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `compl` shall expand to `~`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `not` shall expand to `!`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `not_eq` shall expand to `!=`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `or` shall expand to `||`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `or_eq` shall expand to `|=`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `xor` shall expand to `^`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 ‚Äî `xor_eq` shall expand to `^=`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p2 (GAP) ‚Äî These macros shall be usable in `#if`/`#elif` preprocessing directives (e.g. `#if INT_MAX >= 32767 and LONG_MAX > INT_MAX`), since they expand to operator punctuators that the controlling-expression evaluator accepts. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: `#if ‚Ä¶ and ‚Ä¶ or ‚Ä¶` compiled and ran on all three)*
- ¬ß7.1.3 ‚Äî Each of these eleven names is reserved as a macro only when `<iso646.h>` is included; while so defined the program shall not `#define` or `#undef` it (constraint of ¬ß7.1.3). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable) *(no diagnostic required; mcc, gcc, and clang all silently accept `#undef and` / `#define and 5` ‚Äî consensus is no diagnostic)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.9p1 (GAP) ‚Äî The header shall be idempotent / multiple-inclusion safe (include guard). *(mcc: `#ifndef _ISO646_H` guard present.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.10 Sizes of integer types `<limits.h>`

> ¬ß7.10p2 forwards to ¬ß5.2.4.2.1 for the macros, their meanings, and the value constraints. C99 added `LLONG_MIN`/`LLONG_MAX`/`ULLONG_MAX` (not in C90). C11 added to ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 the sentence requiring each macro to have the same type as the corresponding object after integer promotions; C99 lacked that explicit type requirement. Probe: every macro printed identical values across mcc/gcc/clang on x86-64 (CHAR_BIT=8, 32-bit `int`, 64-bit `long`/`long long`, signed plain `char`).

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.10p1 ‚Äî The header `<limits.h>` shall define several macros that expand to various limits and parameters of the standard integer types. *(mcc: `runtime/include/limits.h`, which `#include_next`s the host `<limits.h>` when hosted and supplies fallbacks otherwise.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.10p2 / ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî The values defined in `<limits.h>` shall be replaced by constant expressions suitable for use in `#if` preprocessing directives. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed `#if ULLONG_MAX > 0 && LLONG_MIN < 0` etc.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî Each defined limit shall have the same type as would an expression that is an object of the corresponding type converted according to the integer promotions. *(C11 addition; absent in C99.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed via `_Generic`: UINT_MAX‚Üíunsigned int, INT_MAX‚Üíint, ULONG_MAX‚Üíunsigned long, LLONG_MAX‚Üílong long, USHRT_MAX/UCHAR_MAX‚Üíint (promoted) on all three)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî Each macro's implementation-defined value shall be equal to or greater in magnitude than (absolute value of) the value shown, with the same sign. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `CHAR_BIT` ‚Äî number of bits for the smallest object that is not a bit-field (a byte); value shall be ‚â• 8. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=8)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SCHAR_MIN` ‚Äî minimum value for an object of type `signed char`; value shall be ‚â§ ‚àí127. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=‚àí128)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SCHAR_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `signed char`; value shall be ‚â• +127. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=127)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `UCHAR_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `unsigned char`; value shall be ‚â• 255. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=255)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `MB_LEN_MAX` ‚Äî maximum number of bytes in a multibyte character, for any supported locale; value shall be ‚â• 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(host glibc =16; mcc bundled fallback also 16)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SHRT_MIN` ‚Äî minimum value for an object of type `short int`; value shall be ‚â§ ‚àí32767. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=‚àí32768)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `SHRT_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `short int`; value shall be ‚â• +32767. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=32767)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `USHRT_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `unsigned short int`; value shall be ‚â• 65535. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=65535)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `INT_MIN` ‚Äî minimum value for an object of type `int`; value shall be ‚â§ ‚àí32767. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=‚àí2147483648)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `INT_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `int`; value shall be ‚â• +32767. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=2147483647)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `UINT_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `unsigned int`; value shall be ‚â• 65535. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=4294967295)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LONG_MIN` ‚Äî minimum value for an object of type `long int`; value shall be ‚â§ ‚àí2147483647. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=‚àí9223372036854775808)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LONG_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `long int`; value shall be ‚â• +2147483647. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=9223372036854775807)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `ULONG_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `unsigned long int`; value shall be ‚â• 4294967295. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=18446744073709551615)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LLONG_MIN` ‚Äî minimum value for an object of type `long long int`; value shall be ‚â§ ‚àí9223372036854775807. *(C99 addition; not present in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=‚àí9223372036854775808)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `LLONG_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `long long int`; value shall be ‚â• +9223372036854775807. *(C99 addition; not present in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=9223372036854775807)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî `ULLONG_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type `unsigned long long int`; value shall be ‚â• 18446744073709551615. *(C99 addition; not present in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(=18446744073709551615)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî `CHAR_MIN` ‚Äî minimum value for an object of type plain `char`; if `char` is treated as signed it shall equal `SCHAR_MIN`, otherwise (plain `char` unsigned) it shall be 0. *(mcc bundled header selects via `'\xff' > 0`, matching per-target plain-char signedness.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(x86-64 signed: =‚àí128=SCHAR_MIN)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß5.2.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî `CHAR_MAX` ‚Äî maximum value for an object of type plain `char`; if `char` is treated as signed it shall equal `SCHAR_MAX`, otherwise it shall equal `UCHAR_MAX`. Whether plain `char` is signed is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(x86-64 signed: =127=SCHAR_MAX)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.10p1 (GAP) ‚Äî The header shall be multiple-inclusion safe (include guard). *(mcc: `#ifndef _MCC_LIMITS_H` guard; inner host header has its own guard.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.10p1 (GAP) ‚Äî In a freestanding/`-ffreestanding` translation (no host `<limits.h>` to chain to) the header shall still define the required macros from compiler built-ins. *(mcc: `#if __has_include_next(<limits.h>)` guards the chain and the `__CHAR_BIT__`/`__INT_MAX__`/`__LONG_MAX__`/`__LONG_LONG_MAX__` fallbacks define the rest.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed `mcc -ffreestanding -c` with `int a[INT_MAX>0?1:-1]; int b=CHAR_BIT;` ‚Äî compiles)*
- ¬ß6.10.8.2 (GAP, C11) ‚Äî Macros required to use `<limits.h>` indirectly: `__STDC_*` width/limit signalling is not part of ¬ß7.10; no extra macros beyond ¬ß5.2.4.2.1 are mandated. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.11 Localization `<locale.h>`

> mcc bundles **no** `runtime/include/locale.h`; it relies on the host/system `<locale.h>` (glibc here). Consequently every `<locale.h>` requirement below is satisfied to exactly the degree the host C library satisfies it, and mcc's result is byte-identical to gcc's and clang's on the same system. C11 adds `wcsftime` (in `<wchar.h>`) to the list of functions affected by `LC_TIME`; otherwise ¬ß7.11 is unchanged from C99. Probe: `setlocale`/`localeconv` link and run; the entire "C"-locale `struct lconv` matched the standard (decimal_point=".", all other strings "", all `char` members = CHAR_MAX=127) identically on all three.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11p1 ‚Äî The header `<locale.h>` shall declare two functions (`setlocale`, `localeconv`), define one type (`struct lconv`), and define several macros. *(mcc: no bundled `locale.h`; uses the C library's.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11p1 ‚Äî The type `struct lconv` shall contain members related to the formatting of numeric values, with at least the members described in ¬ß7.11.2.1 (in any order, with the specified types); in the "C" locale they shall have the values given in the `localeconv` description. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(host-provided; probed)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11p2 ‚Äî The macro `NULL` shall be defined (as described in ¬ß7.17). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11p2 ‚Äî The macros `LC_ALL`, `LC_COLLATE`, `LC_CTYPE`, `LC_MONETARY`, `LC_NUMERIC`, and `LC_TIME` shall each be defined, expanding to an integer constant expression with distinct values, suitable for use as the first argument to `setlocale`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed distinct: 6/3/0/4/1/2 on all three)*
- ¬ß7.11p2 ‚Äî Additional macros beginning with `LC_` and an uppercase letter may be defined by the implementation (reserved for future additional locale categories). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable) *(host glibc defines extras e.g. `LC_PAPER`, `LC_MESSAGES`; identical for all three)*

#### ¬ß7.11.1 Locale control

##### ¬ß7.11.1.1 The `setlocale` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <locale.h>` followed by `char *setlocale(int category, const char *locale);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `setlocale` selects the appropriate portion of the program's locale as specified by `category` and `locale`, and may be used to change or query the entire current locale or portions thereof. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(host-provided)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `category == LC_ALL` names the program's entire locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `category == LC_COLLATE` affects the behavior of the `strcoll` and `strxfrm` functions. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately probed)
- [ ] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `category == LC_CTYPE` affects the behavior of the character-handling functions and the multibyte and wide-character functions. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately probed)
- [ ] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `category == LC_MONETARY` affects the monetary formatting information returned by `localeconv`. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately probed)
- [ ] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `category == LC_NUMERIC` affects the decimal-point character for the formatted input/output functions and the string conversion functions, plus the nonmonetary formatting information returned by `localeconv`. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately probed)
- [ ] ¬ß7.11.1.1p2 ‚Äî `category == LC_TIME` affects the behavior of the `strftime` and (C11) `wcsftime` functions. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately probed)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p3 ‚Äî `locale == "C"` specifies the minimal environment for C translation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed `setlocale(LC_ALL,"C")` returns "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p3 ‚Äî `locale == ""` specifies the locale-specific native environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(host-provided)*
- ¬ß7.11.1.1p3 ‚Äî Other implementation-defined strings may be passed as the `locale` argument. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p4 ‚Äî At program startup the equivalent of `setlocale(LC_ALL, "C");` is executed (the program begins in the "C" locale). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: `setlocale(LC_ALL,NULL)` at startup returns "C" on all three)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p5/p7 ‚Äî A null pointer for `locale` causes `setlocale` to return a pointer to the string associated with `category` for the program's current locale, without changing the locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p6 ‚Äî The returned string is such that a subsequent `setlocale` call with that string value and its associated `category` will restore that part of the program's locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(host-provided)*
- ¬ß7.11.1.1p6 ‚Äî The string returned by `setlocale` shall not be modified by the program, but may be overwritten by a subsequent call to `setlocale`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî UB if modified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p7 ‚Äî Returns: if a pointer to a string is given for `locale` and the selection can be honored, `setlocale` returns a pointer to the string associated with the specified `category` for the new locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "C" ‚Üí "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.1.1p7 ‚Äî Returns: if the selection cannot be honored, `setlocale` returns a null pointer and the program's locale is not changed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: bogus locale name ‚Üí NULL on all three)*
- ¬ß7.11.1.1p7 footnote ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `setlocale` (no standard library function alters the locale as a side effect). ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.11.2 Numeric formatting convention inquiry

##### ¬ß7.11.2.1 The `localeconv` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <locale.h>` followed by `struct lconv *localeconv(void);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p2 ‚Äî `localeconv` sets the components of an object of type `struct lconv` with values appropriate for formatting numeric quantities (monetary and otherwise) according to the rules of the current locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(host-provided; probed)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî Members of type `char *` are pointers to strings, any of which (except `decimal_point`) can point to `""` to indicate that the value is not available in the current locale or is of zero length. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed in "C": all non-decimal_point strings = "")*
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî Apart from `grouping` and `mon_grouping`, the `char *` strings shall start and end in the initial shift state. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî Members of type `char` are nonnegative numbers, any of which can be `CHAR_MAX` to indicate that the value is not available in the current locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed in "C": all = CHAR_MAX=127)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *decimal_point` ‚Äî the decimal-point character used to format nonmonetary quantities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "." in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *thousands_sep` ‚Äî the character used to separate groups of digits before the decimal-point character in formatted nonmonetary quantities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *grouping` ‚Äî a string whose elements indicate the size of each group of digits in formatted nonmonetary quantities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *mon_decimal_point` ‚Äî the decimal-point character used to format monetary quantities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *mon_thousands_sep` ‚Äî the separator for groups of digits before the decimal-point character in formatted monetary quantities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *mon_grouping` ‚Äî a string whose elements indicate the size of each group of digits in formatted monetary quantities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *positive_sign` ‚Äî the string used to indicate a nonnegative-valued formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *negative_sign` ‚Äî the string used to indicate a negative-valued formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *currency_symbol` ‚Äî the local currency symbol applicable to the current locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char *int_curr_symbol` ‚Äî the international currency symbol; the first three characters hold the alphabetic ISO 4217 currency symbol and the fourth character (immediately preceding the null) is the separator between the symbol and the monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: "" in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char frac_digits` ‚Äî the number of fractional digits (after the decimal-point) to display in a locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char p_cs_precedes` ‚Äî 1 or 0 if `currency_symbol` respectively precedes or succeeds the value for a nonnegative locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char n_cs_precedes` ‚Äî 1 or 0 if `currency_symbol` respectively precedes or succeeds the value for a negative locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char p_sep_by_space` ‚Äî value indicating the separation of `currency_symbol`, the sign string, and the value for a nonnegative locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char n_sep_by_space` ‚Äî value indicating the separation of `currency_symbol`, the sign string, and the value for a negative locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char p_sign_posn` ‚Äî value indicating the positioning of `positive_sign` for a nonnegative locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char n_sign_posn` ‚Äî value indicating the positioning of `negative_sign` for a negative locally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_frac_digits` ‚Äî the number of fractional digits (after the decimal-point) to display in an internationally formatted monetary quantity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_p_cs_precedes` ‚Äî 1 or 0 if `int_curr_symbol` respectively precedes or succeeds the value for a nonnegative internationally formatted monetary quantity. *(C99 addition; not in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_n_cs_precedes` ‚Äî 1 or 0 if `int_curr_symbol` respectively precedes or succeeds the value for a negative internationally formatted monetary quantity. *(C99 addition; not in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_p_sep_by_space` ‚Äî value indicating the separation of `int_curr_symbol`, the sign string, and the value for a nonnegative internationally formatted monetary quantity. *(C99 addition; not in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_n_sep_by_space` ‚Äî value indicating the separation of `int_curr_symbol`, the sign string, and the value for a negative internationally formatted monetary quantity. *(C99 addition; not in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_p_sign_posn` ‚Äî value indicating the positioning of `positive_sign` for a nonnegative internationally formatted monetary quantity. *(C99 addition; not in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: CHAR_MAX in "C")*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p3 ‚Äî `char int_n_sign_posn` ‚Äî value indicating the positioning of `negative_sign` for a negative internationally formatted monetary quantity. *(C99 addition; not in C90.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p4 ‚Äî In `grouping`/`mon_grouping`: an element value of `CHAR_MAX` means no further grouping is to be performed. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p4 ‚Äî In `grouping`/`mon_grouping`: an element value of `0` means the previous element is to be repeatedly used for the remainder of the digits. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p4 ‚Äî In `grouping`/`mon_grouping`: any other (positive) value is the number of digits composing the current group; the next element gives the size of the next group of digits before the current group. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p5 ‚Äî `p_sep_by_space`/`n_sep_by_space`/`int_p_sep_by_space`/`int_n_sep_by_space` are interpreted as: `0` ‚Äî no space separates the currency symbol and value; `1` ‚Äî if the currency symbol and sign string are adjacent, a space separates them from the value, otherwise a space separates the currency symbol from the value; `2` ‚Äî if the currency symbol and sign string are adjacent, a space separates them, otherwise a space separates the sign string from the value. (For an `int_` member, the fourth character of `int_curr_symbol` is used in place of a space.) ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p6 ‚Äî `p_sign_posn`/`n_sign_posn`/`int_p_sign_posn`/`int_n_sign_posn` are interpreted as: `0` ‚Äî parentheses surround the quantity and currency symbol; `1` ‚Äî the sign string precedes the quantity and currency symbol; `2` ‚Äî the sign string succeeds the quantity and currency symbol; `3` ‚Äî the sign string immediately precedes the currency symbol; `4` ‚Äî the sign string immediately succeeds the currency symbol. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p7 ‚Äî In the "C" locale: `decimal_point` shall be `"."`; and `thousands_sep`, `grouping`, `mon_decimal_point`, `mon_thousands_sep`, `mon_grouping`, `positive_sign`, `negative_sign`, `currency_symbol`, and `int_curr_symbol` shall each be `""`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: exact match on all three)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p7 ‚Äî In the "C" locale: `frac_digits`, `p_cs_precedes`, `n_cs_precedes`, `p_sep_by_space`, `n_sep_by_space`, `p_sign_posn`, `n_sign_posn`, `int_frac_digits`, `int_p_cs_precedes`, `int_n_cs_precedes`, `int_p_sep_by_space`, `int_n_sep_by_space`, `int_p_sign_posn`, and `int_n_sign_posn` shall each be `CHAR_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: all = 127 on all three)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.11.2.1p8 ‚Äî Returns: `localeconv` returns a pointer to the filled-in object; the structure it points to shall not be modified by the program, but may be overwritten by a subsequent call to `localeconv`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(probed: non-null pointer returned)*
- ¬ß7.11.2.1p8 ‚Äî Returns: in addition, calls to `setlocale` with category `LC_ALL`, `LC_MONETARY`, or `LC_NUMERIC` may overwrite the contents of the structure pointed to by a `localeconv` return value. ‚Äî (spec; host-provided, not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.11.2.1p9 (EXAMPLE) ‚Äî Informative example tables illustrating `p_sign_posn`/`n_sign_posn`, `p_cs_precedes`, and `p_sep_by_space` formatting rules (non-normative). ‚Äî (spec; informative, not testable)

#### Cross-cutting / bundled-header notes

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.2 (GAP) ‚Äî `<iso646.h>` and `<limits.h>` shall each be self-contained and includable in any order any number of times. *(mcc: both bundled headers are guarded and standalone; `<locale.h>` deferred to host.)* ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß4 / ¬ß7.11 (GAP) ‚Äî Because mcc ships no `runtime/include/locale.h`, full `<locale.h>` conformance in a *freestanding* configuration is **not** provided (locale is a hosted-only facility; ¬ß4p6 lists only `<float.h> <iso646.h> <limits.h> <stdarg.h> <stdbool.h> <stddef.h> <stdint.h>` (+C11 `<stdalign.h> <stdnoreturn.h>`) as freestanding-required, so this is conformant). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(documentary; locale is not required freestanding)*


## ¬ß7.12 <math.h>

> mcc status: 247 TODO checkboxes below; **1 row carries a `~` mcc tag** (a further `~`, the `FP_CONTRACT` pragma, is shared with gcc and is not an mcc-specific gap). mcc ships **no bundled `<math.h>`** ‚Äî it delegates to the host C library header (glibc here) and links the host `libm`, so every function family compiles, links, and runs identically to gcc/clang. mcc predefines `__GNUC__ 4`, so glibc's `<math.h>` takes its GCC path ‚Äî `NAN` prints `nan` (not `-nan`), `signbit` returns a normalized `0`/`1`, and the type-generic classification/comparison macros use the `__builtin_*` forms, all matching gcc/clang. The one remaining mcc `~` is the implementation note that mcc bundles no `<math.h>` and delegates to glibc (a portability note, not a per-call defect).

The header `<math.h>` declares two types (`float_t`, `double_t`), declares many functions, and defines numerous macros. For every listed function family three variants exist: a `double` version with the bare name, a `float` version with an `f` suffix, and a `long double` version with an `l` suffix; the `f`-suffixed function operates on and returns `float`, and the `l`-suffixed function operates on and returns `long double`. The synopsis checkboxes below give all three prototypes for each family.

> C99 vs C11: C11 (¬ß7.12.1p3) adds the *pole error* concept (exact infinite result as a finite argument is approached, e.g. `log(0)`); C99 instead classified these as range/divide-by-zero events without the dedicated term, and several p2 wordings for `ilogb` were tightened in C11. Differences are tagged `(C11)` / `(C99-only)` inline.

### ¬ß7.12 Introduction ‚Äî types and macros

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p1 ‚Äî `<math.h>` shall declare the types `float_t` and `double_t`, define the macros `HUGE_VAL`, `HUGE_VALF`, `HUGE_VALL`, `INFINITY`, `NAN`, `FP_INFINITE`, `FP_NAN`, `FP_NORMAL`, `FP_SUBNORMAL`, `FP_ZERO`, `FP_FAST_FMA`, `FP_FAST_FMAF`, `FP_FAST_FMAL`, `FP_ILOGB0`, `FP_ILOGBNAN`, `MATH_ERRNO`, `MATH_ERREXCEPT`, `math_errhandling`, and `FP_CONTRACT`, and declare all the math functions in this subclause. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (via host glibc header; all macros/decls present)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p2 ‚Äî `float_t` and `double_t` are floating types at least as wide as `float` and `double`, respectively, with `double_t` at least as wide as `float_t`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(float_t)==4`, `sizeof(double_t)==8`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p2 ‚Äî If `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` equals 0, `float_t` and `double_t` are `float` and `double`, respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`FLT_EVAL_METHOD==0` here; types are `float`/`double`)
- ¬ß7.12p2 ‚Äî If `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` equals 1, `float_t` and `double_t` are both `double`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable on this target ‚Äî header-conditional)
- ¬ß7.12p2 ‚Äî If `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` equals 2, `float_t` and `double_t` are both `long double`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable on this target)
- ¬ß7.12p2 ‚Äî For all other values of `FLT_EVAL_METHOD`, `float_t` and `double_t` are implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p3 ‚Äî `HUGE_VAL` expands to a positive `double` constant expression, not necessarily representable as a `float`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (prints `inf`, positive)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p3 ‚Äî `HUGE_VALF` and `HUGE_VALL` are respectively `float` and `long double` analogs of `HUGE_VAL`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p4 ‚Äî `INFINITY` expands to a constant expression of type `float` representing positive or unsigned infinity if available, else to a positive `float` constant expression that overflows at translation time. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`INFINITY>0` is 1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p5 ‚Äî `NAN` is defined if and only if the implementation supports quiet NaNs for the `float` type, and then expands to a constant expression of type `float` representing a quiet NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (defined and quiet; mcc's `NAN` prints `nan` with `signbit(NAN) == 0`, matching gcc/clang. mcc predefines `__GNUC__ 4`, so glibc's `<math.h>` takes its GCC path and routes `NAN` through `__builtin_nanf`.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p6 ‚Äî `FP_INFINITE`, `FP_NAN`, `FP_NORMAL`, `FP_SUBNORMAL`, and `FP_ZERO` each expand to an integer constant expression with a distinct value, usable in `#if` directives; they are the mutually exclusive number-classification categories returned by `fpclassify`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (distinct `1/0/4/3/2`; usable in `#if`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p7 ‚Äî `FP_FAST_FMA`, `FP_FAST_FMAF`, and `FP_FAST_FMAL` are optionally defined; if defined, each expands to the integer constant `1` to indicate that `fma`/`fmaf`/`fmal` (respectively) generally executes about as fast as, or faster than, a multiply and an add of `double`/`float`/`long double` operands ‚Äî i.e. `fma(x,y,z)` is generally as fast as or faster than `(x*y)+z`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three leave `FP_FAST_FMA` undefined on this target ‚Äî consistent)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p8 ‚Äî `FP_ILOGB0` and `FP_ILOGBNAN` expand to integer constant expressions whose values are returned by `ilogb(x)` when `x` is zero or NaN, respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`FP_ILOGB0 == INT_MIN`, `FP_ILOGBNAN == INT_MIN` on glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p8 ‚Äî The value of `FP_ILOGB0` shall be either `INT_MIN` or `-INT_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`INT_MIN` = -2147483648)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p8 ‚Äî The value of `FP_ILOGBNAN` shall be either `INT_MAX` or `INT_MIN`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`INT_MIN` on glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p9 ‚Äî `MATH_ERRNO` and `MATH_ERREXCEPT` expand to the integer constant expressions `1` and `2`, respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12p9 ‚Äî `math_errhandling` expands to an expression of type `int` whose value is `MATH_ERRNO`, `MATH_ERREXCEPT`, or the bitwise OR of both. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (value `3` = both)
- ¬ß7.12p9 ‚Äî The value of `math_errhandling` is constant for the duration of the program. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.12p9 ‚Äî It is unspecified whether `math_errhandling` is a macro or an identifier with external linkage; where a macro is defined, `#undef` may be used to access an actual function, and an identifier with external linkage exists in either case (a macro definition does not suppress the function). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.12p9 ‚Äî The expression `math_errhandling & MATH_ERREXCEPT` can be nonzero only if `FE_DIVBYZERO`, `FE_INVALID`, or `FE_OVERFLOW` (from `<fenv.h>`) is defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ß7.12 (added) ‚Äî mcc ships **no bundled `<math.h>`** in `runtime/include/`; it relies on the host C library's `<math.h>` and `libm`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (works on a glibc host; a non-glibc / freestanding host would have no `<math.h>` at all, whereas gcc/clang are typically paired with their own runtime story. Portability gap, not a per-call defect.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12 (added) ‚Äî mcc **predefines `__GNUC__ 4`** (`__GNUC_MINOR__ 2`, `__GNUC_PATCHLEVEL__ 1`), so glibc's `<math.h>` takes its GCC path for the type-generic classification/comparison macros. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (the normalized `signbit`, the non-trapping `isgreater`-family, and the `+nan` `NAN` all follow from this, matching the gcc==clang consensus.)

### ¬ß7.12.1 Treatment of error conditions

- ¬ß7.12.1p1 ‚Äî The behavior of each function is specified for arguments within its domain; a function is not required to verify that its argument lies within the function's domain. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.1p2 ‚Äî A domain error occurs if an input argument is outside the domain over which the mathematical function is defined; on a domain error the function returns an implementation-defined value. ‚Äî (spec; library/`libm` behavior, shared across all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.1p2 ‚Äî On a domain error, if `math_errhandling & MATH_ERRNO` is nonzero, `errno` acquires the value `EDOM`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared glibc `libm`; e.g. `sqrt(-1)` sets `errno==EDOM`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.1p2 ‚Äî On a domain error, if `math_errhandling & MATH_ERREXCEPT` is nonzero, the "invalid" floating-point exception is raised. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared `libm`)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) A pole error (singularity, infinitary) occurs if the mathematical function has an exact infinite result as the finite input argument(s) are approached in the limit (e.g. `log(0.0)`). ‚Äî (spec; C11 terminology ‚Äî note mcc defaults `__STDC_VERSION__` to C99/199901L, but the host header still defines the C11 machinery)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) On a pole error, the function returns `HUGE_VAL`, `HUGE_VALF`, or `HUGE_VALL` according to the return type, with the same sign as the correct value of the function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared `libm`; `log(0)` returns `-HUGE_VAL`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) On a pole error, if `math_errhandling & MATH_ERRNO` is nonzero, `errno` acquires the value `ERANGE`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared `libm`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) On a pole error, if `math_errhandling & MATH_ERREXCEPT` is nonzero, the "divide-by-zero" floating-point exception is raised. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared `libm`)
- ¬ß7.12.1p4 ‚Äî A range error occurs if the mathematical result of the function cannot be represented in an object of the specified type, owing to extreme magnitude (overflow or underflow). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.12.1p5 ‚Äî A floating result overflows if the magnitude of the (finite) mathematical result is so large that the result cannot be represented, without extraordinary roundoff error, in an object of the specified type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.1p5 ‚Äî If a floating result overflows and the default rounding mode is in effect, the function returns `HUGE_VAL`, `HUGE_VALF`, or `HUGE_VALL` according to the return type, with the sign of the correct value; if `math_errhandling & MATH_ERRNO` is nonzero, `errno` acquires the value `ERANGE`; if `math_errhandling & MATH_ERREXCEPT` is nonzero, the "overflow" floating-point exception is raised. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared `libm`; e.g. `exp(1000)` ‚Üí `HUGE_VAL`, `errno==ERANGE`)
- ¬ß7.12.1p6 ‚Äî A floating result underflows if the magnitude of the mathematical result is so small that the result cannot be represented, without extraordinary roundoff error, in an object of the specified type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.1p6 ‚Äî If the result underflows, the function returns an implementation-defined value whose magnitude is no greater than the smallest normalized positive number in the specified type; whether `errno` acquires `ERANGE` (when `math_errhandling & MATH_ERRNO` is nonzero) is implementation-defined, and whether the "underflow" floating-point exception is raised (when `math_errhandling & MATH_ERREXCEPT` is nonzero) is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined; shared `libm`)

### ¬ß7.12.2 The FP_CONTRACT pragma

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <math.h>` then `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT on-off-switch`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc and clang accept silently; gcc warns `-Wunknown-pragmas` and ignores it ‚Äî all three accept without error)
- [~] ¬ß7.12.2p1 ‚Äî The `FP_CONTRACT` pragma allows (state "on") or disallows (state "off") the implementation to contract expressions (¬ß6.5). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (none of the three on this target act on the directive at default `-O`; mcc parses-and-ignores it. Effect not observable.)
- ¬ß7.12.2p1 ‚Äî Each pragma may occur either outside external declarations or preceding all explicit declarations and statements inside a compound statement; used in any other context, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB placement ‚Äî not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.2p1 ‚Äî Outside external declarations, the pragma takes effect from its occurrence until another `FP_CONTRACT` pragma is encountered or until the end of the translation unit. ‚Äî (spec; not observable as mcc does not contract)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.2p1 ‚Äî Inside a compound statement, the pragma takes effect from its occurrence until another `FP_CONTRACT` pragma (including within a nested compound statement) or until the end of the compound statement; at the end of that compound statement the pragma state is restored to its condition just before the statement. ‚Äî (spec; not observable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.2p1 ‚Äî The default state ("on" or "off") for the pragma is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined)

### ¬ß7.12.3 Classification macros

- ¬ß7.12.3p1 ‚Äî In the synopses of this subclause, `real-floating` indicates that the argument shall be an expression of real floating type. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.12.3.1 The fpclassify macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fpclassify(real-floating x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.1p2 ‚Äî `fpclassify` classifies its argument value as NaN, infinite, normal, subnormal, zero, or into another implementation-defined category; an argument represented in a wider format than its semantic type is first converted to its semantic type, so classification is based on the type of the argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (type-generic over `float`/`double`/`long double`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.1p3 ‚Äî `fpclassify` returns the value of the number-classification macro (`FP_NAN`, `FP_INFINITE`, `FP_NORMAL`, `FP_SUBNORMAL`, or `FP_ZERO`) appropriate to the value of its argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (normal‚Üí4, NaN‚Üí0, inf‚Üí1, zero‚Üí2, subnormal‚Üí3 ‚Äî all match)

#### ¬ß7.12.3.2 The isfinite macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isfinite(real-floating x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.2p2 ‚Äî `isfinite` determines whether its argument has a finite value (zero, subnormal, or normal ‚Äî not infinite or NaN), after first converting an argument in a wider format to its semantic type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.2p3 ‚Äî `isfinite` returns a nonzero value if and only if its argument has a finite value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (finite‚Üí1, inf‚Üí0, NaN‚Üí0)

#### ¬ß7.12.3.3 The isinf macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isinf(real-floating x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.3p2 ‚Äî `isinf` determines whether its argument value is an infinity (positive or negative), after first converting an argument in a wider format to its semantic type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.3p3 ‚Äî `isinf` returns a nonzero value if and only if its argument has an infinite value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isinf(INFINITY)`‚Üí1, normalized)

#### ¬ß7.12.3.4 The isnan macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isnan(real-floating x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.4p2 ‚Äî `isnan` determines whether its argument value is a NaN, after first converting an argument in a wider format to its semantic type (so the determination is based on the type of the argument). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.4p3 ‚Äî `isnan` returns a nonzero value if and only if its argument has a NaN value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isnan(NAN)`‚Üí1, normalized)

#### ¬ß7.12.3.5 The isnormal macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isnormal(real-floating x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.5p2 ‚Äî `isnormal` determines whether its argument has a normal value (not zero, subnormal, infinite, or NaN), after first converting an argument in a wider format to its semantic type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.5p3 ‚Äî `isnormal` returns a nonzero value if and only if its argument has a normal value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (normal‚Üí1)

#### ¬ß7.12.3.6 The signbit macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int signbit(real-floating x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.6p2 ‚Äî `signbit` determines whether the sign of its argument value is negative. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (correct sign of `-0.0`, `-3.0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.3.6p3 ‚Äî `signbit` returns a nonzero value if and only if the sign of its argument value is negative. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc returns the normalized `0`/`1` ‚Äî `signbit(-3.0)`‚Üí`1`, `signbit(-0.0)`‚Üí`1`, `signbit(3.0)`‚Üí`0` ‚Äî matching gcc/clang, because mcc predefines `__GNUC__ 4` so glibc's `<math.h>` takes its GCC `__builtin_signbit` path.)

### ¬ß7.12.4 Trigonometric functions

#### ¬ß7.12.4.1 The acos functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double acos(double x);`, `float acosf(float x);`, `long double acosl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.1p2 ‚Äî The `acos` functions compute the principal value of the arc cosine of `x`; a domain error occurs for arguments not in the interval [‚àí1, +1]. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (shared `libm`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.1p3 ‚Äî The `acos` functions return `arccos x` in the interval [0, œÄ] radians. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.4.2 The asin functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double asin(double x);`, `float asinf(float x);`, `long double asinl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.2p2 ‚Äî The `asin` functions compute the principal value of the arc sine of `x`; a domain error occurs for arguments not in the interval [‚àí1, +1]. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.2p3 ‚Äî The `asin` functions return `arcsin x` in the interval [‚àíœÄ/2, +œÄ/2] radians. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.4.3 The atan functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double atan(double x);`, `float atanf(float x);`, `long double atanl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.3p2 ‚Äî The `atan` functions compute the principal value of the arc tangent of `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.3p3 ‚Äî The `atan` functions return `arctan x` in the interval [‚àíœÄ/2, +œÄ/2] radians. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.4.4 The atan2 functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double atan2(double y, double x);`, `float atan2f(float y, float x);`, `long double atan2l(long double y, long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.4p2 ‚Äî The `atan2` functions compute the arc tangent of `y/x`, using the signs of both arguments to determine the quadrant; a domain error may occur if both arguments are zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.4p3 ‚Äî The `atan2` functions return `arctan(y/x)` in the interval [‚àíœÄ, +œÄ] radians. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.4.5 The cos functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double cos(double x);`, `float cosf(float x);`, `long double cosl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.5p2 ‚Äî The `cos` functions compute the cosine of `x` (measured in radians). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.5p3 ‚Äî The `cos` functions return `cos x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`cos(1)`=0.540302)

#### ¬ß7.12.4.6 The sin functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double sin(double x);`, `float sinf(float x);`, `long double sinl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.6p2 ‚Äî The `sin` functions compute the sine of `x` (measured in radians). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.6p3 ‚Äî The `sin` functions return `sin x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sin(1)`=0.841471; `sinl`/`sinf` match)

#### ¬ß7.12.4.7 The tan functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double tan(double x);`, `float tanf(float x);`, `long double tanl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.7p2 ‚Äî The `tan` functions compute the tangent of `x` (measured in radians). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.4.7p3 ‚Äî The `tan` functions return `tan x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`tan(1)`=1.55741)

### ¬ß7.12.5 Hyperbolic functions

#### ¬ß7.12.5.1 The acosh functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double acosh(double x);`, `float acoshf(float x);`, `long double acoshl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.1p2 ‚Äî The `acosh` functions compute the (nonnegative) arc hyperbolic cosine of `x`; a domain error occurs for arguments less than 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.1p3 ‚Äî The `acosh` functions return `arcosh x` in the interval [0, +‚àû]. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.5.2 The asinh functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double asinh(double x);`, `float asinhf(float x);`, `long double asinhl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.2p2 ‚Äî The `asinh` functions compute the arc hyperbolic sine of `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.2p3 ‚Äî The `asinh` functions return `arsinh x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.5.3 The atanh functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double atanh(double x);`, `float atanhf(float x);`, `long double atanhl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.3p2 ‚Äî The `atanh` functions compute the arc hyperbolic tangent of `x`; a domain error occurs for arguments not in the interval [‚àí1, +1]; a pole error may occur if the argument equals ‚àí1 or +1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.3p3 ‚Äî The `atanh` functions return `artanh x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.5.4 The cosh functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double cosh(double x);`, `float coshf(float x);`, `long double coshl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.4p2 ‚Äî The `cosh` functions compute the hyperbolic cosine of `x`; a range error occurs if the magnitude of `x` is too large. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.4p3 ‚Äî The `cosh` functions return `cosh x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.5.5 The sinh functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double sinh(double x);`, `float sinhf(float x);`, `long double sinhl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
