- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.5p2 ‚Äî The `sinh` functions compute the hyperbolic sine of `x`; a range error occurs if the magnitude of `x` is too large. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.5p3 ‚Äî The `sinh` functions return `sinh x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.5.6 The tanh functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double tanh(double x);`, `float tanhf(float x);`, `long double tanhl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.6p2 ‚Äî The `tanh` functions compute the hyperbolic tangent of `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.5.6p3 ‚Äî The `tanh` functions return `tanh x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.6 Exponential and logarithmic functions

#### ¬ß7.12.6.1 The exp functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double exp(double x);`, `float expf(float x);`, `long double expl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.1p2 ‚Äî The `exp` functions compute the base-e exponential of `x`; a range error occurs if the magnitude of `x` is too large. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.1p3 ‚Äî The `exp` functions return `e^x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`exp(1)`=2.71828)

#### ¬ß7.12.6.2 The exp2 functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double exp2(double x);`, `float exp2f(float x);`, `long double exp2l(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.2p2 ‚Äî The `exp2` functions compute the base-2 exponential of `x`; a range error occurs if the magnitude of `x` is too large. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.2p3 ‚Äî The `exp2` functions return `2^x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.3 The expm1 functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double expm1(double x);`, `float expm1f(float x);`, `long double expm1l(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.3p2 ‚Äî The `expm1` functions compute the base-e exponential of the argument minus 1; a range error occurs if `x` is too large (for small-magnitude `x`, `expm1(x)` is expected to be more accurate than `exp(x) - 1`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.3p3 ‚Äî The `expm1` functions return `e^x ‚àí 1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.4 The frexp functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double frexp(double value, int *exp);`, `float frexpf(float value, int *exp);`, `long double frexpl(long double value, int *exp);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.4p2 ‚Äî The `frexp` functions break a floating-point number into a normalized fraction and an integral power of 2, storing the integer power of 2 in the `int` object pointed to by `exp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`frexp(8,&e)`‚Üí0.5, `e`=4)
- ¬ß7.12.6.4p3 ‚Äî If `value` is not a floating-point number or if the integral power of 2 is outside the range of `int`, the results are unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.4p3 ‚Äî The `frexp` functions return a value `x` with magnitude in the interval [1/2, 1) or zero, such that `value` equals `x √ó 2^(*exp)`; if `value` is zero, both parts of the result (the return value and `*exp`) are zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.5 The ilogb functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int ilogb(double x);`, `int ilogbf(float x);`, `int ilogbl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.5p2 ‚Äî The `ilogb` functions extract the exponent of `x` as a signed `int` value; if `x` is zero they return `FP_ILOGB0`, if `x` is infinite they return `INT_MAX`, if `x` is a NaN they return `FP_ILOGBNAN`, otherwise they are equivalent to calling the corresponding `logb` function and casting the returned value to `int`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`ilogb(8)`=3)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.6.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) A domain error or range error may occur if `x` is zero, infinite, or NaN, and if the correct value is outside the range of the return type the numeric result is unspecified and a domain error or range error may occur. ‚Äî (spec; shared `libm`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.5p3 ‚Äî The `ilogb` functions return the exponent of `x` as a signed `int` value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.6 The ldexp functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double ldexp(double x, int exp);`, `float ldexpf(float x, int exp);`, `long double ldexpl(long double x, int exp);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.6p2 ‚Äî The `ldexp` functions multiply a floating-point number by an integral power of 2; a range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.6p3 ‚Äî The `ldexp` functions return `x √ó 2^exp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`ldexp(1,4)`=16)

#### ¬ß7.12.6.7 The log functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double log(double x);`, `float logf(float x);`, `long double logl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.7p2 ‚Äî The `log` functions compute the base-e (natural) logarithm of `x`; a domain error occurs if the argument is negative; a pole error may occur if the argument is zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.7p3 ‚Äî The `log` functions return `log_e x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.8 The log10 functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double log10(double x);`, `float log10f(float x);`, `long double log10l(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.8p2 ‚Äî The `log10` functions compute the base-10 (common) logarithm of `x`; a domain error occurs if the argument is negative; a pole error may occur if the argument is zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.8p3 ‚Äî The `log10` functions return `log_10 x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.9 The log1p functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.9p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double log1p(double x);`, `float log1pf(float x);`, `long double log1pl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.9p2 ‚Äî The `log1p` functions compute the base-e (natural) logarithm of 1 plus the argument; a domain error occurs if the argument is less than ‚àí1; a pole error may occur if the argument equals ‚àí1 (for small-magnitude `x`, `log1p(x)` is expected to be more accurate than `log(1 + x)`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.9p3 ‚Äî The `log1p` functions return `log_e(1 + x)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.10 The log2 functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.10p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double log2(double x);`, `float log2f(float x);`, `long double log2l(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.10p2 ‚Äî The `log2` functions compute the base-2 logarithm of `x`; a domain error occurs if the argument is less than zero; a pole error may occur if the argument is zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.10p3 ‚Äî The `log2` functions return `log_2 x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.11 The logb functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.11p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double logb(double x);`, `float logbf(float x);`, `long double logbl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.11p2 ‚Äî The `logb` functions extract the exponent of `x` as a signed integer value in floating-point format; a subnormal `x` is treated as if normalized, so that for positive finite `x`, `1 ‚â§ x √ó FLT_RADIX^(‚àílogb(x)) < FLT_RADIX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`logb(8)`=3)
- [ ] ¬ß7.12.6.11p2 ‚Äî A domain error or pole error may occur if the argument is zero. ‚Äî (spec; shared `libm`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.11p3 ‚Äî The `logb` functions return the signed exponent of `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.12 The modf functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.12p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double modf(double value, double *iptr);`, `float modff(float value, float *iptr);`, `long double modfl(long double value, long double *iptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.12p2 ‚Äî The `modf` functions break `value` into integral and fractional parts, each with the same type and sign as the argument, storing the integral part (in floating-point format) in the object pointed to by `iptr`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`modf(3.5,&ip)`‚Üí0.5, `ip`=3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.12p3 ‚Äî The `modf` functions return the signed fractional part of `value`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.6.13 The scalbn and scalbln functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.13p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double scalbn(double x, int n);`, `float scalbnf(float x, int n);`, `long double scalbnl(long double x, int n);`, `double scalbln(double x, long int n);`, `float scalblnf(float x, long int n);`, `long double scalblnl(long double x, long int n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.13p2 ‚Äî The `scalbn` and `scalbln` functions compute `x √ó FLT_RADIX^n` efficiently, normally not by computing `FLT_RADIX^n` explicitly; a range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`scalbn(1,3)`=8)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.6.13p3 ‚Äî The `scalbn` and `scalbln` functions return `x √ó FLT_RADIX^n`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.7 Power and absolute-value functions

#### ¬ß7.12.7.1 The cbrt functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double cbrt(double x);`, `float cbrtf(float x);`, `long double cbrtl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.1p2 ‚Äî The `cbrt` functions compute the real cube root of `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.1p3 ‚Äî The `cbrt` functions return `x^(1/3)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`cbrt(27)`=3)

#### ¬ß7.12.7.2 The fabs functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double fabs(double x);`, `float fabsf(float x);`, `long double fabsl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.2p2 ‚Äî The `fabs` functions compute the absolute value of a floating-point number `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.2p3 ‚Äî The `fabs` functions return `|x|`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.7.3 The hypot functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double hypot(double x, double y);`, `float hypotf(float x, float y);`, `long double hypotl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.3p2 ‚Äî The `hypot` functions compute the square root of the sum of the squares of `x` and `y`, without undue overflow or underflow; a range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.3p3 ‚Äî The `hypot` functions return `‚àö(x¬≤ + y¬≤)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`hypot(3,4)`=5)

#### ¬ß7.12.7.4 The pow functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double pow(double x, double y);`, `float powf(float x, float y);`, `long double powl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.4p2 ‚Äî The `pow` functions compute `x` raised to the power `y`; a domain error occurs if `x` is finite and negative and `y` is finite and not an integer value; a domain error or pole error may occur if `x` is zero and `y` is less than or equal to zero; a range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.4p3 ‚Äî The `pow` functions return `x^y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`powl(2,10)`=1024)

#### ¬ß7.12.7.5 The sqrt functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double sqrt(double x);`, `float sqrtf(float x);`, `long double sqrtl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.5p2 ‚Äî The `sqrt` functions compute the nonnegative square root of `x`; a domain error occurs if the argument is less than zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.7.5p3 ‚Äî The `sqrt` functions return `‚àöx`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sqrt(2)`=1.41421)

### ¬ß7.12.8 Error and gamma functions

#### ¬ß7.12.8.1 The erf functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double erf(double x);`, `float erff(float x);`, `long double erfl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.1p2 ‚Äî The `erf` functions compute the error function of `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.1p3 ‚Äî The `erf` functions return `erf x = (2/‚àöœÄ) ‚à´‚ÇÄÀ£ e^(‚àít¬≤) dt`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`erf(1)`=0.842701)

#### ¬ß7.12.8.2 The erfc functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double erfc(double x);`, `float erfcf(float x);`, `long double erfcl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.2p2 ‚Äî The `erfc` functions compute the complementary error function of `x`; a range error occurs if `x` is too large. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.2p3 ‚Äî The `erfc` functions return `erfc x = 1 ‚àí erf x = (2/‚àöœÄ) ‚à´‚Çì^‚àû e^(‚àít¬≤) dt`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.8.3 The lgamma functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double lgamma(double x);`, `float lgammaf(float x);`, `long double lgammal(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.3p2 ‚Äî The `lgamma` functions compute the natural logarithm of the absolute value of gamma of `x`; a range error occurs if `x` is too large; a pole error may occur if `x` is a negative integer or zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.3p3 ‚Äî The `lgamma` functions return `log_e |Œì(x)|`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`lgamma(5)`=3.17805)

#### ¬ß7.12.8.4 The tgamma functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double tgamma(double x);`, `float tgammaf(float x);`, `long double tgammal(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.4p2 ‚Äî The `tgamma` functions compute the gamma function of `x`; a domain error or pole error may occur if `x` is a negative integer or zero; a range error may occur if the magnitude of `x` is too large or too small. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.8.4p3 ‚Äî The `tgamma` functions return `Œì(x)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`tgamma(5)`=24)

### ¬ß7.12.9 Nearest integer functions

#### ¬ß7.12.9.1 The ceil functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double ceil(double x);`, `float ceilf(float x);`, `long double ceill(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.1p2 ‚Äî The `ceil` functions compute the smallest integer value not less than `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.1p3 ‚Äî The `ceil` functions return `‚åàx‚åâ`, expressed as a floating-point number. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.9.2 The floor functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double floor(double x);`, `float floorf(float x);`, `long double floorl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.2p2 ‚Äî The `floor` functions compute the largest integer value not greater than `x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.2p3 ‚Äî The `floor` functions return `‚åäx‚åã`, expressed as a floating-point number. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.9.3 The nearbyint functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double nearbyint(double x);`, `float nearbyintf(float x);`, `long double nearbyintl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.3p2 ‚Äî The `nearbyint` functions round their argument to an integer value in floating-point format, using the current rounding direction and without raising the "inexact" floating-point exception. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`nearbyint(2.5)`=2 round-to-even)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.3p3 ‚Äî The `nearbyint` functions return the rounded integer value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.9.4 The rint functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double rint(double x);`, `float rintf(float x);`, `long double rintl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.4p2 ‚Äî The `rint` functions differ from the `nearbyint` functions only in that the `rint` functions may raise the "inexact" floating-point exception if the result differs in value from the argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.4p3 ‚Äî The `rint` functions return the rounded integer value, using the current rounding direction. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`rint(2.5)`=2)

#### ¬ß7.12.9.5 The lrint and llrint functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `long int lrint(double x);`, `long int lrintf(float x);`, `long int lrintl(long double x);`, `long long int llrint(double x);`, `long long int llrintf(float x);`, `long long int llrintl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.5p2 ‚Äî The `lrint` and `llrint` functions round their argument to the nearest integer value, rounding according to the current rounding direction; if the rounded value is outside the range of the return type, the numeric result is unspecified and a domain error or range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`lrint(2.5)`=2)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.5p3 ‚Äî The `lrint` and `llrint` functions return the rounded integer value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.9.6 The round functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double round(double x);`, `float roundf(float x);`, `long double roundl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.6p2 ‚Äî The `round` functions round their argument to the nearest integer value in floating-point format, rounding halfway cases away from zero, regardless of the current rounding direction. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`round(2.5)`=3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.6p3 ‚Äî The `round` functions return the rounded integer value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.9.7 The lround and llround functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `long int lround(double x);`, `long int lroundf(float x);`, `long int lroundl(long double x);`, `long long int llround(double x);`, `long long int llroundf(float x);`, `long long int llroundl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.7p2 ‚Äî The `lround` and `llround` functions round their argument to the nearest integer value, rounding halfway cases away from zero, regardless of the current rounding direction; if the rounded value is outside the range of the return type, the numeric result is unspecified and a domain error or range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`llround(2.5)`=3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.7p3 ‚Äî The `lround` and `llround` functions return the rounded integer value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.9.8 The trunc functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double trunc(double x);`, `float truncf(float x);`, `long double truncl(long double x);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.8p2 ‚Äî The `trunc` functions round their argument to the integer value, in floating-point format, nearest to but no larger in magnitude than the argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`trunc(2.7)`=2)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.9.8p3 ‚Äî The `trunc` functions return the truncated integer value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.10 Remainder functions

#### ¬ß7.12.10.1 The fmod functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double fmod(double x, double y);`, `float fmodf(float x, float y);`, `long double fmodl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.1p2 ‚Äî The `fmod` functions compute the floating-point remainder of `x/y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.1p3 ‚Äî The `fmod` functions return `x ‚àí n y` for some integer `n` such that, if `y` is nonzero, the result has the same sign as `x` and magnitude less than the magnitude of `y`; if `y` is zero, whether a domain error occurs or the functions return zero is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.10.2 The remainder functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double remainder(double x, double y);`, `float remainderf(float x, float y);`, `long double remainderl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.2p2 ‚Äî The `remainder` functions compute the remainder `x REM y` required by IEC 60559: when `y ‚âÝ 0`, the result is `r = x ‚àí n y`, where `n` is the integer nearest the exact value of `x/y`; whenever `|n ‚àí x/y| = 1/2`, `n` is chosen to be even. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.2p3 ‚Äî The `remainder` functions return `x REM y`; if `y` is zero, whether a domain error occurs or the functions return zero is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.10.3 The remquo functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double remquo(double x, double y, int *quo);`, `float remquof(float x, float y, int *quo);`, `long double remquol(long double x, long double y, int *quo);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.3p2 ‚Äî The `remquo` functions compute the same remainder as the `remainder` functions and store, in the object pointed to by `quo`, a value whose sign is the sign of `x/y` and whose magnitude is congruent modulo `2^n` to the magnitude of the integral quotient of `x/y`, where `n` is an implementation-defined integer greater than or equal to 3. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`remquo(10,3,&q)`‚Üí1, `q`=3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.10.3p3 ‚Äî The `remquo` functions return `x REM y`; if `y` is zero, the value stored in `*quo` is unspecified and whether a domain error occurs or the functions return zero is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.11 Manipulation functions

#### ¬ß7.12.11.1 The copysign functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double copysign(double x, double y);`, `float copysignf(float x, float y);`, `long double copysignl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.1p2 ‚Äî The `copysign` functions produce a value with the magnitude of `x` and the sign of `y`; they produce a NaN (with the sign of `y`) if `x` is a NaN; on implementations that represent a signed zero but do not treat negative zero consistently in arithmetic, they regard the sign of zero as positive. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`copysign(NAN,-1)` is negative on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.1p3 ‚Äî The `copysign` functions return a value with the magnitude of `x` and the sign of `y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`copysign(3,-1)`=-3)

#### ¬ß7.12.11.2 The nan functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double nan(const char *tagp);`, `float nanf(const char *tagp);`, `long double nanl(const char *tagp);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.2p2 ‚Äî The call `nan("n-char-sequence")` is equivalent to `strtod("NAN(n-char-sequence)", (char**) NULL)`; `nan("")` is equivalent to `strtod("NAN()", (char**) NULL)`; if `tagp` does not point to an n-char sequence or an empty string, the call is equivalent to `strtod("NAN", (char**) NULL)`; calls to `nanf` and `nanl` are equivalent to the corresponding calls to `strtof` and `strtold`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (library `nan("")`‚Üí`nan`, positive ‚Äî distinct from the `NAN` *macro* issue at ¬ß7.12p5)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.2p3 ‚Äî The `nan` functions return a quiet NaN, if available, with content indicated through `tagp`; if the implementation does not support quiet NaNs, the functions return zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.11.3 The nextafter functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double nextafter(double x, double y);`, `float nextafterf(float x, float y);`, `long double nextafterl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.3p2 ‚Äî The `nextafter` functions determine the next representable value, in the type of the function, after `x` in the direction of `y` (where `x` and `y` are first converted to the type of the function); they return `y` if `x` equals `y`; a range error may occur if the magnitude of `x` is the largest finite value representable in the type and the result is infinite or not representable in the type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`nextafter(1,2)`=0x1.0000000000001p+0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.3p3 ‚Äî The `nextafter` functions return the next representable value in the specified format after `x` in the direction of `y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.11.4 The nexttoward functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double nexttoward(double x, long double y);`, `float nexttowardf(float x, long double y);`, `long double nexttowardl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.4p2 ‚Äî The `nexttoward` functions are equivalent to the `nextafter` functions except that the second parameter has type `long double` and the functions return `y` converted to the type of the function if `x` equals `y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`nexttoward(1,2L)`=0x1.0000000000001p+0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.11.4p3 ‚Äî The `nexttoward` functions return the next representable value in the specified format after `x` in the direction of `y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.12 Maximum, minimum, and positive difference functions

#### ¬ß7.12.12.1 The fdim functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double fdim(double x, double y);`, `float fdimf(float x, float y);`, `long double fdiml(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.1p2 ‚Äî The `fdim` functions determine the positive difference between their arguments: `x ‚àí y` if `x > y`, and `+0` if `x ‚â§ y`; a range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fdim(5,2)`=3)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.1p3 ‚Äî The `fdim` functions return the positive difference value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.12.2 The fmax functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double fmax(double x, double y);`, `float fmaxf(float x, float y);`, `long double fmaxl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.2p2 ‚Äî The `fmax` functions determine the maximum numeric value of their arguments; if just one argument is a NaN, they return the other argument; if both are NaNs, they return a NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fmax(1,2)`=2)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.2p3 ‚Äî The `fmax` functions return the maximum numeric value of their arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.12.3 The fmin functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double fmin(double x, double y);`, `float fminf(float x, float y);`, `long double fminl(long double x, long double y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.3p2 ‚Äî The `fmin` functions determine the minimum numeric value of their arguments; if just one argument is a NaN, they return the other argument; if both are NaNs, they return a NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fmin(1,2)`=1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.12.3p3 ‚Äî The `fmin` functions return the minimum numeric value of their arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.13 Floating multiply-add

#### ¬ß7.12.13.1 The fma functions
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.13.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double fma(double x, double y, double z);`, `float fmaf(float x, float y, float z);`, `long double fmal(long double x, long double y, long double z);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.13.1p2 ‚Äî The `fma` functions compute `(x √ó y) + z`, rounded as one ternary operation: they compute the value (as if) to infinite precision and round once to the result format according to the current rounding mode; a range error may occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fma(2,3,4)`=10)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.13.1p3 ‚Äî The `fma` functions return `(x √ó y) + z`, rounded as one ternary operation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.12.14 Comparison macros

- ¬ß7.12.14p1 ‚Äî The relational and equality operators support the usual mathematical relationships between numeric values; for any ordered pair of numeric values exactly one of less, greater, and equal is true; relational operators may raise the "invalid" floating-point exception when argument values are NaNs. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.12.14p1 ‚Äî For a NaN and a numeric value, or for two NaNs, just the unordered relationship is true; the comparison macros in this subclause are quiet (non-exception-raising) versions of the relational operators and facilitate writing efficient NaN-aware code without the "invalid" floating-point exception. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.12.14p2 ‚Äî In the synopses of this subclause, `real-floating` indicates that each argument shall be an expression of real floating type (both arguments shall be such expressions). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14 (added) ‚Äî The comparison macros evaluate each argument exactly once (no double evaluation of operands with side effects). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (host glibc routes through `__builtin_*` / single-eval helpers)

#### ¬ß7.12.14.1 The isgreater macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isgreater(real-floating x, real-floating y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.1p2 ‚Äî `isgreater(x, y)` determines whether `x` is greater than `y`; its value is always equal to `(x) > (y)`, yet unlike `(x) > (y)` it does not raise the "invalid" floating-point exception when `x` and `y` are unordered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isgreater(2,1)`=1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.1p3 ‚Äî The `isgreater` macro returns the value of `(x) > (y)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.14.2 The isgreaterequal macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isgreaterequal(real-floating x, real-floating y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.2p2 ‚Äî `isgreaterequal(x, y)` determines whether `x` is greater than or equal to `y`; its value is always equal to `(x) >= (y)`, yet unlike `(x) >= (y)` it does not raise the "invalid" floating-point exception when `x` and `y` are unordered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isgreaterequal(2,2)`=1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.2p3 ‚Äî The `isgreaterequal` macro returns the value of `(x) >= (y)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.14.3 The isless macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isless(real-floating x, real-floating y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.3p2 ‚Äî `isless(x, y)` determines whether `x` is less than `y`; its value is always equal to `(x) < (y)`, yet unlike `(x) < (y)` it does not raise the "invalid" floating-point exception when `x` and `y` are unordered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isless(2,1)`=0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.3p3 ‚Äî The `isless` macro returns the value of `(x) < (y)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.14.4 The islessequal macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int islessequal(real-floating x, real-floating y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.4p2 ‚Äî `islessequal(x, y)` determines whether `x` is less than or equal to `y`; its value is always equal to `(x) <= (y)`, yet unlike `(x) <= (y)` it does not raise the "invalid" floating-point exception when `x` and `y` are unordered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`islessequal(2,2)`=1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.4p3 ‚Äî The `islessequal` macro returns the value of `(x) <= (y)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.14.5 The islessgreater macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int islessgreater(real-floating x, real-floating y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.5p2 ‚Äî `islessgreater(x, y)` determines whether `x` is less than or greater than `y`; its value is similar to `(x) < (y) || (x) > (y)`, except that it does not raise the "invalid" floating-point exception when `x` and `y` are unordered (nor does it evaluate `x` and `y` twice). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`islessgreater(2,1)`=1)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.5p3 ‚Äî The `islessgreater` macro returns the value of `(x) < (y) || (x) > (y)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.12.14.6 The isunordered macro
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int isunordered(real-floating x, real-floating y);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.6p2 ‚Äî The `isunordered` macro determines whether its arguments are unordered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.12.14.6p3 ‚Äî The `isunordered` macro returns 1 if its arguments are unordered (at least one is a NaN) and 0 otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`isunordered(2,NAN)`=1)


## ¬ß7.13-¬ß7.16 setjmp, signal, stdalign, stdarg

> mcc status: 64 TODO checkboxes; 2 mcc-gaps ‚Äî both diagnostic-quality only (x86_64 `va_start` on a `register` parmN is not warned where the SysV macro reads the frame instead of `parmN`; `va_start` with a non-last second argument is not warned). Every *normatively required* behavior (setjmp/longjmp save-restore incl. `val==0`‚Üí1 and non-volatile-clobber rules, `_Alignas`/`_Alignof` semantics + constraint diagnostics, the four `<stdarg.h>` macros incl. `va_copy`) conforms and matches the gcc==clang consensus.

> Scope: `<setjmp.h>` (¬ß7.13), `<signal.h>` (¬ß7.14), `<stdalign.h>` (¬ß7.15, C11), and `<stdarg.h>` (¬ß7.16). All four are macro-heavy headers whose conformance burden falls almost entirely on the compiler's builtins (`setjmp`/`longjmp` register-save semantics, `__builtin_va_*`, `_Alignas`/`_Alignof`) rather than on a freestanding runtime object. In mcc, `<stdarg.h>` and `<stdalign.h>` are bundled (`runtime/include/`) and forward to `__builtin_va_*` and `__attribute__((aligned))`/`__alignof__`; `<setjmp.h>` and `<signal.h>` are taken from the host C library.
> Freestanding (¬ß4p6 / ¬ß7.1.3): only `<stdarg.h>` and `<stdalign.h>` (plus the type/limit/bool/noreturn headers) are guaranteed; `<setjmp.h>` and `<signal.h>` are hosted-only.
> Verified bundled `<stdarg.h>` (`runtime/include/stdarg.h`): `typedef __builtin_va_list va_list;` and `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_copy`/`va_end` ‚Üí `__builtin_va_*`, plus `typedef va_list __gnuc_va_list;` and `#define _VA_LIST_DEFINED`. Verified bundled `<stdalign.h>` (`runtime/include/stdalign.h`): `alignas`‚Üí`_Alignas`, `alignof`‚Üí`_Alignof`, `__alignas_is_defined`/`__alignof_is_defined`‚Üí`1`, with pre-C11 GNU/MCC back-fill `_Alignas(t)`‚Üí`__attribute__((__aligned__(t)))`, `_Alignof(t)`‚Üí`__alignof__(t)`.
> Verified mcc rejects bundled `<varargs.h>` with an `#error` directing the user to `<stdarg.h>` (legacy K&R varargs intentionally unsupported on all three; gcc/clang likewise reject/deprecate it).

### ¬ß7.13 Non-local jumps `<setjmp.h>`

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13p1 ‚Äî `<setjmp.h>` defines the macro `setjmp`, and declares one function `longjmp` and one type `jmp_buf`, for bypassing the normal function call and return discipline. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (host `<setjmp.h>`; all three see the same glibc header)
- ¬ß7.13p2 ‚Äî `jmp_buf` is an array type suitable for holding the information needed to restore a calling environment. The saved environment is sufficient for `longjmp` to return execution to the correct block and invocation of that block (as if it were called recursively); it does **not** include the state of the floating-point status flags, of open files, or of any other component of the abstract machine. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.13p3 ‚Äî It is unspecified whether `setjmp` is a macro or an identifier with external linkage. If a macro definition of `setjmp` is suppressed to access an actual function, or if a program defines an external identifier named `setjmp`, the behavior is undefined (unlike other library macros, `setjmp` may **not** be accessed as a function). ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.13.1.1 The `setjmp` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <setjmp.h>` then `int setjmp(jmp_buf env);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.1.1p2 (Description) ‚Äî The `setjmp` macro saves its calling environment in its `jmp_buf` argument for later use by `longjmp`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (round-trip verified: `setjmp`/`longjmp` returns to the saved block)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.1.1p3 (Returns) ‚Äî On a direct invocation `setjmp` returns 0; on return via `longjmp` it returns a nonzero value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified direct‚Üí0, via-longjmp‚Üínonzero)
- ¬ß7.13.1.1p4 (Environmental constraint) ‚Äî An invocation of `setjmp` shall appear only in one of: (a) the entire controlling expression of a selection or iteration statement (`if`/`switch`/`while`/`do`/`for`); (b) one operand of a relational/equality operator, the other operand an integer constant expression, the whole being the entire controlling expression of a selection/iteration statement; (c) the operand of unary `!`, the whole being such an entire controlling expression; or (d) the entire expression of an expression statement (possibly cast to `void`). ‚Äî (spec; constraint on the program, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.1.1p4 (UB) ‚Äî If an invocation of `setjmp` appears in any **other** context (e.g. `x = setjmp(env);`, `setjmp(env) + 1`, a function argument), the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB, not a required diagnostic; verified all three silently accept `int x = setjmp(b)+1;` ‚Äî no compiler diagnoses this)

#### ¬ß7.13.2.1 The `longjmp` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <setjmp.h>` then `void longjmp(jmp_buf env, int val);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.13.2.1p2 (Description/UB) ‚Äî `longjmp` restores the environment saved by the most recent `setjmp` invocation in the same program invocation with the corresponding `jmp_buf`. The behavior is undefined if there was no such invocation, or if the function containing the `setjmp` invocation has terminated execution in the interim, or if the `setjmp` invocation was within the scope of an identifier with variably modified type and execution has left that scope in the interim. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.2.1p3 (Description) ‚Äî After `longjmp`, all accessible objects have values and all other components of the abstract machine have state as of the time `longjmp` was called, **except** that automatic objects local to the function containing the corresponding `setjmp` invocation, that are not volatile-qualified and were changed between the `setjmp` and the `longjmp`, have indeterminate values. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (at `-O2`, a `volatile` automatic written before `longjmp` reliably reads back its updated value after the jump on all three; this is the compiler-side obligation)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.13.2.1p4 (Returns) ‚Äî Execution continues as if the corresponding `setjmp` had just returned `val`. `longjmp` cannot cause `setjmp` to return 0; if `val` is 0, `setjmp` returns 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified: `longjmp(b,0)` makes `setjmp` return 1; `longjmp(b,42)` returns 42 ‚Äî host libc behavior, identical across all three)
- ¬ß7.13.2.1p5 (Environmental limit) ‚Äî `longjmp` shall execute correctly in the contexts of interrupts, signals, and any of their associated functions; however, if invoked from a nested signal handler, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; host-libc/runtime, not a compiler obligation; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.14 Signal handling `<signal.h>`

> Hosted-only: not required in a freestanding implementation (¬ß4p6). mcc sources `<signal.h>` from the host C library, so the macro/type/function inventory is identical across all three compilers; mcc's only obligation is to compile handler/`raise` code correctly.
> C99‚ÜíC11 delta: ¬ß7.14.1.1p3's handler restriction broadens to "static **or thread** storage duration that is not a lock-free atomic object", adds `quick_exit`/`_Exit` to the allowed-call list, and adds the `SIG_ERR`-return `errno`-indeterminate clause; ¬ß7.14.2.1p2 adds that `raise` shall not return until the handler does.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14p1 ‚Äî `<signal.h>` declares a type and two functions and defines several macros, for handling conditions reported during execution. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (host header)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14p2 ‚Äî The type defined is `sig_atomic_t`, the (possibly volatile-qualified) integer type of an object that can be accessed as an atomic entity even in the presence of asynchronous interrupts. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sig_atomic_t` usable; verified `volatile sig_atomic_t` handler flag)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14p3 ‚Äî The macros `SIG_DFL`, `SIG_ERR`, and `SIG_IGN` expand to constant expressions with distinct values, of a type compatible with the second argument to and the return value of `signal`, and whose values compare unequal to the address of any declarable function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified all three assignable to `void(*)(int)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14p4 ‚Äî The macros `SIGABRT`, `SIGFPE`, `SIGILL`, `SIGINT`, `SIGSEGV`, `SIGTERM` are defined as positive integer constant expressions of type `int` with distinct values. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified identical values 6/8/4/2/11/15 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14p5 ‚Äî An implementation need not generate any of these signals except via explicit `raise` calls. Additional signals and pointers to undeclarable functions, named with macros beginning `SIG`/`SIG_` + uppercase letter, may be specified; all signal numbers shall be positive. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (implementation-defined; host-defined extra signals e.g. `SIGUSR1` visible to all three)

#### ¬ß7.14.1.1 The `signal` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <signal.h>` then `void (*signal(int sig, void (*func)(int)))(int);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14.1.1p2 (Description) ‚Äî `signal` chooses one of three ways to handle subsequent receipt of `sig`: `SIG_DFL` ‚Üí default; `SIG_IGN` ‚Üí ignore; otherwise `func` is the handler called when the signal occurs. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (host-libc semantics; compiles + dispatches identically)
- ¬ß7.14.1.1p3 (Description) ‚Äî When the signal occurs and `func` points to a function, it is implementation-defined whether `signal(sig, SIG_DFL);` is executed or a set of signals (at least `sig`) is blocked, before the handler is called with argument `sig`. ‚Äî (spec/impl-defined; host-libc, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.14.1.1p3 (Async-signal-safety / UB) ‚Äî If the signal occurred other than via `abort`/`raise`, the behavior is undefined if the handler refers to any object with static **(C11: or thread)** storage duration that is not a lock-free atomic object other than by assigning to a `volatile sig_atomic_t`, or calls any standard library function other than `abort`, `_Exit`, **(C11: `quick_exit`,)** or `signal` with first arg equal to the handled signal. **(C11:** if such a `signal` returns `SIG_ERR`, `errno` is indeterminate.**)** ‚Äî (spec/UB; not a compiler-diagnosable constraint; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.14.1.1p4 (Description) ‚Äî At program startup, `signal(sig, SIG_IGN);` may be established for some implementation-defined signals; `signal(sig, SIG_DFL);` is established for all others. ‚Äî (spec/impl-defined startup state; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.14.1.1p5 (Description) ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `signal`. ‚Äî (spec; host-libc property, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14.1.1p6 (Returns) ‚Äî On success `signal` returns the value of `func` for the most recent successful `signal` call for `sig`; on failure returns `SIG_ERR` and stores a positive value in `errno`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified prior-handler is returned by a second `signal` call)

#### ¬ß7.14.2.1 The `raise` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <signal.h>` then `int raise(int sig);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14.2.1p2 (Description) ‚Äî `raise` carries out the actions of ¬ß7.14.1.1 for `sig`. **(C11:** if a handler is called, `raise` shall not return until after the handler returns.**)** ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified `raise` synchronously invokes the installed handler before returning)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.14.2.1p3 (Returns) ‚Äî `raise` returns zero on success, nonzero on failure. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (host-libc)

### ¬ß7.15 Alignment `<stdalign.h>` (C11)

> Entire header is C11-only (added by C11; not present in C99). (In C23 the macros become keywords, out of N1570 scope.)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p1 (C11) ‚Äî `<stdalign.h>` defines four macros. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (bundled `runtime/include/stdalign.h`; defines exactly the four)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p2 (C11) ‚Äî `alignas` expands to `_Alignas`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p3 (C11) ‚Äî `alignof` expands to `_Alignof`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p4 (C11) ‚Äî `__alignas_is_defined` and `__alignof_is_defined` expand to the integer constant `1` and are suitable for use in `#if` preprocessing directives. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified both `=1` and usable in `#if`)
- ¬ß7.15p5 (C11) ‚Äî A program that undefines, or `#define`s elsewhere, any of `alignas`/`alignof`/`__alignas_is_defined`/`__alignof_is_defined` has undefined behavior (per ¬ß7.1.3 reserved-identifier rules). ‚Äî (spec/UB; not a required diagnostic; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15 (impl) ‚Äî Pre-C11 / GNU/MCC back-fill: when `__STDC_VERSION__ < 201112L`, the bundled header defines `_Alignas(t)`‚Üí`__attribute__((__aligned__(t)))` and `_Alignof(t)`‚Üí`__alignof__(t)` so `alignas`/`alignof` work in older modes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì (gcc/clang use their own header but offer the equivalent fallback)

> Underlying operator/specifier semantics that `<stdalign.h>` exposes (primary checkboxes live in ¬ß6.7.5 and ¬ß6.5.3.4; cross-referenced and re-probed here):
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas(constant-expression)` / `_Alignas(type-name)` gives the alignment of the declared object/member; the value shall be an ICE representing a valid power-of-two alignment, and `_Alignas(type-name)` ‚â° `_Alignas(_Alignof(type-name))`. Zero has no effect; the strictest applies; `_Alignas` shall not be applied to a function parameter, a typedef, a bit-field, or an object whose alignment would be weakened below its type's requirement. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all four illegal targets rejected; `_Alignas(0)` accepted as no-op; `_Alignas(double)` type-name form == `_Alignof(double)`; verified runtime 32-byte alignment of an `alignas(32)` array)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas` on a **bit-field** is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "error: '_Alignas' specified for a bit-field")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas` on a **typedef** is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "error: '_Alignas' specified for a typedef")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas` on a **function parameter** is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "error: '_Alignas' specified for a function parameter")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas` requesting an alignment **weaker** than the type's requirement (e.g. `_Alignas(1) int`) is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "error: requested alignment is less than the minimum alignment of the type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas` with a **non-power-of-two** value (e.g. `_Alignas(3)`) is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "error: alignment must be a positive power of two")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignas(0)` has **no effect** (accepted, alignment unchanged). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignof` shall be applied only to a parenthesized type name, and not to a function type or an incomplete type. It yields the alignment requirement of its operand type as a `size_t` ICE; for an array type the result is the alignment of the element type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified `_Alignof(double)`=8, `_Alignof(long double)`=16, `_Alignof(double[10])`==`_Alignof(double)`=8)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignof` of an **incomplete type** is rejected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: "error: '_Alignof' applied to an incomplete type")
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.3.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignof` of a **function type** is a constraint violation. Default mode: all three accept it as a GNU extension; under `-pedantic-errors` all three reject. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc default accepts; `-pedantic-errors`: "error: '_Alignof' applied to a function type")
- [~] ¬ß6.5.3.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî `_Alignof` applied to an **expression** (GNU `__alignof__` extension, not a type name) is a constraint violation. Default mode: mcc & gcc accept silently, clang warns (`-Wgnu-alignof-expression`); under `-pedantic-errors` all three reject. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc default silently accepts like gcc; clang is the only one warning by default. mcc `-pedantic-errors`: "error: ISO C does not allow '_Alignof' applied to an expression")

### ¬ß7.16 Variable arguments `<stdarg.h>`

> `va_copy` (¬ß7.16.1.2) is C99/C11 only ‚Äî not present in C90; the other three macros date to C90.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p1 ‚Äî `<stdarg.h>` declares a type and defines four macros, for advancing through a list of arguments whose number and types are not known to the called function when it is translated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (bundled `runtime/include/stdarg.h` defines `va_list` + the four macros)
- ¬ß7.16p2 ‚Äî A function may be called with a variable number of arguments of varying types; its parameter list contains one or more parameters, the rightmost of which (`parmN`) plays a special role in the access mechanism. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p3 ‚Äî The type declared is `va_list`, an object type suitable for holding the info needed by `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_end`/`va_copy`. `ap` may be passed to another function; if that function invokes `va_arg` with that `ap`, the `ap` in the calling function is indeterminate and shall be passed to `va_end` before further reference. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified passing `va_list` to a helper that drains it, then `va_end` in the caller ‚Äî works; `va_copy` before passing preserves the original)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p4 ‚Äî The macros defined are `va_start`, `va_arg`, `va_copy`, and `va_end` (`va_copy` is C99/C11; absent in C90). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all four present and forwarding to `__builtin_va_*`)

#### ¬ß7.16.1.1 The `va_arg` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `type va_arg(va_list ap, type);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.1p2 (Description) ‚Äî `va_arg` expands to an expression with the specified type and the value of the next argument; `ap` must have been initialized by `va_start`/`va_copy`; each invocation modifies `ap`; `type` shall be a type name such that `type*` names a pointer to such an object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified successive `va_arg(ap,int)` returns args in order)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.1p2 (UB) ‚Äî If there is no actual next argument, or if `type` is incompatible with the actual next argument (after default promotions), the behavior is undefined, **except**: (a) signed/unsigned corresponding types where the value is representable in both; or (b) one is `void*` and the other a pointer to a character type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (the two excepted cases compile & run identically ‚Äî verified `va_arg(...,unsigned)` for an `int` arg and `va_arg(...,char*)` for a `void*` arg)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.1p3 (Returns) ‚Äî The first `va_arg` after `va_start` returns the argument after `parmN`; successive invocations return remaining args in succession. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.16.1.2 The `va_copy` macro (C99/C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `void va_copy(va_list dest, va_list src);` (added in C99; not in C90). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#define va_copy __builtin_va_copy`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.2p2 (Description) ‚Äî `va_copy` initializes `dest` as a copy of `src`, as if `va_start` then the same `va_arg` sequence had been applied to `dest`. Neither `va_copy` nor `va_start` shall reinitialize `dest` without an intervening `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified two independent drains of a copied `va_list` yield identical sums)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.2p3 (Returns) ‚Äî `va_copy` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (used as a void expression)

#### ¬ß7.16.1.3 The `va_end` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `void va_end(va_list ap);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.3p2 (Description/UB) ‚Äî `va_end` facilitates a normal return from the function whose va-list was referred to by `va_start`/`va_copy`; it may render `ap` unusable until reinitialized. If there is no corresponding `va_start`/`va_copy`, or if `va_end` is not invoked before return, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (compiles & runs; missing `va_end` is UB, not diagnosed by any of the three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.3p3 (Returns) ‚Äî `va_end` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.16.1.4 The `va_start` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `void va_start(va_list ap, parmN);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.4p2 (Description) ‚Äî `va_start` shall be invoked before any access to the unnamed arguments; it initializes `ap` for subsequent `va_arg`/`va_end` (and, C99/C11, `va_copy`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.16.1.4p3 (Description/UB) ‚Äî `parmN` is the rightmost named parameter (just before `, ...`). UB if `parmN` is declared `register`, with a function or array type, or with a type incompatible with its default-promoted type. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ‚Äî **mcc gap (diagnostic):** mcc *has* a `register`-param check (`check_va_start_register` in `src/mccgen.c`) but on the x86_64 SysV target the `va_start` macro reads the register-save area and never references `parmN`, so the check does not fire; gcc warns (`In function ‚Ä¶`) and clang warns (`-Wvarargs: passing a parameter declared with the 'register' keyword to 'va_start' has undefined behavior`). On i386/arm targets, where the macro expands to `&(last)`, the address-of-register diagnostic catches it. UB regardless; mcc still compiles correct code, it just misses the optional warning on x86_64.
- [‚úó] ¬ß7.16.1.4p3 (UB ‚Äî non-last second arg) ‚Äî Passing a second argument that is **not** the last non-variadic parameter is UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ‚Äî **mcc gap (diagnostic):** mcc silently accepts `va_start(ap, a)` where `a` is not the rightmost named parameter; gcc warns and clang warns (`-Wvarargs: second argument to 'va_start' is not the last non-variadic parameter`). (Optional diagnostic only ‚Äî UB, not a required diagnostic; code still compiles.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16.1.4p4 (Returns) ‚Äî `va_start` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

> Constraint cross-reference (the `...` syntax itself; primary checkbox in ¬ß6.7.5.3):
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.5.3p9 ‚Äî The ellipsis terminator `, ...` may occur only at the end of a parameter type list, and the function must have at least one named parameter preceding the ellipsis (so `parmN` exists for `va_start`); `...` is not allowed as the only parameter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì ‚Äî mcc rejects `void f(...)` ("error: identifier expected"); clang rejects ("ISO C requires a named parameter before '...'"); **gcc accepts `void f(...)` as a silent extension** even at `-std=c11` (gcc is the outlier; mcc matches the standard and clang).

#### ¬ß7.16.2 mcc-specific implementation notes (non-normative)

- [‚úì] (impl) ‚Äî mcc's bundled `<stdarg.h>` defines `typedef __builtin_va_list va_list;` and maps the four macros to `__builtin_va_*`; also provides `typedef va_list __gnuc_va_list;` and `#define _VA_LIST_DEFINED`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì (all ¬ß7.16.1.* required behaviors verified above; the two gaps are ¬ß7.16.1.4p3/non-last optional warnings only)
- [‚úì] (impl) ‚Äî mcc's bundled `<stdalign.h>` provides C11 `alignas`/`alignof` + `__alignas_is_defined`/`__alignof_is_defined`=1, and pre-C11 back-fills `_Alignas`/`_Alignof` to `__attribute__((aligned))`/`__alignof__`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì (¬ß7.15p2-p4 and ¬ß6.7.5/¬ß6.5.3.4 operator semantics + all constraint diagnostics verified)
- [‚úì] (impl) ‚Äî `<setjmp.h>` and `<signal.h>` are sourced from the host C library; mcc's burden is preserving non-volatile vs volatile automatics across `longjmp` (¬ß7.13.2.1p3), honoring the `setjmp` context constraint (¬ß7.13.1.1p4), and not assuming any `<signal.h>` facilities in freestanding mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì (verified at `-O2`; no compiler-side regression)
- [‚úì] (impl) ‚Äî mcc's bundled `<varargs.h>` is an intentional `#error` stub directing users to `<stdarg.h>`; legacy K&R varargs are unsupported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:~ (gcc/clang ship a deprecated/obsolete `varargs.h`; none of the three support it for real use)


## ¬ß7.16-¬ß7.18 stdarg/stdbool/stdint-or-atomic boundary

> mcc status: 123 TODO checkboxes in this section; 7 are places where mcc is
> observably weaker than the gcc==clang pair (exactly **1** of which is a hard
> functional conformance gap ‚Äî the others are optional-diagnostic / non-required
> QoI or non-standard predefines). Concretely: (1) `atomic_fetch_add` /
> `atomic_fetch_sub` on an **atomic pointer type** (`_Atomic(int*)`) is rejected
> outright by mcc ("integral or integer-sized pointer target type expected")
> though gcc/clang accept it ‚Äî the one hard functional gap; (2) mcc does **not**
> warn on an invalid `memory_order` constant passed to `atomic_store`/`atomic_load`
> (a runtime-UB constraint ‚Äî diagnostic not *required*, but gcc/clang both warn);
> (3) mcc does **not** warn when `va_start`'s `parmN` is `register`-qualified
> (UB; the check exists in `src/mccgen.c:check_va_start_register` but `vtop->sym`
> is dropped after the rvalue load on x86_64, so it never fires); gcc/clang warn.
> Everything else ‚Äî the full `<stdarg.h>` macro set, the entire `<stdbool.h>`,
> all 36 atomic typedefs, all lock-free macros (all `=2`), `memory_order`
> enumerators (0..5), fences, `atomic_flag`, every generic op, `kill_dependency`,
> `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT`/`atomic_init`, atomic-via-plain-operators ‚Äî matches the
> gcc==clang consensus byte-for-byte. NB: gcc and clang **themselves disagree** on
> atomic pointer `fetch_add` scaling (gcc scales by bytes, clang by elements);
> clang is standard-correct.

> **Clause-7 numbering reconciliation (N1256 C99 vs N1570 C11).** C11 inserted two
> new headers into clause 7 ‚Äî `<stdalign.h>` (C11 ¬ß7.15) and `<stdatomic.h>`
> (C11 ¬ß7.17) ‚Äî which shifts every later header by two section numbers. The headers
> covered here therefore carry *different* clause numbers in the two standards:
>
> | Header | C99 (N1256) | C11 (N1570) |
> |---|---|---|
> | `<stdarg.h>` Variable arguments | ¬ß7.15 | ¬ß7.16 |
> | `<stdatomic.h>` Atomics | ‚Äî (does not exist) | ¬ß7.17 |
> | `<stdbool.h>` Boolean type and values | ¬ß7.16 | ¬ß7.18 |
> | `<stddef.h>` Common definitions | ¬ß7.17 | ¬ß7.19 |
> | `<stdint.h>` Integer types | ¬ß7.18 | ¬ß7.20 |
>
> Hence the "¬ß7.16‚Äì¬ß7.18 boundary" is a *moving* boundary: in C99 ¬ß7.16 = stdbool,
> ¬ß7.17 = stddef, ¬ß7.18 = stdint; in C11 ¬ß7.16 = stdarg, ¬ß7.17 = stdatomic,
> ¬ß7.18 = stdbool. This section fully expands `<stdarg.h>`, `<stdbool.h>`, and the
> C11-only `<stdatomic.h>`. `<stddef.h>` and `<stdint.h>` are expanded in their own
> sections; only their numbering is reconciled above. In mcc the four `<stdarg.h>`
> macros are thin wrappers over `__builtin_va_start`/`__builtin_va_arg`/
> `__builtin_va_copy`/`__builtin_va_end`, and `va_list` is `__builtin_va_list`.

### ¬ß7.15 / ¬ß7.16 (C11) Variable arguments `<stdarg.h>`

> C99 added `va_copy` (¬ß7.15.2); it does not exist in C90. C11 reworded the
> `va_start` description but the macro set is unchanged from C99. Verified: mcc's
> `runtime/include/stdarg.h` defines all four macros plus `va_list`, and a
> `va_start`/`va_copy`/`va_arg`/`va_end` round-trip (including passing the
> `va_list` to a callee, vprintf-style) produces output identical to gcc/clang.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p1 (C11 ¬ß7.16p1) ‚Äî `<stdarg.h>` shall declare a type and define four macros (`va_start`, `va_arg`, `va_end`, `va_copy`) for advancing through a list of arguments whose number and types are not known to the called function when it is translated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16p2) ‚Äî The type declared is `va_list`, an object type suitable for holding information needed by the macros `va_start`, `va_arg`, `va_end`, and `va_copy`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `typedef __builtin_va_list va_list;`)
- ¬ß7.15p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16p2) ‚Äî If access to the varying arguments is desired, the called function shall declare an object (referred to here as `ap`) having type `va_list`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16p2) ‚Äî The object `ap` may be passed as an argument to another function; if that function invokes the `va_arg` macro with parameter `ap`, the value of `ap` in the calling function is indeterminate and shall be passed to the `va_end` macro prior to any further reference to `ap`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (vprintf-style pass-through verified; UB-after-callee not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.15p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16p3) ‚Äî Constraint: each invocation of the `va_start` and `va_copy` macros shall be matched by a corresponding invocation of the `va_end` macro in the same function. ‚Äî (spec; UB on mismatch, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.15.1 / ¬ß7.16.1 (C11) The `va_arg` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.1p1 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `type va_arg(va_list ap, type);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.15.1p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p2) ‚Äî Constraint: the parameter `ap` shall have been initialized by the `va_start` or `va_copy` macro without an intervening invocation of the `va_end` macro for the same `ap`; otherwise the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.1p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p2) ‚Äî The `va_arg` macro expands to an expression that has the specified `type` and the value of the next argument in the call, and modifies `ap` so that the values of successive arguments are returned in turn. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (successive `va_arg` returns 10,20,30 on all three)
- ¬ß7.15.1p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p2) ‚Äî The parameter `type` shall be a type name specified such that the type of a pointer to an object that has the specified type can be obtained simply by postfixing a `*` to `type`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.15.1p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p2) ‚Äî If there is no actual next argument, or if `type` is not compatible with the type of the actual next argument (as promoted according to the default argument promotions), the behavior is undefined, except for the two following cases. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.1p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p2) ‚Äî Exception 1 (well-defined): one type is a signed integer type, the other is the corresponding unsigned integer type, and the value is representable in both types. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`int` arg read as `unsigned` ‚Üí 5 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.1p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p2) ‚Äî Exception 2 (well-defined): one type is pointer to `void` and the other is a pointer to a character type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`void*` arg read as `char*` ‚Üí "hi" on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.1p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16.1p3) ‚Äî Returns: the first invocation of `va_arg` after that of `va_start` returns the value of the argument after that specified by `parmN`; successive invocations return the values of the remaining arguments in succession. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.15.2 / ¬ß7.16.2 (C11) The `va_copy` macro (C99; absent in C90)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.2p1 (C11 ¬ß7.16.2p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `void va_copy(va_list dest, va_list src);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `#define va_copy __builtin_va_copy`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.2p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.2p2) ‚Äî The `va_copy` macro initializes `dest` as a copy of `src`, as if the `va_start` macro had been applied to `dest` followed by the same sequence of uses of the `va_arg` macro as had previously been used to reach the present state of `src`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (double-traversal sum 60+60=120 identical on all three)
- ¬ß7.15.2p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.2p2) ‚Äî Constraint: neither the `va_copy` nor the `va_start` macro shall be invoked to reinitialize `dest` without an intervening invocation of the `va_end` macro for the same `dest`. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.2p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16.2p3) ‚Äî Returns: the `va_copy` macro returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.15.3 / ¬ß7.16.3 (C11) The `va_end` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.3p1 (C11 ¬ß7.16.3p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `void va_end(va_list ap);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `#define va_end __builtin_va_end`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.3p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.3p2) ‚Äî The `va_end` macro facilitates a normal return from the function whose variable argument list was referred to by the expansion of `va_start`, or the function containing the expansion of `va_copy`, that initialized the `va_list ap`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.15.3p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.3p2) ‚Äî The `va_end` macro may modify `ap` so that it is no longer usable (without being reinitialized by `va_start` or `va_copy`). ‚Äî (spec; permissive "may", not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.15.3p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.3p2) ‚Äî If there is no corresponding invocation of the `va_start` or `va_copy` macro, or if `va_end` is not invoked before the return, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.3p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16.3p3) ‚Äî Returns: the `va_end` macro returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.15.4 / ¬ß7.16.4 (C11) The `va_start` macro

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.4p1 (C11 ¬ß7.16.4p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` then `void va_start(va_list ap, parmN);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `#define va_start __builtin_va_start`)
- ¬ß7.15.4p2 (C11 ¬ß7.16.4p2) ‚Äî The `va_start` macro shall be invoked before any access to the unnamed arguments. ‚Äî (spec; UB on violation, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.4p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16.4p3) ‚Äî The `va_start` macro initializes `ap` for subsequent use by `va_arg` and `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.4p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16.4p3) ‚Äî The parameter `parmN` is the identifier of the rightmost parameter in the variable parameter list in the function definition (the one just before the `, ...`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.15.4p3 (C11 ¬ß7.16.4p3) ‚Äî If the parameter `parmN` is declared with the `register` storage class, with a function or array type, or with a type that is not compatible with the type that results after application of the default argument promotions, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (UB; gcc/clang emit `-Wvarargs` "register" warning, mcc emits **no** warning ‚Äî its `check_va_start_register` exists but `vtop->sym` is dropped after the x86_64 rvalue load so it never fires; not a conformance break since the diagnostic is optional)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.15.4p4 (C11 ¬ß7.16.4p4) ‚Äî Returns: the `va_start` macro returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.16 / ¬ß7.18 (C11) Boolean type and values `<stdbool.h>`

> Identical content in C99 and C11 apart from the moved clause number and the
> ¬ß6.10.8 ‚Üí ¬ß6.10.8 (same heading, renumbered in C11) cross-reference. The
> undefine/redefine allowance is flagged obsolescent in both standards' future
> directions. Verified against mcc's `runtime/include/stdbool.h`: exactly the four
> macros, all usable in `#if` and after `#undef`/redefine; matches gcc/clang.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p1 (C11 ¬ß7.18p1) ‚Äî `<stdbool.h>` shall define four macros: `bool`, `true`, `false`, and `__bool_true_false_are_defined`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p2 (C11 ¬ß7.18p2) ‚Äî The macro `bool` shall expand to `_Bool`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(bool x)==sizeof(_Bool)` holds)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p3 (C11 ¬ß7.18p3) ‚Äî The macro `true` shall expand to the integer constant `1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if true==1` and `_Static_assert(true==1)` pass)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p3 (C11 ¬ß7.18p3) ‚Äî The macro `false` shall expand to the integer constant `0`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p3 (C11 ¬ß7.18p3) ‚Äî The macro `__bool_true_false_are_defined` shall expand to the integer constant `1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16p4 (C11 ¬ß7.18p4) ‚Äî Notwithstanding the provisions of ¬ß6.10.8, a program may undefine and perhaps then redefine the macros `bool`, `true`, and `false`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#undef bool/true/false` then `#define bool int` etc. accepted on all three)
- ¬ß7.26.7 (C11 ¬ß7.31.9) ‚Äî (Future directions) The ability to undefine and perhaps then redefine the macros `bool`, `true`, and `false` is an obsolescent feature. ‚Äî (spec; future-direction note, not separately testable)

#### Added gaps ‚Äî `<stdbool.h>` extras

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.16 (C11 ¬ß7.18) ‚Äî The header defines *only* these four macros (no extra `bool`-related identifiers leak); confirmed mcc header has no surplus definitions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.1/¬ß7.18 (C11) ‚Äî `_Bool` (the underlying type `bool` expands to) is a first-class type usable without including the header; `bool x = true;` round-trips and stores 0/1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.17 (C11) Atomics `<stdatomic.h>` (C11-only; not present in C99)

> Entire header is C11-only. `<stdatomic.h>` ties to the `_Atomic` type qualifier
> (¬ß6.7.2.4, ¬ß6.7.3) and to the conditional-feature macro `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`
> (¬ß6.10.8.3): an implementation that defines `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` need not provide
> this header nor support its facilities. In all synopses below, `A` denotes one of
> the atomic types, `C` denotes its corresponding non-atomic type, and `M` is the
> type of the arithmetic operand ‚Äî `int` for atomic integer types and `ptrdiff_t`
> for atomic pointer types. (Note: `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT` was deprecated by C17/DR485 and
> removed in C23; `atomic_init` supersedes it. The `failure ‚â§ success` ordering
> constraint of ¬ß7.17.7.4 was likewise relaxed by C17/DR459.) Verified: none of the
> three compilers defines `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` (all support atomics); mcc's
> `runtime/include/stdatomic.h` is a `__atomic_*`-builtin‚Äìbacked header.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî None of mcc/gcc/clang defines `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` under `-std=c11` (all provide `<stdatomic.h>` and its facilities). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-dM -E` dump: macro absent on all three)

#### ¬ß7.17.1 (C11) Introduction

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `<stdatomic.h>` shall define several macros and declare several types and functions for performing atomic operations on data shared between threads. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Implementations that define the macro `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` (see ¬ß6.10.8.3) need not provide this header nor support any of its facilities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none defines it; all provide the header)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî The header shall define the atomic lock-free macros `ATOMIC_BOOL_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_CHAR_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_CHAR16_T_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_CHAR32_T_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_WCHAR_T_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_SHORT_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_INT_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_LONG_LOCK_FREE`, `ATOMIC_LLONG_LOCK_FREE`, and `ATOMIC_POINTER_LOCK_FREE`, indicating the lock-free property of the corresponding atomic types (both signed and unsigned). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all 10 `#defined`; `#if !defined(...)` guard passes on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî Each lock-free macro shall expand to a constant expression suitable for use in `#if` preprocessing directives. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if ATOMIC_INT_LOCK_FREE` evaluated successfully on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî A lock-free macro value of `0` indicates the corresponding atomic type is never lock-free, `1` indicates it is sometimes lock-free, and `2` indicates it is always lock-free. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (every macro = 2 on x86_64 for all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT` (see ¬ß7.17.8). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `#define ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT {0}`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p4 (C11) ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT` (see ¬ß7.17.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `#define ATOMIC_VAR_INIT(value) (value)`; deprecated by C17 but still present, no deprecation warning on any compiler)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p4 (C11) ‚Äî The types declared shall include `memory_order` (an enumerated type whose enumerators identify memory-ordering constraints), `atomic_flag` (a structure type representing a lock-free primitive atomic flag), and the named atomic integer types of ¬ß7.17.6. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`memory_order` enum, `atomic_flag` struct, and all named types declared)

#### ¬ß7.17.2 (C11) Initialization

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#define ATOMIC_VAR_INIT(value) /* see below */`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.2p2 (C11) ‚Äî The `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT` macro expands to a token sequence suitable for initializing an atomic object of a type that is initialization-compatible with `value`. An atomic object with automatic storage duration that is not explicitly initialized is initially in an indeterminate state; however, the default (zero) initialization for objects with static or thread-local storage duration is guaranteed to produce a valid state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_int a = ATOMIC_VAR_INIT(3)` loads back 3 on all three)
- ¬ß7.17.2p3 (C11) ‚Äî Concurrent access to the variable being initialized via `ATOMIC_VAR_INIT`, even by an atomic operation, constitutes a data race. ‚Äî (spec; concurrency UB, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.2p4 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `void atomic_init(volatile A *obj, C value);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc maps `atomic_init` ‚Üí `atomic_store_explicit(...,__ATOMIC_RELAXED)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.2p5 (C11) ‚Äî The `atomic_init` generic function initializes the atomic object pointed to by `obj` to the value `value`, and also initializes any additional state the implementation might carry for the atomic object; it does not avoid data races, so concurrent access to the variable being initialized, even via an atomic operation, constitutes a data race. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_init(&a,5)` then `atomic_load` reflects the value)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.2p6 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_init` generic function returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.17.3 (C11) Order and consistency

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.3p1 (C11) ‚Äî The enumerated type `memory_order` specifies the detailed regular (non-atomic) memory synchronization operations and may provide for operation ordering; its enumeration constants are `memory_order_relaxed`, `memory_order_consume`, `memory_order_acquire`, `memory_order_release`, `memory_order_acq_rel`, and `memory_order_seq_cst`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all six enumerators present; values 0..5 on all three)
- ¬ß7.17.3p2 (C11) ‚Äî For `memory_order_seq_cst` operations there shall be a single total order S on all such operations, consistent with the "happens before" order and the modification orders of all affected objects. ‚Äî (spec; abstract-machine memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî `memory_order_relaxed`: the operation neither requires nor provides any ordering with respect to other memory operations (no synchronizes-with or ordering constraints). ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî `memory_order_consume`: a load operation performs a consume operation on the affected memory location, ordering subsequent operations that carry a dependency from the loaded value. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî `memory_order_acquire`: a load operation performs an acquire operation on the affected memory location. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî `memory_order_release`: a store operation performs a release operation on the affected memory location. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî `memory_order_acq_rel`: a read-modify-write operation performs both an acquire and a release operation on the affected memory location. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî `memory_order_seq_cst`: a load performs an acquire, a store performs a release, and a read-modify-write performs both, plus participation in the single total order S. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3 (C11) ‚Äî An atomic operation A that performs a release operation on an atomic object M synchronizes with an atomic operation B that performs an acquire operation on M and takes its value from any side effect in the release sequence headed by A (release/acquire synchronization semantics). ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3 (C11) ‚Äî The "happens before" / "carries a dependency" / "dependency-ordered before" / "release sequence" relations defined here shall hold as specified for establishing inter-thread ordering and visibility of side effects. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3p4 (C11) ‚Äî An atomic store with `memory_order_seq_cst` from which an atomic load with `memory_order_seq_cst` takes its value shall be consistent with the total order S. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.17.3 (C11) ‚Äî Implementations should ensure that no "out-of-thin-air" values are computed that circularly depend on their own computation. ‚Äî (spec; "should" recommendation, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.3 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#define kill_dependency(y) /* see below */`. The `kill_dependency` macro terminates a dependency chain: the argument `y` does not carry a dependency into the macro's return value, which equals the value of `y`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`kill_dependency(7)` yields 7 on all three; mcc impl is a statement-expression returning the value)

#### ¬ß7.17.4 (C11) Fences

- ¬ß7.17.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî This subclause introduces synchronization primitives called fences, supporting "fence-fence", "fence-atomic", and "atomic-fence" synchronization; a fence with acquire semantics is an acquire fence and a fence with release semantics is a release fence. ‚Äî (spec; memory model, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `void atomic_thread_fence(memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared `extern void atomic_thread_fence(memory_order)`; call links & runs)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.4p3 (C11) ‚Äî Depending on `order`, `atomic_thread_fence` has no effect if `order == memory_order_relaxed`; is an acquire fence if `order == memory_order_acquire` or `memory_order_consume`; is a release fence if `order == memory_order_release`; is both an acquire and a release fence if `order == memory_order_acq_rel`; and is a sequentially consistent acquire and release fence if `order == memory_order_seq_cst`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (compiles/runs; per-order fence semantics not separately observable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: `atomic_thread_fence` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.4p5 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `void atomic_signal_fence(memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc declares `extern void atomic_signal_fence(memory_order)` + barrier macro)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.4p6 (C11) ‚Äî `atomic_signal_fence` is equivalent to `atomic_thread_fence(order)`, except that the resulting ordering constraints are established only between a thread and a signal handler executed in the same thread. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (compiles/runs)
- ¬ß7.17.4p7 (C11) ‚Äî `atomic_signal_fence` shall not issue any hardware fence instruction; it is a compiler barrier only. ‚Äî (spec; codegen property, not separately testable here)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.4p8 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: `atomic_signal_fence` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.17.5 (C11) Lock-free property

- ¬ß7.17.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî The atomic lock-free macros indicate the lock-free property of atomic types for the corresponding `_Atomic` types; atomic operations that are lock-free should also be address-free (usable on memory shared between processes via shared memory). ‚Äî (spec; "should" recommendation, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `_Bool atomic_is_lock_free(const volatile A *obj);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `atomic_is_lock_free(OBJ)` ‚Üí `__atomic_is_lock_free(sizeof(*(OBJ)),(OBJ))`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.5p3 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_is_lock_free` generic function returns nonzero (true) if and only if the object's operations are lock-free; the result of a lock-free query on one object cannot be generalized to another object even of the same type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_is_lock_free(&atomic_int)` returns 1 on all three)

#### ¬ß7.17.6 (C11) Atomic integer types
