- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.6p1 (C11) ‚Äî For each line in the table of ¬ß7.17.6, the named atomic type (the "atomic type name" column) shall be declared as a type that has the same representation and alignment requirements as the corresponding `_Atomic` direct type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(atomic_llong)==sizeof(long long)`, `_Alignof(atomic_int)>=_Alignof(int)` hold)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.6p1 (C11) ‚Äî The header shall provide the typedef names, each as the `_Atomic`-qualified version of its corresponding direct type: `atomic_bool` (`_Bool`), `atomic_char` (`char`), `atomic_schar` (`signed char`), `atomic_uchar` (`unsigned char`), `atomic_short` (`short`), `atomic_ushort` (`unsigned short`), `atomic_int` (`int`), `atomic_uint` (`unsigned int`), `atomic_long` (`long`), `atomic_ulong` (`unsigned long`), `atomic_llong` (`long long`), `atomic_ullong` (`unsigned long long`), `atomic_char16_t` (`char16_t`/`uint_least16_t`), `atomic_char32_t` (`char32_t`/`uint_least32_t`), `atomic_wchar_t` (`wchar_t`), `atomic_int_least8_t`, `atomic_uint_least8_t`, `atomic_int_least16_t`, `atomic_uint_least16_t`, `atomic_int_least32_t`, `atomic_uint_least32_t`, `atomic_int_least64_t`, `atomic_uint_least64_t`, `atomic_int_fast8_t`, `atomic_uint_fast8_t`, `atomic_int_fast16_t`, `atomic_uint_fast16_t`, `atomic_int_fast32_t`, `atomic_uint_fast32_t`, `atomic_int_fast64_t`, `atomic_uint_fast64_t`, `atomic_intptr_t`, `atomic_uintptr_t`, `atomic_size_t`, `atomic_ptrdiff_t`, `atomic_intmax_t`, and `atomic_uintmax_t`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (a single TU declaring objects of all 36 typedefs compiles on all three)
- ¬ß7.17.6p2 (C11) ‚Äî (Note) The atomic types' representation need not have the same size as their corresponding regular types, though they should have the same size whenever possible to ease compatibility. ‚Äî (spec; informative note, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.17.7 (C11) Operations on atomic types

- ¬ß7.17.7p1 (C11) ‚Äî In the following synopses, `A` refers to one of the atomic types, `C` to its corresponding non-atomic type, and `M` to the operand type ‚Äî `int` for atomic integer types and `ptrdiff_t` for atomic pointer types. ‚Äî (spec; notation, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7p2 (C11) ‚Äî The non-explicit (no-`order`-argument) generic functions are defined to behave as the corresponding `_explicit` function invoked with `memory_order_seq_cst` for its `order` argument(s). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc header literally defines each non-explicit macro as the `_explicit` form with `__ATOMIC_SEQ_CST`)

##### ¬ß7.17.7.1 (C11) The `atomic_store` generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `void atomic_store(volatile A *object, C desired);` and `void atomic_store_explicit(volatile A *object, C desired, memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.17.7.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: the `order` argument shall not be `memory_order_acquire`, `memory_order_consume`, nor `memory_order_acq_rel`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (runtime-UB restriction, diagnostic *not* required; gcc warns `-Winvalid-memory-model`, clang warns `-Watomic-memory-ordering`, **mcc emits no diagnostic** for `atomic_store_explicit(&a,1,memory_order_acquire)` ‚Äî mcc weaker QoI, gcc/clang reject-with-warning)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically replace the value pointed to by `object` with `desired`; memory is affected according to the value of `order`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (store-then-load round-trips identically)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.1p4 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_store` generic functions return no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.17.7.2 (C11) The `atomic_load` generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `C atomic_load(volatile A *object);` and `C atomic_load_explicit(volatile A *object, memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.17.7.2p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: the `order` argument shall not be `memory_order_release` nor `memory_order_acq_rel`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (runtime-UB restriction, diagnostic not required; gcc/clang warn, **mcc emits no diagnostic**)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.2p3 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically returns the value pointed to by `object`; memory is affected according to the value of `order`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.2p4 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_load` generic functions return the value pointed to by `object`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (load after store of 11 returns 11 on all three)

##### ¬ß7.17.7.3 (C11) The `atomic_exchange` generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.3p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `C atomic_exchange(volatile A *object, C desired);` and `C atomic_exchange_explicit(volatile A *object, C desired, memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.3p2 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically replace the value pointed to by `object` with `desired`; memory is affected according to `order`; these are read-modify-write operations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.3p3 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_exchange` generic functions return the value that had previously been pointed to by `object`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (exchange returns prior 11, then prior 20, identical on all three)

##### ¬ß7.17.7.4 (C11) The `atomic_compare_exchange` generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `_Bool atomic_compare_exchange_strong(volatile A *object, C *expected, C desired);`, `_Bool atomic_compare_exchange_strong_explicit(volatile A *object, C *expected, C desired, memory_order success, memory_order failure);`, `_Bool atomic_compare_exchange_weak(volatile A *object, C *expected, C desired);`, and `_Bool atomic_compare_exchange_weak_explicit(volatile A *object, C *expected, C desired, memory_order success, memory_order failure);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all four forms compile and run)
- [~] ¬ß7.17.7.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: the `failure` argument shall not be `memory_order_release` nor `memory_order_acq_rel`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (runtime-UB restriction; gcc/clang warn on a bad constant, mcc does not ‚Äî same QoI pattern as store/load)
- ¬ß7.17.7.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint (C11-as-published; relaxed by C17/DR459): the `failure` argument shall not be a stronger order than the `success` argument. ‚Äî (spec; relaxed by C17, diagnostic not required, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.4p3 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically compares the contents of the memory pointed to by `object` for equality with that pointed to by `expected`, and if equal replaces the contents pointed to by `object` with `desired` (a read-modify-write operation), else loads the contents pointed to by `object` into the memory pointed to by `expected`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (success path returns 1 & updates object; fail path returns 0 & writes actual value into `*expected` ‚Äî `exp2` becomes 30 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.4p3 (C11) ‚Äî The `success` memory order governs the read-modify-write when the comparison is true; the `failure` memory order governs the load when the comparison is false. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both orderings accepted; semantics not separately observable)
- ¬ß7.17.7.4p3 (C11) ‚Äî These operations compare the object representations (bitwise, as by `memcmp`), so an object may compare unequal even when its value is equal if it contains padding or trap-related representation bits. ‚Äî (spec; representation-comparison UB-ish edge, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî A `_weak` compare-exchange may fail spuriously ‚Äî that is, act as if `*object != *expected` even when they are equal ‚Äî returning false and updating `*expected`; a `_strong` compare-exchange shall not fail spuriously. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (both forms accepted; spurious failure is a "may", not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_compare_exchange` generic functions return the result of the comparison (true if `object` was replaced by `desired`, false otherwise). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.17.7.5 (C11) The `atomic_fetch` and modify generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: for each operation `key` ‚àà {`add`, `sub`, `or`, `xor`, `and`}, the header provides `C atomic_fetch_key(volatile A *object, M operand);` and `C atomic_fetch_key_explicit(volatile A *object, M operand, memory_order order);` (i.e. `atomic_fetch_add`, `atomic_fetch_sub`, `atomic_fetch_or`, `atomic_fetch_xor`, `atomic_fetch_and`, and their `_explicit` variants). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all 10 names compile & run for integer atomics on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically replace the value pointed to by `object` with the result of applying the operation `key` to the value pointed to by `object` and the value `operand`; memory is affected according to `order`; these are read-modify-write operations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî For signed integer types, the arithmetic of `atomic_fetch_add`/`atomic_fetch_sub` is performed with silent two's-complement wraparound (no undefined behavior on overflow). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (integer fetch_add/sub round-trip; defined wraparound, not separately fuzzed)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.5p2 (C11) ‚Äî For atomic pointer (address) types, the result is as if computed with `ptrdiff_t` operand type (i.e. the operand scales by the pointee size). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_fetch_add`/`atomic_fetch_sub` (and the `_explicit`/`add_fetch`/`sub_fetch` forms) on `_Atomic(int*)` now scale the operand by the pointee size, matching the C11 `<stdatomic.h>` element-scaled result of gcc and clang; verified for `int*` and `double*` in exec/atomic_ptr. `atomic_fetch_or/and/xor` on a pointer, and any op on a non-atomic pointer, are still rejected. The raw GCC `__atomic_add_fetch` builtin on an `_Atomic`-qualified pointer is accepted more leniently by mcc than by clang.)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7.5p3 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_fetch_key` generic functions return the value that `object` previously pointed to (the value immediately before the effects of the operation). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (integer `fetch_add` returns prior value on all three)

#### ¬ß7.17.8 (C11) Atomic flag type and operations

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8p1 (C11) ‚Äî The `atomic_flag` type provides the classic test-and-set functionality; it is a structure type with two states, set and clear. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `typedef struct { atomic_bool value; } atomic_flag;`)
- ¬ß7.17.8p1 (C11) ‚Äî Operations on an `atomic_flag` object shall be lock-free (it is the one atomic type guaranteed lock-free). ‚Äî (spec; guarantee, not separately testable beyond `is_lock_free`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8p2 (C11) ‚Äî The macro `ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT` shall be defined to initialize an `atomic_flag` to the clear state; e.g. `atomic_flag guard = ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT;`. It may be used only to initialize a flag with static storage duration or a declaration of an automatic object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atomic_flag f = ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT;` then `test_and_set` returns 0 ‚Üí confirms clear init, on all three)
- ¬ß7.17.8p3 (C11) ‚Äî An `atomic_flag` that is not explicitly initialized with `ATOMIC_FLAG_INIT` is initially in an indeterminate state. ‚Äî (spec; indeterminate-state UB, not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.17.8.1 (C11) The `atomic_flag_test_and_set` generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `_Bool atomic_flag_test_and_set(volatile atomic_flag *object);` and `_Bool atomic_flag_test_and_set_explicit(volatile atomic_flag *object, memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc declares both as `extern bool ...(volatile atomic_flag *, ...)`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically set the value pointed to by `object` to true; memory is affected according to `order`; these are read-modify-write operations. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_flag_test_and_set` generic functions return the value of the `atomic_flag` pointed to by `object` immediately before the effects (the previous state). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (first `test_and_set` ‚Üí 0 (was clear), second ‚Üí 1 (was set), identical on all three)
- [~] ¬ß7.17.8.1 (C11) ‚Äî Passing a non-`atomic_flag` argument is diagnosed (mcc declares the real `volatile atomic_flag *` signature rather than a `void*` builtin). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úó clang:‚úì (mcc **warns** "assignment from incompatible pointer type"; clang **errors**; **gcc accepts silently** ‚Äî mcc is between the two, gcc/clang split)

##### ¬ß7.17.8.2 (C11) The `atomic_flag_clear` generic functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî Synopsis: `void atomic_flag_clear(volatile atomic_flag *object);` and `void atomic_flag_clear_explicit(volatile atomic_flag *object, memory_order order);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.17.8.2p2 (C11) ‚Äî Constraint: the `order` argument shall not be `memory_order_acquire`, `memory_order_consume`, nor `memory_order_acq_rel`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (runtime-UB restriction, diagnostic not required; gcc/clang warn, mcc does not ‚Äî same QoI pattern as store/load)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8.2p3 (C11) ‚Äî Atomically set the value pointed to by `object` to false; memory is affected according to `order`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`test_and_set` ‚Üí `clear` ‚Üí `test_and_set` returns 0 again, confirming clear, on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.8.2p4 (C11) ‚Äî Returns: the `atomic_flag_clear` generic functions return no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### Added gaps ‚Äî `<stdatomic.h>` / `_Atomic` extras

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.7.2.4/¬ß6.7.3 (C11) ‚Äî The `_Atomic` type qualifier and the `_Atomic(type-name)` specifier form are both accepted (`_Atomic int`, `int *_Atomic`, `_Atomic(int*)` all declare cleanly). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.5.2.4/¬ß6.5.16.2 (C11) ‚Äî An `_Atomic`-qualified object used with plain operators (`a=5; a++; a+=10;`) performs implicit atomic read-modify-write; result 16 identical on all three. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.1p3 (C11) ‚Äî Both signed and unsigned variants share the lock-free macro for their common rank (e.g. `atomic_int`/`atomic_uint` both governed by `ATOMIC_INT_LOCK_FREE`); confirmed via the per-rank macro set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.6/¬ß7.17.1 (C11) ‚Äî `atomic_char16_t`/`atomic_char32_t` are typedef'd over `uint_least16_t`/`uint_least32_t` (mcc) ‚Äî compatible with the `char16_t`/`char32_t` mapping; objects of both declare cleanly. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__GCC_ATOMIC_*_LOCK_FREE` predefined macros: gcc and clang predefine the full `__GCC_ATOMIC_*` / `__CLANG_ATOMIC_*` set; **mcc predefines only the `__ATOMIC_*` memory-order constants** (0..5), not the `__GCC_ATOMIC_*_LOCK_FREE` family. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (the public `ATOMIC_*_LOCK_FREE` macros are still provided by mcc's header, so portable code is unaffected; only the gcc/clang-internal `__GCC_ATOMIC_*` predefines are absent ‚Äî not a C11 requirement)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17.7 (C11) ‚Äî Each `_explicit` generic accepts a runtime (non-constant) `memory_order` argument, not only a compile-time constant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified via `memory_order` enum object passed through)


## <stddef.h> & <stdint.h>

> mcc status: 51 TODO items; 0 mcc-gaps. Every mechanically testable requirement was probed against mcc, gcc 15.3, and clang 22 on both the hosted (`#include_next` over glibc) and the freestanding (`-ffreestanding -nostdinc`) paths; mcc matches the gcc==clang consensus on all of them.

> Clause numbers differ between revisions: `<stddef.h>` is ¬ß7.17 in C99 (N1256) and ¬ß7.19 in C11 (N1570); `<stdint.h>` is ¬ß7.18 in C99 and ¬ß7.20 in C11. Citations give the C99 number with the C11 number in brackets. mcc ships both headers in `runtime/include/` (`stddef.h`, `stdint.h`). On a hosted target `<stdint.h>` does `#include_next <stdint.h>` (guarded by `__has_include_next`) and only back-fills the C11 contents when the system header was absent (detected via `#ifndef INT8_MAX`); on `-ffreestanding`/`-nostdinc` it defines the full contents itself. `<stddef.h>` is fully self-defined on every path. All requirements below were verified to compile under `mcc -std=c11` on both the hosted and freestanding paths.

### ¬ß7.17 [¬ß7.19] Common definitions <stddef.h>

> C11 difference: C11 adds the type `max_align_t` to `<stddef.h>`; it is absent in C99. mcc gates it on `__STDC_VERSION__ >= 201112L`.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p1 [¬ß7.19p1] ‚Äî `<stddef.h>` shall define the types `ptrdiff_t`, `size_t`, `wchar_t` and ((C11) `max_align_t`), and the macros `NULL` and `offsetof(type, member-designator)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p2 [¬ß7.19p2] ‚Äî `ptrdiff_t` shall be the signed integer type of the result of subtracting two pointers. (mcc: `typedef __PTRDIFF_TYPE__ ptrdiff_t;`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p2 [¬ß7.19p2] ‚Äî `size_t` shall be the unsigned integer type of the result of the `sizeof` operator. (mcc: `typedef __SIZE_TYPE__ size_t;`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.17p2 [¬ß7.19p2] ‚Äî `wchar_t` shall be an integer type whose range of values can represent distinct codes for all members of the largest extended character set among the supported locales; the null character shall have code value zero, and a member of the basic character set shall have a code value equal to its value as the lone character of an integer character constant. (mcc: `typedef __WCHAR_TYPE__ wchar_t;`.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p2 [¬ß7.19p2] ‚Äî (C11) `max_align_t` shall be an object type whose alignment is as great as is supported by the implementation in all contexts. (mcc: `typedef union { long long __ll; long double __ld; } max_align_t;`, defined only when `__STDC_VERSION__ >= 201112L`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p2 [¬ß7.19p2] ‚Äî (C11) `max_align_t` is absent under C99; including `<stddef.h>` with `-std=c99` must not define it. (mcc: gated by `__STDC_VERSION__ >= 201112L`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three reject `max_align_t` under `-std=c99`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p3 [¬ß7.19p3] ‚Äî `NULL` shall expand to an implementation-defined null pointer constant. (mcc: `#define NULL ((void*)0)`, guarded by `#ifndef NULL`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p3 [¬ß7.19p3] ‚Äî `NULL`'s `#ifndef` guard must not warn-redefine when another header (e.g. `<stdio.h>`) already defined `NULL`. (mcc: `#ifndef NULL`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`-Wall` clean with `<stdio.h>` included first)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p3 [¬ß7.19p3] ‚Äî `offsetof(type, member-designator)` shall expand to an integer constant expression of type `size_t` whose value is the offset in bytes, to the structure member designated by `member-designator`, from the beginning of its structure designated by `type`. (mcc: `#define offsetof(type, field) __builtin_offsetof(type, field)`, preceded by `#undef offsetof`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Generic` confirms result type is exactly `size_t`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p3 [¬ß7.19p3] ‚Äî `member-designator` may include array subscripting and member access (e.g. `offsetof(struct S, arr[3])`). (mcc: forwarded to `__builtin_offsetof`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.17p3 [¬ß7.19p3] ‚Äî `type` and `member-designator` shall be such that, given `static type t;`, the expression `&(t.member-designator)` evaluates to an address constant. (Constraint on the program; mcc enforces it via `__builtin_offsetof`.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.17p3 footnote [¬ß7.19p3] ‚Äî If `member-designator` designates a bit-field, the behavior is undefined. (mcc/gcc/clang: rejected as required.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three reject `offsetof` of a bit-field member with a diagnostic)
- [‚úì] (namespace) ¬ß7.1.3 ‚Äî A strictly conforming `<stddef.h>` defines only `ptrdiff_t`, `size_t`, `max_align_t`, `wchar_t`, `NULL`, and `offsetof`; no other identifiers are introduced. (mcc: keeps `ssize_t`/`intptr_t`/`uintptr_t` out of `<stddef.h>` on the ELF path, matching gcc's own `<stddef.h>`; supplies `ssize_t`/`intptr_t`/`uintptr_t` here only on the `_WIN32`/PE target to match MinGW's `<stddef.h>`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (re-declaring `intptr_t`/`ssize_t`/`uintptr_t` as plain `int` after `<stddef.h>` compiles cleanly on all three ‚áí no leak)
- (extension) ‚Äî On `__need_wint_t`, `<stddef.h>` additionally defines `wint_t` (`typedef __WINT_TYPE__ wint_t;`, guarded by `_WINT_T`) and then `#undef`s `__need_wint_t`; this glibc-compatibility hook does not introduce identifiers in the default include. (mcc-specific.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.18 [¬ß7.20] Integer types <stdint.h>

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18p1 [¬ß7.20p1] ‚Äî `<stdint.h>` declares sets of integer types having specified widths and defines corresponding sets of macros, and also defines macros specifying limits of integer types defined in other standard headers. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18p1 [¬ß7.20p1] ‚Äî Types are defined in the following categories: exact-width (¬ß7.18.1.1), minimum-width (¬ß7.18.1.2), fastest minimum-width (¬ß7.18.1.3), integer types wide enough to hold object pointers (¬ß7.18.1.4), and greatest-width integer types (¬ß7.18.1.5). (Cross-reference to subclauses below; mcc provides all five categories.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18p2 [¬ß7.20p2] ‚Äî For each type described herein, if the implementation provides integer types meeting the stated requirements, it shall declare the typedef name and define the associated macros; required types/macros are present unconditionally and optional ones only when provided. (mcc: provides all required types plus the common optional exact-width 8/16/32/64 set on every supported target.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18p3 [¬ß7.20p3] ‚Äî A program shall not define the macros named in this header (e.g. `INTN_MAX`, `INTN_C`); the header may be included more than once with consistent effect. (mcc: idempotent via the `_MCC_STDINT_H` include guard.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (double-inclusion `-Wall` clean)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18p4/p5 [¬ß7.20p4/p5] ‚Äî Each macro name corresponding to a type, and each limit macro, shall expand to a constant expression suitable for use in `#if` preprocessing directives. (mcc: `INTn_MIN/MAX`, `UINTn_MAX`, and the `*_C` results are all integer constant expressions usable in `#if`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (battery of `#if` tests over INT32_MAX/UINT64_MAX/INTMAX_C/PTRDIFF_MAX/SIZE_MAX/WCHAR_MAX/WINT_MAX/SIG_ATOMIC_MAX/INTPTR_MAX all pass)

#### ¬ß7.18.1 [¬ß7.20.1] Integer types

##### ¬ß7.18.1.1 [¬ß7.20.1.1] Exact-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.1p1 [¬ß7.20.1.1p1] ‚Äî `intN_t` shall designate a signed integer type with width exactly `N`, no padding bits, and a two's complement representation (e.g. `int8_t` is exactly 8 bits). (mcc: `int8_t`=`signed char`, `int16_t`=`short`, `int32_t`=`int`, `int64_t`=`__INT64_TYPE__`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof` of int8/16/32/64_t = 1/2/4/8 confirmed)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.1p1 [¬ß7.20.1.1p1] ‚Äî `uintN_t` shall designate an unsigned integer type with width exactly `N` and no padding bits. (mcc: `uint8_t`=`unsigned char`, `uint16_t`=`unsigned short`, `uint32_t`=`unsigned int`, `uint64_t`=`unsigned __INT64_TYPE__`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.1p2/p3 [¬ß7.20.1.1p2/p3] ‚Äî These typedef names are optional; however, if the implementation provides integer types with widths of 8, 16, 32, or 64 bits, no padding bits, and (for the signed types) a two's complement representation, it shall define the corresponding `intN_t`/`uintN_t`. (mcc: defines the full 8/16/32/64 exact-width set.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.18.1.2 [¬ß7.20.1.2] Minimum-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.2p1 [¬ß7.20.1.2p1] ‚Äî `int_leastN_t` shall designate a signed integer type with width at least `N` such that no signed integer type with lesser size has at least the specified width; `uint_leastN_t` shall designate the analogous smallest unsigned type (e.g. `int_least8_t`, `uint_least16_t`). (mcc: each `int_leastN_t`/`uint_leastN_t` aliases the corresponding exact-width type.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.2p2 [¬ß7.20.1.2p2] ‚Äî The required types are `int_least8_t`, `int_least16_t`, `int_least32_t`, `int_least64_t`, `uint_least8_t`, `uint_least16_t`, `uint_least32_t`, `uint_least64_t`. (mcc: all eight present.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.18.1.2p3 [¬ß7.20.1.2p3] ‚Äî All other types of this form are optional. (mcc: defines no others.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.18.1.3 [¬ß7.20.1.3] Fastest minimum-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.3p1 [¬ß7.20.1.3p1] ‚Äî `int_fastN_t` shall designate the fastest signed integer type with width at least `N`; `uint_fastN_t` the fastest unsigned integer type with width at least `N`. (mcc: each `int_fastN_t`/`uint_fastN_t` aliases the corresponding exact-width type.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.18.1.3p2 [¬ß7.20.1.3p2] ‚Äî "Fastest" means usually fastest to operate with among types having at least the specified width; if no clear winner, any qualifying type may be chosen. (Implementation-defined; mcc chooses the exact-width type.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.3p3 [¬ß7.20.1.3p3] ‚Äî The required types are `int_fast8_t`, `int_fast16_t`, `int_fast32_t`, `int_fast64_t`, `uint_fast8_t`, `uint_fast16_t`, `uint_fast32_t`, `uint_fast64_t`. (mcc: all eight present.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.18.1.3p4 [¬ß7.20.1.3p4] ‚Äî All other types of this form are optional. (mcc: defines no others.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.18.1.4 [¬ß7.20.1.4] Integer types capable of holding object pointers

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.4p1 [¬ß7.20.1.4p1] ‚Äî `intptr_t` (optional) shall designate a signed integer type such that any valid `void*` can be converted to it and back, comparing equal to the original. (mcc: `typedef __INTPTR_TYPE__ intptr_t;`; provided on all targets.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.4p1 [¬ß7.20.1.4p1] ‚Äî `uintptr_t` (optional) shall designate an unsigned integer type with the same `void*` round-trip property. (mcc: `typedef __UINTPTR_TYPE__ uintptr_t;`; provided on all targets.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.18.1.5 [¬ß7.20.1.5] Greatest-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.5p1 [¬ß7.20.1.5p1] ‚Äî `intmax_t` (required) shall designate a signed integer type capable of representing any value of any signed integer type. (mcc: `typedef long long intmax_t;`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.5p1 [¬ß7.20.1.5p1] ‚Äî `uintmax_t` (required) shall designate an unsigned integer type capable of representing any value of any unsigned integer type. (mcc: `typedef unsigned long long uintmax_t;`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.18.2 [¬ß7.20.2] Limits of specified-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2p1 [¬ß7.20.2p1] ‚Äî Each of the following object-like macros specifying a min/max limit of a `<stdint.h>` type shall expand to a constant expression usable in `#if`, having the same type as an object of the corresponding type converted per the integer promotions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2p1 [¬ß7.20.2p1] ‚Äî Each implementation-defined value shall be equal to or greater in magnitude than the corresponding value listed, with the same sign, except where the limit is stated to be exactly the given value (exact-width limits). (mcc: exact-width limits match exactly.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.18.2.1 [¬ß7.20.2.1] Limits of exact-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.1p1 [¬ß7.20.2.1p1] ‚Äî `INTN_MIN` shall equal exactly ‚àí(2^(N‚àí1)): `INT8_MIN`=‚àí128, `INT16_MIN`=‚àí32768, `INT32_MIN`=‚àí2147483648, `INT64_MIN`=‚àí9223372036854775808. (mcc: `INT8_MIN (-128)`, `INT16_MIN (-32768)`, `INT32_MIN (-2147483647 - 1)`, `INT64_MIN (-__LONG_LONG_MAX__ - 1)`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.1p1 [¬ß7.20.2.1p1] ‚Äî `INTN_MAX` shall equal exactly 2^(N‚àí1)‚àí1: `INT8_MAX`=127, `INT16_MAX`=32767, `INT32_MAX`=2147483647, `INT64_MAX`=9223372036854775807. (mcc: `INT8_MAX 127`, `INT16_MAX 32767`, `INT32_MAX 2147483647`, `INT64_MAX __LONG_LONG_MAX__`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.1p1 [¬ß7.20.2.1p1] ‚Äî `UINTN_MAX` shall equal exactly 2^N‚àí1: `UINT8_MAX`=255, `UINT16_MAX`=65535, `UINT32_MAX`=4294967295, `UINT64_MAX`=18446744073709551615. (mcc: `UINT8_MAX 255`, `UINT16_MAX 65535`, `UINT32_MAX 4294967295U`, `UINT64_MAX (__LONG_LONG_MAX__ * 2ULL + 1ULL)`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Static_assert` on every value passes)

##### ¬ß7.18.2.2 [¬ß7.20.2.2] Limits of minimum-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.2p1 [¬ß7.20.2.2p1] ‚Äî `INT_LEASTN_MIN` ‚â§ {‚àí127, ‚àí32767, ‚àí2147483647, ‚àí9223372036854775807}; `INT_LEASTN_MAX` ‚â• {127, 32767, 2147483647, 9223372036854775807}; `UINT_LEASTN_MAX` ‚â• {255, 65535, 4294967295, 18446744073709551615} for N = 8/16/32/64. (mcc: each `INT_LEASTN_MIN/MAX` and `UINT_LEASTN_MAX` is `#define`d to the exact-width limit, satisfying the bounds.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.18.2.3 [¬ß7.20.2.3] Limits of fastest minimum-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.3p1 [¬ß7.20.2.3p1] ‚Äî `INT_FASTN_MIN` ‚â§ {‚àí127, ‚àí32767, ‚àí2147483647, ‚àí9223372036854775807}; `INT_FASTN_MAX` ‚â• {127, 32767, 2147483647, 9223372036854775807}; `UINT_FASTN_MAX` ‚â• {255, 65535, 4294967295, 18446744073709551615} for N = 8/16/32/64. (mcc: each `INT_FASTN_MIN/MAX` and `UINT_FASTN_MAX` is `#define`d to the exact-width limit.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.18.2.4 [¬ß7.20.2.4] Limits of integer types capable of holding object pointers

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.4p1 [¬ß7.20.2.4p1] ‚Äî If `intptr_t` is defined, `INTPTR_MIN` ‚â§ ‚àí32767 and `INTPTR_MAX` ‚â• 32767. (mcc: keyed on `__SIZEOF_POINTER__` ‚Äî `INT64_MIN`/`INT64_MAX` when pointer is 8 bytes, else `INT32_MIN`/`INT32_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.4p1 [¬ß7.20.2.4p1] ‚Äî If `uintptr_t` is defined, `UINTPTR_MAX` ‚â• 65535. (mcc: `UINT64_MAX` when pointer is 8 bytes, else `UINT32_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.18.2.5 [¬ß7.20.2.5] Limits of greatest-width integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.5p1 [¬ß7.20.2.5p1] ‚Äî `INTMAX_MIN` ‚â§ ‚àí9223372036854775807 and `INTMAX_MAX` ‚â• 9223372036854775807. (mcc: `INTMAX_MIN INT64_MIN`, `INTMAX_MAX INT64_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.2.5p1 [¬ß7.20.2.5p1] ‚Äî `UINTMAX_MAX` ‚â• 18446744073709551615. (mcc: `UINTMAX_MAX UINT64_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.18.3 [¬ß7.20.3] Limits of other integer types

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.3p1 [¬ß7.20.3p1] ‚Äî Each of the following object-like macros, specifying a min/max limit of an integer type defined in another standard header, shall expand to a constant expression usable in `#if`, has the same type as the corresponding type promoted per the integer promotions, and its value is equal to or greater in magnitude than the value shown, with the same sign. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.3p2 [¬ß7.20.3p2] ‚Äî Limits of `ptrdiff_t`: `PTRDIFF_MIN` ‚â§ ‚àí65535 and `PTRDIFF_MAX` ‚â• 65535. (mcc: `PTRDIFF_MIN INTPTR_MIN`, `PTRDIFF_MAX INTPTR_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime print: `PTRDIFF_MAX=9223372036854775807`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.3p3 [¬ß7.20.3p3] ‚Äî Limits of `sig_atomic_t` (`SIG_ATOMIC_MIN`/`SIG_ATOMIC_MAX`): if signed, `SIG_ATOMIC_MIN` ‚â§ ‚àí127 and `SIG_ATOMIC_MAX` ‚â• 127; if unsigned, `SIG_ATOMIC_MIN`=0 and `SIG_ATOMIC_MAX` ‚â• 255. (mcc: treats `sig_atomic_t` as signed ‚Äî `SIG_ATOMIC_MIN INT32_MIN`, `SIG_ATOMIC_MAX INT32_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: MIN=‚àí2147483648, MAX=2147483647)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.3p4 [¬ß7.20.3p4] ‚Äî Limit of `size_t`: `SIZE_MAX` ‚â• 65535. (mcc: `SIZE_MAX UINTPTR_MAX`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime print: `SIZE_MAX=18446744073709551615`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.3p5 [¬ß7.20.3p5] ‚Äî Limits of `wchar_t` (`WCHAR_MIN`/`WCHAR_MAX`): if signed, `WCHAR_MIN` ‚â§ ‚àí127 and `WCHAR_MAX` ‚â• 127; if unsigned, `WCHAR_MIN`=0 and `WCHAR_MAX` ‚â• 255. (mcc: `WCHAR_MIN INT32_MIN`, `WCHAR_MAX INT32_MAX`, each `#ifndef`-guarded against a prior system/SDK definition.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: MIN=‚àí2147483648, MAX=2147483647 on this target)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.3p6 [¬ß7.20.3p6] ‚Äî Limits of `wint_t` (`WINT_MIN`/`WINT_MAX`): if signed, `WINT_MIN` ‚â§ ‚àí32767 and `WINT_MAX` ‚â• 32767; if unsigned, `WINT_MIN`=0 and `WINT_MAX` ‚â• 65535. (mcc: treats `wint_t` as unsigned ‚Äî `WINT_MIN 0`, `WINT_MAX UINT32_MAX`, each `#ifndef`-guarded.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: WINT_MIN=0, WINT_MAX=4294967295)

#### ¬ß7.18.4 [¬ß7.20.4] Macros for integer constants

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.4p1 [¬ß7.20.4p1] ‚Äî The following function-like macros expand to integer constants suitable for initializing objects of integer types corresponding to types defined in `<stdint.h>`; each macro name corresponds to a similarly named type in ¬ß7.18.1.2/¬ß7.18.1.5. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.18.4p2 [¬ß7.20.4p2] ‚Äî The argument shall be an unsuffixed integer constant (per ¬ß6.4.4.1) whose value does not exceed the limits of the corresponding type. (Constraint on the program.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.4p3 [¬ß7.20.4p3] ‚Äî Each invocation shall expand to an integer constant expression suitable for use in `#if`, whose value and type are obtained by suffixing/casting the unsuffixed argument to the corresponding type. (mcc/gcc/clang: OK.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`#if INTMAX_C(5)!=5` passes)

##### ¬ß7.18.4.1 [¬ß7.20.4.1] Macros for minimum-width integer constants

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.4.1p1 [¬ß7.20.4.1p1] ‚Äî `INTN_C(value)` shall expand to an integer constant expression with type `int_leastN_t`, and `UINTN_C(value)` with type `uint_leastN_t` (e.g. if `uint_least64_t` is `unsigned long long int`, `UINT64_C(0x123)` may expand to `0x123ULL`). (mcc: `INT8_C/INT16_C/INT32_C(x)` and `UINT8_C/UINT16_C(x)` are identity; `UINT32_C(x)` is `x ## U`; `INT64_C`/`UINT64_C` pick `L`/`UL` when `__SIZEOF_LONG__==8` else `LL`/`ULL`, so the result has type `int_least64_t`/`uint_least64_t` exactly even on LP64.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Static_assert(sizeof(INT64_C(1))==sizeof(int_least64_t))` and the `UINT64_C`/`UINT32_C` analogues pass on both hosted and freestanding LP64 paths)

##### ¬ß7.18.4.2 [¬ß7.20.4.2] Macros for greatest-width integer constants

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.4.2p1 [¬ß7.20.4.2p1] ‚Äî `INTMAX_C(value)` shall expand to an integer constant expression with type `intmax_t`, and `UINTMAX_C(value)` with type `uintmax_t`. (mcc: `INTMAX_C(x)` is `x ## LL`, `UINTMAX_C(x)` is `x ## ULL`, matching `intmax_t`/`uintmax_t` = `long long`/`unsigned long long`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Static_assert(sizeof(INTMAX_C(1))==sizeof(intmax_t))` and the unsigned analogue pass)

#### Additional `<stdint.h>` items (gaps the draft omitted)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18.1.1 [¬ß7.20.1.1] (optional) ‚Äî `RSIZE_MAX` and the bounds-checking interfaces of Annex K are NOT mandated by the base standard and are only present when an implementation provides Annex K; absence is conforming. (mcc: `RSIZE_MAX` undefined.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì(absent) gcc:‚úì(absent) clang:‚úì(absent) ‚Äî none of the three define `RSIZE_MAX` by default
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.1/¬ß7.18 [¬ß7.20] ‚Äî On a hosted target mcc obtains all `<stdint.h>` types and macros by `#include_next` over the system `<stdint.h>` (here glibc); the back-fill block under `#ifndef INT8_MAX` is skipped, so glibc's exact typedefs and `*_C` definitions are used. (mcc-specific layering.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì (hosted values match gcc==clang exactly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.18 [¬ß7.20] ‚Äî On `-ffreestanding -nostdinc` (no reachable system header) mcc self-defines the entire C11 `<stdint.h>` content; all types, limit macros, and `*_C` type-correctness hold on this path too. (mcc-specific.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (freestanding probe with INT64 limits, `INT64_C` type check, and `offsetof` all pass)

### Cross-cutting: freestanding & namespace

- [‚úì] ¬ß4p6 / ¬ß6.10.8 ‚Äî `<stddef.h>` and `<stdint.h>` (along with `<float.h>`, `<limits.h>`, `<iso646.h>`, (C11) `<stdalign.h>`, `<stdarg.h>`, `<stdbool.h>`, `<stdnoreturn.h>`) shall be available in a freestanding environment. (mcc: both headers are self-contained on `-ffreestanding -nostdinc -I runtime/include`; `<stddef.h>` always self-defines and `<stdint.h>` back-fills the full C11 contents when no system header is reachable.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (compiled and ran under `-ffreestanding`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.3 ‚Äî All identifiers defined in these headers (the typedefs, the limit/`*_C` macros, `NULL`, `offsetof`) are reserved, and the `__`-prefixed helpers used to implement them are in the implementation's reserved namespace. (mcc: implements the typedefs via reserved predefined macros `__SIZE_TYPE__`/`__PTRDIFF_TYPE__`/`__WCHAR_TYPE__`/`__WINT_TYPE__`/`__INT64_TYPE__`/`__INTPTR_TYPE__`/`__UINTPTR_TYPE__` and the include guards `_STDDEF_H`/`_MCC_STDINT_H`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.20p2 [¬ß7.8] (informative) ‚Äî `<stdint.h>` integer types/macros must remain consistent with `<inttypes.h>`, which itself includes `<stdint.h>` and adds the `PRI*`/`SCN*` format-specifier macros; the limit and `*_C` macros defined here are the ones `<inttypes.h>` relies upon. (mcc: `<inttypes.h>` is layered atop this header.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)


## ¬ß7.21 <stdio.h>

> mcc status: 280 TODO checkboxes below; 1 mcc-gap. mcc ships **no** `<stdio.h>` of its own ‚Äî it consumes the platform (glibc) header and links the platform libc, exactly as gcc and clang do here, so every macro/type/function/runtime-conversion requirement is satisfied identically across all three (verified: BUFSIZ=8192, FOPEN_MAX=16, TMP_MAX=238328, EOF=-1, all conversions, file ops, and the whole `v*` family produce byte-identical results). mcc now performs `-Wformat` checking of `printf`/`scanf` conversion-specifier vs argument types, matching gcc/clang. The remaining mcc-specific gap is **diagnostic only**: mcc silently accepts a call to an **undeclared** stdio function (e.g. the C11-removed `gets`) as an implicit declaration, where gcc/clang error ‚Äî not a conformance violation (implicit-decl is a constraint mcc declines to diagnose), but a divergence from the gcc==clang consensus.

> Numbering follows C11 (N1570); the corresponding C99 (N1256) clause is ¬ß7.19 with identical paragraph structure unless a line is tagged otherwise. `mcc` ships no `<stdio.h>` of its own ‚Äî it consumes the platform libc header ‚Äî so every requirement below is "does the compiler+headers+runtime triple accept/implement it", checked against the system libc that mcc, gcc, and clang each use.
> C11 vs C99 material deltas in this clause: C11 added the `"x"` (exclusive-create) `fopen`/`freopen` mode forms; C11 **removed** the `gets` function (¬ß7.21.7.7 in C99 only); C99 (relative to C90) had earlier added `snprintf`, the `v*scanf`/`vsnprintf` family, the `hh`/`ll`/`j`/`z`/`t` length modifiers, the `a`/`A`/`F` conversions, and the inf/nan output styles.

### ¬ß7.21.1 Introduction

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p1 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall declare three types, several macros, and many functions for performing input and output. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p2 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define the type `size_t` (the unsigned integer type of the result of `sizeof`, as in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p2 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define the type `FILE`, an object type capable of recording all the information needed to control a stream: its file position indicator, a pointer to its associated buffer (if any), an error indicator that records whether a read/write error has occurred, and an end-of-file indicator that records whether end-of-file has been reached. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p2 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define the type `fpos_t`, an object type other than an array type capable of recording all the information needed to specify uniquely every position within a file. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared `fpos_t p;` compiles and `fgetpos`/`fsetpos` accept it on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `NULL` (the null-pointer-constant macro, as in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `_IOFBF`, `_IOLBF`, and `_IONBF`, each expanding to an integer constant expression with distinct value, suitable for use as the third argument to `setvbuf`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (constraint `_IOFBF!=_IOLBF!=_IONBF` checked in a constant-expression array bound)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `BUFSIZ`, an integer constant expression that is the size of the buffer used by the `setbuf` function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (BUFSIZ=8192)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `EOF`, which expands to an integer constant expression, with type `int` and a negative value, that is returned by several functions to indicate end-of-file. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (EOF=-1, `EOF<0` in ICE)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `FOPEN_MAX`, an integer constant expression that is the minimum number of files that can be open simultaneously. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (FOPEN_MAX=16)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `FILENAME_MAX`, an integer constant expression that is the size needed for an array of `char` large enough to hold the longest file name string that the implementation guarantees can be opened. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (FILENAME_MAX=4096)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `L_tmpnam`, an integer constant expression that is the size needed for an array of `char` large enough to hold a temporary file name string generated by the `tmpnam` function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (L_tmpnam=20)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `SEEK_CUR`, `SEEK_END`, and `SEEK_SET`, each expanding to an integer constant expression with distinct value, suitable for use as the third argument to `fseek`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (distinctness checked in ICE)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `TMP_MAX`, an integer constant expression that is the minimum number of unique file names that can be generated by the `tmpnam` function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (TMP_MAX=238328)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p3 ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` shall define `stderr`, `stdin`, and `stdout`, each an expression of type "pointer to `FILE`" that points to the `FILE` object associated, respectively, with the standard error, input, and output streams. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three usable as `FILE*`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.1p4 ‚Äî `FOPEN_MAX` shall be at least 8, including the three standard text streams. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (16 ‚â• 8, checked in ICE)

### ¬ß7.21.2 Streams

- ¬ß7.21.2p1 ‚Äî Input and output shall be mapped into logical data streams (text and binary) whose properties are more uniform than their various inputs and outputs. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî shared runtime model)
- ¬ß7.21.2p2 ‚Äî A text stream shall be an ordered sequence of characters composed into lines, each terminated by a new-line; whether the last line requires a terminating new-line is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî shared runtime)
- ¬ß7.21.2p2 ‚Äî Characters may be added/altered/deleted on input/output to conform to host text conventions; no one-to-one correspondence is required. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî shared runtime)
- ¬ß7.21.2p2 ‚Äî Text data read in shall compare equal to data written only if it is printing chars + HT/NL, no NL is preceded by spaces, and the last char is a new-line. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî shared runtime)
- ¬ß7.21.2p2 ‚Äî Whether trailing space characters before a new-line appear when read back is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî shared runtime)
- ¬ß7.21.2p3 ‚Äî A binary stream shall transparently record internal data; data read back shall compare equal (under the same implementation), except an implementation may append null characters to fill a medium. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable ‚Äî shared runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.2p4 ‚Äî Environmental limits: support text files with lines of at least 254 characters (incl. NL); `BUFSIZ` ‚â• 256. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (BUFSIZ=8192 ‚â• 256, checked in ICE)
- ¬ß7.21.2p5 ‚Äî The characteristics of the stream interfaces and file environment are as described in the stream model. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.21.3 Files

- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p1 ‚Äî A stream shall be associated with an external file by opening it (possibly creating it); creating an existing file discards its former contents if necessary. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p1 ‚Äî For positionable files, the file position indicator starts at character zero unless opened in append mode, where its initial position is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p1 ‚Äî The file position indicator shall be maintained by reads/writes/positioning; all input is as if by `fgetc`, all output as if by `fputc`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p2 ‚Äî Binary files are not truncated except per ¬ß7.21.5.3; whether a write on a text stream truncates beyond that point is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.3p3 ‚Äî Unbuffered streams transmit chars as soon as possible; fully buffered accumulate into a block; line buffered transmit a block on new-line. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`setvbuf`/`setbuf` with `_IOFBF`/`_IOLBF`/`_IONBF` accepted and effective)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p3 ‚Äî Chars are transmitted as a block when a buffer fills, on unbuffered input, or on line-buffered input requiring host transmission; affected by `setbuf`/`setvbuf`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p4 ‚Äî Closing disassociates a file; output streams are flushed before disassociation; a `FILE*` value is indeterminate after the file is closed. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.3p4 ‚Äî Whether a special file is actually created is unspecified; a file may have other implementation-defined restrictions. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.21.3p5 ‚Äî Whether a zero-length file on which nothing was written actually exists is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p6 ‚Äî The file may be reopened and its contents reclaimed/modified if it can be repositioned at its start. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p6 ‚Äî On return from `main` or call to `exit`, all open files are closed (all output flushed); abnormal paths such as `abort` need not close files properly. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p7 ‚Äî The address of the controlling `FILE` object may be significant; a copy of a `FILE` need not serve in place of the original. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.3p8 ‚Äî At startup three text streams are predefined: standard input, standard output, standard error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`stdin`/`stdout`/`stderr` usable without `fopen`)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.3p8 ‚Äî As initially opened, stderr is not fully buffered; stdin/stdout are fully buffered iff the stream can be determined not to refer to an interactive device. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.3p9 ‚Äî Opening nontemporary files requires a file-name string; valid-name rules are implementation-defined, as is whether the same file may be open multiple times. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.21.3p10 ‚Äî The library does not directly support wide-oriented text/binary streams; orientation is in ¬ß7.29.3. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.3p11 ‚Äî Environmental limit: `FOPEN_MAX` shall be at least 8, including the three standard text streams. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (16 ‚â• 8)

### ¬ß7.21.4 Operations on files

#### ¬ß7.21.4.1 The remove function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int remove(const char *filename);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in x-mode probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.1p2 ‚Äî `remove` shall make the named file no longer accessible by that name; a later open by that name fails unless re-created. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.4.1p2 ‚Äî If the file is open, the behavior of `remove` is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: zero on success, nonzero on failure. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.4.2 The rename function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int rename(const char *old, const char *new);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.2p2 ‚Äî `rename` shall make `old` henceforth known by `new`; `old` is no longer accessible. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.4.2p2 ‚Äî If a file named `new` exists prior to the call, the behavior is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: zero on success, nonzero on failure (in which case, if the file existed, it keeps its original name). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.4.3 The tmpfile function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `FILE *tmpfile(void);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.3p2 ‚Äî `tmpfile` shall create a unique temporary binary file auto-removed on close/termination, opened with `"wb+"` mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe wrote/seeked/read a tmpfile successfully on all three)
- ¬ß7.21.4.3p3 ‚Äî Recommended practice: at least `TMP_MAX` temporary files openable over the program lifetime (shareable with `tmpnam`); no simultaneous-open limit beyond `FOPEN_MAX`. (C99 note.) ‚Äî (spec; recommended practice; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.3p4 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the created stream, or a null pointer if it cannot be created. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe got non-null)

#### ¬ß7.21.4.4 The tmpnam function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *tmpnam(char *s);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.4p2 ‚Äî `tmpnam` shall generate a valid file name not the same as an existing file; capable of up to `TMP_MAX` distinct strings. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.4.4p3 ‚Äî `tmpnam` shall generate a different string each call; may modify the same static object each time. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.4p4 ‚Äî If `s` is null, the result is left in an internal static object and a pointer to it is returned; otherwise `s` (‚â• `L_tmpnam` chars) receives the result and `s` is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.4p4 ‚Äî Returns: null pointer if no suitable string can be generated; otherwise the internal-object pointer (null arg) or `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.4.4p5 ‚Äî Environmental limit: `TMP_MAX` shall be at least 25. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (238328 ‚â• 25, checked in ICE)

### ¬ß7.21.5 File access functions

#### ¬ß7.21.5.1 The fclose function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fclose(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.1p2 ‚Äî A successful `fclose` shall flush the stream and close the file; unwritten buffered data is delivered, unread buffered data discarded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.1p2 ‚Äî Whether or not the call succeeds, the stream is disassociated and any `setbuf`/`setvbuf` buffer is disassociated (and deallocated if auto-allocated). ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: zero on success, `EOF` if any errors were detected. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.5.2 The fflush function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fflush(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.2p2 ‚Äî For an output/most-recent-not-input update stream, `fflush` delivers unwritten data; otherwise behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.2p3 ‚Äî If `stream` is null, `fflush` flushes all streams for which the behavior is defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.2p4 ‚Äî Returns: sets the error indicator and returns `EOF` on write error, otherwise zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.5.3 The fopen function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `FILE *fopen(const char * restrict filename, const char * restrict mode);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared with `restrict`, accepted & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.3p2 ‚Äî `fopen` shall open the named file and associate a stream with it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe opened a file)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.3p3 ‚Äî The `mode` string shall accept `"r"`,`"w"`,`"a"`,`"rb"`,`"wb"`,`"ab"`,`"r+"`,`"w+"`,`"a+"` and the binary-update forms `"r+b"`/`"rb+"`,`"w+b"`/`"wb+"`,`"a+b"`/`"ab+"`; otherwise undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) The mode string may take exclusive forms `"wx"`,`"wbx"`,`"w+x"`,`"w+bx"`,`"wb+x"`: exclusive create fails if the file already exists. (C99-only: `x` forms do not exist.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe: second `fopen("...","wx")` returned null = failed-exclusive on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.3p4 ‚Äî Opening with `r` first character shall fail if the file does not exist or cannot be read. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.3p5 ‚Äî Opening with `a` first character forces all writes to the then-current end of file regardless of `fseek`; a binary append may initially position beyond last data due to null padding. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.3p6 ‚Äî In update mode (`+`), both input and output may be performed, but output‚Üíinput requires an intervening `fflush`/positioning, and input‚Üíoutput requires intervening positioning unless input hit EOF. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.5.3p6 ‚Äî Opening a text file with update mode may instead open a binary stream in some implementations. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.3p7 ‚Äî When opened, a stream is fully buffered iff it can be determined not to refer to an interactive device; the error and EOF indicators are cleared. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.3p8 ‚Äî Returns: a pointer to the controlling object, or a null pointer if the open fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.5.4 The freopen function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `FILE *freopen(const char * restrict filename, const char * restrict mode, FILE * restrict stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.4p2 ‚Äî `freopen` shall open the named file and associate `stream` with it; `mode` is used as in `fopen` (incl. C11 `x` forms). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.5.4p2 ‚Äî If `filename` is null, `freopen` attempts to change the stream's mode to `mode`; which mode changes are permitted is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.4p3 ‚Äî `freopen` shall first attempt to close any associated file (failure ignored); the error and EOF indicators are cleared. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.4p4 ‚Äî Returns: null pointer if the open fails, otherwise the value of `stream`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.5.5 The setbuf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void setbuf(FILE * restrict stream, char * restrict buf);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; `setbuf(stderr,NULL)` in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.5p2 ‚Äî `setbuf` shall be equivalent to `setvbuf` with `_IOFBF`/`BUFSIZ`, or (if `buf` is null) with `_IONBF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (void return)

#### ¬ß7.21.5.6 The setvbuf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int setvbuf(FILE * restrict stream, char * restrict buf, int mode, size_t size);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.6p2 ‚Äî `setvbuf` may be used only after association with an open file and before any other operation (other than an unsuccessful `setvbuf`). ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.6p2 ‚Äî `mode` `_IOFBF`/`_IOLBF`/`_IONBF` selects fully/line/unbuffered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; line-buffering effective in probe)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.5.6p2 ‚Äî If `buf` is non-null, the array it points to may be used as the buffer; `size` specifies its size; the array contents are indeterminate at any time. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.5.6p3 ‚Äî Returns: zero on success, nonzero on invalid `mode` or unhonorable request. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

### ¬ß7.21.6 Formatted input/output functions

> mcc `-Wformat` (diagnostic): mcc emits a `-Wformat` warning for a conversion-specifier/argument type mismatch (e.g. `printf("%d","str")` ‚Üí "format '%d' expects an integer argument"), matching gcc (`format '%d' expects ... 'int' but argument has type 'char *'`) and clang. The runtime behavior (UB per p9) is identical because all three call the same glibc `printf`. See the items under ¬ß7.21.6.1 and ¬ß7.21.6.2.

#### ¬ß7.21.6.1 The fprintf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fprintf(FILE * restrict stream, const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p2 ‚Äî `fprintf` shall write output to `stream` under control of `format`, converting subsequent arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.6.1p2 ‚Äî Insufficient arguments ‚Üí undefined; excess arguments are evaluated but ignored; `fprintf` returns at end of format. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p3 ‚Äî The format is a multibyte sequence of ordinary characters (copied) and conversion specifications. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p4 ‚Äî Each conversion spec is `%` then, in sequence: flags, optional minimum field width, optional precision, optional length modifier, conversion specifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p5 ‚Äî Field width/precision may be `*` (taken from an `int` arg, appearing before the value); negative width = `-` flag + positive width; negative precision = omitted precision. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%*d`/`%.*f` produced identical output)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p6 ‚Äî Flag `-`: left-justify within the field. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%-5d` ‚Üí `42   `)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p6 ‚Äî Flag `+`: signed conversion always begins with a sign. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%+d` ‚Üí `+3`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p6 ‚Äî Flag space: prefix a space if no sign would appear; ignored if `+` also present. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`% d` ‚Üí ` 3`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p6 ‚Äî Flag `#`: alternative form (force `o` leading 0; `0x`/`0X` prefix on nonzero `x`/`X`; always a decimal point for `a/A/e/E/f/F/g/G`; keep trailing zeros for `g/G`); else undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%#x` ‚Üí `0xff`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p6 ‚Äî Flag `0`: zero-pad to field width for numeric conversions (except inf/NaN); ignored with `-`; for `d/i/o/u/x/X` ignored when a precision is given; else undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%05d` ‚Üí `00042`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `hh`: `d/i/o/u/x/X` apply to `signed/unsigned char`; `n` to pointer-to-`signed char`. (C99 added `hh`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%hhd` ‚Üí `-3`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `h`: applies to `short`/`unsigned short`; `n` to pointer-to-`short`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%hd` ‚Üí `-4`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `l` (ell): applies to `long`/`unsigned long`; `n` to pointer-to-`long`; `c`‚Üí`wint_t`; `s`‚Üípointer-to-`wchar_t`; no effect on `a/A/e/E/f/F/g/G`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%ld` ‚Üí `6`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `ll`: applies to `long long`/`unsigned long long`; `n` to pointer-to-`long long`. (C99 added `ll`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%lld` ‚Üí `7`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `j`: applies to `intmax_t`/`uintmax_t`; `n` to pointer-to-`intmax_t`. (C99 added `j`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%ju` ‚Üí `8`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `z`: applies to `size_t`/its signed counterpart; `n` to pointer thereto. (C99 added `z`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%zu` ‚Üí `9`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `t`: applies to `ptrdiff_t`/its unsigned counterpart; `n` to pointer thereto. (C99 added `t`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%td` ‚Üí `10`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî Length modifier `L`: applies to `long double` for `a/A/e/E/f/F/g/G`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.6.1p7 ‚Äî A length modifier with any other conversion specifier is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `d`,`i`: signed decimal `[-]dddd`; precision = min digits; default 1; zero value with precision 0 ‚Üí no characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `o`,`u`,`x`,`X`: unsigned octal/decimal/hex; `abcdef` for `x`, `ABCDEF` for `X`; precision = min digits; default 1; zero/precision-0 ‚Üí no characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `f`,`F`: decimal `[-]ddd.ddd`; precision digits after point (default 6); no point if precision 0 and no `#`; rounded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `f`,`F` (non-finite): infinity ‚Üí `[-]inf`/`[-]infinity`; NaN ‚Üí `[-]nan`/`[-]nan(...)`; `F` yields `INF`/`INFINITY`/`NAN`; `#`/`0` have no effect. (C99 added `F` and inf/nan styles.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%f`‚Üí`inf`, `%F`‚Üí`-INF`, `%e`‚Üí`-nan` at runtime identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `e`,`E`: `[-]d.ddde¬±dd`; precision digits after point (default 6); exponent ‚â• 2 digits; `E` uppercase; inf/NaN as `f`/`F`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `g`,`G`: style `f`/`e` (or `F`/`E`) with precision = significant digits (0‚Üí1); `e` used iff exponent < ‚àí4 or ‚â• precision; trailing zeros removed unless `#`; inf/NaN as `f`/`F`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%g` of 123456 ‚Üí `123456`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `a`,`A`: `[-]0xh.hhhhp¬±d`; precision controls hex digits; `abcdef`/`ABCDEF`; `A` uses `X`/`P`. (C99 added `a`/`A`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%a`‚Üí`0x1.8p+0`, `%A`‚Üí`0X1.8P+0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `a`,`A` (rounding): exact if representable in the precision, otherwise correctly rounded per the current rounding direction. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `c`: without `l`, `int` arg ‚Üí `unsigned char` written; with `l`, `wint_t` as if `ls`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `s` (no `l`): pointer to a char array, written up to (not incl.) the null; precision limits bytes; without precision the array must contain a null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%.3s` of "hello" ‚Üí `hel`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `s` (with `l`): pointer to `wchar_t` array converted as if `wcrtomb`; written up to (not incl.) the null; precision limits bytes; no partial multibyte char written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `p`: pointer to `void` converted to printing characters in an implementation-defined manner. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `n`: pointer to a signed integer receiving the count written so far; no argument converted (one consumed); flags/width/precision ‚Üí undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p8 ‚Äî `%`: a `%` is written; complete spec is `%%`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.6.1p9 ‚Äî An invalid conversion spec, or an argument of the wrong type, is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p10 ‚Äî A nonexistent/small field width never truncates; the field expands to contain the result. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`%*d` width 4 with "7" still prints `   7`)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.6.1p11 ‚Äî Recommended practice: for `a`/`A` with `FLT_RADIX` a power of 2, correctly round to a hex float of the given precision. ‚Äî (spec; recommended practice; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.6.1p12 ‚Äî Recommended practice: for `e/E/f/F/g/G`, correct rounding within `DECIMAL_DIG` bounds. (C99.) ‚Äî (spec; recommended practice; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p13 ‚Äî The result is rounded per the current rounding direction; the precision indicates the rounding precision. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p14 ‚Äî Returns: number of characters transmitted, or a negative value on output/encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.1p15 ‚Äî Environmental limit: at least 4095 characters producible by a single conversion. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] **GAP** ¬ß7.21.6.1p4/p7/p9 ‚Äî A compiler *may* (and gcc/clang do under `-Wall`/`-Wformat`) diagnose `printf`/`fprintf` conversion-specifier vs argument-type mismatches and invalid length-modifier/specifier pairings. mcc emits such warnings too (verified: `printf("%d\n","x")` warns "format '%d' expects an integer argument" under mcc, as under gcc and clang). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc checks `printf` formats like gcc/clang ‚Äî diagnostic-only, not a conformance defect)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.2 The fscanf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fscanf(FILE * restrict stream, const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p2 ‚Äî `fscanf` shall read input under control of `format`, using subsequent arguments as pointers to receiving objects. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.6.2p2 ‚Äî Insufficient arguments ‚Üí undefined; excess arguments evaluated but ignored. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p3 ‚Äî The format is a multibyte sequence of white-space directives, ordinary characters, and conversion specifications. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p4 ‚Äî Each conversion spec is `%` then: optional `*`, optional max field width (> 0), optional length modifier, conversion specifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p5 ‚Äî Directives are executed in turn; on completion or a directive failure the function returns; failures are input failures or matching failures. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p6 ‚Äî A white-space directive reads up to the first non-white-space char (left unread) or until no more chars; it never fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p7 ‚Äî An ordinary-character directive reads matching characters; a mismatch (or EOF/encoding/read error) fails the directive, leaving differing/subsequent chars unread. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.6.2p8 ‚Äî A conversion specification defines a set of matching input sequences and is executed in the following steps. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p9 ‚Äî Input white-space is skipped unless the specifier is `[`, `c`, or `n`; skipped white-space is not counted against the field width. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p10 ‚Äî An input item (longest matching prefix within the field width) is read; zero length ‚Üí matching failure (or input failure on EOF/encoding/read error). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî The item is converted per the specifier; on mismatch the directive fails; unless `*`, the result is stored in the next non-received argument; wrong type/unrepresentable ‚Üí undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `hh`: `d/i/o/u/x/X/n` ‚Üí pointer to `signed/unsigned char`. (C99 added `hh`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `h`: ‚Üí pointer to `short`/`unsigned short`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `l`: integer specs ‚Üí pointer to `long`/`unsigned long`; float specs ‚Üí pointer to `double`; `c/s/[` ‚Üí pointer to `wchar_t`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `%lf` read `45.6` correctly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `ll`: ‚Üí pointer to `long long`/`unsigned long long`. (C99 added `ll`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `j`: ‚Üí pointer to `intmax_t`/`uintmax_t`. (C99 added `j`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `z`: ‚Üí pointer to `size_t`/its signed counterpart. (C99 added `z`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `t`: ‚Üí pointer to `ptrdiff_t`/its unsigned counterpart. (C99 added `t`.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî Length modifier `L`: float specs ‚Üí pointer to `long double`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.6.2p11 ‚Äî A length modifier with any other specifier is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `d`: optionally-signed decimal as `strtol` base 10; arg pointer to signed integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `%d` read `123`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `i`: optionally-signed integer as `strtol` base 0; arg pointer to signed integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `o`: octal as `strtoul` base 8; arg pointer to unsigned integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `u`: decimal as `strtoul` base 10; arg pointer to unsigned integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `x`: hex as `strtoul` base 16; arg pointer to unsigned integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `%x` read `ff`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `a`,`e`,`f`,`g` (and `A`,`E`,`F`,`G`): floating/inf/NaN as `strtod`; arg pointer to floating. (C99 made `a/A/F` and uppercase aliases valid.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `c`: exactly field-width chars (1 default); arg pointer to char array (no null added); with `l`, multibyte‚Üí`wchar_t` via `mbrtowc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `s`: non-white-space sequence; arg pointer to char array (null added); with `l`, multibyte‚Üí`wchar_t` array (null wide char added). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `[`: nonempty sequence from the scanset; arg pointer to char array (null added); with `l`, ‚Üí `wchar_t` array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `[` (scanset syntax): chars up to the matching `]`; leading `^` negates; leading `]`/`^]` includes `]`; significance of `-` is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `p`: implementation-defined sequence (matching `%p` output); arg pointer to pointer-to-`void`; round-trip pointers compare equal. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `n`: no input consumed; arg pointer to signed integer receiving the count read so far; does not increment the assignment count; `*`/field-width ‚Üí undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p12 ‚Äî `%`: matches a single `%`; no conversion/assignment; complete spec `%%`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- ¬ß7.21.6.2p13 ‚Äî An invalid conversion specification is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p14 ‚Äî `A`,`E`,`F`,`G`,`X` are valid and behave as `a`,`e`,`f`,`g`,`x`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p15 ‚Äî Trailing white-space is left unread unless matched; literal-match/suppressed-assignment success is observable only via `%n`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.2p16 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on input failure before the first conversion completes; otherwise the number of items assigned (possibly fewer or zero). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] **GAP** ¬ß7.21.6.2p4/p11/p13 ‚Äî gcc/clang diagnose `scanf`/`fscanf` specifier vs pointer-argument-type mismatches under `-Wformat`; mcc does too (verified: `scanf("%d",&d)` with `double d` warns "format '%d' expects a pointer to int argument", same root cause as the `fprintf` check). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (diagnostic-only)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.3 The printf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int printf(const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.3p2 ‚Äî `printf` shall be equivalent to `fprintf` with `stdout` interposed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: number of characters transmitted, or negative on output/encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.4 The scanf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int scanf(const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.4p2 ‚Äî `scanf` shall be equivalent to `fscanf` with `stdin` interposed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on early input failure; otherwise the number of items assigned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.5 The snprintf function

> C99-only addition: `snprintf` did not exist in C90.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int snprintf(char * restrict s, size_t n, const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.5p2 ‚Äî `snprintf` shall be like `fprintf` but write into array `s`; if `n` is zero nothing is written and `s` may be null; otherwise chars beyond `n-1` are discarded and a null terminator is written; overlap is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe: `snprintf(b,5,...)` of "abcdefgh" ‚Üí `abcd`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: the number of characters that would have been written (excl. null), or negative on encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe returned 8 from a 5-byte buffer on all three)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.6 The sprintf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int sprintf(char * restrict s, const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.6p2 ‚Äî `sprintf` shall be like `fprintf` but write into array `s` with a null terminator; overlap is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.6p3 ‚Äî Returns: the number of characters written (excl. null), or negative on encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.7 The sscanf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int sscanf(const char * restrict s, const char * restrict format, ...);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.7p2 ‚Äî `sscanf` shall be like `fscanf` but read from string `s`; reaching the end of the string is equivalent to EOF; overlap is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe parsed `"123 45.6 ff"` correctly)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.7p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on early input failure; otherwise the number of items assigned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.8 The vfprintf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vfprintf(FILE * restrict stream, const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; wrapped in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.8p2 ‚Äî `vfprintf` shall be like `fprintf` with the varargs replaced by `arg` (initialized by `va_start`); it does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `vf(stdout,"a%d\n",1)` ‚Üí `a1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.8p3 ‚Äî Returns: number of characters transmitted, or negative on error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.9 The vfscanf function

> C99-only addition: `vfscanf` did not exist in C90.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.9p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vfscanf(FILE * restrict stream, const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.9p2 ‚Äî `vfscanf` shall be like `fscanf` with varargs replaced by `arg`; it does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.9p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on early input failure; otherwise the number of items assigned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.10 The vprintf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.10p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vprintf(const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; wrapped in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.10p2 ‚Äî `vprintf` shall be like `printf` with varargs replaced by `arg`; it does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `vp("vp %d\n",99)` ‚Üí `vp 99`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.10p3 ‚Äî Returns: number of characters transmitted, or negative on error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.11 The vscanf function

> C99-only addition: `vscanf` did not exist in C90.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.11p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vscanf(const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.11p2 ‚Äî `vscanf` shall be like `scanf` with varargs replaced by `arg`; it does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.11p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on early input failure; otherwise the number of items assigned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.12 The vsnprintf function

> C99-only addition: `vsnprintf` did not exist in C90.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.12p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vsnprintf(char * restrict s, size_t n, const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; wrapped in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.12p2 ‚Äî `vsnprintf` shall be like `snprintf` with varargs replaced by `arg`; it does not invoke `va_end`; overlap is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `vsn(b,64,"b%d",2)` ‚Üí `b2`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.12p3 ‚Äî Returns: the number that would have been written (excl. null), or negative on encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.13 The vsprintf function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.13p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vsprintf(char * restrict s, const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.13p2 ‚Äî `vsprintf` shall be like `sprintf` with varargs replaced by `arg`; it does not invoke `va_end`; overlap is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
