- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.13p3 ‚Äî Returns: the number written (excl. null), or negative on encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.6.14 The vsscanf function

> C99-only addition: `vsscanf` did not exist in C90.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.14p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>` ‚Ä¶ `int vsscanf(const char * restrict s, const char * restrict format, va_list arg);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; wrapped in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.14p2 ‚Äî `vsscanf` shall be like `sscanf` with varargs replaced by `arg`; it does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `vsf("7","%d",&x)` set x=7)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.6.14p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on early input failure; otherwise the number of items assigned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

### ¬ß7.21.7 Character input/output functions

#### ¬ß7.21.7.1 The fgetc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fgetc(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.1p2 ‚Äî If not at EOF and a next char is present, `fgetc` shall obtain it as an `unsigned char` converted to `int` and advance the position indicator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe read `h`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` (and sets the EOF indicator) at end-of-file; otherwise the next char; on read error sets the error indicator and returns `EOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.2 The fgets function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *fgets(char * restrict s, int n, FILE * restrict stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.2p2 ‚Äî `fgets` shall read at most `n-1` chars; stops after a new-line (retained) or EOF; writes a null after the last char. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: `s` on success; null at EOF-with-no-chars (array unchanged); null on read error (array contents indeterminate). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.3 The fputc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fputc(int c, FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.3p2 ‚Äî `fputc` shall write `c` (as `unsigned char`) at the position indicator and advance it; for non-positionable or append streams the char is appended. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: the char written; on write error sets the error indicator and returns `EOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.4 The fputs function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fputs(const char * restrict s, FILE * restrict stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.4p2 ‚Äî `fputs` shall write the string `s`; the terminating null is not written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe wrote "hello" to a tmpfile)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on write error; otherwise a nonnegative value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.5 The getc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int getc(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; glibc may implement as a macro)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.5p2 ‚Äî `getc` shall be like `fgetc`, except a macro implementation may evaluate `stream` more than once (no side effects in the argument). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: the next char; `EOF` (with indicator set) at EOF or on read error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.6 The getchar function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int getchar(void);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.6p2 ‚Äî `getchar` shall be equivalent to `getc(stdin)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.6p3 ‚Äî Returns: the next char from `stdin`; `EOF` (with indicator set) at EOF or on read error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.7 The gets function (C99-only ‚Äî removed in C11)

> Present in C99 ¬ß7.19.7.7; removed from the C11 library. A conforming C11 `<stdio.h>` shall not declare `gets`. Verified: none of the three's glibc header declares `gets`. gcc and clang therefore **reject** a call to `gets` (error: implicit/undeclared function in C99+ default mode); **mcc silently accepts** the implicit declaration ‚Äî an mcc divergence from the gcc==clang consensus (see GAP below).

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.7p1 ‚Äî (C99-only) Synopsis: `char *gets(char *s);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (header correctly omits `gets` on all three, per C11 removal)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.7.7p2 ‚Äî (C99-only) `gets` shall read chars from `stdin` until EOF or a new-line (discarded), writing a null after the last char. ‚Äî (spec; C99-only; function removed ‚Äî runtime n/a)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.7.7p3 ‚Äî (C99-only) Returns: `s` on success; null at EOF-with-no-chars (array unchanged); null on read error (array indeterminate). ‚Äî (spec; C99-only; function removed ‚Äî runtime n/a)
- [‚úó] **GAP** ¬ß7.21.7.7 / ¬ß6.5.2.2 ‚Äî Calling the (C11-removed, undeclared) `gets` should be a constraint violation requiring a diagnostic in C99/C11 (implicit function declaration). gcc errors (`-Wimplicit-function-declaration`), clang errors (`call to undeclared function`); **mcc compiles it silently** ‚Äî mcc accepts implicit function declarations by default. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc accepts; gcc/clang reject ‚Äî affects any undeclared stdio function, not just `gets`)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.8 The putc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int putc(int c, FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.8p2 ‚Äî `putc` shall be like `fputc`, except a macro implementation may evaluate `stream` more than once. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.8p3 ‚Äî Returns: the char written; `EOF` (with error indicator set) on write error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.9 The putchar function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.9p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int putchar(int c);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.9p2 ‚Äî `putchar` shall be equivalent to `putc(c, stdout)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `putchar('Z')` ‚Üí `Z`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.9p3 ‚Äî Returns: the char written; `EOF` (with error indicator set) on write error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.10 The puts function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.10p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int puts(const char *s);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.10p2 ‚Äî `puts` shall write the string `s` to `stdout` and append a new-line; the terminating null is not written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.10p3 ‚Äî Returns: `EOF` on write error; otherwise a nonnegative value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.7.11 The ungetc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.11p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int ungetc(int c, FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.11p2 ‚Äî `ungetc` shall push `c` (as `unsigned char`) back; pushed chars are returned in reverse order; an intervening positioning call discards pushback; external storage is unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe pushed back `h`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.11p3 ‚Äî At least one character of pushback is guaranteed; too many calls without an intervening read/positioning may fail. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.11p4 ‚Äî If `c` equals `EOF`, the operation fails and the input stream is unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.7.11p5 ‚Äî A successful `ungetc` clears the EOF indicator; position-indicator semantics differ for text (unspecified until pushback consumed) vs binary (decremented; indeterminate if it was zero). ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.7.11p6 ‚Äî Returns: the char pushed back (after conversion), or `EOF` if the operation fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

### ¬ß7.21.8 Direct input/output functions

#### ¬ß7.21.8.1 The fread function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.8.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t fread(void * restrict ptr, size_t size, size_t nmemb, FILE * restrict stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.8.1p2 ‚Äî `fread` shall read up to `nmemb` elements of `size` bytes via `fgetc`-equivalent reads, advancing the position indicator; error ‚Üí indeterminate position; partial element ‚Üí indeterminate value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.8.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: the number of elements read (may be < `nmemb` on error/EOF); if `size` or `nmemb` is zero, returns zero with array/stream unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.8.2 The fwrite function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.8.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t fwrite(const void * restrict ptr, size_t size, size_t nmemb, FILE * restrict stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.8.2p2 ‚Äî `fwrite` shall write up to `nmemb` elements of `size` bytes via `fputc`-equivalent writes, advancing the position indicator; error ‚Üí indeterminate position. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.8.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: the number of elements written (< `nmemb` only on write error); if `size` or `nmemb` is zero, returns zero with stream unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

### ¬ß7.21.9 File positioning functions

#### ¬ß7.21.9.1 The fgetpos function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fgetpos(FILE * restrict stream, fpos_t * restrict pos);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.1p2 ‚Äî `fgetpos` shall store the current parse state and position into `*pos` for later use by `fsetpos`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: zero on success; nonzero on failure with an implementation-defined positive value in `errno`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.9.2 The fseek function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fseek(FILE *stream, long int offset, int whence);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.2p2 ‚Äî `fseek` shall set the position indicator; a read/write error sets the error indicator and the call fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.2p3 ‚Äî For a binary stream, the new position is `offset` added to `SEEK_SET`/`SEEK_CUR`/`SEEK_END`; a binary stream need not meaningfully support `SEEK_END`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe `fseek(tf,0,SEEK_SET)`)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.9.2p4 ‚Äî For a text stream, `offset` shall be zero, or a value from an earlier `ftell` with `whence` = `SEEK_SET`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.9.2p5 ‚Äî A successful `fseek` undoes `ungetc` effects, clears the EOF indicator, and establishes the new position; the next update-stream operation may be input or output. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.2p6 ‚Äî Returns: nonzero only for a request that cannot be satisfied. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.9.3 The fsetpos function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fsetpos(FILE *stream, const fpos_t *pos);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.3p2 ‚Äî `fsetpos` shall set the `mbstate_t` (if any) and position from `*pos` (from an earlier `fgetpos` on the same file); a read/write error sets the error indicator and the call fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [ ] ¬ß7.21.9.3p3 ‚Äî A successful `fsetpos` undoes `ungetc` effects, clears the EOF indicator, and establishes the new parse state and position; the next update-stream operation may be input or output. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.3p4 ‚Äî Returns: zero on success; nonzero on failure with an implementation-defined positive value in `errno`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.9.4 The ftell function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `long int ftell(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.4p2 ‚Äî `ftell` shall obtain the current position; for a binary stream this is the byte count from the start; for a text stream it is unspecified information usable by `fseek`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe: `ftell` after writing "hello" returned 5)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: the current position on success; ‚àí1L on failure with an implementation-defined positive value in `errno`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.9.5 The rewind function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void rewind(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.5p2 ‚Äî `rewind` shall set the position indicator to the start; equivalent to `(void)fseek(stream,0L,SEEK_SET)` plus clearing the error indicator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.9.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (void return)

### ¬ß7.21.10 Error-handling functions

#### ¬ß7.21.10.1 The clearerr function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void clearerr(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.1p2 ‚Äî `clearerr` shall clear the EOF and error indicators for the stream. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (void return)

#### ¬ß7.21.10.2 The feof function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int feof(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.2p2 ‚Äî `feof` shall test the EOF indicator for the stream. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe reported feof=0 before EOF)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: nonzero iff the EOF indicator is set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.10.3 The ferror function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int ferror(FILE *stream);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.3p2 ‚Äî `ferror` shall test the error indicator for the stream. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probe reported ferror=0)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: nonzero iff the error indicator is set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)

#### ¬ß7.21.10.4 The perror function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void perror(const char *s);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared & callable; used in probe)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.4p2 ‚Äî `perror` shall map `errno` to a message and write to stderr: optional `s:` prefix, the error message, and a new-line; the message text matches `strerror(errno)` and is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime ‚Äî shared libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.21.10.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (void return)


## ¬ß7.22 <stdlib.h>

> mcc status: 240 TODO items below; 1 mcc divergence from the gcc==clang consensus ‚Äî and it is by-design, not a defect (mcc defaults to C99, hiding the C11-only `aligned_alloc`/`at_quick_exit`/`quick_exit` until `-std=c11`). mcc has **no bundled `<stdlib.h>`** ‚Äî it resolves to the host glibc `/usr/include/stdlib.h`, the same header gcc/clang use, so types, macros, and runtime behavior are byte-for-byte identical across all three. mcc's only relevant difference is that its **default language mode is C99 (`__STDC_VERSION__==199901L`)** whereas gcc 15 defaults to C23 and clang 22 to C17; the C11-only functions (`aligned_alloc`, `at_quick_exit`, `quick_exit`) are gated by glibc behind `__USE_ISOC11`, so mcc must be invoked with `-std=c11` (or newer / `-D_ISOC11_SOURCE`) to see them ‚Äî which it supports and then conforms. mcc honors `_Noreturn`, `restrict`, and glibc's `__attribute__((__noreturn__))` on the library prototypes.

> Clause numbering follows C11 (N1570) ¬ß7.22; the corresponding C99 (N1256) clause is ¬ß7.20 with the same subsection suffixes unless noted. Items added by C11 are tagged **(C11)** (`aligned_alloc`, `at_quick_exit`, `quick_exit`, the `_Noreturn` qualification on `exit`/`_Exit`, the data-race wording); items added by C99 over C90 are tagged **(C99)** (`lldiv_t`, `atoll`, `strtof`, `strtold`, `strtoll`, `strtoull`, `_Exit`, `llabs`, `lldiv`). Nothing in this header was removed or changed by C11 relative to C99.

### ¬ß7.22 General

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p1 ‚Äî The header `<stdlib.h>` shall declare types and functions in five categories ‚Äî numeric conversion, pseudo-random sequence generation, memory management, communication with the environment, searching/sorting/integer arithmetic, and multibyte/wide conversion ‚Äî and shall define several macros. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî The header shall define the type `size_t` (the unsigned integer type of the result of the `sizeof` operator; described in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî The header shall define the type `wchar_t` (an integer type whose range of values can represent distinct codes for all members of the largest extended character set among the supported locales; described in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî The header shall define the structure type `div_t`, the type of the value returned by `div`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî The header shall define the structure type `ldiv_t`, the type of the value returned by `ldiv`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî The header shall define the structure type `lldiv_t`, the type of the value returned by `lldiv`. **(C99)** (not present in C90). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p3 ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `NULL`, which expands to an implementation-defined null pointer constant (described in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p3 ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `EXIT_FAILURE`, which expands to an integer constant expression usable as the argument to `exit` to return unsuccessful termination status to the host environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all expand to `1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p3 ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `EXIT_SUCCESS`, which expands to an integer constant expression usable as the argument to `exit` to return successful termination status to the host environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all expand to `0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p3 ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `RAND_MAX`, which expands to an integer constant expression that is the maximum value returned by `rand`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all `2147483647`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22p3 ‚Äî The header shall define the macro `MB_CUR_MAX`, which expands to a positive integer expression of type `size_t` that is the maximum number of bytes in a multibyte character for the extended character set specified by the current locale (category `LC_CTYPE`), and which is never greater than `MB_LEN_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc `(size_t)__ctype_get_mb_cur_max()`)

### ¬ß7.22.1 Numeric conversion functions

- ¬ß7.22.1p1 ‚Äî The functions `atof`, `atoi`, `atol`, and `atoll` need not affect the value of `errno` on an error; if the value of the result cannot be represented, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.22.1.1 The atof function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `double atof(const char *nptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.1p2 ‚Äî Description: `atof` converts the initial portion of the string pointed to by `nptr` to `double` representation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.1p2 ‚Äî Except for the behavior on error, `atof` is equivalent to `strtod(nptr, (char **)NULL)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `atof` returns the converted value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`atof("1.5")`‚Üí1.5 on all three)

#### ¬ß7.22.1.2 The atoi, atol, and atoll functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int atoi(const char *nptr);`, `long int atol(const char *nptr);`, and `long long int atoll(const char *nptr);`. `atoll` is **(C99)**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.2p2 ‚Äî Description: these functions convert the initial portion of the string pointed to by `nptr` to `int`, `long int`, and `long long int` representation, respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.22.1.2p2 ‚Äî Except for the behavior on error, they are equivalent to `atoi`: `(int)strtol(nptr, (char **)NULL, 10)`; `atol`: `strtol(nptr, (char **)NULL, 10)`; `atoll`: `strtoll(nptr, (char **)NULL, 10)`. ‚Äî (spec; glibc-shared, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: these functions return the converted value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.1.3 The strtod, strtof, and strtold functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double strtod(const char * restrict nptr, char ** restrict endptr);`, `float strtof(const char * restrict nptr, char ** restrict endptr);`, and `long double strtold(const char * restrict nptr, char ** restrict endptr);`. `strtof` and `strtold` are **(C99)**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc accepts `restrict`-qualified prototypes)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p2 ‚Äî Description: these functions convert the initial portion of the string pointed to by `nptr` to `double`, `float`, and `long double` representation, respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p2 ‚Äî First, they decompose the input string into three parts: leading white space; a subject sequence resembling a floating-point constant or representing an infinity or NaN; and a final string of unrecognized characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p2 ‚Äî Then they attempt to convert the subject sequence to a floating-point number, and return the result. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p3 ‚Äî The expected form of the subject sequence is an optional sign, then a decimal/hex significand with optional exponent, or `INF`/`INFINITY`, or `NAN`/`NAN(n-char-sequence_opt)`, ignoring case as specified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strtod("INFINITY")`‚Üíinf, `strtod("0x1p4")`‚Üí16 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p3 ‚Äî The subject sequence is the longest initial subsequence of the input string, starting with the first non-white-space character, that is of the expected form; it contains no characters if the input string is not of the expected form. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p4 ‚Äî If the subject sequence has the expected form for a floating-point number, it is interpreted as a floating constant per ¬ß6.4.4.2, with the locale decimal-point character and assumed zero exponent rules. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p4 ‚Äî If the subject sequence begins with a minus sign, the sequence is interpreted as negated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p4 ‚Äî `INF` or `INFINITY` is interpreted as an infinity, if representable, else like a too-large floating constant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p4 ‚Äî `NAN`/`NAN(n-char-sequence_opt)` is interpreted as a quiet NaN if supported, else like a non-expected-form part; the n-char meaning is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p4 ‚Äî A pointer to the final string is stored in `*endptr`, provided that `endptr` is not a null pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p5 ‚Äî If the subject sequence has the hexadecimal form and `FLT_RADIX` is a power of 2, the value resulting from the conversion is correctly rounded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.1.3p6 (Recommended practice) ‚Äî Hexadecimal form with non-power-of-2 `FLT_RADIX` and inexact result should be one of the two adjacent numbers with correctly-signed error. ‚Äî (spec; recommended practice, moot on this implementation)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p7 ‚Äî Returns: these functions return the converted value, if any. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p7 ‚Äî If no conversion could be performed, zero is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p7 ‚Äî On overflow with default rounding, ¬±`HUGE_VAL`/`HUGE_VALF`/`HUGE_VALL` is returned and `errno` is set to `ERANGE`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.3p7 ‚Äî On underflow, the magnitude returned is no greater than the smallest normalized positive number; whether `errno` becomes `ERANGE` is implementation-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.1.4 The strtol, strtoll, strtoul, and strtoull functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `long int strtol(const char * restrict nptr, char ** restrict endptr, int base);`, `long long int strtoll(...);`, `unsigned long int strtoul(...);`, and `unsigned long long int strtoull(...);`. `strtoll` and `strtoull` are **(C99)**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p2 ‚Äî Description: these functions convert the initial portion of the string to `long`/`long long`/`unsigned long`/`unsigned long long` representation, respectively. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p2 ‚Äî First, they decompose the input string into leading white space; a subject sequence resembling an integer in the radix given by `base`; and a final string of unrecognized characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p2 ‚Äî Then they attempt to convert the subject sequence to an integer, and return the result. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p3 ‚Äî If `base` is zero, the expected form is that of an integer constant per ¬ß6.4.4.1, optionally signed, without an integer suffix. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p3 ‚Äî If `base` is between 2 and 36, the expected form is a sequence of letters and digits in that radix, optionally signed, without an integer suffix. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p3 ‚Äî Letters `a`/`A` through `z`/`Z` are ascribed values 10‚Äì35; only letters and digits with value less than `base` are permitted. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p3 ‚Äî If `base` is 16, the characters `0x`/`0X` may optionally precede the sequence, following the sign if present. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p4 ‚Äî The subject sequence is the longest initial subsequence, starting with the first non-white-space character, of the expected form. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p4 ‚Äî The subject sequence contains no characters if the input is empty/all-white-space, or the first non-white-space character is other than a sign or a permissible letter or digit. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p5 ‚Äî With `base` zero and expected form, characters from the first digit are interpreted as an integer constant per ¬ß6.4.4.1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p5 ‚Äî With `base` 2‚Äì36 and expected form, that base is used, ascribing each letter its value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p5 ‚Äî If the subject sequence begins with a minus sign, the converted value is negated in the return type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p5 ‚Äî A pointer to the final string is stored in `*endptr`, provided that `endptr` is not a null pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.22.1.4p6 ‚Äî In other than the `"C"` locale, additional locale-specific subject sequence forms may be accepted. ‚Äî (spec; locale-dependent, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p7 ‚Äî If the subject sequence is empty or not of the expected form, no conversion is performed; `nptr` is stored in `*endptr` if `endptr` is not null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p8 ‚Äî Returns: these functions return the converted value, if any. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p8 ‚Äî If no conversion could be performed, zero is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.1.4p8 ‚Äî On out-of-range, `LONG_MIN`/`LONG_MAX`/`LLONG_MIN`/`LLONG_MAX`/`ULONG_MAX`/`ULLONG_MAX` is returned and `errno` is set to `ERANGE`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strtol("99999999999999999999")` clamps to `LONG_MAX` on all three)

### ¬ß7.22.2 Pseudo-random sequence generation functions

#### ¬ß7.22.2.1 The rand function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int rand(void);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.1p2 ‚Äî Description: `rand` computes a sequence of pseudo-random integers in the range 0 to `RAND_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.2.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî No guarantees as to the quality of the random sequence; low-order bits may be non-random; applications with particular requirements should use a sufficient generator. ‚Äî (spec; footnote/advisory, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `rand` returns a pseudo-random integer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.1p4 ‚Äî The value of the `RAND_MAX` macro shall be at least 32767. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`RAND_MAX`=2147483647 ‚â• 32767 on all three)

#### ¬ß7.22.2.2 The srand function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void srand(unsigned int seed);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.2p2 ‚Äî Description: `srand` uses `seed` as a seed for a new sequence of pseudo-random numbers returned by subsequent calls to `rand`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.2p2 ‚Äî If `srand` is then called with the same seed value, the sequence of pseudo-random numbers shall be repeated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.2p2 ‚Äî If `rand` is called before any `srand`, the same sequence is generated as when `srand` is first called with seed 1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.2.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: `srand` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.22.3 Memory management functions

> C11 added `aligned_alloc` (¬ß7.22.3.1) and the data-race wording (¬ß7.22.3p2); C99 has neither.

- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî The order and contiguity of storage allocated by successive calls to `aligned_alloc` **(C11)**, `calloc`, `malloc`, and `realloc` is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified behavior, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî A successful allocation is suitably aligned for any object type with a fundamental alignment requirement, usable for such objects or arrays until deallocated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî The lifetime of an allocated object extends from the allocation until the deallocation. ‚Äî (spec; semantic statement, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî Each such allocation shall yield a pointer to an object disjoint from any other object. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî The returned pointer points to the start (lowest byte address) of the allocated space. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî If the space cannot be allocated, a null pointer is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3p1 ‚Äî If the requested size is zero, the behavior is implementation-defined (null, or a non-dereferenceable nonzero-size-like pointer). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc returns a freeable non-null pointer on all three)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3p2 ‚Äî For determining a data race, memory allocation functions behave as though they accessed only memory accessible through their arguments and not other static-duration storage. **(C11)** ‚Äî (spec; memory-model wording, not testable here)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3p2 ‚Äî These functions may visibly modify the storage they allocate/deallocate; a deallocation synchronizes with the next allocation of that same region or part thereof. **(C11)** ‚Äî (spec; memory-model wording, not testable here)

#### ¬ß7.22.3.1 The aligned_alloc function **(C11)**

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis **(C11)**: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void *aligned_alloc(size_t alignment, size_t size);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc needs `-std=c11`; in default C99 mode glibc hides it behind `__USE_ISOC11`, yielding an implicit-declaration warning ‚Äî same gating glibc applies to any C99-default compiler)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.1p2 ‚Äî Description **(C11)**: `aligned_alloc` allocates space with the given `alignment` and `size`, value indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runs identically with `-std=c11`)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3.1p2 ‚Äî Constraint **(C11)**: `alignment` shall be a valid supported alignment, and `size` shall be an integral multiple of `alignment`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime constraint, glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.1p3 ‚Äî Returns **(C11)**: `aligned_alloc` returns either a null pointer or a pointer to the allocated space. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.3.2 The calloc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void *calloc(size_t nmemb, size_t size);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.2p2 ‚Äî Description: `calloc` allocates space for an array of `nmemb` objects, each of size `size`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.2p2 ‚Äî The space is initialized to all bits zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3.2p2 (footnote) ‚Äî All-bits-zero need not be the representation of floating-point zero or a null pointer constant. ‚Äî (spec; footnote, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: `calloc` returns either a null pointer or a pointer to the allocated space. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.3.3 The free function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void free(void *ptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.3p2 ‚Äî Description: `free` deallocates the space pointed to by `ptr`, making it available for further allocation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.3p2 ‚Äî If `ptr` is a null pointer, no action occurs. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3.3p2 ‚Äî Otherwise, if the argument does not match a pointer earlier returned, or the space was already deallocated, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: `free` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.3.4 The malloc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void *malloc(size_t size);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.4p2 ‚Äî Description: `malloc` allocates space of the specified `size`, value indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: `malloc` returns either a null pointer or a pointer to the allocated space. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.3.5 The realloc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void *realloc(void *ptr, size_t size);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p2 ‚Äî Description: `realloc` deallocates the old object pointed to by `ptr` and returns a pointer to a new object of the specified `size`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p2 ‚Äî The contents of the new object are the same as the old object up to the lesser of the new and old sizes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3.5p2 ‚Äî Any bytes in the new object beyond the old size have indeterminate values. ‚Äî (spec; indeterminate-value statement, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p3 ‚Äî If `ptr` is a null pointer, `realloc` behaves like `malloc` for the specified size. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.3.5p3 ‚Äî Otherwise, if `ptr` does not match an earlier-returned pointer, or the space was already deallocated, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p3 ‚Äî If the new size is zero, the behavior is implementation-defined per ¬ß7.22.3p1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p3 ‚Äî If memory for the new object cannot be allocated, the old object is not deallocated and its value is unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3.5p4 ‚Äî Returns: `realloc` returns a pointer to the new object (possibly the same value), or a null pointer if it could not be allocated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.22.4 Communication with the environment

> C11 added `at_quick_exit` (¬ß7.22.4.3) and `quick_exit` (¬ß7.22.4.7), the `_Noreturn` qualification on the `exit`/`_Exit`/`quick_exit` prototypes, and the `quick_exit`/`at_quick_exit` interaction clauses in `exit` and `_Exit`. The `_Exit` function itself is **(C99)**.

#### ¬ß7.22.4.1 The abort function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `_Noreturn void abort(void);`. (`_Noreturn` on the prototype is **(C11)**.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc honors glibc's `__attribute__((__noreturn__))`: no "control reaches end of non-void" after `abort()`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.1p2 ‚Äî Description: `abort` causes abnormal program termination, unless `SIGABRT` is caught and the handler does not return. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.4.1p2 ‚Äî Whether open streams are flushed/closed or temporary files removed is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.1p2 ‚Äî An implementation-defined "unsuccessful termination" status is returned via `raise(SIGABRT)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `abort` does not return to its caller. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.4.2 The atexit function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int atexit(void (*func)(void));`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.2p2 ‚Äî Description: `atexit` registers `func` to be called without arguments at normal program termination. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.2p2 (footnote) **(C11)** ‚Äî The `atexit` registrations are distinct from the `at_quick_exit` registrations. ‚Äî (spec; footnote, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.2p3 ‚Äî The implementation shall support the registration of at least 32 functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc supports unbounded registration)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.2p4 ‚Äî Returns: `atexit` returns zero if registration succeeds, nonzero if it fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.4.3 The at_quick_exit function **(C11)**

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis **(C11)**: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int at_quick_exit(void (*func)(void));`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc needs `-std=c11`; glibc gates behind `__USE_ISOC11`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.3p2 ‚Äî Description **(C11)**: `at_quick_exit` registers `func` to be called without arguments should `quick_exit` be called. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.3p2 **(C11)** ‚Äî If a function is registered multiple times, it is called as many times as registered. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.3p2 (footnote) **(C11)** ‚Äî The `at_quick_exit` registrations are distinct from the `atexit` registrations. ‚Äî (spec; footnote, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.3p3 **(C11)** ‚Äî The implementation shall support the registration of at least 32 functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.3p4 ‚Äî Returns **(C11)**: `at_quick_exit` returns zero if registration succeeds, nonzero if it fails. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.4.4 The exit function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `_Noreturn void exit(int status);`. (`_Noreturn` on the prototype is **(C11)**.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc treats `exit()` as noreturn; no fall-off diagnostic)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p2 ‚Äî Description: `exit` causes normal program termination to occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p2 ‚Äî No functions registered by `at_quick_exit` are called. **(C11)** ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.4p3 ‚Äî Calling `exit` more than once, or calling `quick_exit` in addition to `exit`, is undefined. (`quick_exit` clause **(C11)**.) ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p4 ‚Äî First, all functions registered by `atexit` are called in reverse order of registration, with the staggered-call ordering rule. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (registering a,b,c then exit prints `cba` on all three)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.4p4 ‚Äî If during such a registered function a `longjmp` is made that would terminate the call, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p5 ‚Äî Next, all open streams with unwritten buffered data are flushed, all open streams are closed, and all `tmpfile` files are removed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p6 ‚Äî Finally, control is returned to the host environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p6 ‚Äî If `status` is zero or `EXIT_SUCCESS`, an implementation-defined "successful termination" status is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p6 ‚Äî If `status` is `EXIT_FAILURE`, an implementation-defined "unsuccessful termination" status is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.22.4.4p6 ‚Äî Otherwise the status returned is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.4p7 ‚Äî Returns: `exit` cannot return to its caller. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.4.5 The _Exit function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `_Noreturn void _Exit(int status);`. `_Exit` is **(C99)**; `_Noreturn` on the prototype is **(C11)**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.5p2 ‚Äî Description: `_Exit` causes normal program termination and control to be returned to the host environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.5p2 ‚Äî No functions registered by `atexit`, none by `at_quick_exit`, and no `signal` handlers are called. (`at_quick_exit` clause **(C11)**.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.5p2 ‚Äî The status returned is determined as for `exit` (¬ß7.22.4.4p6). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.22.4.5p2 ‚Äî Whether open streams are flushed/closed or temporary files removed is implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: `_Exit` cannot return to its caller. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.4.6 The getenv function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `char *getenv(const char *name);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.6p2 ‚Äî Description: `getenv` searches a host-provided environment list for a string matching `name`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`getenv("PATH")` non-null on all three)
- ¬ß7.22.4.6p2 ‚Äî The set of environment names and the method for altering the environment list are implementation-defined. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.6p2 ‚Äî The `getenv` function need not avoid data races with other threads that modify the environment list. **(C11)** ‚Äî (spec; thread-safety wording, not testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.6p3 ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `getenv`. ‚Äî (spec; as-if requirement, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.6p3 ‚Äî Returns: `getenv` returns a pointer to a string associated with the matched member. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.6p3 ‚Äî The string shall not be modified by the program, but may be overwritten by a subsequent `getenv` call. ‚Äî (spec; usage constraint, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.6p3 ‚Äî If `name` cannot be found, a null pointer is returned. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.4.7 The quick_exit function **(C11)**

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis **(C11)**: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `_Noreturn void quick_exit(int status);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc needs `-std=c11`; glibc gates behind `__USE_ISOC11`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.7p2 ‚Äî Description **(C11)**: `quick_exit` causes normal program termination to occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.7p2 **(C11)** ‚Äî No functions registered by `atexit` and no `signal` handlers are called. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.7p3 **(C11)** ‚Äî Calling `quick_exit` more than once, or calling `exit` in addition to `quick_exit`, is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.7p3 (footnote) **(C11)** ‚Äî Functions registered by `at_quick_exit` and called at quick termination may, e.g., flush a buffer or write a marker. ‚Äî (spec; footnote, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.7p4 **(C11)** ‚Äî Functions registered by `at_quick_exit` are called in reverse order of registration, with the staggered-call ordering rule. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.4.7p4 **(C11)** ‚Äî If during such a registered function a `longjmp` would terminate the call, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.7p5 **(C11)** ‚Äî After calling all registered functions, control is returned via the function call `_Exit(status)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.7p6 ‚Äî Returns **(C11)**: `quick_exit` cannot return to its caller. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.4.8 The system function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int system(const char *string);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.8p2 ‚Äî Description: if `string` is a null pointer, `system` determines whether the host environment has a command processor. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.4.8p2 ‚Äî If `string` is not null, `system` passes it to the command processor in an implementation-documented manner; this may cause non-conforming behavior or termination. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.4.8p3 ‚Äî Returns: if the argument is a null pointer, `system` returns nonzero only if a command processor is available. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.4.8p3 ‚Äî If the argument is not null and `system` returns, it returns an implementation-defined value. ‚Äî (spec; implementation-defined, not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.22.5 Searching and sorting utilities

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5p1 ‚Äî These utilities use a comparison function called with two arguments pointing to the key object and an array element, in that order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.5p1 ‚Äî The comparison function shall return an integer <, =, or > zero as the key object is less than, matches, or is greater than the array element. ‚Äî (spec; caller obligation, glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.5p1 ‚Äî The array partitioning requirement: for `bsearch` the three groups in order; for `qsort` all elements in any order. ‚Äî (spec; caller obligation, not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.5p2 ‚Äî When the same objects are passed more than once to the comparison function, results shall be consistent and define a total ordering. ‚Äî (spec; caller obligation, not testable)
- ¬ß7.22.5p3 ‚Äî A sequence point occurs immediately before and after each call to the comparison function, and between any call and any movement of the passed objects. ‚Äî (spec; sequencing guarantee, not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5p4 ‚Äî The implementation may reorder elements between calls but shall not otherwise alter any individual element's contents. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.5.1 The bsearch function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void *bsearch(const void *key, const void *base, size_t nmemb, size_t size, int (*compar)(const void *, const void *));`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.1p2 ‚Äî Description: `bsearch` searches an array of `nmemb` objects starting at `base` for an element matching `*key`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (found correct element on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.1p2 ‚Äî The size of each element is specified by `size`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.1p2 ‚Äî `compar` is called with two arguments pointing to the `key` object and an array element, in that order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.5.1p2 ‚Äî `compar` shall return <, =, or > zero per the key/element ordering. ‚Äî (spec; caller obligation, not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.5.1p2 ‚Äî The array partitioning into less/equal/greater groups in order. ‚Äî (spec; caller obligation, not testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.5.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî In practice, the entire array is sorted according to the comparison function. ‚Äî (spec; footnote, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `bsearch` returns a pointer to a matching element, or a null pointer if no match is found. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.5.1p3 ‚Äî If two elements compare equal, which is matched is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified, not testable)

#### ¬ß7.22.5.2 The qsort function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `void qsort(void *base, size_t nmemb, size_t size, int (*compar)(const void *, const void *));`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.2p2 ‚Äî Description: `qsort` sorts an array of `nmemb` objects starting at `base`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ({3,1,2}‚Üí{1,2,3} on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.2p2 ‚Äî The size of each object is specified by `size`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.2p3 ‚Äî Contents are sorted into ascending order per `compar`, called with two arguments pointing to the objects being compared. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- ¬ß7.22.5.2p3 ‚Äî `compar` shall return <, =, or > zero as the first argument is less than, equal to, or greater than the second. ‚Äî (spec; caller obligation, not separately testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.5.2p4 ‚Äî If two elements compare equal, their order in the result is unspecified (the sort is not required to be stable). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.5.2p5 ‚Äî Returns: `qsort` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.22.6 Integer arithmetic functions

#### ¬ß7.22.6.1 The abs, labs, and llabs functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` with `int abs(int j);`, `long int labs(long int j);`, and `long long int llabs(long long int j);`. `llabs` is **(C99)**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.1p2 ‚Äî Description: these functions compute the absolute value of an integer `j`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`abs(-1)`=1, `labs(-1L)`=1, `llabs(-1LL)`=1 on all three)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.6.1p2 ‚Äî If the result cannot be represented, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.6.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî The absolute value of the most negative number cannot be represented in two's complement. ‚Äî (spec; footnote, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: these functions return the absolute value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.22.6.2 The div, ldiv, and lldiv functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` with `div_t div(int numer, int denom);`, `ldiv_t ldiv(long int numer, long int denom);`, and `lldiv_t lldiv(long long int numer, long long int denom);`. `lldiv` is **(C99)**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.2p2 ‚Äî Description: these functions compute `numer / denom` and `numer % denom` in a single operation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`div(-7,2)`‚Üíquot=-3, rem=-1, truncation toward zero, on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: these functions return a structure of type `div_t`/`ldiv_t`/`lldiv_t` comprising both quotient and remainder. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.6.2p3 ‚Äî The structures contain (in either order) members `quot` and `rem`, each of the same type as the arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (member access `.quot`/`.rem` compiles and yields correct types)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.6.2p3 ‚Äî If either part of the result cannot be represented, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)

### ¬ß7.22.7 Multibyte/wide character conversion functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7p1 ‚Äî The behavior of the multibyte character functions is affected by the `LC_CTYPE` category of the current locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7p1 ‚Äî For a state-dependent encoding, each function starts in its initial conversion state at program startup and can be returned there by a call with character pointer `s` a null pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7p1 ‚Äî A subsequent call with `s` other than null causes the internal conversion state to be altered as necessary. ‚Äî (spec; state behavior, glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7p1 ‚Äî A call with `s` null returns nonzero or zero according to whether encodings do or do not have state-dependent encodings. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7p1 ‚Äî Changing the `LC_CTYPE` category causes the conversion state of these functions to be indeterminate. ‚Äî (spec; indeterminate-state statement, not testable)

#### ¬ß7.22.7.1 The mblen function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int mblen(const char *s, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.1p2 ‚Äî Description: if `s` is not null, `mblen` determines the number of bytes in the multibyte character pointed to by `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`mblen("a",1)`=1 on all three)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7.1p2 ‚Äî Except that the conversion state of `mbtowc` is not affected, `mblen` is equivalent to `mbtowc((wchar_t *)0, s, n)`. ‚Äî (spec; equivalence, glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7.1p3 ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `mblen`. ‚Äî (spec; as-if requirement, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: if `s` is null, returns nonzero/zero per state-dependent encoding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.1p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, returns 0 (null char), the byte count (valid multibyte char), or ‚àí1 (invalid). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.7.2 The mbtowc function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int mbtowc(wchar_t * restrict pwc, const char * restrict s, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.2p2 ‚Äî Description: if `s` is not null, `mbtowc` inspects at most `n` bytes from `s` to determine the bytes needed to complete the next multibyte character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`mbtowc(&w,"a",1)`=1 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.2p2 ‚Äî If complete and valid, it determines the corresponding wide character and, if `pwc` is not null, stores it in `*pwc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7.2p2 ‚Äî If the corresponding wide character is the null wide character, the function is left in the initial conversion state. ‚Äî (spec; state behavior, glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7.2p3 ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `mbtowc`. ‚Äî (spec; as-if requirement, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.2p4 ‚Äî Returns: if `s` is null, returns nonzero/zero per state-dependent encoding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.2p4 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, returns 0 (null char), the byte count (valid), or ‚àí1 (invalid). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.2p4 ‚Äî In no case will the returned value be greater than `n` or `MB_CUR_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.7.3 The wctomb function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `int wctomb(char *s, wchar_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.3p2 ‚Äî Description: `wctomb` determines the bytes needed for the multibyte character corresponding to `wc` and stores its representation in `s` (if `s` is not null). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wctomb(buf,L'a')`=1 on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.3p2 ‚Äî At most `MB_CUR_MAX` characters are stored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7.3p2 ‚Äî If `wc` is a null wide character, a null byte is stored (preceded by any needed shift sequence) and the function is left in the initial conversion state. ‚Äî (spec; state behavior, glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.7.3p3 ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `wctomb`. ‚Äî (spec; as-if requirement, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.3p4 ‚Äî Returns: if `s` is null, returns nonzero/zero per state-dependent encoding. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.3p4 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, returns ‚àí1 if `wc` is not a valid multibyte character, else the byte count. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.7.3p4 ‚Äî In no case will the returned value be greater than `MB_CUR_MAX`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

### ¬ß7.22.8 Multibyte/wide string conversion functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8p1 ‚Äî The behavior of the multibyte string functions is affected by the `LC_CTYPE` category of the current locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.8.1 The mbstowcs function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `size_t mbstowcs(wchar_t * restrict pwcs, const char * restrict s, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.1p2 ‚Äî Description: `mbstowcs` converts a multibyte sequence beginning in the initial shift state from `s` into wide characters, storing not more than `n` into `pwcs`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.8.1p2 ‚Äî No multibyte characters following a null character (converted to a null wide character) are examined or converted. ‚Äî (spec; semantic, glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.8.1p2 ‚Äî Each multibyte character is converted as if by `mbtowc`, except the conversion state of `mbtowc` is not affected. ‚Äî (spec; equivalence, glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.1p2 ‚Äî No more than `n` elements are modified in `pwcs`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.8.1p2 ‚Äî If copying takes place between overlapping objects, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: if an invalid multibyte character is encountered, returns `(size_t)(-1)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.1p3 ‚Äî Otherwise returns the number of array elements modified, not including a terminating null wide character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

#### ¬ß7.22.8.2 The wcstombs function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdlib.h>` and `size_t wcstombs(char * restrict s, const wchar_t * restrict pwcs, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.2p2 ‚Äî Description: `wcstombs` converts a wide-character sequence from `pwcs` into multibyte characters beginning in the initial shift state, storing into `s`, stopping at the `n`-byte limit or a stored null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.8.2p2 ‚Äî Each wide character is converted as if by `wctomb`, except the conversion state of `wctomb` is not affected. ‚Äî (spec; equivalence, glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.2p2 ‚Äî No more than `n` bytes are modified in `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [ ] ¬ß7.22.8.2p2 ‚Äî If copying takes place between overlapping objects, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog, not testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: if a wide character with no valid multibyte representation is encountered, returns `(size_t)(-1)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.8.2p3 ‚Äî Otherwise returns the number of bytes modified, not including a terminating null character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc-shared)

### ¬ß7.22 Added gap items (beyond the consolidated draft)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22 (header resolution) ‚Äî mcc ships **no** `<stdlib.h>` in `runtime/include/`; `#include <stdlib.h>` resolves to the host `/usr/include/stdlib.h` (glibc), identical to gcc/clang. So all library entity definitions and runtime behavior are inherited from glibc and conform. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [~] ¬ß7.22 (default language mode) ‚Äî mcc's default `__STDC_VERSION__` is `199901L` (C99), versus gcc 15 `202311L` (C23) and clang 22 `201710L` (C17). Consequently, with no `-std=` flag the C11-only functions (`aligned_alloc`/`at_quick_exit`/`quick_exit`), gated by glibc behind `__USE_ISOC11`, are not visible to mcc and produce implicit-declaration warnings; `-std=c11` (or newer) makes them visible and conforming. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc default is C99 by design, not a defect; the C11 surface appears under `-std=c11`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22 (`_Noreturn` keyword) ‚Äî mcc accepts the `_Noreturn` function specifier in both default and `-std=c11` modes, as required for the ¬ß7.22.4 prototypes' qualification. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22 (`restrict` qualifier) ‚Äî mcc accepts the `restrict`-qualified pointer parameters used by `strtod`/`strtof`/`strtold`/`strtol`-family/`mbtowc`/`mbstowcs`/`wcstombs` prototypes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22 (`__attribute__((__noreturn__))` honored) ‚Äî mcc honors glibc's GNU `noreturn` attribute on `abort`/`exit`/`_Exit`/`quick_exit`: code after such a call is treated as unreachable, with no spurious "control reaches end of non-void function" diagnostic. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22 (idempotent inclusion) ‚Äî `<stdlib.h>` is protected against multiple inclusion (`_STDLIB_H` guard); including it twice in a translation unit is well-defined and compiles cleanly on all three. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22.3p1 (zero-size allocation, observed) ‚Äî On this glibc, `malloc(0)`/`calloc(0,0)`/`realloc(p,0)` return a non-null, `free`-able pointer (the "as if nonzero size" branch of the implementation-defined choice), identically across mcc/gcc/clang. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.22 (GNU/POSIX extras visible, non-normative) ‚Äî Because the header is glibc's, non-C entities such as `posix_memalign`, `mkstemp`, `realpath`, `setenv`/`unsetenv`, `random`/`srandom`, `strtoq`, `__compar_fn_t`, `qsort_r` are also reachable under default/feature-test settings on all three compilers; these are outside C11 ¬ß7.22 and not required, but their presence is identical across the three. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (non-normative)


## ¬ß7.23 <string.h> & ¬ß7.24 <tgmath.h>

> mcc status: 118 TODOs; 0 mcc-gaps. `<string.h>` is **not** bundled by mcc ‚Äî it resolves to the system `/usr/include/string.h` (glibc) and links glibc's runtime, so every string function compiles, runs, and matches gcc/clang byte-for-byte. The **bundled `runtime/include/tgmath.h`** matches the gcc==clang consensus: `nexttoward` keys type-generic selection on its first argument only (`nexttoward(f,ld)`‚Üí`nexttowardf`), and `creal`/`cimag` are `_Generic`-based, selecting `crealf`/`creall` (and `cimagf`/`cimagl`) for `float`/`long double` complex arguments instead of narrowing to `double` precision.

> **Numbering note.** The task labels this section ¬ß7.23 <string.h> / ¬ß7.24 <tgmath.h>, but the actual ISO clause numbers differ by edition. In **C99 (N1256)** these headers are **¬ß7.21 <string.h>** and **¬ß7.22 <tgmath.h>**; in **C11 (N1570)** they are **¬ß7.24 <string.h>** and **¬ß7.25 <tgmath.h>** (C11 inserted `<stdnoreturn.h>` at ¬ß7.23, shifting the later library headers up by three). The per-requirement citations below use **C11 N1570 numbering as primary**, with the C99 ¬ß7.21/¬ß7.22 number given in each heading. Function semantics are identical between C99 and C11 unless tagged `(C11)`/`(C99-only)`.

### ¬ß7.24.1 / ¬ß7.21.1 String function conventions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.1p1 ‚Äî `<string.h>` shall declare one type (`size_t`), define one macro (`NULL`), and declare several functions useful for manipulating arrays of character type and other objects treated as arrays of character type; `size_t` and `NULL` are as described in `<stddef.h>` (¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc header on mcc's path; `size_t`/`NULL` resolve, all functions declared)
- ¬ß7.24.1p1 ‚Äî Various methods are used for determining the lengths of the arrays, but in all cases a `char *` or `void *` argument points to the initial (lowest-addressed) byte of the array; if an array is accessed beyond the end of an object, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.1p2 ‚Äî Where an argument declared as `size_t n` specifies the length of the array for a function, `n` can have the value zero on a call to that function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.24.1p2 ‚Äî Unless explicitly stated otherwise in the description of a particular function, pointer arguments on a call with `n == 0` shall still have valid values, as described in ¬ß7.1.4. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.1p2 ‚Äî On a call with `n == 0`: a function that locates a character finds no occurrence, a function that compares two character sequences returns zero, and a function that copies characters copies zero characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.24.2 / ¬ß7.21.2 Copying functions

#### ¬ß7.24.2.1 / ¬ß7.21.2.1 The memcpy function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void *memcpy(void * restrict s1, const void * restrict s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî both pointer parameters are `restrict`-qualified (the objects must not overlap). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc prototype; mcc parses `restrict`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.1p2 ‚Äî `memcpy` copies `n` characters from the object pointed to by `s2` into the object pointed to by `s1`; if copying takes place between objects that overlap, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `memcpy` returns the value of `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.2.2 / ¬ß7.21.2.2 The memmove function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void *memmove(void *s1, const void *s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî no `restrict` (overlap is permitted). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.2p2 ‚Äî `memmove` copies `n` characters as if via a temporary array so overlapping moves work correctly. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; overlap copy verified at runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: `memmove` returns the value of `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.2.3 / ¬ß7.21.2.3 The strcpy function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strcpy(char * restrict s1, const char * restrict s2);` ‚Äî `restrict`-qualified (objects must not overlap). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.3p2 ‚Äî `strcpy` copies the string pointed to by `s2` (including the terminating null character) into the array pointed to by `s1`; overlap is UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; verified at runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: `strcpy` returns the value of `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.2.4 / ¬ß7.21.2.4 The strncpy function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strncpy(char * restrict s1, const char * restrict s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî `restrict`-qualified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.4p2 ‚Äî `strncpy` copies not more than `n` characters (characters following a null are not copied) from `s2` to `s1`; overlap is UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.4p2 ‚Äî If there is no null character among the first `n` characters of `s2`, the result in `s1` is not null-terminated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.4p3 ‚Äî If `s2` is a string shorter than `n` characters, null characters are appended to the copy until `n` characters have been written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.2.4p4 ‚Äî Returns: `strncpy` returns the value of `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.24.3 / ¬ß7.21.3 Concatenation functions

#### ¬ß7.24.3.1 / ¬ß7.21.3.1 The strcat function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strcat(char * restrict s1, const char * restrict s2);` ‚Äî `restrict`-qualified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.3.1p2 ‚Äî `strcat` appends a copy of `s2` (including the null) to the end of `s1`; `s2`'s initial char overwrites `s1`'s null; overlap is UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; verified at runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.3.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `strcat` returns the value of `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.3.2 / ¬ß7.21.3.2 The strncat function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strncat(char * restrict s1, const char * restrict s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî `restrict`-qualified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.3.2p2 ‚Äî `strncat` appends not more than `n` characters from `s2`, always appends a terminating null; overlap is UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; verified `strncat(b,"XYZ",2)` ‚Üí `‚Ä¶XY`)
- ¬ß7.24.3.2p2 (footnote) ‚Äî Thus, the maximum number of characters that can end up in `s1` is `strlen(s1)+n+1`. ‚Äî (spec footnote; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.3.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: `strncat` returns the value of `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.24.4 / ¬ß7.21.4 Comparison functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4p1 ‚Äî The sign of a nonzero value returned by `memcmp`, `strcmp`, `strncmp` is determined by the sign of the difference of the first differing pair of characters (both as `unsigned char`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.4.1 / ¬ß7.21.4.1 The memcmp function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int memcmp(const void *s1, const void *s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.1p2 ‚Äî `memcmp` compares the first `n` characters of `s1` to the first `n` of `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.24.4.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî Padding "holes" in structures are indeterminate; short strings and unions may also misbehave when compared with `memcmp`. ‚Äî (spec footnote; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `memcmp` returns an integer >, =, or < zero per `s1` >, =, or < `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.4.2 / ¬ß7.21.4.2 The strcmp function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int strcmp(const char *s1, const char *s2);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.2p2 ‚Äî `strcmp` compares the string pointed to by `s1` to that pointed to by `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: integer >, =, or < zero per `s1` >, =, or < `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strcmp("a","b")<0` verified)

#### ¬ß7.24.4.3 / ¬ß7.21.4.3 The strcoll function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int strcoll(const char *s1, const char *s2);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.3p2 ‚Äî `strcoll` compares `s1` to `s2` interpreted per the `LC_COLLATE` category of the current locale. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc/locale)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: integer >, =, or < zero per the locale-collated comparison. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.4.4 / ¬ß7.21.4.4 The strncmp function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int strncmp(const char *s1, const char *s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.4p2 ‚Äî `strncmp` compares not more than `n` characters (characters after a null are not compared). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: integer >, =, or < zero per the possibly-null-terminated arrays. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.4.5 / ¬ß7.21.4.5 The strxfrm function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t strxfrm(char * restrict s1, const char * restrict s2, size_t n);` ‚Äî `restrict`-qualified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.5p2 ‚Äî `strxfrm` transforms `s2` into `s1` so `strcmp` of transforms matches `strcoll` of originals. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.5p2 ‚Äî No more than `n` characters placed in `s1` (incl. null); if `n` is zero, `s1` may be null; overlap is UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.4.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: length of the transformed string (excl. null); if `‚â• n` the contents of `s1` are indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.24.4.5p4 (example) ‚Äî `1 + strxfrm(NULL, s, 0)` yields the size of the array needed for the transform of `s`. ‚Äî (spec example; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.24.5 / ¬ß7.21.5 Search functions

#### ¬ß7.24.5.1 / ¬ß7.21.5.1 The memchr function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void *memchr(const void *s, int c, size_t n);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.1p2 ‚Äî `memchr` locates the first occurrence of `c` (as `unsigned char`) in the initial `n` characters of `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`memchr("xyz",'y',3)` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if it reads the characters sequentially and stops as soon as a matching character is found. (Sentence added in C11; absent in C99.) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; behavioral, not observable except for OOB-stop)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the located character, or a null pointer if not found. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.2 / ¬ß7.21.5.2 The strchr function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strchr(const char *s, int c);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.2p2 ‚Äî `strchr` locates the first occurrence of `c` (as `char`) in `s`; the terminating null is part of the string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strchr("abc",'b')` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.2p3 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the located character, or a null pointer if not found. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.3 / ¬ß7.21.5.3 The strcspn function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t strcspn(const char *s1, const char *s2);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.3p2 ‚Äî `strcspn` computes the length of the max initial segment of `s1` consisting of characters *not* from `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: the length of the segment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.4 / ¬ß7.21.5.4 The strpbrk function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strpbrk(const char *s1, const char *s2);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.4p2 ‚Äî `strpbrk` locates the first occurrence in `s1` of any character from `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.4p3 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the character, or a null pointer if none of `s2` occurs in `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.5 / ¬ß7.21.5.5 The strrchr function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strrchr(const char *s, int c);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.5p2 ‚Äî `strrchr` locates the last occurrence of `c` (as `char`) in `s`; the terminating null is part of the string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.5p3 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the character, or a null pointer if `c` does not occur. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.6 / ¬ß7.21.5.6 The strspn function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t strspn(const char *s1, const char *s2);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.6p2 ‚Äî `strspn` computes the length of the max initial segment of `s1` consisting entirely of characters from `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.6p3 ‚Äî Returns: the length of the segment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.7 / ¬ß7.21.5.7 The strstr function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strstr(const char *s1, const char *s2);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.7p2 ‚Äî `strstr` locates the first occurrence in `s1` of the sequence of characters (excl. null) in `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strstr("abcdef","cd")` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.7p3 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the located string, or null if not found; if `s2` has zero length, returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.5.8 / ¬ß7.21.5.8 The strtok function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strtok(char * restrict s1, const char * restrict s2);` ‚Äî `restrict`-qualified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p2 ‚Äî A sequence of calls breaks `s1` into tokens delimited by characters from `s2`; first call non-null first arg, subsequent calls null; `s2` may vary. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p3 ‚Äî First call searches `s1` for the first character not in `s2`; if none, no tokens (returns null); else that is the start of the first token. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p4 ‚Äî Then searches for a separator char; if none, token extends to end; else the separator is overwritten by a null and the next-start pointer is saved. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p5 ‚Äî Each subsequent null-first-arg call starts from the saved pointer and behaves as above. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.24.5.8p6 (C11) ‚Äî `strtok` is not required to avoid data races with other calls to `strtok`. (Sentence new in C11.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.24.5.8p6 ‚Äî The implementation shall behave as if no library function calls `strtok`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p7 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the first character of a token, or null if there is no token. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.5.8p8 (example) ‚Äî `strtok("?a???b,,,#c","?")`/`(NULL,",")`/`(NULL,"#,")`/`(NULL,"?")` yield `"a"`, `"???b"`, `"c"`, null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified: all three print `a ??b c` for the prefix used in probe)

### ¬ß7.24.6 / ¬ß7.21.6 Miscellaneous functions

#### ¬ß7.24.6.1 / ¬ß7.21.6.1 The memset function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `void *memset(void *s, int c, size_t n);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.1p2 ‚Äî `memset` copies `c` (as `unsigned char`) into each of the first `n` characters of `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`memset(d,'Q',1)` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.1p3 ‚Äî Returns: `memset` returns the value of `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.6.2 / ¬ß7.21.6.2 The strerror function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *strerror(int errnum);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.2p2 ‚Äî `strerror` maps `errnum` to a message string; it shall map any `int` value to a message. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.24.6.2p3 (C11) ‚Äî `strerror` is not required to avoid data races with other calls. (Sentence new in C11.) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.24.6.2p3 ‚Äî Behaves as if no library function calls `strerror`; the array shall not be modified by the program but may be overwritten by a later `strerror`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.2p4 ‚Äî Returns: pointer to the string, contents of which are locale-specific. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.24.6.3 / ¬ß7.21.6.3 The strlen function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t strlen(const char *s);` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.3p2 ‚Äî `strlen` computes the length of the string pointed to by `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.6.3p3 ‚Äî Returns: number of characters that precede the terminating null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`strlen("hello")==5` verified)

#### Added: declarations/macros expected in `<string.h>` (presence checks)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.24.1p1 (added) ‚Äî `<string.h>` shall make `size_t` available without dragging in extra `<stddef.h>` macros; on mcc this is satisfied by the glibc header (it includes `<bits/types.h>`/defines `__size_t`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
