- [‚úì] ¬ß7.1.3 (added) ‚Äî All `<string.h>` identifiers above are reserved; redeclaring them with a different signature is a constraint violation only in strict modes ‚Äî all three accept the standard prototypes from the glibc header. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] (added) ‚Äî POSIX/glibc extras visible through this glibc header (`strdup`, `strndup`, `strtok_r`, `memccpy`, `stpcpy`, `strsep`, `strnlen`, `memmem`, `strcasecmp`‚Ä¶) are **not** ISO C99/C11 and appear only under the appropriate `_*_SOURCE` feature-test macros; their availability is identical across mcc/gcc/clang since all use the same header. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (not a C99/C11 requirement)

#### Annex K ¬ßK.3.7 Bounds-checking interfaces in `<string.h>` (C11, optional)

> C11 Annex K is conditional and normatively optional; an implementation defines `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` only if it provides these. mcc/gcc/clang on Linux do **not** define it (verified: `#ifdef __STDC_LIB_EXT1__` is false under all three), so none of `<string.h>`'s `_s` functions are required of mcc.

- [ ] ¬ßK.3.7 (C11, optional) ‚Äî When `__STDC_WANT_LIB_EXT1__` is defined by the program and `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` by the implementation, `<string.h>` additionally declares `errno_t`, `rsize_t` and `memcpy_s`, `memmove_s`, `strcpy_s`, `strncpy_s`, `strcat_s`, `strncat_s`, `memset_s`, `strtok_s`, `strerror_s`, `strerrorlen_s`, `strnlen_s`, each with runtime-constraint handling (¬ßK.3.7.1‚Äì¬ßK.3.7.4). ‚Äî mcc:n/a gcc:n/a clang:n/a (`__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` undefined on all three; optional, not required)

### ¬ß7.25 / ¬ß7.22 Type-generic math `<tgmath.h>`

> C11 adds no new macros relative to C99 here; the macro set and selection rules are identical between editions. `<tgmath.h>` is hosted-only and relies on generic-selection semantics; mcc's bundled `runtime/include/tgmath.h` builds the macros on the C11 `_Generic` keyword (and `__real__`/`__imag__` for the complex extractors).

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p1 / ¬ß7.22p1 ‚Äî `<tgmath.h>` shall include the headers `<math.h>` and `<complex.h>` and shall define several type-generic macros. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc's `tgmath.h` `#include`s `<math.h>`, `<complex.h>`, `<float.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p2 / ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî For each unsuffixed `<math.h>`/`<complex.h>` function with a `double` corresponding-real-type generic parameter, **except `modf`**, there is a corresponding type-generic macro; the `double`-real-type parameters are the *generic parameters*. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`modf` is **not** redefined as a macro by mcc ‚Äî verified the macro family omits it)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p2 / ¬ß7.22p2 ‚Äî Use of a type-generic macro invokes a function whose corresponding real type and type domain are determined by the argument types of the generic parameters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified via `sizeof` of the selected return type)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p2 (footnote) ‚Äî `modf` is excepted because its second parameter is `double *`, whose argument type cannot be varied generically; the macro family does not include `modf`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (no `modf` macro defined in any of the three `<tgmath.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p3 / ¬ß7.22p3 ‚Äî Real-type rule: any `long double` generic arg ‚Üí real type `long double`; otherwise any `double` *or integer* generic arg ‚Üí `double` (integers treated as `double`); otherwise (all `float`) ‚Üí `float`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`exp(n)`‚Üídouble, `acosh(f)`‚Üí`acoshf`, `atan(ld)`‚Üí`atanl` all verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p4 / ¬ß7.22p4 ‚Äî Type-domain rule: any complex generic arg ‚Üí the corresponding complex function (where it exists); otherwise the real function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`log(fc)`‚Üí`clogf`, `sqrt(dc)`‚Üí`csqrt` verified)

#### ¬ß7.25p5 / ¬ß7.22p5 Macros with both a real (`<math.h>`) and a complex (`<complex.h>`) function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p5 / ¬ß7.22p5 ‚Äî For each unsuffixed `<math.h>` function with a `c`-prefixed `<complex.h>` counterpart, the type-generic macro has the same name as the `<math.h>` function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p5 / ¬ß7.22p5 ‚Äî The dual-domain macros are exactly `acos asin atan acosh asinh atanh cos sin tan cosh sinh tanh exp log pow sqrt fabs` (paired with `cacos‚Ä¶cabs`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all 17 defined in mcc's `tgmath.h` via `__tgmath_rc`/`__tgmath_rc2`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p5 / ¬ß7.22p5 ‚Äî A complex argument invokes the `c`-prefixed function of the selected real type; a real argument invokes the real `<math.h>` function of the selected real type. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`pow(ldc,f)`‚Üí`cpowl` (32-byte ld complex) verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p5 / ¬ß7.22p5 ‚Äî The `fabs`/`cabs` pairing: a real argument ‚Üí `fabsf`/`fabs`/`fabsl`; a complex argument ‚Üí `cabsf`/`cabs`/`cabsl` (which return the **real** magnitude). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`fabs(fc)`‚Üí4 bytes `cabsf`, `fabs(dc)`‚Üí8 bytes `cabs`, `fabs(ld)`‚Üí16 bytes `fabsl` verified)

#### ¬ß7.25p6 / ¬ß7.22p6 Macros with only a real (`<math.h>`) function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p6 / ¬ß7.22p6 ‚Äî For each unsuffixed `<math.h>` function without a `c`-prefixed counterpart (other than `modf`), the type-generic macro has the same name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p6 / ¬ß7.22p6 ‚Äî The real-only macros are exactly `atan2 cbrt ceil copysign erf erfc exp2 expm1 fdim floor fma fmax fmin fmod frexp hypot ilogb ldexp lgamma llrint llround log10 log1p log2 logb lrint lround nearbyint nextafter nexttoward remainder remquo rint round scalbn scalbln tgamma trunc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all 38 defined in mcc's `tgmath.h`)
- ¬ß7.25p6 / ¬ß7.22p6 ‚Äî Use of one of these real-only macros with any complex argument results in undefined behavior. ‚Äî (UB; not separately testable ‚Äî `ceil(fc)`/`rint(dc)` are UB)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p6 / ¬ß7.22p6 (non-generic parameters) ‚Äî Parameters not of corresponding real type `double` do not participate in type determination: the integer exponent of `ldexp`/`scalbn` (and the `long` of `scalbln`), the `int *` of `frexp`, the `int *` of `remquo`, and the `long double` second argument of `nexttoward`. ‚Äî **mcc:‚úì** gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì ‚Äî `ldexp`/`scalbn`/`scalbln`/`frexp` correctly key only on the first arg (`__tgmath_real_2_1` uses `_Generic((x),‚Ä¶)`); `remquo` correctly keys on `(x)+(y)`; and `nexttoward` keys only on `x`, so its `long double` second argument is non-generic ‚Äî matching gcc/clang.

##### Added gap: `nexttoward` second argument is wrongly generic (mcc)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p6 / ¬ß7.22p6 (gap) ‚Äî `nexttoward(x, y)`'s second parameter has type `long double` and is **non-generic**; only `x` determines the selected function. mcc defines `#define nexttoward(x,y) __tgmath_real_2_1(x,y,nexttoward)`, i.e. `_Generic((x), ‚Ä¶)` keyed on `x` only, so the `long double` second argument does not affect selection: `nexttoward(f, ld)` selects **`nexttowardf`** (returns `float`, `sizeof`=4), matching the standard and gcc/clang. ‚Äî **mcc:‚úì** gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three select `nexttowardf`).

#### ¬ß7.25p7 / ¬ß7.22p7 Macros with only a complex (`<complex.h>`) function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p7 / ¬ß7.22p7 ‚Äî For each unsuffixed `<complex.h>` function that is not a `c`-prefixed counterpart to a `<math.h>` function, the type-generic macro has the same name. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`carg`/`conj`/`cproj` are type-generic in mcc via `__tgmath_cx`; `creal`/`cimag` are type-generic too via `_Generic`, matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p7 / ¬ß7.22p7 ‚Äî The complex-only macros are exactly `carg cimag conj cproj creal`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`carg`,`conj`,`cproj`,`creal`,`cimag` are all genuine type-generic tgmath macros, matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p7 / ¬ß7.22p7 ‚Äî Use of these macros with a real argument is well-defined: the real argument is regarded as complex with `+0` imaginary part and the complex function of the selected real type is invoked (`creal(x)` of real `x` yields `x`, `cimag(x)` yields `+0`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`creal(d)`‚Üídouble 8 bytes; value correct)

##### Added gap: `creal`/`cimag` are not type-generic in mcc (precision)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p7 / ¬ß7.22p7 (gap) ‚Äî As tgmath macros, `creal`/`cimag` must select `crealf`/`cimagf` (return `float`) for a `float complex` argument and `creall`/`cimagl` (return `long double`) for a `long double complex` argument. mcc's `tgmath.h` redefines them with `_Generic` ‚Äî `#define creal(z) _Generic((z), float _Complex: crealf(z), long double _Complex: creall(z), default: (__real__(double _Complex)(z)))` (and the parallel `cimag`) ‚Äî so `creal(ldc)` ‚Üí mcc `sizeof`=16 (`creall`, full precision) and `cimag(fc)` ‚Üí mcc `sizeof`=4 (`cimagf`), matching gcc/clang. ‚Äî **mcc:‚úì** gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `creal(ldc)`=16, `cimag(fc)`=4; gcc/clang: 16 and 4).

#### ¬ß7.25p8 / ¬ß7.22p8 Examples and overall behavior

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p8 / ¬ß7.22p8 (example) ‚Äî Resolution table: `exp(n)`‚Üídouble; `acosh(f)`‚Üí`acoshf`; `sin(d)`‚Üí`sin`; `atan(ld)`‚Üí`atanl`; `log(fc)`‚Üí`clogf`; `sqrt(dc)`‚Üí`csqrt`; `pow(ldc,f)`‚Üí`cpowl`; `remainder(n,n)`‚Üídouble; `nextafter(d,f)`‚Üí`nextafter`; `nexttoward(f,ld)`‚Üí`nexttowardf`; `copysign(n,ld)`‚Üí`copysignl`; `ceil(fc)`/`rint(dc)`‚ÜíUB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all rows verified equal across the three, including `nexttoward(f,ld)` ‚Üí `nexttowardf`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25 / ¬ß7.22 (general) ‚Äî A type-generic macro selects, for the determined real type and type domain, exactly the suffixed library function the standard would otherwise name (`f`/`l` suffix; `c`-prefix in the complex domain), so an unsuffixed call need not be written manually. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (holds for all macros, including `nexttoward`, `creal`, and `cimag`)

#### Added: `<tgmath.h>` structural checks

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p1 (added) ‚Äî `<tgmath.h>` is a no-op under C++ (`#ifndef __cplusplus`) ‚Äî mcc guards the macro body, matching gcc/clang where `<tgmath.h>` is similarly disabled/handled for C++. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (not a C99/C11 hosted-C requirement, but structurally present)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25 (added) ‚Äî `<tgmath.h>` correctly handles ABIs where `long double == double` (e.g. AArch64 Mach-O): mcc folds the duplicate `long double` `_Generic` arm into `default` to avoid an "two compatible types" ill-formed `_Generic` (`#if LDBL_MANT_DIG == DBL_MANT_DIG`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (target-portability hardening; verified present in header)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.25p2 (added) ‚Äî Each generic macro is usable in a parenthesized form only as a macro (no function-pointer access to a "tgmath function"); taking the address of a tgmath macro is not required by the standard and is not supported by any of the three (macros expand to a `_Generic` call expression). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (consistent)


## ¬ß7.25-¬ß7.27 threads(C11)/time

> mcc status: 165 TODO checkboxes in this section; 9 are mcc-gaps. The two former hard BUGs are fixed ‚Äî mcc's bundled `<threads.h>` now defines the `thread_local` macro (expanding to `_Thread_local`) and `TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS` expands to an integer constant expression, both matching gcc/clang. The remaining gaps are 8 `~` and 1 `‚úó`: (a) shim-signature divergences (`cnd_timedwait`/`mtx_timedlock` lack `restrict`; `thrd_exit` lacks `_Noreturn`; `thrd_sleep` signature/return, ¬ß7.26.x); (b) three C11-mode-gating divergences for `TIME_UTC`/`timespec_get`/`struct timespec` that need `-std=c11` because mcc defaults to C99 while gcc/clang default to C23 (¬ß7.27.x); and (c) the root-cause `‚úó` that mcc's bundled `<threads.h>` activates its pthread shim instead of delegating to glibc. Every `thrd_*`/`mtx_*`/`cnd_*`/`tss_*`/`call_once` symbol compiles, links (`-pthread`) and runs identically on all three; all of `<time.h>` is the shared glibc runtime and conforms identically on all three.

> **Clause-number note.** In **C11 (N1570)** `<threads.h>` is **¬ß7.26** and `<time.h>` is **¬ß7.27**. In **C99 (N1256)** there is no `<threads.h>`, and `<time.h>` is **¬ß7.23**. All `<threads.h>` material and the `struct timespec` / `timespec_get` / `TIME_UTC` items are **(C11)** additions; the rest of `<time.h>` is common to C99 and C11. Citations below use the C11 numbers, with the C99 number for `<time.h>` given in parentheses. (There is no ¬ß7.25 in this range ‚Äî N1570 ¬ß7.25 is `<threads.h>`'s predecessor numbering; the standard places threads at ¬ß7.26.)
>
> **Implementation status summary (this section):**
> - **mcc:** bundles `runtime/include/threads.h` ‚Äî a thin conforming shim over POSIX `pthreads` (`thrd_t=pthread_t`, `mtx_t=pthread_mutex_t`, `cnd_t=pthread_cond_t`, `tss_t=pthread_key_t`, `once_flag=pthread_once_t`). All `thrd_*`/`mtx_*`/`cnd_*`/`tss_*`/`call_once` symbols compile and link; `thrd_create`+`thrd_join` round-trips the worker's `int` result correctly (verified res=42). mcc does **not** define `__STDC_NO_THREADS__` (it claims thread support).
>   - **Root-cause (mcc, verified):** under mcc, `#include <threads.h>` resolves to the **bundled shim**, *not* glibc's `/usr/include/threads.h` ‚Äî proven by the `PTHREAD_DESTRUCTOR_ITERATIONS`-undeclared diagnostic, a token that exists only in the shim. (The header's `__has_include_next`/`ONCE_FLAG_INIT` guard is intended to delegate to the system header, but as mcc is actually invoked the shim wins, which is what surfaces the two BUGs below.)
>   - **BUG (mcc):** `TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS` is `#define`d to `PTHREAD_DESTRUCTOR_ITERATIONS`, which is not visible as an integer constant expression under mcc's glibc preprocessing ‚Üí `int n = TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS;` fails with "`PTHREAD_DESTRUCTOR_ITERATIONS` undeclared". Violates ¬ß7.26.1p3 (must expand to an ICE). *(verified: error on both `int arr[TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS];` and `int n = TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS;`; gcc/clang accept.)*
>   - **BUG (mcc):** the bundled `<threads.h>` never defines the `thread_local` macro, so `thread_local int x;` fails ("warning: type defaults to int" then a hard parse failure) even though the underlying `_Thread_local` keyword works. Violates ¬ß7.26.1p3 (must expand to `_Thread_local`). *(verified: mcc emits "type defaults to int"; gcc/clang compile clean.)*
>   - **Note (mcc):** `<time.h>` is not bundled ‚Äî delegated to the system header. mcc's default language mode is **C99** (`__STDC_VERSION__ == 199901L`), so glibc gates `TIME_UTC`, `timespec_get`, and `struct timespec` behind C11; under mcc default they fail (`'TIME_UTC' undeclared`, implicit-decl of `timespec_get`). With `-std=c11` all three work (`timespec_get(&ts,TIME_UTC)==TIME_UTC` and `TIME_UTC==1` verified).
> - **gcc 15 / clang 22:** full `<threads.h>` and `<time.h>` via glibc; `timespec_get`, `TIME_UTC`, `struct timespec` all present by default (their default mode is C23, so no feature-macro gating is needed).

### ¬ß7.26 Threads `<threads.h>` (C11)

> C99-only readers: this entire `<threads.h>` subsection is **new in C11**; C99 has no standard threading header.

#### ¬ß7.26.1 Introduction (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p1 ‚Äî (C11) The header `<threads.h>` shall define macros and declare types, enumeration constants, and functions that support multiple threads of execution. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) An implementation that defines the macro `__STDC_NO_THREADS__` need not provide `<threads.h>` nor support any of its facilities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified: `__STDC_NO_THREADS__` is **not** defined by any of the three ‚Äî full support claimed.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) The macro `thread_local` shall expand to `_Thread_local`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc's bundled `<threads.h>` defines `thread_local` as `_Thread_local`, so `thread_local int x;` compiles, matching gcc/clang.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) The macro `ONCE_FLAG_INIT` shall expand to a value that can be used to initialize an object of type `once_flag`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `#define ONCE_FLAG_INIT PTHREAD_ONCE_INIT`; `once_flag f=ONCE_FLAG_INIT;` compiles+runs.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) The macro `TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS` shall expand to an integer constant expression representing the maximum number of times that destructors will be called when a thread terminates. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc's `TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS` expands to an integer constant expression, so `int arr[TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS];` compiles, matching gcc/clang.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `cnd_t` shall be a complete object type that holds an identifier for a condition variable. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef pthread_cond_t cnd_t;`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `thrd_t` shall be a complete object type that holds an identifier for a thread. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef pthread_t thrd_t;`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `tss_t` shall be a complete object type that holds an identifier for a thread-specific storage pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef pthread_key_t tss_t;`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `mtx_t` shall be a complete object type that holds an identifier for a mutex. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef pthread_mutex_t mtx_t;`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `tss_dtor_t` shall be the function pointer type `void (*)(void*)`, used as a destructor for a thread-specific storage pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef void (*tss_dtor_t)(void *);`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `thrd_start_t` shall be the function pointer type `int (*)(void*)` that is passed to `thrd_create` to create a new thread. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef int (*thrd_start_t)(void *);`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) The type `once_flag` shall be a complete object type that holds a flag for use by `call_once`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `typedef pthread_once_t once_flag;`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `mtx_plain` shall be a value passed to `mtx_init` to create a mutex object that supports neither timeout nor test-and-return. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified mtx_plain=0 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `mtx_recursive` shall be a value passed to `mtx_init` to create a mutex object that supports recursive locking. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified mtx_recursive=1 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `mtx_timed` shall be a value passed to `mtx_init` to create a mutex object that supports timeout. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified mtx_timed=2 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `thrd_timedout` shall be returned by a timed wait function to indicate that the time specified in the call was reached without acquiring the requested resource. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified thrd_timedout=4 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `thrd_success` shall be returned by a function to indicate that the requested operation succeeded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified thrd_success=0 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `thrd_busy` shall be returned by a function to indicate that the requested operation failed because a resource requested by a test-and-return function is already in use. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified thrd_busy=1 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `thrd_error` shall be returned by a function to indicate that the requested operation failed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified thrd_error=2 on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.1p5 ‚Äî (C11) The enumeration constant `thrd_nomem` shall be returned by a function to indicate that the requested operation failed because it was unable to allocate memory. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified enum values identical across all three: `thrd_success=0, thrd_busy=1, thrd_error=2, thrd_nomem=3, thrd_timedout=4`; `mtx_plain=0, mtx_recursive=1, mtx_timed=2`.)*

#### ¬ß7.26.2 Initialization functions (C11)

##### ¬ß7.26.2.1 The `call_once` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.2.1p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `#include <threads.h>` / `void call_once(once_flag *flag, void (*func)(void));`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: thin wrapper over `pthread_once`; signature matches.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.2.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) The `call_once` function shall use the `once_flag` pointed to by `flag` to ensure `func` is called exactly once, the first time `call_once` is called with that value of `flag`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(semantics provided by `pthread_once`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.2.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) Completion of an effective call to `call_once` shall synchronize with all subsequent calls to `call_once` with the same value of `flag`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ordering guarantee via `pthread_once`; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.2.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `call_once` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(declared `void`.)*

#### ¬ß7.26.3 Condition variable functions (C11)

##### ¬ß7.26.3.1 The `cnd_broadcast` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.1p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `#include <threads.h>` / `int cnd_broadcast(cnd_t *cond);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.26.3.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_broadcast` shall unblock all of the threads that are blocked on the condition variable pointed to by `cond` at the time of the call. ‚Äî (spec; runtime semantics via `pthread_cond_broadcast`; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) If no threads are blocked on `cond` at the time of the call, `cnd_broadcast` shall do nothing. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `cnd_broadcast` returns `thrd_success` on success, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc maps `pthread_cond_broadcast` rc to thrd_success/thrd_error.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.3.2 The `cnd_destroy` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `void cnd_destroy(cnd_t *cond);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.26.3.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_destroy` shall release all resources used by the condition variable pointed to by `cond`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_destroy` requires that no threads be blocked waiting for the condition variable pointed to by `cond`. ‚Äî (spec; precondition/UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.2p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `cnd_destroy` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(declared `void`.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.3.3 The `cnd_init` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.3p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int cnd_init(cnd_t *cond);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_init` shall create a condition variable. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified compile+run.)*
- ¬ß7.26.3.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) If it succeeds, `cnd_init` shall set the variable pointed to by `cond` to a value that uniquely identifies the newly created condition variable. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ß7.26.3.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `cnd_init` returns `thrd_success` on success, `thrd_nomem` if no memory could be allocated for the newly created condition, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ *(all three map `pthread_cond_init` rc to thrd_error on failure; none distinguishes `thrd_nomem` ‚Äî a benign conformance latitude shared by the shim and glibc.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.3.4 The `cnd_signal` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int cnd_signal(cnd_t *cond);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.26.3.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_signal` shall unblock one of the threads that are blocked on the condition variable pointed to by `cond` at the time of the call (if any threads are blocked). ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) If no threads are blocked on `cond` at the time of the call, `cnd_signal` shall do nothing and return success. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.4p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `cnd_signal` returns `thrd_success` on success, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.3.5 The `cnd_timedwait` function (C11)
- [~] ¬ß7.26.3.5p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int cnd_timedwait(cnd_t *restrict cond, mtx_t *restrict mtx, const struct timespec *restrict ts);`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc shim signature `(cnd_t*, mtx_t*, const struct timespec*)` lacks `restrict` qualifiers; still callable, but needs `-std=c11` for `struct timespec` visibility.)*
- ¬ß7.26.3.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_timedwait` shall atomically unlock the mutex pointed to by `mtx` and endeavor to block until the condition variable pointed to by `cond` is signaled by `cnd_signal`/`cnd_broadcast`, or until after the `TIME_UTC`-based calendar time pointed to by `ts`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) When the calling thread becomes unblocked it shall lock the mutex pointed to by `mtx` before it returns. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_timedwait` requires that the mutex pointed to by `mtx` be locked by the calling thread. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `cnd_timedwait` returns `thrd_success` upon success, `thrd_timedout` if the time specified in the call was reached without acquiring the requested resource, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc maps `ETIMEDOUT`‚Üí`thrd_timedout`, else error/success.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.3.6 The `cnd_wait` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.6p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int cnd_wait(cnd_t *cond, mtx_t *mtx);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.26.3.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_wait` shall atomically unlock the mutex pointed to by `mtx` and endeavor to block until the condition variable pointed to by `cond` is signaled by `cnd_signal`/`cnd_broadcast`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) When the calling thread becomes unblocked it shall lock the mutex pointed to by `mtx` before it returns. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.3.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) `cnd_wait` requires that the mutex pointed to by `mtx` be locked by the calling thread. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.3.6p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `cnd_wait` returns `thrd_success` on success or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.26.4 Mutex functions (C11)

##### ¬ß7.26.4.1 The `mtx_destroy` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.1p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `void mtx_destroy(mtx_t *mtx);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_destroy` shall release any resources used by the mutex pointed to by `mtx`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified compile+run.)*
- ¬ß7.26.4.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) No threads can be blocked waiting for the mutex pointed to by `mtx`. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `mtx_destroy` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(declared `void`.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.4.2 The `mtx_init` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int mtx_init(mtx_t *mtx, int type);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_init` shall create a mutex object with properties indicated by `type`, which must have one of these **four** values: `mtx_plain` (plain, non-recursive); `mtx_timed` (non-recursive, supporting timeout); `mtx_plain | mtx_recursive` (recursive); `mtx_timed | mtx_recursive` (recursive, supporting timeout). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc shim honors `mtx_recursive` via `PTHREAD_MUTEX_RECURSIVE`; verified `mtx_plain` and `mtx_timed` init+lock+unlock.)*
- ¬ß7.26.4.2p3 ‚Äî (C11) If `mtx_init` succeeds, it shall set the mutex pointed to by `mtx` to a value that uniquely identifies the newly created mutex. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.2p4 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `mtx_init` returns `thrd_success` on success, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.4.3 The `mtx_lock` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.3p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int mtx_lock(mtx_t *mtx);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_lock` shall block until it locks the mutex pointed to by `mtx`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified lock/unlock round-trip.)*
- ¬ß7.26.4.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) If the mutex is non-recursive it shall not already be locked by the calling thread. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.4.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) Prior calls to `mtx_unlock` on the same mutex shall synchronize with this operation. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ordering; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `mtx_lock` returns `thrd_success` on success, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.4.4 The `mtx_timedlock` function (C11)
- [~] ¬ß7.26.4.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int mtx_timedlock(mtx_t *restrict mtx, const struct timespec *restrict ts);`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc shim signature lacks `restrict`; compiles+links under `-std=c11`. On Linux mcc approximates with a trylock-spin, not `pthread_mutex_timedlock` ‚Äî a portability shim for macOS, semantically conforming.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_timedlock` shall endeavor to block until it locks the mutex pointed to by `mtx` or until after the `TIME_UTC`-based calendar time pointed to by `ts`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc spin honors the absolute deadline via `clock_gettime(CLOCK_REALTIME)`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.4.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) The specified mutex shall support timeout (i.e., was created `mtx_timed` or `mtx_timed | mtx_recursive`). ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.4.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) If the operation succeeds, prior calls to `mtx_unlock` on the same mutex shall synchronize with this operation. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ordering; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.4p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `mtx_timedlock` returns `thrd_success` on success, `thrd_timedout` if the time specified was reached without acquiring the requested resource, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.4.5 The `mtx_trylock` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.5p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int mtx_trylock(mtx_t *mtx);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_trylock` shall endeavor to lock the mutex pointed to by `mtx`; if the mutex is already locked, the function shall return without blocking. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc maps `EBUSY`‚Üí`thrd_busy`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.4.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) If the operation succeeds, prior calls to `mtx_unlock` on the same mutex shall synchronize with this operation. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ordering; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.4.5p3 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_trylock` may spuriously fail to lock an unused resource, in which case it returns `thrd_busy` (an implementation may, but is not required to, behave this way). ‚Äî (spec; optional behavior; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.5p4 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `mtx_trylock` returns `thrd_success` on success, `thrd_busy` if the resource requested is already in use, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.4.6 The `mtx_unlock` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.6p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int mtx_unlock(mtx_t *mtx);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) `mtx_unlock` shall unlock the mutex pointed to by `mtx`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified lock/unlock round-trip.)*
- ¬ß7.26.4.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) The mutex pointed to by `mtx` shall be locked by the calling thread. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.4.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) The `mtx_unlock` operation shall synchronize with subsequent operations that lock the same mutex. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ordering; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.4.6p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `mtx_unlock` returns `thrd_success` on success or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.26.5 Thread functions (C11)

##### ¬ß7.26.5.1 The `thrd_create` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.1p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int thrd_create(thrd_t *thr, thrd_start_t func, void *arg);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_create` shall create a new thread executing `func(arg)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: malloc'd trampoline forwards func/arg into `pthread_create`; verified runs.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) If `thrd_create` succeeds, it shall set the object pointed to by `thr` to the identifier of the newly created thread. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified ‚Äî `thrd_create`+`thrd_join` returns the worker's value (res=42) on all three.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî (C11) A program that has more than one thread (i.e., has invoked `thrd_create` at least once) does not regard the completion of `func` as undefined behavior; returning from `func` shall have the same effect as calling `thrd_exit` with the return value of `func`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc trampoline returns `(void*)(intptr_t)func(arg)`, matching thrd_exit semantics; verified result round-trip.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_create` returns `thrd_success` on success, `thrd_nomem` if no memory could be allocated for the thread requested, or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc returns `thrd_nomem` on the trampoline-alloc `malloc` failure and on `pthread_create` failure `thrd_error`.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.5.2 The `thrd_current` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `thrd_t thrd_current(void);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_current` shall identify the thread that called it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `return pthread_self();`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.2p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_current` returns the identifier of the thread that called it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified compile+call.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.5.3 The `thrd_detach` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.3p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int thrd_detach(thrd_t thr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_detach` shall tell the operating system to dispose of any resources allocated to the thread identified by `thr` when that thread terminates. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_detach`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.5.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) The thread identified by `thr` shall not have been previously detached or joined with another thread. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_detach` returns `thrd_success` on success or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.5.4 The `thrd_equal` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int thrd_equal(thrd_t thr0, thrd_t thr1);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_equal` shall determine whether the thread identified by `thr0` refers to the thread identified by `thr1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_equal`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.4p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_equal` returns zero if `thr0` and `thr1` refer to different threads; otherwise it returns a nonzero value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.4p2 (footnote, C11) ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_equal(thrd_current(), thrd_current())` is required to return nonzero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(NEW; `pthread_equal(self,self)` is nonzero on all three.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.5.5 The `thrd_exit` function (C11)
- [~] ¬ß7.26.5.5p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `_Noreturn void thrd_exit(int res);`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(NEW divergence: mcc's shim declares `thrd_exit` without `_Noreturn` (`static inline void thrd_exit(int)`), whereas glibc marks it `__attribute__((__noreturn__))`. Functionally `pthread_exit` does not return; the missing attribute only loses a UB/dead-code diagnostic. Both link+run.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) For every thread-specific storage key which was created with a non-null destructor and for which the value is non-null, `thrd_exit` shall set the value associated with the key to a null pointer value and then invoke the destructor with the previous value of the key. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(provided by `pthread_exit` TSD-destructor machinery.)*
- ¬ß7.26.5.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) The order in which destructors are invoked is unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.5.5p3 ‚Äî (C11) If, after this, there remain keys with both non-null destructors and non-null values, the implementation shall repeat this process up to `TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS` times. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.5p4 ‚Äî (C11) Following this, `thrd_exit` shall terminate execution of the calling thread and set its result code to `res`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified via join result round-trip.)*
- ¬ß7.26.5.5p5 ‚Äî (C11) The program shall terminate normally after the last thread has been terminated; the behavior shall be as if the program called `exit` with the status `EXIT_SUCCESS` at thread-termination time. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.5p6 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_exit` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(declared `void`, does not return.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.5.6 The `thrd_join` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.6p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int thrd_join(thrd_t thr, int *res);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_join` shall join the thread identified by `thr` with the current thread by blocking until the other thread has terminated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_join`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) If `res` is not a null pointer, `thrd_join` shall store the thread's result code in the integer pointed to by `res`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified res=42 stored.)*
- ¬ß7.26.5.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) The termination of the other thread shall synchronize with the completion of `thrd_join`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime ordering; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.5.6p2 ‚Äî (C11) The thread identified by `thr` shall not have been previously detached or joined with another thread. ‚Äî (spec; precondition; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.6p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_join` returns `thrd_success` on success or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.5.7 The `thrd_sleep` function (C11)
- [~] ¬ß7.26.5.7p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int thrd_sleep(const struct timespec *duration, struct timespec *remaining);`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `return nanosleep(dur,rem);` ‚Äî needs `-std=c11` for `struct timespec`; signature matches.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.7p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_sleep` shall suspend execution of the calling thread until either the interval specified by `duration` has elapsed or a signal which is not being ignored is received. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(via `nanosleep`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.7p3 ‚Äî (C11) If interrupted by a signal and `remaining` is non-null, the amount of time remaining (the requested interval minus the time actually slept) shall be stored in the interval it points to. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(`nanosleep` populates `rem`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.5.7p3 ‚Äî (C11) The `duration` and `remaining` arguments may point to the same object. ‚Äî (spec; allowed aliasing; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.5.7p4 ‚Äî (C11) The suspension time may be longer than requested ... but, except for the case of being interrupted by a signal, the suspension time shall not be less than that specified, as measured by the system clock `TIME_UTC`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime timing; not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ß7.26.5.7p5 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_sleep` returns zero if the requested time has elapsed, `-1` if it has been interrupted by a signal, or a negative value if it fails. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(NEW divergence: mcc returns `nanosleep`'s raw value ‚Äî `0` on success, `-1` with `errno` on interrupt/failure ‚Äî which conflates the "interrupted (-1)" and "other failure (some negative)" distinction the way glibc's own thrd_sleep does; both behave the same here, conforming for the `TIME_UTC` interrupt path.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.5.8 The `thrd_yield` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.8p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `void thrd_yield(void);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.8p2 ‚Äî (C11) `thrd_yield` shall endeavor to permit other threads to run, even if the current thread would ordinarily continue to run. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `sched_yield`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.5.8p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `thrd_yield` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(declared `void`.)*

#### ¬ß7.26.6 Thread-specific storage functions (C11)

##### ¬ß7.26.6.1 The `tss_create` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.1p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int tss_create(tss_t *key, tss_dtor_t dtor);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) `tss_create` shall create a thread-specific storage pointer with destructor `dtor`, which may be null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_key_create`; verified create+set+get+delete.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) If `tss_create` is successful, it shall set the thread-specific storage pointed to by `key` to a value that uniquely identifies the newly created pointer and return `thrd_success`; otherwise `thrd_error` shall be returned and the thread-specific storage pointed to by `key` shall be set to an undefined value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.26.6.1p3 (footnote) ‚Äî (C11) A call to `tss_create` from within a thread-specific storage destructor results in undefined behavior. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.1p4 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `tss_create` returns `thrd_success` on success or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.6.2 The `tss_delete` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.2p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `void tss_delete(tss_t key);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) `tss_delete` shall release any resources used by the thread-specific storage identified by `key`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_key_delete`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.6.2p2 ‚Äî (C11) Calling `tss_delete` will not result in the invocation of any destructors, even for thread-specific data created prior to the call. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.2p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `tss_delete` returns no value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(declared `void`.)*

##### ¬ß7.26.6.3 The `tss_get` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.3p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `void *tss_get(tss_t key);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.3p2 ‚Äî (C11) `tss_get` shall return the value for the current thread held in the thread-specific storage identified by `key`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_getspecific`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.6.3p2 (footnote) ‚Äî (C11) A call to `tss_get` from within a thread-specific storage destructor results in undefined behavior. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.3p3 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `tss_get` returns the value for the current thread if successful, or zero (null) if unsuccessful. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.26.6.4 The `tss_set` function (C11)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.4p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int tss_set(tss_t key, void *val);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.4p2 ‚Äî (C11) `tss_set` shall set the value for the current thread held in the thread-specific storage identified by `key` to `val`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(mcc: `pthread_setspecific`.)*
- ¬ß7.26.6.4p2 (footnote) ‚Äî (C11) A call to `tss_set` from within a thread-specific storage destructor results in undefined behavior. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.26.6.4p3 ‚Äî (C11) `tss_set` shall not invoke the destructor associated with the key on the value being replaced. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26.6.4p4 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: `tss_set` returns `thrd_success` on success or `thrd_error` if the request could not be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

#### ¬ß7.26 ‚Äî additional/structural items (NEW)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.26 (link requirement) ‚Äî All `thrd_*`/`mtx_*`/`cnd_*`/`tss_*`/`call_once` facilities are backed by POSIX threads; programs must link with `-pthread` (or `-lpthread`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(NEW; identical requirement on all three on this glibc; verified link with `-pthread`.)*
- [‚úó] ¬ß7.26.1p3 (mcc root-cause) ‚Äî Under mcc, `#include <threads.h>` resolves to the **bundled pthread shim**, not glibc's `<threads.h>`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó gcc:n/a clang:n/a *(NEW; this is the direct cause of the `thread_local` and `TSS_DTOR_ITERATIONS` failures ‚Äî gcc/clang always use glibc's header. Confirmed by the `PTHREAD_DESTRUCTOR_ITERATIONS` diagnostic, a shim-only token.)*

### ¬ß7.27 Date and time `<time.h>` (C11 ¬ß7.27 / C99 ¬ß7.23)

> **C99 vs C11.** The body of `<time.h>` is shared. C11 **adds** the `TIME_UTC` macro (¬ß7.27.1p2), the `struct timespec` type (¬ß7.27.1p3), the `timespec_get` function (¬ß7.27.2.5), the data-race wording in ¬ß7.27.3p1, and the out-of-range/year UB sentences in `asctime` (¬ß7.27.3.1p2). The `strftime` conversion specifiers `%C %D %e %F %g %G %h %r %R %t %T %u %V %z` and the `E`/`O` modifiers (¬ß7.27.3.5p3‚Äìp4) were added in **C99** relative to C90. mcc does not bundle `<time.h>`; all three compilers use the same glibc `<time.h>`, so the only mcc-specific divergence is the default-language-mode gating of the three C11 additions (mcc default = C99; gcc/clang default = C23).

#### ¬ß7.27.1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1) Components of time
- ¬ß7.27.1p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p1) ‚Äî The header `<time.h>` shall define two macros and declare several types and functions for manipulating time ... *calendar time* / *local time* / *Daylight Saving Time*. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p2) ‚Äî The macro `NULL` shall be defined as described in ¬ß7.19 (C99 ¬ß7.17). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(glibc `<time.h>` pulls `NULL`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p2) ‚Äî The macro `CLOCKS_PER_SEC` shall expand to an expression with type `clock_t` that is the number per second of the value returned by the `clock` function. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified usable in `clock()/CLOCKS_PER_SEC`.)*
- [~] ¬ß7.27.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) The macro `TIME_UTC` shall expand to an integer constant greater than 0 that designates the UTC time base. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `TIME_UTC==1` under `-std=c11`. mcc default C99 mode: `'TIME_UTC' undeclared` ‚Äî gated off by glibc behind `__STDC_VERSION__ >= 201112L`. gcc/clang default C23 ‚Üí present unconditionally. mcc-gap only at default `-std`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p3) ‚Äî The type `size_t` shall be the unsigned integer type of the result of `sizeof` (declared as in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p3) ‚Äî The types `clock_t` and `time_t` shall be real types capable of representing times. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified usable as arithmetic types.)*
- [~] ¬ß7.27.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) The type `struct timespec` shall hold an interval specified in seconds and nanoseconds. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(present via system `<time.h>`; mcc requires `-std=c11`+. NB inside `<threads.h>` it is visible even in mcc default mode because `<pthread.h>` defines it under its own POSIX feature gate.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p3 ‚Äî (C11) `struct timespec` shall contain at least the members `time_t tv_sec;` and `long tv_nsec;` (`[0, 999999999]`), in that order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(glibc layout; verified `.tv_sec/.tv_nsec` usable under `-std=c11`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p3) ‚Äî The type `struct tm` shall hold the components of a calendar time, called the broken-down time. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.1p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p4) ‚Äî `struct tm` shall contain at least the members, in any order: `tm_sec [0,60]`, `tm_min [0,59]`, `tm_hour [0,23]`, `tm_mday [1,31]`, `tm_mon [0,11]`, `tm_year` (since 1900), `tm_wday [0,6]`, `tm_yday [0,365]`, `tm_isdst`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified all members assignable + `asctime` round-trip "Wed Jan  1 13:02:03 1997".)*
- ¬ß7.27.1p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p4) ‚Äî The value of `tm_isdst` shall be positive if DST is in effect, zero if not, negative if unavailable. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.1p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.1p4) ‚Äî Range note: `tm_sec` allows `[0, 60]` to accommodate a positive leap second (C99/C11; C90 used `[0,61]`). ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.27.2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2) Time manipulation functions

##### ¬ß7.27.2.1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1) The `clock` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.1p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <time.h>` / `clock_t clock(void);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.27.2.1p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1p2) ‚Äî The `clock` function shall determine the processor time used. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1p3) ‚Äî Returns: best approximation to processor time since an implementation-defined era related only to program invocation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `clock()` callable.)*
- ¬ß7.27.2.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1p3) ‚Äî To determine the time in seconds, divide by `CLOCKS_PER_SEC`. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.2.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1p3) ‚Äî If the processor time used is not available, `clock` returns `(clock_t)(-1)`. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.2.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.1p3) ‚Äî If the value cannot be represented, the function returns an unspecified value. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.27.2.2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.2) The `difftime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.2p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.2p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `double difftime(time_t time1, time_t time0);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.2p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.2p2) ‚Äî Computes `time1 - time0`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified callable.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.2p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.2p3) ‚Äî Returns: the difference expressed in seconds as a `double`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.2.3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3) The `mktime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.3p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `time_t mktime(struct tm *timeptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.3p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3p2) ‚Äî Converts the broken-down local time in `*timeptr` into a calendar time with the same encoding as `time`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.27.2.3p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3p2) ‚Äî The original values of `tm_wday` and `tm_yday` shall be ignored. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.2.3p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3p2) ‚Äî The original values of the other components are not restricted to the ranges in ¬ß7.27.1p4. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.2.3p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3p2) ‚Äî On success, `tm_wday`/`tm_yday` set appropriately, other components forced to range; `tm_mday` not set until `tm_mon`/`tm_year` determined. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.3p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.3p3) ‚Äî Returns: the calendar time as `time_t`, or `(time_t)(-1)` if it cannot be represented. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.2.4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.4) The `time` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.4p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.4p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `time_t time(time_t *timer);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.4p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.4p2) ‚Äî Determines the current calendar time; encoding unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified callable.)*
- ¬ß7.27.2.4p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.4p3) ‚Äî Returns: best approximation to current calendar time; `(time_t)(-1)` if not available. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.4p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.2.4p3) ‚Äî If `timer` is not null, the return value is also assigned to the object it points to. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.2.5 The `timespec_get` function (C11)
- [~] ¬ß7.27.2.5p1 ‚Äî (C11) Synopsis: `int timespec_get(struct timespec *ts, int base);`. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(under `-std=c11` present+functional ‚Äî verified `timespec_get(&ts,TIME_UTC)==TIME_UTC`. mcc default C99 mode: implicit-declaration warning for `timespec_get` and `TIME_UTC` undeclared. gcc/clang default C23 ‚Üí present unconditionally.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.5p2 ‚Äî (C11) Sets `*ts` to the current calendar time for the specified time base. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified under `-std=c11`.)*
- ¬ß7.27.2.5p3 ‚Äî (C11) If `base` is `TIME_UTC`, `tv_sec` = seconds since an implementation-defined epoch (truncated), `tv_nsec` = nanoseconds rounded to clock resolution. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.2.5p3 (footnote) ‚Äî (C11) Available resolution is system dependent and may even be greater than 1 second. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.2.5p4 ‚Äî (C11) Returns: nonzero value `base` on success, zero otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified returns `TIME_UTC`.)*

#### ¬ß7.27.3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3) Time conversion functions
- ¬ß7.27.3p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3p1) ‚Äî Except `strftime`, these functions return a pointer to one of two static objects: a broken-down time structure or an array of `char`. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.3p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3p1) ‚Äî Execution of any of these may overwrite the object of the same type from a previous call. ‚Äî (spec; runtime; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.3p1 ‚Äî (C11) The implementation shall behave as if no other library functions call these functions. ‚Äî (spec; C11 data-race wording; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.27.3.1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.1) The `asctime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.1p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.1p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *asctime(const struct tm *timeptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.1p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.1p2) ‚Äî Converts to the form `Sun Sep 16 01:03:52 1973\n\0` via the specified algorithm. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified identical "Wed Jan  1 13:02:03 1997" on all three.)*
- ¬ß7.27.3.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) If any member is outside its normal range, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.3.1p2 ‚Äî (C11) If the calculated year exceeds four digits or is less than year 1000, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.1p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.1p3) ‚Äî Returns: a pointer to the string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.3.2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.2) The `ctime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.2p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.2p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `char *ctime(const time_t *timer);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.2p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.2p2) ‚Äî Equivalent to `asctime(localtime(timer))`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.2p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.2p3) ‚Äî Returns: the pointer returned by `asctime`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.3.3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.3) The `gmtime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.3p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.3p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `struct tm *gmtime(const time_t *timer);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified callable.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.3p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.3p2) ‚Äî Converts calendar time to broken-down time expressed as UTC. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.3p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.3p3) ‚Äî Returns: a pointer to the broken-down time, or null if it cannot be converted to UTC. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.3.4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.4) The `localtime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.4p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.4p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `struct tm *localtime(const time_t *timer);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.4p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.4p2) ‚Äî Converts calendar time to broken-down time expressed as local time. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.4p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.4p3) ‚Äî Returns: a pointer to the broken-down time, or null if it cannot be converted to local time. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

##### ¬ß7.27.3.5 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5) The `strftime` function
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p1 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p1) ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t strftime(char *restrict s, size_t maxsize, const char *restrict format, const struct tm *restrict timeptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî Places characters into `s` as controlled by `format`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî The format shall be a multibyte character sequence, beginning and ending in its initial shift state. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî The format string shall consist of zero or more conversion specifiers and ordinary multibyte characters. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî A conversion specifier: `%`, optionally `E`/`O`, then a behavior character. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî All ordinary multibyte characters (including the terminating null) shall be copied unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified literal text + `%%` round-trip.)*
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî If copying takes place between objects that overlap, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p2 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p2) ‚Äî No more than `maxsize` characters shall be placed into the array. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p3) ‚Äî Each conversion specifier replaced using `LC_TIME` of the current locale and the bracketed `tm` members. ‚Äî (spec; descriptive; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p3) ‚Äî If any specified value is outside the normal range, the characters stored are unspecified. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%a` ‚Äî abbreviated weekday name. `[tm_wday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%A` ‚Äî full weekday name. `[tm_wday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%b` ‚Äî abbreviated month name. `[tm_mon]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%B` ‚Äî full month name. `[tm_mon]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%c` ‚Äî locale's date and time representation. `[all]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%C` ‚Äî year/100 truncated (00‚Äì99). `[tm_year]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%C`‚Üí`19`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%d` ‚Äî day of month (01‚Äì31). `[tm_mday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%D` ‚Äî `"%m/%d/%y"`. `[tm_mon, tm_mday, tm_year]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%D`‚Üí`01/01/97`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%e` ‚Äî day of month (1‚Äì31), single digit preceded by space. `[tm_mday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%e`‚Üí`" 1"`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%F` ‚Äî `"%Y-%m-%d"` (ISO 8601 date). `[tm_year, tm_mon, tm_mday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%F`‚Üí`1997-01-01`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%g` ‚Äî last 2 digits of week-based year (00‚Äì99). `[tm_year, tm_wday, tm_yday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%G` ‚Äî week-based year (e.g., 1997). `[tm_year, tm_wday, tm_yday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%h` ‚Äî `"%b"`. `[tm_mon]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%h`‚Üí`Jan`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%H` ‚Äî hour, 24-hour (00‚Äì23). `[tm_hour]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%I` ‚Äî hour, 12-hour (01‚Äì12). `[tm_hour]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%j` ‚Äî day of year (001‚Äì366). `[tm_yday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%m` ‚Äî month (01‚Äì12). `[tm_mon]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%M` ‚Äî minute (00‚Äì59). `[tm_min]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%n` ‚Äî a new-line character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%p` ‚Äî locale's AM/PM designation. `[tm_hour]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%r` ‚Äî locale's 12-hour clock time. `[tm_hour, tm_min, tm_sec]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%R` ‚Äî `"%H:%M"`. `[tm_hour, tm_min]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%R`‚Üí`13:02`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%S` ‚Äî second (00‚Äì60). `[tm_sec]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%t` ‚Äî a horizontal-tab character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%T` ‚Äî `"%H:%M:%S"` (ISO 8601 time). `[tm_hour, tm_min, tm_sec]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%T`‚Üí`13:02:03`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%u` ‚Äî ISO 8601 weekday (1‚Äì7), Monday=1. `[tm_wday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified `%u`‚Üí`3`.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%U` ‚Äî week number, first Sunday = week 1 (00‚Äì53). `[tm_year, tm_wday, tm_yday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%V` ‚Äî ISO 8601 week number (01‚Äì53). `[tm_year, tm_wday, tm_yday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%w` ‚Äî weekday (0‚Äì6), Sunday=0. `[tm_wday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%W` ‚Äî week number, first Monday = week 1 (00‚Äì53). `[tm_year, tm_wday, tm_yday]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%x` ‚Äî locale's date representation. `[all]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%X` ‚Äî locale's time representation. `[all]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%y` ‚Äî last 2 digits of year (00‚Äì99). `[tm_year]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%Y` ‚Äî the year as a decimal number. `[tm_year]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî (C99) Conversion specifier `%z` ‚Äî offset from UTC in ISO 8601 (`-0430`), or none if undeterminable. `[tm_isdst]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%Z` ‚Äî locale's time zone name/abbreviation, or none. `[tm_isdst]` ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p3 ‚Äî Conversion specifier `%%` ‚Äî a `%` character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p4) ‚Äî (C99) Some specifiers can be modified by `E`/`O` to indicate an alternative format. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(runtime libc; identical.)*
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p4) ‚Äî (C99) If the alternative format does not exist for the current locale, the modifier shall be ignored. ‚Äî (spec; locale-dependent; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p4) ‚Äî (C99) `%Ec %EC %Ex %EX %Ey %EY` ‚Üí locale's alternative representation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(runtime libc; identical.)*
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p4 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p4) ‚Äî (C99) `%Od %Oe %OH %OI %Om %OM %OS %Ou %OU %OV %Ow %OW %Oy` ‚Üí locale's alternative numeric symbols. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(runtime libc; identical.)*
- ¬ß7.27.3.5p5 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p5) ‚Äî If a conversion specifier is not one of the above, the behavior is undefined. ‚Äî (spec; UB; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.27.3.5p6 (C99 ¬ß7.23.3.5p6) ‚Äî Returns: number of characters placed (excluding the null) if total ‚â§ `maxsize`; otherwise zero and the array contents are indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì *(verified return count + zero-on-overflow behavior identical on all three.)*


## ¬ß7.28-¬ß7.31 uchar(C11)/wchar/wctype

> mcc status: 232 TODO checkboxes in this section; **0 mcc-gaps** (mcc rejects the C11 `u`/`U` character-constant and string-literal prefixes under `-std=c99 -pedantic-errors`, matching gcc and clang). Everything else conforms: mcc supplies the compiler-level pieces ‚Äî the `wchar_t`/`wint_t`/`char16_t`/`char32_t` types, the `u`/`U`/`L` literal prefixes, and the `__STDC_UTF_16__`/`__STDC_UTF_32__` (C11-gated, value `1`), `__STDC_ISO_10646__`, `__CHAR16_TYPE__`/`__CHAR32_TYPE__` predefined macros ‚Äî and delegates the entire `<wchar.h>`/`<wctype.h>`/`<uchar.h>` *runtime* to the host glibc (the bundled `runtime/include/uchar.h` `include_next`-wraps the system header with a C11 freestanding fallback; `<wchar.h>`/`<wctype.h>` are taken verbatim from glibc). Every function below was compiled, linked, **and run** against glibc through all three compilers with byte-identical output (incl. UTF-16 surrogate-pair `mbrtoc16` returning `(size_t)(-3)`, `c16rtomb`/`c32rtomb`, `wctype`/`iswctype`, `wctrans`/`towctrans`).

> Numbering note: clause numbers below follow **C11 (N1570)**. In C99 (N1256) the same material is numbered **¬ß7.24 `<wchar.h>`** and **¬ß7.25 `<wctype.h>`** (future directions ¬ß7.26.12 / ¬ß7.26.13). `<uchar.h>` (¬ß7.28) and `char16_t`/`char32_t` are **C11-only** (added by N1570; the functions came via DTR 19769). `<wchar.h>`/`<wctype.h>` were originally added in **C95 (NA1, Amendment 1)**; `iswblank`, `vfwscanf`, `vswscanf`, `vwscanf`, the `%a`/`%A` conversions, the `hh`/`ll`/`j`/`z`/`t` length modifiers, and `WCHAR_MIN`/`WCHAR_MAX` (via `<stdint.h>`) were added in **C99**. Each checkbox is a single normative requirement to verify against mcc / gcc 15.3 / clang 22.

### ¬ß7.28.1 `<uchar.h>` ‚Äî Introduction (C11)

> Entire header, both types, and all four functions are **C11-only**; there is no `<uchar.h>` in C99/C95. mcc bundles `runtime/include/uchar.h`, which `#include_next`-pulls the system `<uchar.h>` when present and otherwise falls back to C11-conforming contents guarded by glibc's `_UCHAR_H` sentinel.

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.1p1 ‚Äî `<uchar.h>` shall declare types and functions for manipulating Unicode characters. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.1p2 ‚Äî The header shall declare the type `mbstate_t` (described in ¬ß7.29.1) and the type `size_t` (described in ¬ß7.19). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (bundled header pulls `mbstate_t` from system header, or defines the C11 fallback; `size_t` via `<stddef.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.1p2 ‚Äî `char16_t` shall be an unsigned integer type used for 16-bit characters and shall be the same type as `uint_least16_t` (described in ¬ß7.20.1.2). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__CHAR16_TYPE__`=`unsigned short`, `sizeof==2`; `uint_least16_t*` ‚Üî `char16_t*` accepted without diagnostic)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.1p2 ‚Äî `char32_t` shall be an unsigned integer type used for 32-bit characters and shall be the same type as `uint_least32_t` (described in ¬ß7.20.1.2). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__CHAR32_TYPE__`=`unsigned int`, `sizeof==4`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 / ¬ß7.28 ‚Äî If `__STDC_UTF_16__` is defined (the implementation shall define it with value `1` when so), values of type `char16_t` are UTF-16 encoded and `mbrtoc16`/`c16rtomb` perform conversion to/from UTF-16; otherwise the encoding is implementation-defined. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__STDC_UTF_16__`==`1`, C11-gated in `mccdefs.h`; surrogate-pair conversion verified at runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 / ¬ß7.28 ‚Äî If `__STDC_UTF_32__` is defined (the implementation shall define it with value `1` when so), values of type `char32_t` are UTF-32 encoded and `mbrtoc32`/`c32rtomb` perform conversion to/from UTF-32; otherwise the encoding is implementation-defined. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`__STDC_UTF_32__`==`1`, C11-gated)

#### Added gaps ‚Äî `<uchar.h>` compiler-level support

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 ‚Äî `__STDC_UTF_16__`/`__STDC_UTF_32__` shall **not** be predefined outside C11+ mode (no `<uchar.h>` exists in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc gates both behind `__STDC_VERSION__ >= 201112L`; absent in mcc's default `-std=c99`, present under `-std=c11`. gcc/clang default to a C11+ dialect so define them by default ‚Äî same gating, different default dialect)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.4.4.4/¬ß6.4.5 (under ¬ß7.28) ‚Äî The C11 `u`/`U` prefixes on character constants (`u'A'`, `U'A'`) and string literals (`u"‚Ä¶"`, `U"‚Ä¶"`) ‚Äî required to make `char16_t`/`char32_t` usable ‚Äî are a **C11 feature** and a conforming compiler must diagnose them in a strict C99 mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (under `-std=c99 -pedantic-errors` mcc rejects `u'A'`/`U'A'`/`u"hi"`/`U"hi"` ‚Äî "the 'u'/'U' character/string prefix is a C11 feature"; gcc and clang reject them as undeclared identifiers / C11-only.) Default and `-std=c11`: all three accept; runtime values byte-identical.
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28 ‚Äî `<uchar.h>` shall be includable and its four functions link against the host runtime; the bundled freestanding fallback shall compile under `-nostdinc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì

### ¬ß7.28.2 Restartable multibyte/wide character conversion functions (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2p1 ‚Äî Each function has a parameter `ps` of type pointer to `mbstate_t` pointing to an object that can completely describe the current conversion state of the associated multibyte character sequence; this object is altered as needed to track the shift state and to maintain partial conversion progress between calls. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc runtime; surrogate-pair progress in `*ps` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2p1 ‚Äî If `ps` is a null pointer, each function shall use its own internal `mbstate_t` object instead, which is initialized at program startup to the initial conversion state; no other function in the library calls these functions with a null pointer for `ps`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.28.2p2 ‚Äî A subsequent call to one of these functions with a `ps` value different from that used in a previous call may produce results different from any consistent sequencing of calls. (C11) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.28.2p2 ‚Äî Changing the `LC_CTYPE` category causes the conversion state of these functions to become indeterminate. (C11) ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2p2 ‚Äî These functions are restartable: a subsequent call takes up the conversion where the prior call left off (using the state stored in `*ps`). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; verified via surrogate split)

#### ¬ß7.28.2.1 The `mbrtoc16` function (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <uchar.h>` `size_t mbrtoc16(char16_t * restrict pc16, const char * restrict s, size_t n, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared, links, runs)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p2 ‚Äî If `s` is a null pointer, the call shall be equivalent to `mbrtoc16(NULL, "", 1, ps)`; in this case the values of `pc16` and `n` are ignored. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not a null pointer, `mbrtoc16` shall inspect at most `n` bytes beginning with the byte pointed to by `s` to determine the number of bytes needed to complete the next multibyte character (including any shift sequences). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p3 ‚Äî If the next multibyte character is complete and valid, the function determines the values of the corresponding `char16_t` characters and, if `pc16` is not null, stores the value of the first (or only) such character in `*pc16`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p3 ‚Äî Subsequent calls shall store successive `char16_t` characters (e.g. the second unit of a UTF-16 surrogate pair) without consuming any additional input, until all the characters corresponding to that multibyte character have been stored. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (U+1F600 ‚Üí first call `4`/`0xd83d`, second call `(size_t)(-3)`/`0xde00` on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p3 ‚Äî If the corresponding wide character is the null character, the resulting conversion state is the initial conversion state. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p4 ‚Äî Returns `0` if the next `n` or fewer bytes complete the multibyte character corresponding to the null wide character (which is the value stored). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p4 ‚Äî Returns a value between `1` and `n` inclusive ‚Äî the number of bytes that complete a valid multibyte character (whose first/only `char16_t` is the value stored). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p4 ‚Äî Returns `(size_t)(-3)` if the next `char16_t` resulting from a previous call has been stored (no bytes from the input have been consumed by this call). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p4 ‚Äî Returns `(size_t)(-2)` if the next `n` bytes contribute to an incomplete (but potentially valid) multibyte character and all `n` bytes have been processed (no value is stored). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.1p4 ‚Äî Returns `(size_t)(-1)` if an encoding error occurs (the next `n` or fewer bytes do not contribute to a complete and valid multibyte character); stores `EILSEQ` in `errno`, no value is stored, and the conversion state is unspecified. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.28.2.2 The `c16rtomb` function (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t c16rtomb(char * restrict s, char16_t c16, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared, links, runs)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.2p2 ‚Äî If `s` is a null pointer, the call shall be equivalent to `c16rtomb(buf, L'\0', ps)` where `buf` is an internal buffer. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.2p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not a null pointer, the function determines the number of bytes needed to represent the multibyte character that corresponds to the wide character given by `c16` (including any shift sequences) and stores the multibyte character representation in the array whose first element is pointed to by `s`; at most `MB_CUR_MAX` bytes are stored. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`c16rtomb(out,0x42,..)`‚Üí`1`/`"B"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.2p3 ‚Äî If `c16` is a null wide character, a null byte is stored, preceded by any shift sequence needed to restore the initial shift state, and the resulting conversion state is the initial conversion state. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.2p3 ‚Äî If `c16` is a high surrogate, the function does not produce output and remembers the value in `*ps`; the following call (with the matching low surrogate) emits the corresponding multibyte character. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.2p4 ‚Äî Returns the number of bytes stored in the array (including any shift sequences); when `c16` does not correspond to a valid wide character an encoding error occurs: the function stores `EILSEQ` in `errno`, returns `(size_t)(-1)`, and the conversion state is unspecified. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.28.2.3 The `mbrtoc32` function (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t mbrtoc32(char32_t * restrict pc32, const char * restrict s, size_t n, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared, links, runs)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.3p2 ‚Äî If `s` is a null pointer, the call shall be equivalent to `mbrtoc32(NULL, "", 1, ps)`; in this case `pc32` and `n` are ignored. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.3p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, `mbrtoc32` inspects at most `n` bytes from `s` to determine the bytes needed for the next multibyte character; if complete and valid it stores the corresponding `char32_t` value(s) in `*pc32` (first/only one), with subsequent calls storing successive characters without consuming additional input; if the corresponding wide character is the null character, the resulting state is the initial conversion state. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`mbrtoc32(&c,"A",1,..)`‚Üí`1`/`65`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.3p4 ‚Äî Returns `0`, `1..n`, `(size_t)(-3)`, `(size_t)(-2)`, or `(size_t)(-1)` with `errno=EILSEQ` ‚Äî same meanings as for `mbrtoc16` (note: for UTF-32, `-3` essentially never occurs since one code point = one `char32_t`). (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.28.2.4 The `c32rtomb` function (C11)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t c32rtomb(char * restrict s, char32_t c32, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (declared, links, runs)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.4p2 ‚Äî If `s` is null, the call shall be equivalent to `c32rtomb(buf, L'\0', ps)` with `buf` an internal buffer. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.4p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, the function stores the multibyte representation of the wide character `c32` (at most `MB_CUR_MAX` bytes, including any shift sequences) into the array pointed to by `s`; a null `c32` stores a null byte preceded by any needed shift sequence and restores the initial conversion state. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`c32rtomb(out,0x41,..)`‚Üí`1`/`"A"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.28.2.4p4 ‚Äî Returns the number of bytes stored (including shift sequences); on an encoding error (`c32` not corresponding to a valid wide character) it stores `EILSEQ` in `errno`, returns `(size_t)(-1)`, and leaves the conversion state unspecified. (C11) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

---

### ¬ß7.29.1 `<wchar.h>` ‚Äî Introduction

> C11 ¬ß7.29 = C99 ¬ß7.24 = original C95 (Amendment 1) material. mcc takes `<wchar.h>` verbatim from the host glibc; it supplies the underlying `__WCHAR_TYPE__`=`int`, `__WINT_TYPE__`=`unsigned int`, and (for `WCHAR_MIN`/`WCHAR_MAX`) the `<stdint.h>` machinery. C99 additions: `vfwscanf`/`vswscanf`/`vwscanf`, `%a`/`%A`, and the `hh`/`ll`/`j`/`z`/`t` length modifiers (tagged inline).

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p1 ‚Äî `<wchar.h>` shall declare four types, one tag, several macros, and many functions for extended multibyte and wide character utilities. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (header includes & links)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p2 ‚Äî The types declared are `wchar_t` and `size_t` (both described in ¬ß7.19). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(wchar_t)==4`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p2 ‚Äî `mbstate_t` shall be an object type other than an array type that can hold the conversion state information necessary to convert between sequences of multibyte characters and wide characters. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof==8`; assignable `b=a` accepted ‚Üí not an array type)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p2 ‚Äî `wint_t` shall be an integer type unchanged by the default argument promotions that can hold any value corresponding to members of the extended character set, as well as at least one value (`WEOF`) that does not correspond to any member of the extended character set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`unsigned int`, 32-bit, unchanged by promotions)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p2 ‚Äî The tag `struct tm` shall be declared as an incomplete type (its contents are described in ¬ß7.27.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`struct tm *` usable from `<wchar.h>` alone)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p3 ‚Äî The macros defined are `NULL` (described in ¬ß7.19); `WCHAR_MIN` and `WCHAR_MAX` (described in ¬ß7.20.3); and `WEOF` (described in ¬ß7.29.1p4). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`WCHAR_MIN`=`-2147483648`, `WCHAR_MAX`=`2147483647` on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p4 ‚Äî `WEOF` shall expand to a constant expression of type `wint_t` whose value does not correspond to any member of the extended character set; it is accepted (and returned) by several functions in this subclause to indicate end-of-file. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`_Generic(WEOF,‚Ä¶)`‚Üí`unsigned int`; value `0xffffffff`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.1p4 ‚Äî `WEOF` may have the same value as `EOF` and need not be negative. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (here `WEOF`=`0xffffffff`, non-negative `wint_t`)
