- ¬ß7.29.1p5 ‚Äî The functions declared are grouped as: formatted wide I/O, wide I/O, general wide string utilities, wide time conversion, and extended multibyte/wide conversion utilities. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.29.2 Formatted wide character input/output functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2p1 ‚Äî Whenever a `*` is used in place of a field width or precision, an `int` argument supplies it; a negative field width is treated as a `-` flag followed by a positive field width, and a negative precision is treated as though omitted. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc runtime; `swprintf(L"%*d",‚Ä¶)` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2p2 ‚Äî The formatted wide-character I/O functions behave as their byte counterparts except that they read/write wide characters and the formats are wide strings; `%c`/`%s` operate per function with the `l` length modifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.1 The `fwprintf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fwprintf(FILE * restrict stream, const wchar_t * restrict format, ...);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p2 ‚Äî `fwprintf` writes output under control of `format`; insufficient arguments ‚Üí UB; excess arguments are evaluated but ignored; returns at end of format. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p3 ‚Äî `format` is zero or more directives: ordinary wide characters copied unchanged; and conversion specifications. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p4 ‚Äî Each conversion specification is introduced by `%`, then in sequence: flags; optional minimum field width; optional precision; optional length modifier; conversion specifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p5 ‚Äî The flags `-`, `+`, space, `#`, `0` have the same meanings as for `fprintf`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p6 ‚Äî A nonnegative decimal minimum field width pads the value as for `fprintf`; `*` denotes an `int` argument. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p7 ‚Äî An optional precision `.`+integer (or `*`) has the same per-conversion meaning as for `fprintf`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p8 ‚Äî The length modifiers `hh`, `h`, `l`, `ll`, `j`, `z`, `t`, `L` have the same meanings as for `fprintf` (`hh`,`ll`,`j`,`z`,`t` added in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p9 ‚Äî The conversion specifiers `d i o u x X f F e E g G a A p n %` behave as for `fprintf` (`a`/`A` added in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p9 ‚Äî For `c` without `l`, the `int` argument is converted to a wide character as if by `btowc` and written; with `l`, the `wint_t` argument is converted to `wchar_t` and written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p9 ‚Äî For `s` without `l`, the argument is a multibyte-character array, each converted (as if by repeated `mbrtowc`) to a wide character and written up to the null, honoring precision. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p9 ‚Äî For `s` with `l`, the argument is a `wchar_t` array, written up to the null, honoring precision. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; `swprintf(L"%ls",L"x")` verified)
- ¬ß7.29.2.1p10 ‚Äî Invalid conversion specification ‚Üí UB; wrong-type argument ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p11 ‚Äî A nonexistent or small field width never causes truncation; the field is expanded to contain the result. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.1p12 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide characters transmitted, or a negative value on output/encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.2 The `fwscanf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fwscanf(FILE * restrict stream, const wchar_t * restrict format, ...);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p2 ‚Äî `fwscanf` reads under control of `format`, using subsequent arguments as pointers; insufficient args ‚Üí UB; excess args evaluated but ignored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p3 ‚Äî `format` is zero or more directives: white-space wide chars; an ordinary wide char; or a conversion specification. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p4 ‚Äî Each conversion specification: `%`, optional `*`, optional nonzero field width, optional length modifier, conversion specifier. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p5 ‚Äî A white-space directive reads up to the first non-white-space wide character (left unread), or until no more input. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p6 ‚Äî An ordinary-wide-character directive reads the next character; mismatch fails the directive leaving the char unread. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p7 ‚Äî A conversion specification skips leading white space (except `[`,`c`,`n`), reads an input item (except `n`), and converts it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p8 ‚Äî The length modifiers `hh h l ll j z t L` have the same meaning as for `fscanf` (`hh`,`ll`,`j`,`z`,`t` added in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p9 ‚Äî The conversion specifiers `d i o u x X a/e/E/f/F/g/G c s [ p n %` behave as for `fscanf` on wide characters (`a`/`A` added in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p10 ‚Äî For `c` without `l`, matched wide chars are converted as if by `wcrtomb` into a `char` array; with `l`, stored as `wchar_t` (no null for `c`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p10 ‚Äî For `s`/`[` without `l`, converted (as if by `wcrtomb`) into a `char` array + null; with `l`, into a `wchar_t` array + null wide char. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p11 ‚Äî Conversion uses `wcrtomb` with an `mbstate_t` reset to the initial state before each converting directive. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p12 ‚Äî Trailing white space is left unread unless matched; literal-match/suppressed-assignment success is determinable only via `%n`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.2p13 ‚Äî Returns `EOF` on input failure before any conversion; otherwise the number of items assigned (possibly fewer/zero on early matching failure). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.3 The `swprintf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int swprintf(wchar_t * restrict s, size_t n, const wchar_t * restrict format, ...);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.3p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fwprintf` but writes into a `wchar_t` array; at most `n` wide chars including the always-appended terminating null (unless `n` is zero). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`swprintf(buf,64,L"%d-%ls",7,L"x")`‚Üí`3`/`"7-x"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.3p3 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide characters written (excl. null), or a negative value on encoding error or if `n` or more wide chars were requested. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.4 The `swscanf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int swscanf(const wchar_t * restrict s, const wchar_t * restrict format, ...);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.4p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fwscanf` but reads from a wide string; reaching the end is equivalent to EOF. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.4p3 ‚Äî Returns the same as `fwscanf`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.5 The `vfwprintf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `#include <stdarg.h>`/`<wchar.h>` `int vfwprintf(FILE * restrict stream, const wchar_t * restrict format, va_list arg);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.5p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fwprintf` with the variable arguments replaced by `arg` (initialized by `va_start`); does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.5p3 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide characters transmitted, or negative on output/encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.6 The `vfwscanf` function (C99)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int vfwscanf(FILE * restrict stream, const wchar_t * restrict format, va_list arg);`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.6p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fwscanf` with the variable arguments replaced by `arg`; does not invoke `va_end`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.6p3 ‚Äî Returns the same as `fwscanf`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.7 The `vswprintf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int vswprintf(wchar_t * restrict s, size_t n, const wchar_t * restrict format, va_list arg);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.7p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `swprintf` with variable arguments replaced by `arg`; does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.7p3 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide characters written (excl. null), or negative on encoding error or if `n` or more requested. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.8 The `vswscanf` function (C99)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int vswscanf(const wchar_t * restrict s, const wchar_t * restrict format, va_list arg);`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.8p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `swscanf` with variable arguments replaced by `arg`; does not invoke `va_end`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.8p3 ‚Äî Returns the same as `fwscanf`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.9 The `vwprintf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.9p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int vwprintf(const wchar_t * restrict format, va_list arg);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.9p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `wprintf` with variable arguments replaced by `arg`; does not invoke `va_end`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.9p3 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide characters transmitted, or negative on output/encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.10 The `vwscanf` function (C99)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.10p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int vwscanf(const wchar_t * restrict format, va_list arg);`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.10p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `wscanf` with variable arguments replaced by `arg`; does not invoke `va_end`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.10p3 ‚Äî Returns the same as `fwscanf`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.11 The `wprintf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.11p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wprintf(const wchar_t * restrict format, ...);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.11p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fwprintf` with `stdout` interposed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.11p3 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide characters transmitted, or negative on output/encoding error. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.2.12 The `wscanf` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.12p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wscanf(const wchar_t * restrict format, ...);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.12p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fwscanf` with `stdin` interposed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.2.12p3 ‚Äî Returns the same as `fwscanf`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.29.3 Wide character input/output functions

#### ¬ß7.29.3.1 The `fgetwc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t fgetwc(FILE *stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.1p2 ‚Äî If not at EOF and a next wide character is present, obtains it (as `wchar_t`‚Üí`wint_t`) and advances the file position indicator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.1p3 ‚Äî Returns the next wide character; on EOF sets the EOF indicator and returns `WEOF`; on read error sets the error indicator and returns `WEOF`; on encoding error sets `errno=EILSEQ` and returns `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.2 The `fgetws` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *fgetws(wchar_t * restrict s, int n, FILE * restrict stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.2p2 ‚Äî Reads at most `n-1` wide chars; stops after a retained newline or at EOF; writes a null wide char after the last read. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.2p3 ‚Äî Returns `s` on success; null pointer if EOF before any read (array unchanged); null pointer on read/encoding error (array indeterminate). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.3 The `fputwc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t fputwc(wchar_t c, FILE *stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.3p2 ‚Äî Writes `c` at the position indicated by the file position indicator (or appends in append mode), advancing the indicator. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.3p3 ‚Äî Returns the wide character written; on write error sets the error indicator and returns `WEOF`; on encoding error sets `errno=EILSEQ` and returns `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.4 The `fputws` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fputws(const wchar_t * restrict s, FILE * restrict stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.4p2 ‚Äî Writes the wide string `s`; the terminating null wide character is not written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.4p3 ‚Äî Returns `EOF` on write/encoding error, otherwise a nonnegative value. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.5 The `fwide` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int fwide(FILE *stream, int mode);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.5p2 ‚Äî Determines/sets the orientation: `mode>0` attempts wide, `mode<0` attempts byte, `mode==0` does not alter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.5p2 ‚Äî In all cases does not change the orientation of a stream that already has one. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.5p3 ‚Äî Returns `>0` if wide-oriented after the call, `<0` if byte-oriented, `0` if no orientation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.6 The `getwc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t getwc(FILE *stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.6p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fgetwc`, except it may evaluate `stream` more than once if a macro. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.6p3 ‚Äî Returns the next wide character, or `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.7 The `getwchar` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t getwchar(void);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.7p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `getwc(stdin)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.7p3 ‚Äî Returns the next wide character from `stdin`, or `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.8 The `putwc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t putwc(wchar_t c, FILE *stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.8p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `fputwc`, except it may evaluate `stream` more than once if a macro. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.8p3 ‚Äî Returns the wide character written, or `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.9 The `putwchar` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.9p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t putwchar(wchar_t c);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.9p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `putwc(c, stdout)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.9p3 ‚Äî Returns the wide character written, or `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.3.10 The `ungetwc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.10p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t ungetwc(wint_t c, FILE *stream);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.10p2 ‚Äî Pushes `c` (converted to `wchar_t`) back; subsequent reads return pushed-back chars in reverse; a successful intervening file-positioning call discards them. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.10p2 ‚Äî One wide character of pushback is guaranteed; too many calls without an intervening read/position may fail. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.10p3 ‚Äî If `c` equals `WEOF`, the operation fails and the stream is unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.10p4 ‚Äî A successful call clears the EOF indicator; the file position after reading/discarding pushed-back chars equals its prior value; for text/binary streams the indicator is decremented per successful call (indeterminate if it was zero). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.3.10p5 ‚Äî Returns the wide character pushed back (after conversion), or `WEOF` on failure. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.29.4 General wide string utilities

- ¬ß7.29.4p1 ‚Äî `<wchar.h>` declares wide-string functions; a `wchar_t *`/`const wchar_t *` argument points to the initial element of an array; accessing beyond the end is UB. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.29.4.1 Wide string numeric conversion functions

##### ¬ß7.29.4.1.1 The `wcstod`, `wcstof`, `wcstold` functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `double wcstod(...);` `float wcstof(...);` `long double wcstold(...);` (`wcstof`/`wcstold` added in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.1p2 ‚Äî Convert the initial portion of `nptr` to `double`/`float`/`long double`; decompose into white space, subject sequence, and final string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcstod(L"3.14xyz",0)`‚Üí`3.14`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.1p3 ‚Äî The expected subject form is the same as for `strtod`, using wide characters (sign; decimal/hex significand with optional radix and exponent; or `INF`/`INFINITY`/`NAN`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.1p4 ‚Äî Convert the longest matching initial subsequence; store the final-string pointer in `*endptr`; on no conversion store `nptr` in `*endptr`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.1p5 ‚Äî Hex digits and the radix character behave as for `strtod`, rounded per the current rounding direction. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.1p6 ‚Äî Returns the converted value; `0` if none; `¬±HUGE_VAL*` with `errno=ERANGE` on overflow; an underflow value with implementation-defined `ERANGE`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.1.2 The `wcstol`, `wcstoll`, `wcstoul`, `wcstoull` functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `long int wcstol(...);` `long long int wcstoll(...);` `unsigned long int wcstoul(...);` `unsigned long long int wcstoull(...);` (`wcstoll`/`wcstoull` added in C99). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.2p2 ‚Äî Convert the initial portion of `nptr` to the respective integer type; decompose into white space, subject sequence in radix `base`, and final string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcstol(L"  -42",0,10)`‚Üí`-42`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.2p3 ‚Äî The expected subject form is the same as for `strtol`/`strtoul`; `base` shall be 0 or 2..36. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.2p4 ‚Äî If `base` is zero, the form is an integer constant (decimal/octal/hex); the subject sequence is the longest matching initial subsequence. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.2p5 ‚Äî Store the final-string pointer in `*endptr`; on no conversion store `nptr`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.1.2p6 ‚Äî Returns the converted value (unsigned functions negate a signed sequence); `0` if none; range limit (`LONG_MIN`‚Ä¶`ULLONG_MAX`) with `errno=ERANGE` on out-of-range. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.4.2 Wide string copying functions

##### ¬ß7.29.4.2.1 The `wcscpy` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcscpy(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.1p2 ‚Äî Copies `s2` (including the null) into `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcscpy(buf,L"Hello")` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.2.2 The `wcsncpy` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcsncpy(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.2p2 ‚Äî Copies at most `n` wide chars (none after a null); overlapping objects ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.2p3 ‚Äî If `s2` is shorter than `n`, null wide chars are appended until `n` are written. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.2p4 ‚Äî Returns `s1` (result need not be null-terminated). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.2.3 The `wmemcpy` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wmemcpy(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.3p2 ‚Äî Copies `n` wide chars; overlapping objects ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.3p3 ‚Äî Returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.2.4 The `wmemmove` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wmemmove(wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.4p2 ‚Äî Copies `n` wide chars as if via a non-overlapping temporary (overlap handled correctly). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.2.4p3 ‚Äî Returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.4.3 Wide string concatenation functions

##### ¬ß7.29.4.3.1 The `wcscat` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcscat(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.3.1p2 ‚Äî Appends a copy of `s2` (including the null) to the end of `s1`; overlap ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcscat(buf,L" World")`‚Üí`"Hello World"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.3.1p3 ‚Äî Returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.3.2 The `wcsncat` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcsncat(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.3.2p2 ‚Äî Appends at most `n` wide chars (stopping at a null); always appends a terminating null; overlap ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.3.2p3 ‚Äî Returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.4.4 Wide string comparison functions

- ¬ß7.29.4.4p1 ‚Äî Unless stated otherwise, these functions compare wide characters as values of type `wchar_t`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.4.1 The `wcscmp` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wcscmp(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.1p2 ‚Äî Compares `s1` to `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcscmp(L"Hello World",L"Hello World")`‚Üí`0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.1p3 ‚Äî Returns `>0`/`0`/`<0` as `s1` is greater/equal/less. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.4.2 The `wcscoll` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wcscoll(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.2p2 ‚Äî Compares `s1` to `s2`, both interpreted per the `LC_COLLATE` category. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.2p3 ‚Äî Returns `>0`/`0`/`<0` per the locale interpretation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.4.3 The `wcsncmp` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wcsncmp(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.3p2 ‚Äî Compares at most `n` wide chars (none after a null). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.3p3 ‚Äî Returns `>0`/`0`/`<0` accordingly. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.4.4 The `wcsxfrm` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcsxfrm(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.4p2 ‚Äî Transforms `s2` into `s1` so that `wcscmp` of two transformed strings matches `wcscoll` of the originals; at most `n` wide chars (incl. null) are placed. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.4p3 ‚Äî Returns the transformed length (excl. null); if `‚â• n`, `s1` contents are indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.4p3 ‚Äî If `n` is zero, `s1` may be a null pointer. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.4.5 The `wmemcmp` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wmemcmp(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.5p2 ‚Äî Compares the first `n` wide chars of `s1` and `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.4.5p3 ‚Äî Returns `>0`/`0`/`<0` accordingly. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.4.5 Wide string search functions

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.1 The `wcschr` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcschr(const wchar_t *s, wchar_t c);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.1p2 ‚Äî Locates the first occurrence of `c` in `s`; the terminating null is part of the string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcschr(L"abcd",L'c')`‚Üí`L"cd"`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.1p3 ‚Äî Returns a pointer to the located wide char, or null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.2 The `wcscspn` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcscspn(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.2p2 ‚Äî Computes the length of the max initial segment of `s1` with no wide char from `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.2p3 ‚Äî Returns the segment length. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.3 The `wcspbrk` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcspbrk(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.3p2 ‚Äî Locates the first occurrence in `s1` of any wide char from `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.3p3 ‚Äî Returns a pointer to the wide char, or null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.4 The `wcsrchr` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcsrchr(const wchar_t *s, wchar_t c);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.4p2 ‚Äî Locates the last occurrence of `c` in `s`; the null is part of the string. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.4p3 ‚Äî Returns a pointer to the wide char, or null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.5 The `wcsspn` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcsspn(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.5p2 ‚Äî Computes the length of the max initial segment of `s1` consisting entirely of wide chars from `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.5p3 ‚Äî Returns the segment length. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.6 The `wcsstr` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcsstr(const wchar_t *s1, const wchar_t *s2);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.6p2 ‚Äî Locates the first occurrence in `s1` of the wide-char sequence (excl. null) in `s2`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.6p3 ‚Äî Returns a pointer to the located substring, or null; a zero-length `s2` returns `s1`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.7 The `wcstok` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wcstok(wchar_t * restrict s1, const wchar_t * restrict s2, wchar_t ** restrict ptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (note: the C `wcstok` is 3-argument/reentrant, unlike 2-argument `strtok`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.7p2 ‚Äî Breaks `s1` into tokens delimited by chars from `s2`; `ptr` points to a caller-provided `wchar_t*` for continuation state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.7p3 ‚Äî The first call has non-null `s1` and seeds `*ptr`; subsequent calls pass null `s1` and the prior `*ptr`; `s2` may differ per call. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.7p4 ‚Äî The first call searches for the first non-separator char; if none, returns null (and writes null through `ptr`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.7p4 ‚Äî Otherwise marks the token start, searches for a separator; if none the token runs to the end; if found, overwrites it with a null and saves the next-char pointer in `*ptr`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.7p5 ‚Äî Returns a pointer to the first wide char of a token, or null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.5.8 The `wmemchr` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wmemchr(const wchar_t *s, wchar_t c, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.8p2 ‚Äî Locates the first occurrence of `c` in the initial `n` wide chars of `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.5.8p3 ‚Äî Returns a pointer to the located wide char, or null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.4.6 Miscellaneous functions

##### ¬ß7.29.4.6.1 The `wcslen` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.6.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcslen(const wchar_t *s);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.6.1p2 ‚Äî Computes the length of `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wcslen(L"Hello World")`‚Üí`11`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.6.1p3 ‚Äî Returns the number of wide chars before the null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.4.6.2 The `wmemset` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.6.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wchar_t *wmemset(wchar_t *s, wchar_t c, size_t n);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.6.2p2 ‚Äî Copies `c` into each of the first `n` wide chars of `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.4.6.2p3 ‚Äî Returns `s`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.29.5 Wide character time conversion functions

#### ¬ß7.29.5.1 The `wcsftime` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.5.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcsftime(wchar_t * restrict s, size_t maxsize, const wchar_t * restrict format, const struct tm * restrict timeptr);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.5.1p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `strftime` but writes into a `wchar_t` array, with `maxsize` wide chars, a wide `format`, and `LC_TIME`-appropriate wide sequences. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.5.1p3 ‚Äî Returns the count of wide chars (excl. null) if `‚â§ maxsize`; otherwise `0` and the array is indeterminate. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.29.6 Extended multibyte/wide character conversion utilities

- ¬ß7.29.6p1 ‚Äî `<wchar.h>` declares extended conversion functions whose behavior is affected by `LC_CTYPE`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6p2 ‚Äî For the restartable functions of ¬ß7.29.6.3/¬ß7.29.6.4, a `ps` of null uses an internal `mbstate_t`; no library function calls these with a null `ps`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- ¬ß7.29.6p3 ‚Äî Changing `LC_CTYPE` makes the restartable functions' conversion state indeterminate. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

#### ¬ß7.29.6.1 Single-byte/wide character conversion functions

##### ¬ß7.29.6.1.1 The `btowc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t btowc(int c);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.1.1p2 ‚Äî Determines whether `c` is a valid single-byte character in the initial shift state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.1.1p3 ‚Äî Returns `WEOF` for `EOF` or an invalid single-byte char; otherwise the wide-character representation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`btowc('A')`‚Üí`65`)

##### ¬ß7.29.6.1.2 The `wctob` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.1.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int wctob(wint_t c);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.1.2p2 ‚Äî Determines whether `c` maps to a single-byte multibyte character in the initial shift state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.1.2p3 ‚Äî Returns `EOF` if not single-byte; otherwise the `unsigned char`‚Üí`int` single-byte representation. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wctob(L'A')`‚Üí`65`)

#### ¬ß7.29.6.2 Conversion state functions

##### ¬ß7.29.6.2.1 The `mbsinit` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int mbsinit(const mbstate_t *ps);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.2.1p2 ‚Äî If `ps` is not null, determines whether `*ps` describes an initial conversion state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns nonzero if `ps` is null or `*ps` is the initial state; otherwise zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.6.3 Restartable multibyte/wide character conversion functions

- ¬ß7.29.6.3p1 ‚Äî These differ from `mbtowc`/`wctomb`/`mblen` by an extra `ps` parameter and not assuming null-terminated input; on entry `*ps` describes the current state. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.29.6.3.1 The `mbrlen` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t mbrlen(const char * restrict s, size_t n, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.1p2 ‚Äî Equivalent to `mbrtowc(NULL, s, n, ps?:&internal)` except `ps` is evaluated once. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.1p3 ‚Äî Returns `0..n`, `(size_t)(-1)`, or `(size_t)(-2)` per `mbrtowc` semantics. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.6.3.2 The `mbrtowc` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t mbrtowc(wchar_t * restrict pwc, const char * restrict s, size_t n, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p2 ‚Äî If `s` is null, equivalent to `mbrtowc(NULL, "", 1, ps)`; `pwc`/`n` ignored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, inspect at most `n` bytes; on a complete valid char store the wide char in `*pwc` (if non-null); a null wide char yields the initial state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p4 ‚Äî Returns `0` when the bytes complete the null wide char. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p4 ‚Äî Returns `1..n` ‚Äî the byte count completing a valid char (whose value is stored). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p4 ‚Äî Returns `(size_t)(-2)` for an incomplete char with all `n` bytes processed (no value stored). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.2p4 ‚Äî Returns `(size_t)(-1)` on encoding error; `errno=EILSEQ`, state unspecified, no value stored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.6.3.3 The `wcrtomb` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcrtomb(char * restrict s, wchar_t wc, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.3p2 ‚Äî If `s` is null, equivalent to `wcrtomb(buf, L'\0', ps)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.3p3 ‚Äî If `s` is not null, store the multibyte representation of `wc` (‚â§ `MB_CUR_MAX` bytes); a null `wc` stores a null byte preceded by any shift sequence and yields the initial state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.3.3p4 ‚Äî Returns the byte count stored; on an invalid `wc` stores `EILSEQ` and returns `(size_t)(-1)`, state unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.29.6.4 Restartable multibyte/wide string conversion functions

- ¬ß7.29.6.4p1 ‚Äî These differ from `mbstowcs`/`wcstombs` by an extra `ps`, storing a result pointer back through the source pointer-to-pointer, and handling encoding-error termination. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

##### ¬ß7.29.6.4.1 The `mbsrtowcs` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t mbsrtowcs(wchar_t * restrict dst, const char ** restrict src, size_t len, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.1p2 ‚Äî Converts a multibyte sequence from `*src` (state `*ps`) to wide chars in `dst` (if non-null), up to and including a terminating null. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.1p2 ‚Äî Stops early on an invalid sequence, or (if `dst` non-null) after `len` wide chars; each conversion is as if by `mbrtowc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.1p3 ‚Äî If `dst` is non-null, `*src` is set to null (terminating null reached) or just past the last char converted; reaching the null yields the initial state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.1p4 ‚Äî Returns the count of multibyte chars converted (excl. null); on an invalid char returns `(size_t)(-1)`, `errno=EILSEQ`, state unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.29.6.4.2 The `wcsrtombs` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `size_t wcsrtombs(char * restrict dst, const wchar_t ** restrict src, size_t len, mbstate_t * restrict ps);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.2p2 ‚Äî Converts a wide sequence from `*src` (state `*ps`) to multibyte chars in `dst` (if non-null), up to and including a terminating null (after any shift sequence). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.2p2 ‚Äî Stops early on a wide char with no valid multibyte char, or (if `dst` non-null) when the next char would exceed `len` bytes; each conversion is as if by `wcrtomb`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.2p3 ‚Äî If `dst` is non-null, `*src` is set to null (terminating null reached) or just past the last char converted; reaching the null yields the initial state. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.29.6.4.2p4 ‚Äî Returns the resulting byte count (excl. null); on an invalid wide char returns `(size_t)(-1)`, `errno=EILSEQ`, state unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

---

### ¬ß7.30.1 `<wctype.h>` ‚Äî Introduction

> C11 ¬ß7.30 = C99 ¬ß7.25 = original C95 (Amendment 1) material. mcc takes `<wctype.h>` verbatim from the host glibc. The only C99 addition to this header is `iswblank` (¬ß7.30.2.1.3).

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.1p1 ‚Äî `<wctype.h>` shall declare three data types, one macro, and many wide-char classification/mapping functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (header includes & links)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.1p2 ‚Äî The three types are `wint_t`; `wctrans_t` (a scalar type holding locale-specific mappings); and `wctype_t` (a scalar type holding locale-specific classifications). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wctype_t`/`wctrans_t` used as scalars)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.1p3 ‚Äî The macro defined is `WEOF`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (also visible via `<wctype.h>` alone)
- ¬ß7.30.1p4 ‚Äî Wide-char classification/mapping behavior is affected by `LC_CTYPE`. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ß7.30.1p4 ‚Äî The functions accept any value representable as `wchar_t` or equal to `WEOF`; any other value ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ß7.30.2 Wide character classification utilities

#### ¬ß7.30.2.1 Wide character classification functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1p1 ‚Äî The functions test for membership in overlapping classes defined for the `"C"` locale, paralleling the narrow `<ctype.h>` classes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; consistent with ¬ß7.4)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1p2 ‚Äî In the `"C"` locale, `iswprint` is true exactly for the chars where `iswalnum`/`iswpunct`/the wide space hold, with membership relationships paralleling ¬ß7.4. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.1 The `iswalnum` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswalnum(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.1p2 ‚Äî Tests for any wide char where `iswalpha` or `iswdigit` is true. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.2 The `iswalpha` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswalpha(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.2p2 ‚Äî Tests for `iswupper`/`iswlower` chars or an implementation-defined set with none of `iswcntrl`/`iswdigit`/`iswpunct`/`iswspace`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`iswalpha(L'a')` true on all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.2p2 ‚Äî In the `"C"` locale, true only for `iswupper`/`iswlower` chars. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.3 The `iswblank` function (C99)

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.3p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswblank(wint_t wc);`. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.3p2 ‚Äî Tests for a standard blank wide char (or an implementation-defined `iswspace` word-separator); in `"C"`, true only for space and tab. (C99) ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`iswblank(L'\t')`‚Üítrue)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.4 The `iswcntrl` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.4p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswcntrl(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.4p2 ‚Äî Tests for any control wide character. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.5 The `iswdigit` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.5p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswdigit(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.5p2 ‚Äî Tests for a decimal-digit character (per ¬ß5.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`iswdigit(L'1')`‚Üítrue)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.6 The `iswgraph` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.6p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswgraph(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.6p2 ‚Äî Tests for any printing wide char except space (`iswprint` true, `iswspace` false). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.7 The `iswlower` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.7p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswlower(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.7p2 ‚Äî Tests for a lowercase letter or an implementation-defined set with none of `iswcntrl`/`iswdigit`/`iswpunct`/`iswspace`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.8 The `iswprint` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.8p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswprint(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.8p2 ‚Äî Tests for any printing wide char (including space). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.9 The `iswpunct` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.9p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswpunct(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.9p2 ‚Äî Tests for a printing wide char in an implementation-defined set with neither `iswspace` nor `iswalnum`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.10 The `iswspace` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.10p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswspace(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.10p2 ‚Äî Tests for a locale-specific white-space wide char with none of `iswalnum`/`iswgraph`/`iswpunct`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`iswspace(L' ')`‚Üítrue)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.11 The `iswupper` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.11p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswupper(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.11p2 ‚Äî Tests for an uppercase letter or an implementation-defined set with none of `iswcntrl`/`iswdigit`/`iswpunct`/`iswspace`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`iswupper(L'A')`‚Üítrue)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.1.12 The `iswxdigit` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.12p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswxdigit(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.1.12p2 ‚Äî Tests for a hexadecimal-digit character (per ¬ß6.4.4.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.30.2.2 Extensible wide character classification functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2p1 ‚Äî `wctype`/`iswctype` provide extensible classification and a common interface to the ¬ß7.30.2.1 functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.2.1 The `wctype` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wctype_t wctype(const char *property);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.1p2 ‚Äî Constructs a `wctype_t` for the class named by `property`; the ¬ß7.30.2.2.2 strings are valid in all locales. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wctype("alpha")` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns a nonzero `wctype_t` valid for `iswctype` if `property` names a valid class; otherwise zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.2.2.2 The `iswctype` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `int iswctype(wint_t wc, wctype_t desc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.2p2 ‚Äî Determines whether `wc` has the property `desc`; `LC_CTYPE` must match the `wctype` call that produced `desc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.2p3 ‚Äî `iswctype(wc, wctype("X"))` is equivalent to the corresponding ¬ß7.30.2.1 call for each of `alnum alpha blank cntrl digit graph lower print punct space upper xdigit`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`iswctype(L'q',wctype("alpha"))`‚Üí`1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.2.2.2p4 ‚Äî Returns nonzero iff `wc` has the property `desc`; `desc==0` ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

### ¬ß7.30.3 Wide character case mapping utilities

#### ¬ß7.30.3.1 Wide character case mapping functions

##### ¬ß7.30.3.1.1 The `towlower` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.1.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t towlower(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.1.1p2 ‚Äî Converts an uppercase letter to the corresponding lowercase letter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`towlower(L'Z')`‚Üí`z`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.1.1p3 ‚Äî If `iswupper(wc)` and a corresponding `iswlower` char exists, returns that (locale-consistent) char; otherwise returns the argument unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.3.1.2 The `towupper` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.1.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t towupper(wint_t wc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.1.2p2 ‚Äî Converts a lowercase letter to the corresponding uppercase letter. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`towupper(L'a')`‚Üí`A`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.1.2p3 ‚Äî If `iswlower(wc)` and a corresponding `iswupper` char exists, returns that (locale-consistent) char; otherwise returns the argument unchanged. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ß7.30.3.2 Extensible wide character case mapping functions

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2p1 ‚Äî `wctrans`/`towctrans` provide extensible mapping and a common interface to the ¬ß7.30.3.1 functions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.3.2.1 The `wctrans` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.1p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wctrans_t wctrans(const char *property);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.1p2 ‚Äî Constructs a `wctrans_t` for the mapping named by `property`; the ¬ß7.30.3.2.2 strings are valid in all locales. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`wctrans("toupper")` verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.1p3 ‚Äî Returns a nonzero `wctrans_t` valid for `towctrans` if `property` names a valid mapping; otherwise zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

##### ¬ß7.30.3.2.2 The `towctrans` function

- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.2p1 ‚Äî Synopsis: `wint_t towctrans(wint_t wc, wctrans_t desc);`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.2p2 ‚Äî Maps `wc` using `desc`; `LC_CTYPE` must match the `wctrans` call that produced `desc`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.2p3 ‚Äî `towctrans(wc, wctrans("tolower"))` ‚â° `towlower(wc)`, and `towctrans(wc, wctrans("toupper"))` ‚â° `towupper(wc)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`towctrans(L'm',wctrans("toupper"))`‚Üí`M`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß7.30.3.2.2p4 ‚Äî Returns the mapped value of `wc`; `desc==0` ‚Üí UB. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

---

### ¬ß7.31.15 Future library directions ‚Äî `<wchar.h>` (C11 numbering; ¬ß7.26.12 in C99)

- ¬ß7.31.15p1 ‚Äî Function names beginning with `wcs` + a lowercase letter may be added to `<wchar.h>`; the `wcs` prefix is reserved in this context. (C11; ¬ß7.26.12 in C99) ‚Äî (spec; reservation/not separately testable ‚Äî mcc neither defines extra `wcs*` names nor diagnoses program use, matching gcc/clang)

### ¬ß7.31.16 Future library directions ‚Äî `<wctype.h>` (C11 numbering; ¬ß7.26.13 in C99)

- ¬ß7.31.16p1 ‚Äî Function names beginning with `is` or `to` + a lowercase letter may be added to `<wctype.h>`; these prefixes are reserved in this context. (C11; ¬ß7.26.13 in C99) ‚Äî (spec; reservation/not separately testable)

> Note: `<uchar.h>` (¬ß7.28) has no entry under ¬ß7.31 (Future library directions) in C11.


## Annexes F, G, K (normative)

> mcc status: 188 TODO items in this section; **no mcc-specific gap remains** (no `mcc:‚úó`/`~` where mcc diverges from a gcc==clang consensus). The `isgreater`/`isless`-family quiet-NaN FE item (¬ßF.10.11p1) in the conditional-conformant numeric annexes that mcc *opts into* (by defining `__STDC_IEC_559__` and `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__`) conforms: mcc predefines `__GNUC__ 4` and expands those comparison macros to the non-trapping `__builtin_isgreater`/`__builtin_isless`/‚Ä¶, so `isgreater(NaN,1.0)` raises no FE_INVALID and matches gcc/clang. mcc's complex `*` and `/` implement the ¬ßG.5.1 infinity-recovery tables (¬ßG.5.1p3/p4, umbrella ¬ßG.5p2), matching gcc/clang. The `_Imaginary`-type rows (¬ßG.2‚Äì¬ßG.7) are consensus `‚úó` ‚Äî none of the three implement `_Imaginary`, which is itself conforming. Annex K is **not provided by any of the three** on glibc (no `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`) ‚Äî that omission is itself conforming, so no Annex-K item is an mcc-specific gap. All `<math.h>`/`<complex.h>`/`<fenv.h>` *runtime* special-value behavior is supplied by glibc libm and is therefore byte-identical across mcc/gcc/clang.

> Numbering note: C11 (N1570) inserted **¬ßF.6 The return statement** and renumbered everything after it, so the old C99 (N1256) ¬ßF.6‚Äì¬ßF.9 became C11 ¬ßF.7‚Äì¬ßF.10. Headings below use the **C11** numbers with the C99 number noted in parentheses.
> Conditional-conformance note: Annexes F and G are normative but *conditional* ‚Äî their requirements bind only when the implementation defines `__STDC_IEC_559__` (Annex F) / `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__` (Annex G). **mcc defines BOTH** (probed: `__STDC_IEC_559__=1`, `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__=1`, same as gcc/clang), so it has opted into the full Annex F/G binding. Annex K is **C11-only and entirely optional**: its identifiers exist only when the implementation defines `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` *and* the program defines `__STDC_WANT_LIB_EXT1__` to the integer constant `1` before first including the relevant header. **None of mcc/gcc/clang define `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`** (probed: all `undef`).

### Conditional-conformance macros (gap-probe summary)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF/¬ßG/¬ßK ‚Äî `__STDC_IEC_559__`, `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__`, `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` predefined-macro presence. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: IEC_559=1, IEC_559_COMPLEX=1, LIB_EXT1 undefined ‚Äî identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8 ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__` shall be **undefined** when complex types are supported. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (undefined in all three; `double _Complex` works)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2.2 / ¬ß7.12 ‚Äî `<math.h>` shall define `math_errhandling` and `MATH_ERREXCEPT`; when Annex F binds, `MATH_ERREXCEPT` shall be set. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: `math_errhandling==3`, `MATH_ERREXCEPT` bit set ‚Äî glibc)

### ¬ßF.1 Introduction
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.1p1 ‚Äî An implementation that defines `__STDC_IEC_559__` shall conform to the specifications in this annex (the IEC 60559:1989 / IEEE 754 binding); an implementation that does not define `__STDC_IEC_559__` is not required to conform to it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three define it and meet the format requirements below)
- ¬ßF.1p1 ‚Äî Where a binding between the C language and IEC 60559 is indicated, the IEC 60559-specified behavior is adopted by reference unless stated otherwise. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßF.1p2 (footnote) ‚Äî IEC 60559 (originally IEC 559:1989) floating-point arithmetic is also the IEEE 754 / IEEE 854 standard; the terms are used interchangeably in this annex. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ßF.2 Types
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2p1 ‚Äî The C `float` type shall match the IEC 60559 single format; the `double` type shall match the IEC 60559 double format. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (FLT_RADIX=2, FLT/DBL mantissa/exp values identical)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2p1 ‚Äî `long double` shall match an IEC 60559 extended format, else a non-IEC-60559 extended format, else the IEC 60559 double format; any non-IEC-60559 extended `long double` shall have more precision than `double` and at least the range of `double`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: `LDBL_MANT_DIG=64`, `LDBL_MAX_EXP=16384` ‚Äî the x86 80-bit double-extended format)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2p1 (footnote) ‚Äî Permitted `long double` choices include the IEC 60559 double-extended format (e.g. the 80-bit format with p ‚â• 64, e_max ‚â• 16383) or plain IEC 60559 double; the recommended extended-format parameters are documented for reference. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (80-bit, p=64, e_max=16383 ‚Äî satisfies the recommended parameters)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2p2 ‚Äî The values of the `FLT_*`, `DBL_*`, and `LDBL_*` characteristics in `<float.h>` shall be consistent with the IEC 60559 formats actually in use. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `<float.h>` values identical across all three)

#### ¬ßF.2.1 Infinities, signed zeros, and NaNs
- ¬ßF.2.1p1 ‚Äî This annex uses *NaN* to denote a quiet NaN; signaling NaNs (where supported) are denoted by *signaling NaN* explicitly. ‚Äî (spec; terminology ‚Äî not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2.1p1 ‚Äî The `INFINITY` macro in `<math.h>` shall expand to a constant expression of type `float` representing positive (or unsigned) infinity. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`sizeof(INFINITY)==sizeof(float)`; `isinf(INFINITY)` true ‚Äî glibc `<math.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2.1p1 ‚Äî The `NAN` macro in `<math.h>` shall be defined **if and only if** the implementation supports quiet NaNs for `float`, expanding to a quiet-NaN `float` constant. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`NAN` defined, `isnan(NAN)` true ‚Äî glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.2.1p1 ‚Äî Operations and functions of this annex distinguish `+0` from `‚àí0` and shall observe the sign of zero wherever IEC 60559 specifies it. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `signbit(-0.0-0.0)` etc. ‚Äî sign of zero preserved by all three)

### ¬ßF.3 Operators and functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p1 ‚Äî The C unary `‚àí` and binary `+`, `‚àí`, `*`, `/` operators provide the IEC 60559 negate/add/subtract/multiply/divide ‚Äî correctly rounded in the current rounding direction and signaling the IEC 60559 exceptions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed: `1.0/0.0` raises FE_DIVBYZERO under all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p1 ‚Äî The `sqrtf`/`sqrt`/`sqrtl` functions provide the IEC 60559 (correctly rounded) square root. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p1 ‚Äî The `remainder` family ‚Üí IEC 60559 *remainder*; `rint` ‚Üí round-to-integer in the current mode; `nearbyint` ‚Üí same but no "inexact". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p1 ‚Äî `<fenv.h>` (`fegetround`/`fesetround`, the exception-flag functions, the `FE_*` macros) provides the IEC 60559 rounding modes (`FE_TONEAREST`/`FE_TOWARDZERO`/`FE_UPWARD`/`FE_DOWNWARD`) and the five status flags (`FE_INVALID`/`FE_DIVBYZERO`/`FE_OVERFLOW`/`FE_UNDERFLOW`/`FE_INEXACT`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed: `fesetround(FE_UPWARD)`+`fegetround` round-trips; `feclearexcept`/`fetestexcept` work ‚Äî system `<fenv.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p1 ‚Äî `copysign`‚Üícopysign; `scalbn`/`scalbln`‚Üíscalb; `logb`‚Üílogb; `nextafter`/`nexttoward`‚Üínextafter; `fmod`‚Üímod; `ceil`/`floor`/`trunc`/`round`‚Üíround-to-integral; binary‚Üîdecimal in `<stdlib.h>`/`<stdio.h>`/`<wchar.h>`‚ÜíIEC 60559 conversions. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm/libc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p1 ‚Äî The `fma` family provides the IEC 60559 fused multiply-add (single final rounding). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm `fma`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p2 ‚Äî `feraiseexcept`/`feclearexcept`/`fetestexcept` and `fegetexceptflag`/`fesetexceptflag` provide status-flag manipulation; `feholdexcept`/`feupdateenv` and `fegetenv`/`fesetenv` save/restore the environment. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (system `<fenv.h>`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.3p3 ‚Äî Conversion between integer and floating types, and between floating types, shall round per the current rounding direction and signal the IEC 60559 exceptions (detailed in ¬ßF.4). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (hardware FP conversions emitted by all three)

### ¬ßF.4 Floating to integer conversion
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.4p1 ‚Äî Finite in-range-but-inexact float‚Üíinteger truncates toward zero; whether "inexact" is raised is unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (truncation toward zero; cvttsd2si on x86)
- [~] ¬ßF.4p1 ‚Äî float‚Üíinteger of ‚àû/NaN, or a truncated value out of the destination range, raises "invalid" and the result is unspecified. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (raising of the flag is hardware-dependent; mcc emits the same cvtt instruction as gcc/clang ‚Äî no observable divergence)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî Integer‚Üífloating that cannot be represented exactly rounds per the current rounding direction and raises "inexact". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (hardware cvtsi2sd)

### ¬ßF.5 Binary-decimal conversion
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.5p1 ‚Äî Conversion from the widest IEC 60559 format to a `DECIMAL_DIG`-digit decimal string and back is the identity (exact round-trip). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`DECIMAL_DIG=21` in all three; round-trip via glibc strtold/printf)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.5p2 ‚Äî Conversions in `strtod`/`scanf`/`printf` shall be correctly rounded as far as required and honor the current rounding direction. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.5p3 ‚Äî A binary‚Üîdecimal conversion that overflows raises "overflow", underflows raises "underflow", is inexact raises "inexact". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.5 (added) ‚Äî `<float.h>` shall define `DECIMAL_DIG` (C99) ‚Äî the number of decimal digits for the widest supported format. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `DECIMAL_DIG=21`)

### ¬ßF.6 The return statement (C11) *(new in C11; no C99 counterpart)*
> C99 had no ¬ßF.6; the subclause was added in C11 and pushed C99 ¬ßF.6‚Äì¬ßF.9 to C11 ¬ßF.7‚Äì¬ßF.10.
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.6p1 (C11) ‚Äî If the return expression is evaluated in a format wider than the return type (per `FLT_EVAL_METHOD`), it is converted as if by assignment to the return type before returning. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (NA in practice: `FLT_EVAL_METHOD==0` in all three ‚Äî no excess precision, so no narrowing needed)

### ¬ßF.7 Contracted expressions *(C99 ¬ßF.6)*
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.7p1 ‚Äî A contracted expression is correctly rounded once for the whole expression and treats infinities/NaNs/signed-zeros/subnormals/rounding consistently. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (at -O0 none contract; default `FP_CONTRACT` honored)
- [ ] ¬ßF.7p2 ‚Äî A contracted expression raises exceptions consistently with non-contracted evaluation, except "inexact"/"underflow"/"overflow" only for the final single-rounded result. ‚Äî (spec; not separately observable without contraction)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.7p3 ‚Äî `<math.h>` defines the `FP_CONTRACT` pragma; its default state is implementation-defined and shall be documented. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc parses `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT` silently ‚Äî handled in `src/mccpp.c:1926`; gcc warns "ignoring #pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT" under -Wall; clang accepts silently)

### ¬ßF.8 Floating-point environment *(C99 ¬ßF.7)*
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.8p1 ‚Äî Governed by the `FENV_ACCESS` pragma; `<fenv.h>` gives access to the IEC 60559 status flags and control modes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:~ clang:‚úì (mcc recognizes `#pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS` ‚Äî `src/mccpp.c:1928`, and acts on it in codegen `src/mccgen.c:2509`; gcc warns "ignoring #pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS"; clang accepts)

#### ¬ßF.8.1 Environment management
- [~] ¬ßF.8.1p1 ‚Äî Code that tests flags or changes modes must execute as if `FENV_ACCESS` were ON so implicit flag/mode effects are observed. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (all three give correct flag/mode behavior at -O0; full `FENV_ACCESS ON` value-fencing is not guaranteed under optimization by any)

#### ¬ßF.8.2 Translation
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.8.2p1 ‚Äî During translation the IEC 60559 default modes are in effect: round to nearest; all exceptions cleared; no traps. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (constant folding uses round-to-nearest in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.8.2p2 ‚Äî Translation-time FP evaluation uses round-to-nearest and cannot depend on a runtime-set rounding mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (compile-time constant folding is round-to-nearest)

#### ¬ßF.8.3 Execution
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.8.3p1 ‚Äî At program startup the FP environment is the default: round-to-nearest, all flags clear, no traps. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (C runtime/`crt` sets default FP env; probed `fegetround`==FE_TONEAREST at start)

#### ¬ßF.8.4 Constant expressions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.8.4p1 ‚Äî A required constant expression is evaluated in the default environment; otherwise it may be evaluated during execution and observe the runtime rounding mode under `FENV_ACCESS ON`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc folds required constants at translation; see ¬ßF.8.2)
- [~] ¬ßF.8.4p2 ‚Äî Rounding a constant with the runtime mode rather than the default is permitted only where the value need not be a constant expression and `FENV_ACCESS` is ON. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (no observable divergence; mcc honors FENV_ACCESS in codegen)

#### ¬ßF.8.5 Initialization
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.8.5p1 ‚Äî Non-constant FP initializers are evaluated (and raise exceptions) at the point of initialization under the runtime environment; constant-expression initializers are evaluated in the default environment at translation time. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (runtime initializers emit runtime FP code in all three)

#### ¬ßF.8.6 Changing the environment
- ¬ßF.8.6p1 ‚Äî Code that changes modes or tests/clears flags must execute under `FENV_ACCESS ON`; a function that changes the environment shall restore it on return unless documented otherwise. ‚Äî (spec/library convention; not a compiler property ‚Äî not separately testable)
- [~] ¬ßF.8.6p2 ‚Äî Operations under `FENV_ACCESS` OFF may assume the default environment and be optimized; under ON the visible flag/mode semantics shall be preserved. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (mcc fences runtime-rounding ops under FENV_ACCESS ON per `src/mccgen.c:2509`; no observed divergence)

### ¬ßF.9 Optimization *(C99 ¬ßF.8)*
- [ ] ¬ßF.9p1 ‚Äî Identifies transformations that may/may not be applied while preserving IEC 60559 semantics. ‚Äî (spec; rules tested individually below)

#### ¬ßF.9.1 Floating-point arithmetic and value-changing optimizations
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.1p1 ‚Äî The implementation shall not apply optimizations that change the value (including the sign of a zero) of an FP expression except as permitted below. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed at -O0 and -O2; none apply value-changing FP transforms by default ‚Äî `-ffast-math`/`-funsafe-math-optimizations` would be the opt-in)

#### ¬ßF.9.2 Expression transformations
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `x/2` ‚Üî `x*0.5` is **allowed**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (exact; no divergence)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `1*x` ‚Üí `x` and `x/1` ‚Üí `x` are **allowed**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `x/x` ‚Üí `1.0` is **NOT allowed**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none fold `x/x`; would be wrong for 0/‚àû/NaN)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `x*0.0` ‚Üí `0.0` is **NOT allowed**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `INFINITY*0.0` ‚Üí NaN in all three at -O0 and -O2)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `x+0.0` ‚Üí `x` is **NOT allowed** (fails for x=‚àí0.0). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed: `f(-0.0)=x+0.0` yields `+0.0` (signbit 0) in all three ‚Äî the forbidden fold is NOT applied)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `x‚àí0.0` ‚Üí `x` is **allowed**. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed: `x-0.0` of ‚àí0.0 stays ‚àí0.0 (signbit set) in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `0.0‚àíx` ‚Üí `‚àíx` is **NOT allowed** in general; `‚àíx` vs `0.0‚àíx` must be distinguished. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none mis-fold this by default)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî `x‚àíy` ‚Üî `‚àí(y‚àíx)` is **NOT allowed** (sign-of-zero). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.2 ‚Äî Re-association of `+`/`*` (changing roundings) is **NOT allowed** unless provably identical. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (no FP reassociation without `-fassociative-math`/`-ffast-math`)

#### ¬ßF.9.3 Relational operators
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.3p1 ‚Äî `x != x` ‚Üí `false` and `x == x` ‚Üí `true` are **NOT allowed** (wrong for NaN). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed: `NAN==NAN` is false, `NAN!=NAN` is true at runtime in all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.9.3p2 ‚Äî `x < y` and `!(x >= y)` are not equivalent when an operand is NaN; the implementation shall not interconvert them. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none perform the De-Morgan FP rewrite by default)

### ¬ßF.10 Mathematics `<math.h>` *(C99 ¬ßF.9)*
> All ¬ßF.10.x function special-value behavior below is supplied by **glibc libm**, which mcc links exactly as gcc/clang do (mcc bundles no `<math.h>`/libm ‚Äî it uses the system ones). Consequently every special-value result is byte-identical across the three. Tags reflect that shared-runtime reality; the lone mcc-specific divergence in this clause is the comparison macros of ¬ßF.10.11.
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10p1 ‚Äî Each function produces a correctly rounded result honoring the current rounding direction where IEC 60559 specifies it, and raises exceptions consistently. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10p2 ‚Äî "invalid" for domain error, "divide-by-zero" for pole, "overflow"/"underflow" for range; prescribed values for ¬±0/¬±‚àû/NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10p3 ‚Äî A NaN argument (except where fully specified) is returned as a NaN with no exception raised solely for a quiet NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10p4 ‚Äî A function with >1 floating argument computes as if infinitely precise and rounds once. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10p5 ‚Äî "inexact"/subnormal-"underflow" behavior follows IEC 60559; no spurious exceptions for in-domain arguments. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)

#### ¬ßF.10.1 Trigonometric functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.1 ‚Äî `acos(1)`‚Üí+0; `acos(|x|>1)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; probed `acos(1.0)==0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.2 ‚Äî `asin(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `asin(|x|>1)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.3 ‚Äî `atan(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `atan(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±œÄ/2. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.4 ‚Äî `atan2` full IEC 60559 quadrant table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.5 ‚Äî `cos(¬±0)`‚Üí1; `cos(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.6 ‚Äî `sin(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `sin(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc; probed `sin(0.0)==0`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.1.7 ‚Äî `tan(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `tan(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.2 Hyperbolic functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.2.1 ‚Äî `acosh(1)`‚Üí+0; `acosh(x<1)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN; `acosh(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.2.2 ‚Äî `asinh(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `asinh(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.2.3 ‚Äî `atanh(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `atanh(¬±1)`‚Üí"divide-by-zero",¬±‚àû; `atanh(|x|>1)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.2.4 ‚Äî `cosh(¬±0)`‚Üí1; `cosh(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.2.5 ‚Äî `sinh(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `sinh(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.2.6 ‚Äî `tanh(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `tanh(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.3 Exponential and logarithmic functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.1 ‚Äî `exp(¬±0)`‚Üí1; `exp(‚àí‚àû)`‚Üí+0; `exp(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.2 ‚Äî `exp2(¬±0)`‚Üí1; `exp2(‚àí‚àû)`‚Üí+0; `exp2(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.3 ‚Äî `expm1(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `expm1(‚àí‚àû)`‚Üí‚àí1; `expm1(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.4 ‚Äî `frexp` special values; stored exponent unspecified for ¬±0/¬±‚àû/NaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.5 ‚Äî `ilogb(0)`‚Üí"invalid",`FP_ILOGB0`; `ilogb(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí"invalid",`INT_MAX`; `ilogb(NaN)`‚Üí"invalid",`FP_ILOGBNAN`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.6 ‚Äî `ldexp(x,0)`‚Üíx; `ldexp(¬±0/¬±‚àû,n)`‚Üíarg; overflow/underflow raise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.7 ‚Äî `log(¬±0)`‚Üí"divide-by-zero",‚àí‚àû; `log(1)`‚Üí+0; `log(x<0)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN; `log(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.8 ‚Äî `log10` same special values as `log`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.9 ‚Äî `log1p(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `log1p(‚àí1)`‚Üí"divide-by-zero",‚àí‚àû; `log1p(x<‚àí1)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN; `log1p(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.10 ‚Äî `log2(¬±0)`‚Üí"divide-by-zero",‚àí‚àû; `log2(1)`‚Üí+0; `log2(x<0)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN; `log2(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.11 ‚Äî `logb(¬±0)`‚Üí"divide-by-zero",‚àí‚àû; `logb(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû; `logb(¬±1)`‚Üí+0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.12 ‚Äî `modf(¬±0,iptr)`‚Üí¬±0,stores¬±0; `modf(¬±‚àû,iptr)`‚Üí¬±0,stores¬±‚àû; `modf(NaN,iptr)`‚ÜíNaN,storesNaN. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.3.13 ‚Äî `scalbn`/`scalbln`: ¬±0/¬±‚àû‚Üíarg; else x¬∑FLT_RADIX^n, correctly rounded with overflow/underflow. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.4 Power and absolute-value functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.4.1 ‚Äî `cbrt(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `cbrt(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.4.2 ‚Äî `fabs(¬±0)`‚Üí+0; `fabs(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû; `fabs(NaN)`‚ÜíNaN; never raises. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc / `__builtin_fabs`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.4.3 ‚Äî `hypot(x,¬±‚àû)`=`hypot(¬±‚àû,y)`‚Üí+‚àû for any other operand incl. NaN; `hypot` symmetric in sign/order. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.4.4 ‚Äî `pow` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.4.5 ‚Äî `sqrt(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `sqrt(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû; `sqrt(x<0)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN; correctly rounded. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc / hardware `sqrtsd`)

#### ¬ßF.10.5 Error and gamma functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.5.1 ‚Äî `erf(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `erf(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±1. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.5.2 ‚Äî `erfc(‚àí‚àû)`‚Üí2; `erfc(+‚àû)`‚Üí+0; may raise "underflow" for large +x. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.5.3 ‚Äî `lgamma(1)`/`lgamma(2)`‚Üí+0; non-positive integer‚Üí"divide-by-zero",+‚àû; `lgamma(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.5.4 ‚Äî `tgamma(¬±0)`‚Üí"divide-by-zero",¬±‚àû; negative integer‚Üí"invalid",NaN; `tgamma(‚àí‚àû)`‚Üí"invalid",NaN; `tgamma(+‚àû)`‚Üí+‚àû. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.6 Nearest integer functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.1 ‚Äî `ceil(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `ceil(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû; whether "inexact" is raised is impl-defined. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.2 ‚Äî `floor(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `floor(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû; "inexact" as `ceil`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.3 ‚Äî `nearbyint(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `nearbyint(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû; shall **not** raise "inexact". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.4 ‚Äî `rint(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `rint(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû; may raise "inexact". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.5 ‚Äî `lrint`/`llrint`: out-of-range‚Üí"invalid",unspecified; else round per current mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.6 ‚Äî `round(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `round(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû; halfway away from zero regardless of mode. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.7 ‚Äî `lround`/`llround`: out-of-range‚Üí"invalid",unspecified; halfway away from zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.6.8 ‚Äî `trunc(¬±0)`‚Üí¬±0; `trunc(¬±‚àû)`‚Üí¬±‚àû; toward zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.7 Remainder functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.7.1 ‚Äî `fmod` special values (¬±0, finite/¬±‚àû, ¬±‚àû‚Üí"invalid", ¬±0 divisor‚Üí"invalid"). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.7.2 ‚Äî `remainder` special values (mirrors `fmod` invalid cases). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.7.3 ‚Äî `remquo` returns `remainder`'s value for special cases and stores low-order quotient bits with sign of x/y. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.8 Manipulation functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.8.1 ‚Äî `copysign(x,y)`‚Üíx with sign of y (even NaN); never raises. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc / `__builtin_copysign`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.8.2 ‚Äî `nan("‚Ä¶")`‚Üíquiet NaN per tag; never raises. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.8.3 ‚Äî `nextafter(x,y)` next representable; `nextafter(x,x)`‚Üíx; overflow‚Üí"overflow"+"inexact"; subnormal/underflow‚Üí"underflow"+"inexact". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.8.4 ‚Äî `nexttoward` like `nextafter` with `long double` second arg; `nexttoward(x,x)`‚Üíx converted to type of x. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.9 Maximum, minimum, and positive difference functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.9.1 ‚Äî `fdim(x,y)`‚Üíx‚àíy if x>y else +0; range error‚Üí"overflow". ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.9.2 ‚Äî `fmax` returns larger; NaN ignored vs a number; `fmax(NaN,NaN)`‚ÜíNaN; no exception for NaN arg. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.9.3 ‚Äî `fmin` returns smaller; NaN ignored vs a number; `fmin(NaN,NaN)`‚ÜíNaN; no exception for NaN arg. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc)

#### ¬ßF.10.10 Floating multiply-add
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.10.1 ‚Äî `fma(x,y,z)` correctly rounded fused; 0¬∑‚àû/‚àû¬∑0‚Üí"invalid",NaN even if z NaN; ‚àû + oppositely-signed ‚àû‚Üí"invalid",NaN; else single-rounded with overflow/underflow/inexact only for the final result. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc `fma`)

#### ¬ßF.10.11 Comparison macros (C11)
> C99 placed the `<math.h>` comparison-macro quiet-NaN guarantee in ¬ßF.9 prose; C11 gives it its own subclause ¬ßF.10.11.
- [‚úì] ¬ßF.10.11p1 (C11) ‚Äî `isgreater`, `isgreaterequal`, `isless`, `islessequal`, `islessgreater`, `isunordered` shall **not** raise "invalid" when an argument is a quiet NaN (unlike the bare `<`/`>`/`<=`/`>=`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `isgreater(NaN,1.0)` ‚Äî mcc raises no `FE_INVALID` and returns `0`, identical to gcc/clang, while the bare `NaN > 1.0` still raises `FE_INVALID` on all three. mcc predefines `__GNUC__ 4`, so glibc's `<math.h>` expands these to the non-trapping `__builtin_isgreater`/`__builtin_isless`/‚Ä¶ forms.)

### ¬ßG.1 Introduction
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.1p1 ‚Äî An implementation that defines `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__` shall conform to this annex; it should also define `__STDC_IEC_559__`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc defines both ‚Äî probed)
- ¬ßG.1p2 (note) ‚Äî This annex augments Annex F with complex types; its complex-operation specs take precedence over the general `<complex.h>` semantics. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ßG.2 Types
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.2p1 ‚Äî One complex type per real floating type (`float`/`double`/`long double _Complex`), same representation/alignment as an array of two reals, real part first. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three: `double _Complex` is two contiguous doubles, real first; probed `cimag`/`creal`)
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.2p1 ‚Äî One imaginary type per real floating type (`float`/`double`/`long double _Imaginary`), required as a conforming extension whenever this annex applies. ‚Äî **mcc:‚úó gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó** (consensus gap ‚Äî NOT mcc-specific: all three reject `_Imaginary` ‚Äî mcc "imaginary types are not supported", clang same, gcc "expected identifier". Strictly nonconforming for an Annex-G implementation, but identical across the three.)
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.2p2 ‚Äî `<complex.h>` shall define `_Imaginary_I`; when imaginary types are supported, `I` expands to `_Imaginary_I` (not `_Complex_I`). ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (none define `_Imaginary_I` ‚Äî probed `#ifdef` false in all three; `I` expands to `_Complex_I` everywhere)

### ¬ßG.3 Conventions
- [ ] ¬ßG.3p1 ‚Äî A complex/imaginary value with ‚â•1 infinite part is an *infinity*, even if its other part is NaN. ‚Äî (spec/convention; exercised by ¬ßG.5/¬ßG.6 behavior)
- ¬ßG.3p1 ‚Äî A complex/imaginary value is *finite* iff both parts are finite. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßG.3p1 ‚Äî A complex/imaginary value is *zero* if each part is a (possibly signed) zero. ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ßG.4 Conversions
#### ¬ßG.4.1 Imaginary types
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.4.1p1 ‚Äî Conversions among imaginary types follow the real-floating rules. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types in any ‚Äî see ¬ßG.2p1)

#### ¬ßG.4.2 Real and imaginary
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.4.2p1 ‚Äî Imaginary‚Üíreal (other than `_Bool`) yields +0. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types)
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.4.2p2 ‚Äî Real‚Üíimaginary yields +imaginary-zero. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types)

#### ¬ßG.4.3 Imaginary and complex
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.4.3p1 ‚Äî Imaginary‚Üícomplex yields +0 real part, the value as imaginary part. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types)
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.4.3p2 ‚Äî Complex‚Üíimaginary yields the imaginary part (real part discarded). ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types)

### ¬ßG.5 Binary operators
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.5p1 ‚Äî `*`/`/`/`+`/`‚àí` on complex/imaginary/real yield the type per the usual arithmetic conversions extended to imaginary types and follow ¬ßG.5.1‚Äì¬ßG.5.2. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (real‚Üîcomplex `+`/`‚àí` and `*`/`/` work in mcc; the imaginary-type axis is absent in all three; mcc's complex `*`/`/` value handling follows the ¬ßG.5.1p3/p4 infinity-recovery tables, matching gcc/clang)
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.5p2 ‚Äî Every binary-operator table's result-type AND special-value handling shall be exactly as specified (not the na√Øve arithmetic-conversion implementation). ‚Äî **mcc:‚úì** gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc's complex `*` and `/` implement the ¬ßG.5.1 infinity-recovery tables, matching gcc/clang ‚Äî see the two items below)

#### ¬ßG.5.1 Multiplicative operators
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.5.1p1 ‚Äî real¬∑imaginary‚Üíimaginary; imaginary¬∑imaginary‚Üíreal; imaginary/imaginary‚Üíreal. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types, so the imaginary-result typing cannot be exercised in any)
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.5.1p2 ‚Äî `imaginary*imaginary` is the negated product of the imaginary parts (real); `imaginary/imaginary` is the real quotient; the per-operand tables shall be honored. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types)
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.5.1p3 ‚Äî Complex `*` uses `(ac‚àíbd)+(ad+bc)i`, but a na√Øve NaN+iNaN result with an infinite operand shall be recovered to the proper signed infinity via the ¬ßG.5.1p3 algorithm. ‚Äî **mcc:‚úì** gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `(INFINITY+0i)*(1+1i)` ‚Üí mcc gives `inf+inf¬∑i`, matching gcc/clang. mcc applies `__muldc3`-style infinity recovery to the complex multiply.)
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.5.1p4 ‚Äî Complex `/` uses `(a+bi)/(c+di)` with recovery: infinite dividend√∑finite divisor‚Üíinfinity; infinite divisor‚ÜíNaN-or-zero, per the ¬ßG.5.1p4 algorithm. ‚Äî **mcc:‚úì** gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (probed `(1+1i)/(INFINITY+INFINITY¬∑i)` ‚Üí mcc gives `0‚àí0i` (divisor is infinite, so result is `0`), matching gcc/clang. mcc applies `__divdc3`-style recovery/scaling to the complex divide.)
- [~] ¬ßG.5.1p5 ‚Äî The `CX_LIMITED_RANGE` pragma (¬ß7.3.4) permits the na√Øve formulas (no recovery, no scaling); default "off". ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (mcc *recognizes* `#pragma STDC CX_LIMITED_RANGE` ‚Äî `src/mccpp.c:1930`, `src/mccgen.c:4882` ‚Äî and gcc warns "ignoring" it; but because mcc's default-off path is *already* the na√Øve formula (the ¬ßG.5.1p3/p4 gap), the pragma has no observable effect in mcc. gcc/clang recover by default and the pragma is a no-op at -O0 in practice.)

#### ¬ßG.5.2 Additive operators
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.5.2p1 ‚Äî real¬±imaginary‚Üícomplex with parts from the respective operands, no cross-cancellation, signs of zeros preserved. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types; real¬±complex works)
