- [~] ¬ßG.5.2p2 ‚Äî imaginary¬±imaginary‚Üíimaginary; complex¬±complex‚Üícomponentwise; signed zeros/infinities handled componentwise. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (complex¬±complex componentwise add works identically in all three; the imaginary¬±imaginary half is unreachable ‚Äî no imaginary types)

### ¬ßG.6 Complex arithmetic `<complex.h>`
> All ¬ßG.6.x special-value behavior is supplied by **glibc libm** (mcc bundles `runtime/include/complex.h` declaring the functions, but the implementations are glibc's), so results are identical across the three. `cpow` and any function that internally multiplies/divides complex values goes through glibc's own `__muldc3`/careful code; mcc's own inline complex `*`/`/` now applies the same ¬ßG.5.1 infinity recovery, so the two paths agree.
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6p1 ‚Äî Each listed function returns the specified result for the special arguments and raises/does-not-raise exceptions as specified; "NaN+iNaN" signals "invalid" only where indicated. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6p2 ‚Äî Functions are continuous onto both sides of their branch cuts, taking the sign of zero into account. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6p3 ‚Äî The non-tabulated functions (`cacos`/`casin`/`catan`, `ccos`/`csin`/`ctan`, the `*sinh`/`*tanh`/`*cosh` companions, `csqrt`) are defined via the ¬ßG.6 identities and honor them for special values. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6p4 ‚Äî Each function maps `conj(z)` to `conj(f(z))` except where the branch cut requires otherwise. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)

#### ¬ßG.6.1 Trigonometric functions
##### ¬ßG.6.1.1 The `cacos` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.1.1p1 ‚Äî `cacos` full special-value table with ¬ßG.6p4 conjugate symmetry. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)

#### ¬ßG.6.2 Hyperbolic functions
##### ¬ßG.6.2.1 The `cacosh` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.2.1p1 ‚Äî `cacosh` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.2.2 The `casinh` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.2.2p1 ‚Äî `casinh` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.2.3 The `catanh` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.2.3p1 ‚Äî `catanh` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.2.4 The `ccosh` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.2.4p1 ‚Äî `ccosh` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.2.5 The `csinh` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.2.5p1 ‚Äî `csinh` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.2.6 The `ctanh` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.2.6p1 ‚Äî `ctanh` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)

#### ¬ßG.6.3 Exponential and logarithmic functions
##### ¬ßG.6.3.1 The `cexp` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.3.1p1 ‚Äî `cexp` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.3.2 The `clog` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.3.2p1 ‚Äî `clog` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)

#### ¬ßG.6.4 Power and absolute-value functions
##### ¬ßG.6.4.1 The `cpow` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.4.1p1 ‚Äî `cpow(z,w)`=`cexp(w¬∑clog(z))`; branch-cut/continuity of ¬ßG.6p2 shall hold. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm `cpow`; the internal complex multiply is glibc's, not mcc's inline operator)
##### ¬ßG.6.4.2 The `csqrt` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.4.2p1 ‚Äî `csqrt` full special-value table. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm)
##### ¬ßG.6.4.3 The `cabs` functions
- [‚úì] ¬ßG.6.4.3 ‚Äî `cabs(x+iy)`‚Üí+‚àû if either part infinite (even if other NaN); NaN if no infinity and ‚â•1 NaN; else `hypot(x,y)`. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (glibc libm `cabs`)

### ¬ßG.7 Type-generic math `<tgmath.h>`
- [~] ¬ßG.7p1 ‚Äî A type-generic macro for a `<complex.h>` function shall, for a complex argument, invoke the corresponding complex function with ¬ßG.6 special-value behavior; for an imaginary argument it determines the function/result type per ¬ßG.4. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:~ clang:~ (mcc bundles `runtime/include/tgmath.h`; complex-argument dispatch works in all three; the imaginary-argument axis is unreachable ‚Äî no imaginary types)
- [‚úó] ¬ßG.7p2 ‚Äî Where an imaginary argument can be handled by a real function on the imaginary part, the implementation may do so with the appropriate type/sign conversion. ‚Äî mcc:‚úó(consensus) gcc:‚úó clang:‚úó (no imaginary types in any)

### ¬ßK.1 Background *(C11; the entire Annex K is optional and conditional on `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`)*
> Annex K does not exist in C99; it is C11-only. **None of mcc/gcc/clang define `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`** (probed: all `undef`), so none provide Annex K. Because Annex K is optional, this omission is **conforming** ‚Äî therefore no Annex-K item below is an mcc-specific gap. The `_s` identifiers are simply absent in all three (glibc does not implement Annex K). Tags reflect "not provided; omission conforming".
- [‚úì] ¬ßK.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Annex K specifies optional bounds-checking interfaces; an implementation that defines `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` shall conform. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none define `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`; omission is conforming)
- [ ] ¬ßK.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Annex K identifiers are not declared/defined unless `__STDC_WANT_LIB_EXT1__` is defined as the integer constant `1` before the header is first included. ‚Äî (spec; not provided by any ‚Äî untestable when absent)

### ¬ßK.2 Scope
- [‚úì] ¬ßK.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî Annex K provides replacement/new functions and types supporting runtime-constraint checking; providing it is optional. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (optional; none provide it)
- [ ] ¬ßK.2p2 (C11) ‚Äî If defined, `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` shall expand to `201112L`. ‚Äî mcc:n/a gcc:n/a clang:n/a (undefined in all three ‚Äî vacuously satisfied)

### ¬ßK.3 Library
> Every item in ¬ßK.3 is **not provided by mcc/gcc/clang** (no `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__`; glibc ships no `_s` functions, no `errno_t`/`rsize_t`/`RSIZE_MAX`/`constraint_handler_t`). All are tagged `‚Äî (C11 Annex K optional; not provided by mcc/gcc/clang ‚Äî omission conforming)`; none is an mcc-specific gap.
#### ¬ßK.3.1 Introduction
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî Header identifiers visible only when `__STDC_WANT_LIB_EXT1__`==1 at inclusion; re-inclusion with a different definition has impl-defined effect. ‚Äî (C11 Annex K optional; not provided by mcc/gcc/clang ‚Äî omission conforming)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî Identifiers ending in `_s` plus the Annex K macros/types are reserved when an Annex K header is included with the extension enabled. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.3p1 (C11) ‚Äî Whether an Annex K function sets `errno` is unspecified unless documented. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî Each function has runtime-constraints; a violation calls the registered constraint handler. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.4p2 (C11) ‚Äî A function checks runtime-constraints before any other operation except those needed to detect the violation. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.4p3 (C11) ‚Äî After the handler returns, the function returns the indicated error value and does not perform its nominal operation. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.1.4p4 (C11) ‚Äî If a call violates ‚â•2 constraints, any one may be reported (which is unspecified). ‚Äî (not provided by any)

#### ¬ßK.3.2 Errors `<errno.h>`
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.2.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `<errno.h>` with the extension shall define `errno_t` as `int`. ‚Äî (not provided by any; probed `errno_t` undeclared)

#### ¬ßK.3.3 Common definitions `<stddef.h>`
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.3.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `<stddef.h>` with the extension shall define `rsize_t` = `size_t`. ‚Äî (not provided by any; mcc's bundled `runtime/include/stddef.h` has no `rsize_t`)

#### ¬ßK.3.4 Integer types `<stdint.h>`
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.4.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `<stdint.h>` with the extension shall define `RSIZE_MAX` (recommended ‚â§ `SIZE_MAX >> 1`). ‚Äî (not provided by any; mcc's bundled `runtime/include/stdint.h` has no `RSIZE_MAX`)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.4.1p2 (C11) ‚Äî Sizes > `RSIZE_MAX` are treated as runtime-constraint violations. ‚Äî (not provided by any)

#### ¬ßK.3.5 Input/output `<stdio.h>`
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `<stdio.h>` with the extension shall define `errno_t`, `rsize_t`, `L_tmpnam_s`, `TMP_MAX_S`, and the `_s` I/O functions. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.1.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `tmpfile_s` ‚Äî runtime-constraint `streamptr` non-null; creates/opens a temp binary file. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.1.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî `tmpnam_s(char*s, rsize_t maxsize)` ‚Äî writes a unique name; `TMP_MAX_S` bounds the guarantee. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.2.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `fopen_s` ‚Äî non-null streamptr/filename/mode; opens with default deny-other-access. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.2.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî `freopen_s` ‚Äî non-null newstreamptr/mode/stream (filename may be null). ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.1p1 (C11) ‚Äî `fprintf_s` ‚Äî non-null stream/format, no `%n`, no null `%s`. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.2p1 (C11) ‚Äî `fscanf_s` ‚Äî `%c`/`%s`/`%[` each take pointer + `rsize_t` count. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.3p1 (C11) ‚Äî `printf_s` ‚â° `fprintf_s(stdout,‚Ä¶)`. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.4p1 (C11) ‚Äî `scanf_s` ‚â° `fscanf_s` from `stdin`. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.5p1 (C11) ‚Äî `snprintf_s` ‚Äî `n`‚âÝ0, ‚â§`RSIZE_MAX`; always null-terminates when `n>0`. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.6p1 (C11) ‚Äî `sprintf_s` ‚Äî full result incl. null must fit in `n` (truncation is a violation). ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.7p1 (C11) ‚Äî `sscanf_s` ‚Äî reads from a string; `%c`/`%s`/`%[` take pointer + `rsize_t`. ‚Äî (not provided by any)
- [ ] ¬ßK.3.5.3.8p1 (C11) ‚Äî `vfprintf_s` ‚Äî va_list form of `fprintf_s`. ‚Äî (not provided by any)

## Annexes C, D, E, H, I, J (sequence points, UCN ranges, limits, portability)

> mcc status: 285 TODO checkboxes in this section; 7 are mcc-gaps vs the gcc==clang consensus
> (7 partial `~`, all in Annex D). There are no *hard* conformance gaps: mcc now
> validates UCNs in identifiers against the ¬ßD.1/¬ßD.2 range tables ‚Äî it rejects a `ÃÄ` combining mark as the *initial* character of an
> identifier (D.2) and rejects out-of-range names such as `Ôøø`, matching gcc/clang. The
> residual `~` rows are that mcc accepts the permitted D.1/D.2 blocks but does not enforce
> each as a closed set.
> Annex E (all `<limits.h>`/`<float.h>` minimum magnitudes, including the C11-added subnormal/
> decimal-digit/true-min macros) is fully satisfied. Annex I warnings are *informative/optional*, so
> mcc conforms even though it emits only the unknown-`#pragma` warning of the catalog. Annexes
> C, H, J are sequence-point / portability *catalogs* recapitulating normative text and are mostly
> not separately testable; the language-level sequence points and the testable `register`/`&`
> constraint match gcc==clang.

These annexes are the standard's cross-cutting catalogs. Annexes **C, D, E are normative**; Annexes **H, I, J are informative** (they recapitulate normative text stated elsewhere). Each checkbox below restates one catalog entry as a discrete requirement; the parenthetical `(6.x.y)` is the originating normative clause the annex points to. C11 (N1570) and C99 (N1256) agree on the *content* of these annexes except where tagged. The two main divergences are (a) clause-number drift ‚Äî the C11 library moved from ¬ß7.19/¬ß7.24/¬ß7.20.5 to ¬ß7.21/¬ß7.29/¬ß7.22.5, and initializers moved from ¬ß6.7.8 to ¬ß6.7.9 ‚Äî and (b) genuine list changes: Annex D's range list was wholly rewritten between C99 and C11, and Annex C/J absorbed the C11 "sequenced before" memory model and the C11-only library facilities (atomics, threads, `_Generic`, bounds-checked Annex K).

### ¬ßC Sequence points (normative)

> C11 restates Annex C under the "sequenced before"/"indeterminately sequenced" model of ¬ß5.1.2.3 and ¬ß6.5p2; the *enumerated* sequence points below are identical to C99, but the underlying relation changes from C99's "between the previous and next sequence point" to C11's partial-order sequencing. The C11-added sequence point "between the evaluation of a full declarator and any initialization" is folded into the full-expression list.

- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs between the evaluations of the function designator and the actual arguments in a function call and the actual call itself (6.5.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs between the evaluations of the first and second operands of the logical-AND operator `&&` (6.5.13). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (short-circuit suppresses RHS side effect, verified at runtime)
- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs between the evaluations of the first and second operands of the logical-OR operator `||` (6.5.14). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (RHS side effect suppressed when LHS true, verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs between the evaluations of the first and second operands of the comma operator `,` (6.5.17). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (LHS side effect committed before RHS, verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs between the evaluation of the first operand of the conditional operator `?:` and whichever of the second and third operands is evaluated (6.5.15). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (only the selected arm's side effect occurs, verified)
- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs between the evaluation of a full expression and the evaluation of the next full expression to be evaluated; the full expressions are those enumerated immediately below (6.8). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A full expression is an initializer that is not part of a compound literal (C99 6.7.8 / C11 6.7.9). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A full expression is the expression in an expression statement (6.8.3). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A full expression is the controlling expression of a selection statement (`if` or `switch`) (6.8.4). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A full expression is the controlling expression of a `while` or `do` statement (6.8.5). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A full expression is each of the three (optional) expressions of a `for` statement (6.8.5.3). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A full expression is the (optional) expression in a `return` statement (6.8.6.4). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- [‚úì] ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs immediately before a library function returns (7.1.4). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (provided by the shared host libc; not a codegen choice)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs after the actions associated with each formatted input/output function conversion specifier (C99 7.19.6, 7.24.2 / C11 7.21.6, 7.29.2). ‚Äî (spec; library-internal, not separately testable)
- ¬ßC ‚Äî A sequence point occurs immediately before and immediately after each call to a comparison function passed to `qsort`/`bsearch`, and also between any call to the comparison function and any movement of the objects passed as arguments to that call (C99 7.20.5 / C11 7.22.5). ‚Äî (spec; library-internal, not separately testable)

### ¬ßD Universal character names for identifiers ‚Äî C99 ¬ßD / C11 ¬ßD.1, ¬ßD.2 (normative)

> The range *lists* differ materially between standards. **C99 ¬ßD** enumerates an older, per-script catalog (Latin/Greek/Cyrillic/Armenian/Hebrew/Arabic/Devanagari/‚Ä¶ ranges) plus separate "special characters" and "digits" sublists. **C11** rewrote the annex around contiguous Unicode blocks and split it into **¬ßD.1 "Ranges of characters allowed"** and **¬ßD.2 "Ranges of characters disallowed initially."** The block ranges below are the **C11 ¬ßD.1/¬ßD.2** values; under C99 the same requirement (6.4.2.1) holds but against the older list.
>
> **mcc gap:** mcc does *not* validate UCNs in identifiers against these tables. It accepts the permitted ranges (‚úì) but also accepts UCNs in *no* permitted range (e.g. `Ôøø`) and accepts a ¬ßD.2 combining mark as the *initial* character ‚Äî both of which gcc and clang reject. mcc does still reject UCNs that name a basic-source-character (e.g. `A` = 'A'), per 6.4.3.

- [‚úì] ¬ßD ‚Äî A universal character name appearing in an identifier shall designate a character whose short identifier (ISO/IEC 10646) lies within one of the permitted ranges enumerated below (6.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects an out-of-range identifier character such as `Ôøø` ‚Äî "universal character Ôøø is not valid in an identifier" ‚Äî matching gcc/clang; raw-UTF-8 identifiers are validated against Annex D.1/D.2 like the `\u` escape form)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî Latin block permitted: 00A8, 00AA, 00AD, 00AF, 00B2‚Äì00B5, 00B7‚Äì00BA, 00BC‚Äì00BE, 00C0‚Äì00D6, 00D8‚Äì00F6, 00F8‚Äì00FF. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc accepts these but does not enforce the block as a closed set)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî General-extension blocks permitted: 0100‚Äì167F, 1681‚Äì180D, 180F‚Äì1FFF. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; not enforced)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî Format/punctuation-adjacent blocks permitted: 200B‚Äì200D, 202A‚Äì202E, 203F‚Äì2040, 2054, 2060‚Äì206F. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; not enforced)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî Symbol/CJK-radical blocks permitted: 2070‚Äì218F, 2460‚Äì24FF, 2776‚Äì2793, 2C00‚Äì2DFF, 2E80‚Äì2FFF. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; not enforced)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî CJK punctuation blocks permitted: 3004‚Äì3007, 3021‚Äì302F, 3031‚Äì303F. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; not enforced)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî Hangul/CJK ideograph block permitted: 3040‚ÄìD7FF. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; not enforced)
- [~] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî Compatibility/presentation blocks permitted: F900‚ÄìFD3D, FD40‚ÄìFDCF, FDF0‚ÄìFE44, FE47‚ÄìFFFD. ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (accepted; not enforced)
- [‚úì] ¬ßD.1 (C11) ‚Äî Supplementary-plane blocks permitted: 10000‚Äì1FFFD, 20000‚Äì2FFFD, 30000‚Äì3FFFD, 40000‚Äì4FFFD, 50000‚Äì5FFFD, 60000‚Äì6FFFD, 70000‚Äì7FFFD, 80000‚Äì8FFFD, 90000‚Äì9FFFD, A0000‚ÄìAFFFD, B0000‚ÄìBFFFD, C0000‚ÄìCFFFD, D0000‚ÄìDFFFD, E0000‚ÄìEFFFD. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (`\U00010000` accepted by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ßD.2 (C11) ‚Äî Combining-mark ranges 0300‚Äì036F, 1DC0‚Äì1DFF, 20D0‚Äì20FF, FE20‚ÄìFE2F shall not appear as the *initial* character of an identifier (allowed only in non-initial position). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc rejects `ÃÄ` as an identifier's first character ‚Äî "universal character ÃÄ is not valid as the first character of an identifier" ‚Äî matching gcc, which errors "not valid at the start of an identifier", and clang, which errors. Non-initial `aÃÄ` is accepted by all three; raw-UTF-8 identifiers are validated against Annex D.1/D.2 like the `\u` escape form.)
- [‚úì] ¬ßD (C99-only) ‚Äî Under C99 the allowed list is the older per-script enumeration (e.g. Latin 00C0‚Äì00D6/00D8‚Äì00F6/00F8‚Äì01F5/‚Ä¶, Greek 0384/0388‚Äì03CE/‚Ä¶, Cyrillic 0401‚Äì04F9, plus separate "special characters" 00B5/00B7/02D0/02D1/0387/0640/0E46/0EC6/3005/3031‚Äì3035/309D‚Äì309E/30FC‚Äì30FE and "digits" 0660‚Äì0669/06F0‚Äì06F9/0966‚Äì096F/‚Ä¶); an implementation conforming to C99 must validate against that table rather than the C11 blocks (6.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc validates identifier characters against the Annex D.1/D.2 (C11) blocks in both C99 and C11 modes, matching gcc/clang, which likewise apply the C11 table regardless of `-std`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßD ‚Äî *(gap)* A `\uXXXX` escape naming a basic-source-character or a value in the range D800‚ÄìDFFF or below 00A0 (other than the explicitly named control points) is rejected as a UCN that cannot designate an identifier character (6.4.3p2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three reject `A`)

### ¬ßE Implementation limits (normative)

> Annex E's *minimum-magnitude* table is unchanged from C99 to C11. C11 adds new `<float.h>` macros (subnormal flags, decimal-digit counts, true-min) but assigns them **no** Annex-E minimum magnitudes. All rows below were verified by static-array-size probes against mcc's bundled `<limits.h>`/`<float.h>`.

- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî The values in `<limits.h>` and `<float.h>` shall be replaced by implementation-defined constant expressions whose magnitudes (absolute values) are greater than or equal to those shown, with the same sign (5.2.4.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `CHAR_BIT` shall be ‚â• 8 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: 8 via `__CHAR_BIT__`)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `SCHAR_MIN` shall be ‚â§ ‚àí127, `SCHAR_MAX` ‚â• +127, `UCHAR_MAX` ‚â• 255 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (‚àí128/127/255)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `CHAR_MIN`/`CHAR_MAX` shall equal the `signed char` limits or the `unsigned char` limits according to plain-`char` signedness (no fixed magnitude of their own) (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc selects via `'\xff' > 0` test)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `MB_LEN_MAX` shall be ‚â• 1 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: 16)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `SHRT_MIN` shall be ‚â§ ‚àí32767, `SHRT_MAX` ‚â• +32767, `USHRT_MAX` ‚â• 65535 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (‚àí32768/32767/65535)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `INT_MIN` shall be ‚â§ ‚àí32767, `INT_MAX` ‚â• +32767, `UINT_MAX` ‚â• 65535 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `LONG_MIN` shall be ‚â§ ‚àí2147483647, `LONG_MAX` ‚â• +2147483647, `ULONG_MAX` ‚â• 4294967295 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `LLONG_MIN` shall be ‚â§ ‚àí9223372036854775807, `LLONG_MAX` ‚â• +9223372036854775807, `ULLONG_MAX` ‚â• 18446744073709551615 (5.2.4.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_RADIX` shall be ‚â• 2 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: 2)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `DECIMAL_DIG` shall be ‚â• 10 (C99 addition) (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: 21 on x86-64)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_DIG` ‚â• 6; `DBL_DIG` ‚â• 10; `LDBL_DIG` ‚â• 10 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (6/15/18)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_MIN_10_EXP`, `DBL_MIN_10_EXP`, `LDBL_MIN_10_EXP` shall each be ‚â§ ‚àí37 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_MAX_10_EXP`, `DBL_MAX_10_EXP`, `LDBL_MAX_10_EXP` shall each be ‚â• +37 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_MAX`, `DBL_MAX`, `LDBL_MAX` shall each be ‚â• 1E+37 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_EPSILON` ‚â§ 1E-5; `DBL_EPSILON` ‚â§ 1E-9; `LDBL_EPSILON` ‚â§ 1E-9 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_MIN`, `DBL_MIN`, `LDBL_MIN` shall each be ‚â§ 1E-37 (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî `FLT_MANT_DIG`/`FLT_MIN_EXP`/`FLT_MAX_EXP` (and their `DBL_`/`LDBL_` analogues) appear in Annex E but carry **no** fixed minimum magnitude (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all defined; 24/-125/128, 53/-1021/1024, 64/-16381/16384)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE (C11) ‚Äî The C11-added `<float.h>` macros `FLT_HAS_SUBNORM`/`DBL_HAS_SUBNORM`/`LDBL_HAS_SUBNORM`, `FLT_DECIMAL_DIG`/`DBL_DECIMAL_DIG`/`LDBL_DECIMAL_DIG`, and `FLT_TRUE_MIN`/`DBL_TRUE_MIN`/`LDBL_TRUE_MIN` are defined by 5.2.4.2.2 but are **not** assigned Annex-E minimum magnitudes. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all nine present in mcc's `<float.h>`; HAS_SUBNORM=1, DECIMAL_DIG 9/17/21, TRUE_MIN denormals)
- [‚úì] ¬ßE ‚Äî *(gap)* `FLT_ROUNDS` and `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` are defined in `<float.h>` (5.2.4.2.2); they have no Annex-E magnitude but are required members. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (mcc: `FLT_ROUNDS`=1, `FLT_EVAL_METHOD`=0 on x86-64 / 2 on i386)

### ¬ßH Language-independent arithmetic ‚Äî relation to LIA-1 (informative)

> Annex H is *informative*; it binds nothing beyond the normative clauses it references, so every row is "(spec; not separately testable)". mcc's underlying arithmetic (two's-complement integers, IEEE-754 binary float, wraparound unsigned) realizes the LIA-1 mapping the same way gcc/clang do.

- ¬ßH.1 ‚Äî Annex H documents the relationship between this standard and ISO/IEC 10967-1 (LIA-1); it is informative and binds nothing beyond the normative clauses it references (H.1). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2 ‚Äî The C arithmetic types are mapped to the LIA-1 datatypes and operations (H.2). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2.1 ‚Äî The C `_Bool`/`bool` type corresponds to the LIA-1 boolean datatype (H.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2.2 ‚Äî The C standard and extended integer types model LIA-1 integer datatypes; the LIA-1 `bounded`, `modulo`, `minint`, `maxint` parameters map to the `<limits.h>` values (H.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2.2 ‚Äî LIA-1 `integer_overflow` corresponds to C's undefined behavior on signed integer overflow; unsigned types provide LIA-1 `modulo` (non-trapping, wraparound) arithmetic (H.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2.3 ‚Äî The C floating types model LIA-1 floating-point datatypes; the LIA-1 parameters `r` (radix), `p` (precision), `emin`, `emax` map to `FLT_RADIX`, `*_MANT_DIG`, `*_MIN_EXP`, `*_MAX_EXP` (H.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2.3.1 ‚Äî LIA-1 floating overflow/underflow notifications correspond to C's `<fenv.h>` exception flags `FE_OVERFLOW`/`FE_UNDERFLOW` (H.2.3.1). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.2.4 ‚Äî C's integer‚Üîinteger, integer‚Üîfloating, and floating‚Üîfloating conversions correspond to the LIA-1 conversion operations and their notifications (H.2.4). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.3 ‚Äî Annex H documents the LIA-1 notification mechanisms and how a C implementation realizes them (H.3). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.3.1 ‚Äî LIA-1 "recording of indicators" maps to the `<fenv.h>` floating-point status flags; "alteration of control flow"/trap maps to signals such as `SIGFPE` (H.3.1). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)
- ¬ßH.3.2 ‚Äî Changing the rounding/notification environment is performed via the `<fenv.h>` functions in conjunction with `#pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS` (H.3.2). ‚Äî (spec; not separately testable)

### ¬ßI Common warnings (informative)

> Annex I is purely *informative*: **none** of these warnings is required, and an implementation may also warn in any other situation it chooses. mcc therefore conforms on every row regardless of whether it emits the warning. Probed under `-Wall -Wextra`: of this catalog mcc emits only the unknown-`#pragma` warning; gcc and clang additionally emit the unused-object, `/*`-in-comment, and partly-bracketed-initializer warnings.

- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A new struct/union type first appearing in a parameter declaration (whose scope ends at the end of the function declarator) may be diagnosed (6.7.2.3, 6.9.1). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; mcc does not warn, gcc/clang do)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A block that initializes an object of automatic storage duration is jumped into, bypassing the initializer (6.8). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; mcc does not warn)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî An implicit narrowing conversion is encountered (e.g. `long int`‚Üí`int`, `double`‚Üí`int`, or `void *`‚Üía pointer to any type other than a character type) (6.3, C99 6.7.8 / C11 6.7.9). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; mcc does not warn without `-Wconversion`-style flags)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A hexadecimal floating constant cannot be represented exactly in its evaluation format (6.4.4.2). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; not emitted)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî An integer character constant contains more than one character, or a wide character constant contains more than one multibyte character (6.4.4.4). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; gcc/clang warn under `-Wmultichar`, mcc accepts silently)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî The characters `/*` are found within a comment (6.4.9). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì(warns) clang:‚úì(warns) (informative/optional; mcc does not warn)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî An "unordered" binary operator (one not `,`, `&&`, or `||`) has a side effect to an lvalue in one operand and a side effect on, or an access to, the identical lvalue in the other operand (6.5). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; gcc/clang warn `-Wsequence-point`, mcc does not)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A function is called but no prototype has been supplied (6.5.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; emitted under `-Wmissing-prototypes`-style flags by gcc/clang; not by mcc)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî The arguments in a function call do not agree in number and type with those of the parameters of a (non-prototype) function definition (6.5.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî An object is defined but not used (6.9). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì(warns) clang:‚úì(warns) (informative/optional; mcc emits no unused-variable warning)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A value is given to an object of enumerated type other than via an enumeration constant of that type, an object of the same enumerated type, or a function returning that type (6.7.2.2). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî An aggregate has a partly bracketed initialization (C99 6.7.8 / C11 6.7.9). ‚Äî mcc:~ gcc:‚úì(warns) clang:‚úì(warns) (informative/optional; mcc accepts `int a[2][2]={1,2,3,4}` with no warning)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A statement cannot be reached (6.8). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; none of the three warn by default on `return;return;`)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A statement has no apparent effect (6.8). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî A constant expression is used as the controlling expression of a selection statement (6.8.4). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional; none of the three warn on `if(1)`)
- [~] ¬ßI ‚Äî An incorrectly formed preprocessing group is encountered while skipping a conditionally excluded preprocessing group (6.10.1). ‚Äî mcc:~ (informative/optional)
- [‚úì] ¬ßI ‚Äî An unrecognized `#pragma` directive is encountered (6.10.6). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì(warns) gcc:‚úì(warns) clang:‚úì(warns) (mcc emits "#pragma ‚Ä¶ ignored", matching gcc/clang `-Wunknown-pragmas`)

### ¬ßJ.1 Unspecified behavior (informative)

> Annex J.1 is an *informative* catalog of unspecified-behavior points; the listed behaviors are by definition not constrained, so a conforming implementation may choose any of the allowed alternatives. Not separately testable as conformance ‚Äî each row is a documentation pointer. mcc behaves within the allowed latitude in every case (verified incidentally: evaluation-order, padding, and zero-size-allocation behaviors all fall inside the permitted set).

- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The manner of, and whether any, static initialization of an object happens before `main` is entered, in cases not otherwise specified (5.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order in which two declarators referring to the same object are processed (where not otherwise specified) (5.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The value of bytes corresponding to any padding bits in an object representation (6.2.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The values of bytes corresponding to union members other than the one most recently stored into (6.2.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The representation actually used when a value has more than one object representation (e.g. a value with multiple representations) (6.2.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî Whether two string literals (or two compatible-element compound literals) result in distinct or shared/overlapping storage (6.4.5). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog) ‚Äî mcc pools identical string literals like gcc/clang
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order in which subexpressions are evaluated and the order in which side effects take place, except as specified for `&&`, `||`, `?:`, `,`, and function-call sequencing (6.5). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order in which the function designator, the arguments, and subexpressions within the arguments are evaluated in a function call (6.5.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order of side effects among compound-literal initializer-list expressions (6.5.2.5). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order in which the operands of an assignment operator are evaluated (6.5.16). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The alignment of the addressable storage unit allocated to hold a bit-field (6.7.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî Whether a call to an inline function uses the inline definition or the external definition of the function (6.7.4). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî Whether, when the operand of `sizeof` is not a VLA, the operand's size expression is evaluated (it does not affect the result) (C99 6.7.6.2 / 6.5.3.4). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order in which any side effects occur among the initialization-list expressions in an aggregate initializer (C99 6.7.8 / C11 6.7.9). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The layout of storage for function parameters (6.9.1). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî Whether and how a function makes use of the register storage suggested by `register` (6.7.1) ‚Äî *the effectiveness of the hint is implementation-defined per J.3.8; whether the object actually occupies a register is unspecified*. ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî When a fully expanded macro replacement contains a function-like macro name, whether it is treated as a macro invocation (the order/extent of re-expansion across nesting) (6.10.3.4). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order in which `#` and `##` operations are evaluated during macro replacement (6.10.3.2, 6.10.3.3). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The state of the floating-point status flags when execution passes from code that ignores them to code that observes them, absent `FENV_ACCESS` (7.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; unspecified-behavior catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The order and contiguity of storage allocated by successive calls to `calloc`/`malloc`/`realloc` (C99 7.20.3 / C11 7.22.3). ‚Äî (spec; library/host-allocator behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The amount of storage allocated by a memory-management request of zero size (a null or a unique non-dereferenceable pointer may be returned) (C99 7.20.3 / 7.22.3). ‚Äî (spec; library/host-allocator behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî Which of two elements that compare equal is matched by `bsearch`, and the relative order in the array of two `qsort` elements that compare equal (C99 7.20.5 / 7.22.5). ‚Äî (spec; library/host behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî Whether `errno` is a macro or an identifier declared with external linkage (7.5). ‚Äî (spec; host `<errno.h>` behavior ‚Äî a macro on glibc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.1 ‚Äî The contents of the array pointed to by `setbuf`/`setvbuf`, the value of `argv`-string contents after `main` returns, and other locale/time-dependent string contents, within the bounds the standard allows (miscellaneous library entries enumerated in J.1). ‚Äî (spec; library/host behavior)

### ¬ßJ.2 Undefined behavior (informative)

> Annex J.2 is an *informative* enumeration of behaviors made undefined by the normative clauses it cites; it is not guaranteed exhaustive. Because the behavior is *undefined*, an implementation conforms whatever it does ‚Äî so these are catalog rows, not pass/fail tests, except where the cited normative clause *also* imposes a constraint (those few are probed below). C11 entries marked **(C11)** cover atomics/threads/`_Generic`/Annex K and the "unsequenced side effect" reformulation of the C99 "modified more than once between sequence points" rule.

- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A "shall"/"shall not" requirement that appears outside a constraint is violated (4p2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A nonempty source file does not end in a new-line not immediately preceded by a backslash, or ends with a partial preprocessing token or comment (5.1.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Token concatenation by backslash-newline splicing produces a universal character name (5.1.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A program in a hosted environment does not define `main` with one of the permitted signatures (`int main(void)`, `int main(int, char *[])`, or an implementation-defined form) (5.1.2.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A character not in the basic source character set occurs except in an identifier, comment, string/character constant, header name, or where the standard permits (5.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An identifier, comment, string literal, character constant, or header name contains an invalid multibyte character or does not begin and end in the initial shift state (5.2.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The same identifier has both internal and external linkage in the same translation unit (6.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An object is referred to outside of its lifetime (6.2.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The value of a pointer to an object whose lifetime has ended is used (6.2.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The value of an object with automatic storage duration is used while it is indeterminate (6.2.4, C99 6.7.8/6.8 / C11 6.7.9/6.8). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A trap representation is read by an lvalue expression that does not have character type (6.2.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A trap representation is produced by a side effect that modifies all or part of an object via a non-character-type lvalue (6.2.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Two declarations of the same object or function specify types that are not compatible (6.2.7). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog) ‚Äî mcc/gcc/clang all diagnose the in-TU case as a constraint
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A program attempts to modify a string literal (6.4.5). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog) ‚Äî mcc places literals in read-only storage like gcc/clang
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The characters `'`, `\`, `"`, `//`, or `/*` occur between the `<` and `>` delimiters or between the `"` delimiters of a header-name preprocessing token (6.4.7). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A side effect on a scalar object is unsequenced relative to either a different side effect on the same scalar object or a value computation using that object **(C11 6.5p2)**; equivalently in C99, an object is modified more than once, or modified and read, between two adjacent sequence points (C99 6.5p2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn `-Wsequence-point`, mcc does not)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An exceptional condition occurs during the evaluation of an expression (e.g. signed integer overflow) (6.5). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An object's stored value is accessed through an lvalue of a type not in the permitted aliasing list for the object's effective type (6.5). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An argument to a function has a type incompatible with the corresponding parameter of a function defined with a prototype (6.5.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A function is defined with a type incompatible with the type (derived from its declaration) pointed to by the expression that calls it (6.5.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 (C11) ‚Äî A member of an atomic structure or union is accessed directly (6.5.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The operand of `sizeof` or (C11) `_Alignof` is a function type, an incomplete type, the parenthesized name of such a type, or a bit-field member, used where prohibited (6.5.3.4, C11 6.5.3.4). ‚Äî (spec; constraint, diagnosed by all three)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Pointers that do not point into, or just one past the end of, the same array object are compared with relational operators (6.5.8). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An object is assigned to an inexactly overlapping object, or to an exactly overlapping object of incompatible type (6.5.16.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An expression is shifted by a negative number, or by an amount ‚â• the width of the promoted left operand (6.5.7). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn on constant out-of-range shift, mcc may not)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Integer division or remainder is computed with a second operand of zero (6.5.5). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn `-Wdiv-by-zero` on constant 0)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Addition/subtraction of an integer and a pointer produces a result that does not point into, or just one past the end of, the same array object (6.5.6). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Pointer arithmetic is performed on a pointer that does not point into, or just one past, an array object (6.5.6). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An array subscript is out of range, even where an object is seemingly accessible with the given subscript (6.5.6, 6.5.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The unary `*` operator is applied to a pointer with an invalid value (null, misaligned for the referenced type, or pointing past the object) (6.5.3.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Conversion to or from an integer type produces a value outside the range that can be represented (6.3.1.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Conversion between two pointer types produces a result that is incorrectly aligned (6.3.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A pointer is converted to other than an integer or pointer type (6.3.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; constraint, diagnosed by all three)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Demotion of a floating value to a narrower floating type produces a value outside the representable range (6.3.1.5). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An lvalue does not designate an object when evaluated (6.3.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A non-array lvalue with incomplete type is used in a context that requires the value of the designated object (6.3.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; constraint, diagnosed by all three)
- [‚úì] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An lvalue designating an object of automatic storage duration that could have been declared `register` is used in a context that requires the address-of operator `&` (6.3.2.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (this *is* a constraint for `register`-declared objects: all three error "address of register variable requested"; verified)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An attempt is made to modify, through a non-const lvalue, an object defined with a const-qualified type (6.7.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An attempt is made to refer to, through a non-volatile lvalue, an object defined with a volatile-qualified type (6.7.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `restrict`-qualified pointer's aliasing guarantee is violated (a restricted object is modified via one pointer and accessed via another based pointer) (6.7.3.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A function with external linkage is declared `inline` (without `extern`) but no external definition exists in the translation unit, and the function is used (6.7.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The value of an unnamed member of a structure or union is used (C99 6.7.8 / C11 6.7.9). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A non-constant initializer is used for an object that requires a constant one (static storage duration) (C99 6.7.8 / C11 6.7.9). ‚Äî (spec; constraint, diagnosed by all three)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî An identifier with internal linkage and incomplete type is declared by a tentative definition not completed by the end of the translation unit (6.9.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `goto`, `switch`, or fall-through jumps into the scope of an identifier having a variably modified type / VLA from outside that scope (6.8.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; constraint for VM jumps, diagnosed by all three)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A function is called with a number of arguments not equal to the number of parameters (no prototype in scope) (6.5.2.2, 6.9.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `return` statement with an expression executes in a `void` function, or a `return` without an expression executes in a non-`void` function and the caller uses the value (6.8.6.4). ‚Äî (spec; constraint for the `void`+expr case, diagnosed by all three)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî Execution reaches the closing `}` of a non-`void` function and the caller uses the (nonexistent) returned value (6.9.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn `-Wreturn-type`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî `va_arg` is invoked with a type incompatible with the type of the actual next argument (after default promotions), or is invoked when there is no actual next argument (C99 7.16.1.1 / C11 7.16). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `va_start`/`va_copy` is not matched by a corresponding `va_end` in the same function, or `va_arg` is used on a `va_list` after `va_end` (7.16). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî `va_start` is used with a `parmN` declared `register`, of function or array type, or of a type incompatible with the default argument promotions (7.16.1.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn `-Wvarargs`, mcc accepts silently)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A library-function argument has an invalid value or a type inappropriate for the parameter (7.1.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A library-function pointer argument does not point to a valid object or range (e.g. a null pointer where one is not permitted) (7.1.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The `assert` macro is suppressed (to access an actual function) or is otherwise redefined (7.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A standard-library reserved identifier or macro name is the subject of a `#define` or `#undef`, or a file with the same name as a standard header is supplied (7.1.3, 7.1.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A conversion-state object (`mbstate_t`) is used by a function with a different conversion state or in an indeterminate state (C99 7.24.6 / C11 7.28). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The array set as a stream buffer by `setvbuf` is accessed while it is in use (C99 7.19.5.6 / C11 7.21.5.6). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `FILE` object's pointer is copied/used after the lifetime of the `FILE` object ends (C99 7.19.3 / C11 7.21.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî On an update stream, an output, input, or file-positioning operation is performed without the required intervening operation after switching direction (C99 7.19.5.3 / C11 7.21.5.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `printf`/`scanf` conversion specification is invalid, an argument has the wrong type, or there are insufficient arguments for the format (C99 7.19.6 / C11 7.21.6). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn `-Wformat`, mcc does not)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `%n` directive's argument is not a valid pointer to an integer of the matching type (C99 7.19.6 / C11 7.21.6). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî `realloc` or `free` is passed a pointer not previously returned by `malloc`/`calloc`/`realloc`, or already freed (C99 7.20.3 / C11 7.22.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The value of a pointer that refers to space deallocated by `free`/`realloc` is used (C99 7.20.3 / C11 7.22.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî `longjmp` is invoked from a nested signal handler, or to an environment whose function has terminated, or in a way that violates the `setjmp`/`longjmp` rules (7.13.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A signal handler returns when the signal was `SIGFPE`, `SIGILL`, `SIGSEGV`, or any other implementation-defined value corresponding to a computational exception (7.14.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A signal handler calls any standard library function other than the async-signal-safe set (`abort`, `_Exit`, `quick_exit`, `signal` for the same signal **(C11)**, or atomic lock-free operations **(C11)**) (7.14.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A signal handler refers to a static (or thread, **C11**) storage-duration object that is not a lock-free atomic object **(C11)** and is not of type `volatile sig_atomic_t` (7.14.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `setjmp` macro invocation appears outside the permitted contexts (the controlling expression of a selection/iteration statement; one operand of a relational/equality operator with an integer constant in the other operand; the operand of `!`; or a standalone expression statement) (7.13.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî After `longjmp`, an automatic-storage-duration object local to the `setjmp`-containing function, changed between `setjmp` and `longjmp` and not `volatile`-qualified, is accessed (7.13.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A string- or wide-string-handling function is passed an array that is not null-terminated, or it reads/writes beyond the end of an object (C99 7.21/7.24 / C11 7.24/7.29). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî `memcpy`, `strcpy`, etc. are called with source and destination objects that overlap (C99 7.21.2 / C11 7.24.2). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A copy/concatenation function's `n` parameter specifies a length larger than the destination object (C99/C11 7.21). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `<math.h>` function argument is outside the function's domain, or the result cannot be represented (the range error case treated as undefined) (7.12). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `<ctype.h>`/`<wctype.h>` function is passed an argument not representable as `unsigned char` and not equal to `EOF`/`WEOF` (C99 7.4/7.30 / C11 7.4/7.30). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The `strtol`/`strtoul`/`strtod` family is passed a `base` outside {0, 2‚Ä¶36} or other invalid arguments (C99 7.20.1 / C11 7.22.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A character/locale conversion function is passed an invalid `mbstate_t` or operates across a locale change mid-sequence (C99 7.24/7.28 / C11 7.28). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 (C11) ‚Äî An atomic operation is performed on an object whose address is not suitably aligned, or with `memory_order` arguments invalid for that operation (7.17). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 (C11) ‚Äî A thread function passed to `thrd_create` is invalid, or `mtx_t`/`cnd_t`/`tss_t` objects are used uninitialized or after destruction (7.26). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `tss_t` destructor **(C11)** or an `atexit`/`at_quick_exit`-registered function does not return normally (7.26.6, C99 7.20.4 / C11 7.22.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [‚úì] ¬ßJ.2 (C11) ‚Äî A `_Generic` primary expression whose controlling-expression type matches no association is, by contrast, a **constraint** violation rather than UB (6.5.1.1) ‚Äî noted here to delimit the boundary. ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all three diagnose no-match `_Generic` as an error)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `#include` directive (after macro replacement) does not match one of the two permitted forms, or a `#line` directive yields a line number out of range (> 2147483647) (6.10.2, 6.10.4). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The result of the `#` operator is not a valid character string literal, or the result of `##` is not a valid preprocessing token (6.10.3.2, 6.10.3.3). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang/mcc diagnose `##`-forms-invalid-token)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A macro is redefined incompatibly (after expansion) without an intervening `#undef` (6.10.3). ‚Äî (spec; constraint, diagnosed by all three)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A `#pragma STDC` directive uses an invalid on-off-switch or an unknown sub-pragma (6.10.6). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî The `defined` operator is generated by macro expansion during the evaluation of a `#if`/`#elif` (6.10.1). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.2 ‚Äî A predefined macro name, or the identifier `defined`, is the subject of a `#define` or `#undef` (6.10.8). ‚Äî (spec; UB catalog; gcc/clang warn, mcc may not)
- [‚úì] ¬ßJ.2 (C11) ‚Äî A program relies on `__STDC_ANALYZABLE__` or `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` (Annex K) semantics that the implementation does not define (6.10.8). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none of the three define either macro, so neither facility is claimed; Annex K not provided)

### ¬ßJ.3 Implementation-defined behavior (informative)

> Annex J.3 enumerates choices each implementation must document per 4p6. These are *documentation* obligations, not pass/fail conformance tests; mcc's choices match the platform ABI (and thus gcc/clang) in every case probed. C11 adds threads/atomics/alignment categories and the `__STDC_NO_*` feature macros; C99 lacks those rows. Each row below is the documentation pointer; "(spec; impl-defined)" means the behavior is whatever mcc documents/realizes, consistent with the host platform.

- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.1 (Translation) ‚Äî How a diagnostic message is identified, and whether each non-fatal diagnostic is reported (3.10, 5.1.1.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.1 ‚Äî Whether each nonempty sequence of white-space characters other than new-line is retained or replaced by one space (5.1.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.2 (Environment) ‚Äî The mapping of physical source-file multibyte characters to the source character set (5.1.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc treats source as UTF-8 like gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.2 ‚Äî The name and type of the function called at program startup in a freestanding environment; the effect of program termination in a freestanding environment (5.1.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.2 ‚Äî Any alternative manner in which `main` may be defined; the values given to `argc`/`argv`; whether `argv[0]` is the program name; the environment names available and the method for altering the environment (5.1.2.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.2 ‚Äî What constitutes an interactive device (5.1.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.2 (C11) ‚Äî Whether a program can have more than one thread of execution in a freestanding environment (5.1.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.2 ‚Äî The set of signals, their semantics, and the default handling; the signals for which `signal` returns an error; the signal-blocking performed if a handler is called; whether the equivalent of `signal(sig, SIG_DFL)` is executed prior to a handler call (7.14.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host `<signal.h>`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.3 (Identifiers) ‚Äî Which additional multibyte characters may appear in identifiers and their correspondence to universal character names (6.4.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; note mcc does not restrict the set, see ¬ßD gap)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.3 ‚Äî The number of significant initial characters in an identifier (6.4.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc has no truncation limit, matching gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 (Characters) ‚Äî The number of bits in a byte (3.6). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: `CHAR_BIT`=8)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî The values of the members of the execution character set (5.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; ASCII/UTF-8)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî The unique value produced for each member of the execution character set by each standard alphabetic escape sequence (5.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî The value of a `char` object into which a character other than a member of the basic execution character set has been stored (6.2.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî Whether a plain `char` has the same range, representation, and behavior as `signed char` or as `unsigned char` (6.2.5, 6.3.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: signed on x86, unsigned on ARM/AArch64, matching the ABI)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî The mapping of source-character-set members (in character constants and string literals) to the execution character set (6.4.4.4, 6.4.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî The value of an integer character constant containing more than one character or a non-basic-set character, and the value of a wide character constant containing more than one multibyte character or a character outside the extended execution set (6.4.4.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc supports multichar `'ab'` like gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 ‚Äî The current locale used to convert a wide character constant (single multibyte character) to a wide-character code, and likewise for wide string literals (6.4.4.4, 6.4.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.4 (C11) ‚Äî Whether differently-prefixed wide-string-literal tokens may be concatenated and, if so, the treatment of the resulting multibyte character sequence (6.4.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 (Integers) ‚Äî Any extended integer types that exist and their syntax (6.2.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc has none beyond the standard set, like gcc/clang sans `__int128` extension)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 ‚Äî Whether signed integers use sign-and-magnitude, two's complement, or ones' complement, and whether the extraordinary value is a trap representation or a normal value (6.2.6.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: two's complement, no trap)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 ‚Äî The rank of any extended integer type relative to another extended integer type of the same precision (6.3.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; N/A ‚Äî no extended integer types)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 ‚Äî The result of, or the signal raised by, converting an integer to a signed integer type when the value cannot be represented (6.3.1.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: modular wraparound, no signal, like gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 ‚Äî The results of bitwise operations on signed integers (6.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; two's-complement semantics)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 ‚Äî The sign of the remainder of integer division (note: C99/C11 fix `/` and `%` to truncate toward zero, so this entry's outcome is constrained, but the row persists) (6.5.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined but constrained; mcc truncates toward zero)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.5 ‚Äî The result of right-shifting a negative-valued signed integer (6.5.7). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: arithmetic shift, sign-preserving, like gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 (Floating point) ‚Äî The accuracy of floating-point operations and of the `<math.h>`/`<complex.h>` library functions returning floating-point results (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc uses host libm)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî The accuracy of conversions between floating-point internal representations and string representations performed by the library functions (C99 7.20.1.3, 7.24.4.1.1 / C11 7.22.1.3, 7.29.4.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî The rounding behaviors characterized by the value of `FLT_ROUNDS` (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: `FLT_ROUNDS`=1 round-to-nearest)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî The evaluation methods characterized by the value of `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` (5.2.4.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: 0 on x86-64/SSE, 2 on i386/x87)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî The direction of rounding when an integer is converted to a floating-point value that cannot represent it exactly (6.3.1.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî The direction of rounding when a floating-point value is converted to a narrower floating type (6.3.1.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî How the nearest representable, or the larger/smaller adjacent representable, value is chosen for certain floating constants (6.4.4.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî Whether and how floating-point expressions are contracted when not disallowed by `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT` (6.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.6 ‚Äî The default state for `#pragma STDC FENV_ACCESS` and for `#pragma STDC FP_CONTRACT` (7.6.1, 7.12.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.7 (Arrays and pointers) ‚Äî The result of converting a pointer to an integer or vice versa (6.3.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: identity on `intptr_t`-width)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.7 ‚Äî The size of the result of subtracting two pointers to elements of the same array object (the type `ptrdiff_t`) (6.5.6). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: 64-bit `long` on LP64)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.8 (Hints) ‚Äî The extent to which `register` storage-class suggestions are effective (6.7.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.8 ‚Äî The extent to which `inline` function-specifier suggestions are effective (6.7.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.9 (Structures/unions/enumerations/bit-fields) ‚Äî Whether a plain `int` bit-field is treated as `signed int` or `unsigned int` (6.7.2, 6.7.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: signed, matching gcc/clang on this ABI)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.9 ‚Äî Which types, other than `_Bool`/`signed int`/`unsigned int`, are allowed for bit-fields (6.7.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc allows `char`/`short`/`long`/`long long` like gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.9 ‚Äî Whether a bit-field may straddle a storage-unit boundary (6.7.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.9 ‚Äî The order of allocation of bit-fields within a storage unit (6.7.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: LSB-first on little-endian targets, matching the ABI)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.9 ‚Äî The alignment of non-bit-field members of structures, permitting insertion of padding (6.7.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc follows the System V / target ABI)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.9 ‚Äî The integer type compatible with each enumerated type (6.7.2.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc: `int` unless values exceed its range)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.10 (Qualifiers) ‚Äî What constitutes an access to an object that has volatile-qualified type (6.7.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 (Preprocessing directives) ‚Äî The locations within preprocessing directives where header-name preprocessing tokens are recognized (6.4, 6.4.7). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî How a non-`STDC` `#pragma` is interpreted, and the behavior on each recognized non-`STDC` `#pragma` (6.10.6). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc warns and ignores unknown pragmas)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî Whether a single-character character constant in a `#if`/`#elif` controlling expression matches the value of the same constant in the execution character set, and whether such a constant may be negative (6.10.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî The places searched for a `<...>`-delimited and a `"..."`-delimited header, and how header names are mapped to file names (6.10.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc `-I`/`-B` plus `include_next` to host headers)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî The method by which the preprocessing tokens of a macro-replaced `#include` directive are combined into a header name (6.10.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî The nesting limit for `#include` processing (6.10.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî Whether the `#` operator inserts a `\` before the `\` that begins a universal character name in a character constant or string literal during stringization (6.10.3.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî The behavior on each recognized `#pragma STDC` sub-pragma, and the default state of `#pragma STDC CX_LIMITED_RANGE` (6.10.6, 7.3.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.11 ‚Äî The definitions of `__DATE__` and `__TIME__` when the date or time of translation, respectively, is not available (6.10.8.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc supplies both from the build clock)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 (Library functions) ‚Äî Any library facilities available to a freestanding program, beyond the minimal required set (5.1.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc bundles the freestanding headers `<float.h> <limits.h> <stdarg.h> <stddef.h> <stdbool.h> <stdint.h> <stdalign.h> <stdnoreturn.h> <iso646.h>` plus `<stdatomic.h> <threads.h> <uchar.h> <tgmath.h> <complex.h>`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The format of the diagnostic printed by a failed `assert`, and the termination behavior (7.2.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host `<assert.h>`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The representation of the floating-point status flags stored by `fegetexceptflag`, and the result of `feraiseexcept` raising "overflow"/"underflow" along with "inexact" (7.6.2.2, 7.6.2.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host `<fenv.h>`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The strings other than `"C"` and `""` that may be passed to `setlocale`, and the way the locale categories affect behavior (7.11.1.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The types `float_t` and `double_t` when `FLT_EVAL_METHOD` is negative or otherwise unspecified (7.12). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host `<math.h>`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Domain/range/pole errors, and whether `math_errhandling` has the value `MATH_ERRNO`, `MATH_ERREXCEPT`, or their bitwise OR (7.12.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host `<math.h>`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Whether a domain error occurs or zero is returned when the second argument of `fmod`/`remainder`/`remquo` is zero; the values returned by math functions on domain error; whether `errno` is set to `ERANGE` on underflow (7.12.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libm)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The base-2 logarithm of the modulus used by `frexp`/`ldexp`/`scalbn`/`scalbln`/`logb` when `FLT_RADIX` is not 2 (7.12.6). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; N/A ‚Äî `FLT_RADIX`=2)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Whether `signal` returns from a handler installed for `SIGABRT` raised by `abort` (7.14.1.1, C99 7.20.4.1 / C11 7.22.4.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The null pointer constant to which the macro `NULL` expands (7.19, 7.17). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc `<stddef.h>` defines `NULL` as `((void*)0)`)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Whether the last line of a text stream requires a terminating new-line; the number of null characters appended on writing a binary stream; the initial file-position of an append-mode stream; whether a write on a text stream truncates the file beyond that point (C99 7.19.2 / C11 7.21.2). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî How `fopen` modes are implemented; how `setvbuf` buffer characteristics, `tmpnam`/`tmpfile` naming, and file buffering behave (C99 7.19.3/7.19.4 / C11 7.21.3/7.21.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The value to which `errno` is set by the library functions on certain failures, and whether `errno` keeps its value across successful calls (7.5). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Whether `fflush` on an input/update stream causes a re-read; the meaning of any `n` argument; the behavior of `setvbuf`, of multiple `ungetc` without intervening read, of `%p` formatting/parsing, and of negative field widths/precisions (C99 7.19.6 / C11 7.21.6). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The default rounding direction and the conversions of `INF`/`NAN`/hex floats performed by `strtod`/`strtof`/`strtold` and by `printf`/`scanf` (C99 7.20.1.3, 7.19.6 / C11 7.22.1.3, 7.21.6). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Whether `calloc`/`malloc`/`realloc`/`aligned_alloc` return null or non-null for a zero-size request, and the order/contiguity of returned storage (C99 7.20.3 / C11 7.22.3). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host allocator)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The termination status returned to the host by `abort`, `exit`, `_Exit`, and a `return` from `main`, when the value is not `0`/`EXIT_SUCCESS`/`EXIT_FAILURE` (C99 7.20.4.1/.3/.4 / C11 7.22.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The value returned by `system` with a null argument (whether a command processor exists) and with a non-null argument (C99 7.20.4.6 / C11 7.22.4.8). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî The local time zone, Daylight Saving Time, and `<time.h>` eras; the ranges and precisions of `clock_t`/`time_t`; the era for `clock()`; the `strftime` conversion specifiers and their `"C"`-locale interpretation (C99 7.23 / C11 7.27). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; host libc)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 ‚Äî Whether `<stdint.h>` defines the optional exact-width, minimum-width, and fastest-minimum-width types, and the values of their limit macros (C99 7.18 / C11 7.20). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc's `<stdint.h>` defines the full exact/min/fast set)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.12 (C11) ‚Äî The values of `<stdalign.h>`, `<stdatomic.h>`, and `<threads.h>` parameters; whether each atomic type is lock-free (`ATOMIC_*_LOCK_FREE`); and the alignment used by `aligned_alloc` for over-aligned requests (6.2.8, 7.17, 7.26). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc bundles all three headers; `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__`/`__STDC_NO_THREADS__` are undefined, i.e. both are provided, matching gcc/clang)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.13 (Architecture) ‚Äî The values or expressions assigned to the macros in `<float.h>`, `<limits.h>`, and `<stdint.h>` (5.2.4.2, C99 7.18 / C11 7.20). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc values verified against Annex E above)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.13 (C11) ‚Äî The result of attempting to indirectly access an object with automatic storage duration from a thread other than the one with which it is associated (6.2.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.13 ‚Äî The number, order, and encoding of bytes in any object, when not explicitly specified (6.2.6.1). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc follows target endianness/ABI)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.3.13 ‚Äî The value of the result of the `sizeof` and (C11) `_Alignof` operators (6.5.3.4). ‚Äî (spec; impl-defined; mcc sizes/alignments match the target ABI and gcc/clang)

### ¬ßJ.4 Locale-specific behavior (informative)

> Annex J.4 catalogs behaviors that vary with the current locale; documenting them satisfies the 4p6 documentation duty for locale-specific behavior. These are *runtime library* behaviors supplied by the host libc (mcc links against the system C library), so mcc, gcc, and clang share identical behavior. Clause numbers drift (C99 7.21/7.23/7.30 ‚Üí C11 7.24/7.27/7.30; multibyte at C99 7.20.7/7.24.6 ‚Üí C11 7.22.7/7.29.6).

- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî Whether `islower`/`isupper`/`isalpha`/etc. return true for characters beyond the required ones, depending on the `LC_CTYPE` category (7.4.1). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The collation sequence of the execution character set used by `strcoll`/`strxfrm` (and `wcscoll`/`wcsxfrm`), per `LC_COLLATE` (C99 7.21.4.3/7.21.4.5 / C11 7.24.4.3/7.24.4.5). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The contents of the error-message strings returned by `strerror`, per the locale (C99 7.21.6.2 / C11 7.24.6.2). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The date/time formats and the locale-specific era, AM/PM, and day/month names used by `strftime`/`wcsftime`, per `LC_TIME` (C99 7.23.3.5 / C11 7.27.3.5). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The decimal-point character and the monetary/numeric formatting members of the `struct lconv` returned by `localeconv`, per `LC_NUMERIC` and `LC_MONETARY` (7.11.2.1). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The set of characters tested for by the wide character-classification functions (`iswalpha`/`iswupper`/`iswlower`/etc.), per the locale (C99 7.30.2 / C11 7.30.2). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The mapping performed by `tolower`/`toupper` and `towlower`/`towupper`, and by locale-specific `wctrans`/`wctype` mappings, per `LC_CTYPE` (7.4.2, 7.30.3). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)
- [ ] ¬ßJ.4 ‚Äî The behavior of the multibyte/wide conversion functions (`mblen`, `mbtowc`, `wctomb`, `mbstowcs`, `wcstombs`, and the restartable `mbrlen`/`mbrtowc`/`wcrtomb`/`mbsrtowcs`/`wcsrtombs` family), which depend on the `LC_CTYPE` multibyte encoding and shift state (C99 7.20.7/7.24.6 / C11 7.22.7/7.29.6). ‚Äî (spec; locale/host-library behavior)

### ¬ßJ.5 / feature-test macros ‚Äî *(added gaps)* implementation-defined feature reporting

> These predefined macros are the machine-readable counterpart of several J.2/J.3 rows (6.10.8). Probed by `-E` expansion under `-std=c11`; mcc agrees with the gcc==clang consensus on every one.

- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC_VERSION__` reports the supported standard (6.10.8.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all `201112L` under `-std=c11`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.1 ‚Äî `__STDC_HOSTED__` is `1` in a hosted implementation (6.10.8.1). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all `1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.2 ‚Äî `__STDC_ISO_10646__` reports the ISO/IEC 10646 revision honored by `wchar_t` (6.10.8.2). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all `201706L`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_IEC_559__` is defined (to `1`) iff IEC 60559 floating-point is supported (Annex F; 6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (all `1`)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 ‚Äî `__STDC_IEC_559_COMPLEX__` reports IEC 60559-compatible complex arithmetic (Annex G; 6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none define it on this platform ‚Üí consistent)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_ATOMICS__` is defined iff `<stdatomic.h>`/`_Atomic` are absent (6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (undefined in all three ‚Üí atomics provided)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_THREADS__` is defined iff `<threads.h>` is absent (6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (undefined in all three ‚Üí threads provided)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_VLA__` is defined iff variable-length arrays are not supported (6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (undefined in all three ‚Üí VLAs supported)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_NO_COMPLEX__` is defined iff `<complex.h>`/`_Complex` are absent (6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (undefined in all three ‚Üí complex provided)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_ANALYZABLE__` is defined iff the implementation conforms to Annex L (6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none define it ‚Üí Annex L not claimed, consistent)
- [‚úì] ¬ß6.10.8.3 (C11) ‚Äî `__STDC_LIB_EXT1__` is defined (to a `yyyymmL` value) iff the bounds-checking Annex K interfaces are provided (K.3.7.1; 6.10.8.3). ‚Äî mcc:‚úì gcc:‚úì clang:‚úì (none define it ‚Üí Annex K not provided, consistent)

---

## Appendix ‚Äî mcc project status: deliberate differences & limitations

The mcc-project-specific status that used to close this file ‚Äî the conformance
philosophy & severity tags, platform/host limitations, and the **deliberate**
documented differences from gcc/clang (`[~]`/`[DIFF]` items kept on purpose) ‚Äî
now lives in
[docs/NOTES.md ¬ß C99/C11 conformance](NOTES.md#c99c11-conformance--mcc-project-status-deliberate-differences--limitations).
The clause-by-clause map above remains the source of truth for what the standards
require and the per-compiler status.
